# Toras Menachem

## – 2 – Year 5711 – Part One

## 1st Day of Rosh Hashanah, 5711

#### 3

– While walking to Tashlich –

*Unedited*

**A.** Regarding the calendar placement of Rosh Hashanah on the days *B-G-H-Z* (Monday, Tuesday, Thursday, Shabbos), and not on the days *A-D-V* (Sunday, Wednesday, Friday), as per the mnemonic "Not *A-D-V* Rosh"[1](#_ftn1) — one must understand: How is it possible that Rosh Hashanah can never fall on a Friday (*A-D-V*), when the *first* Rosh Hashanah (the day Adam HaRishon was created) occurred on a Friday?

Seemingly, one could say that the rule "Not *A-D-V* Rosh" applies to the calendar established by calculation, whereas in the time when they sanctified the months based on visual sighting, it was possible for Rosh Hashanah to fall on *A-D-V* days. However, according to Rav Saadia Gaon[2](#_ftn2), even in the time when they sanctified based on sighting, the primary determination according to Torah is by calculation; thus, the rule "Not *A-D-V* Rosh" is absolute, even in the time of sighting. We must therefore understand the reason for the difference between the first Rosh Hashanah (which fell on a Friday) and Rosh Hashanah in all subsequent years.

This is preceded by what the Rambam writes[3](#_ftn3): "Why do we not set this calculation on the days of *A-D-V*... therefore they established a day of determination and a day of postponement in order to hit the true day of gathering." The Raavad challenged this, stating: "According to his words, it is never appropriate to set it on the day of the molad, and what sin did *A-D-V* commit that the molad should never fall on it in truth and it is always postponed, and what merit did *B-G-H-Z* have that it should be and not be postponed?"

It can be said that the Rambam did not explain the reason for the postponement of *A-D-V* specifically (and wrote a weak reason), because the true reason is according to *Kabbalah* (as follows below). The Rambam, who was a great Kabbalist, was extremely careful not to reveal matters of Kabbalah even by way of allusion (like Rashi), because it was a time of danger to reveal such matters even in hints (as explained in the sichos of the Rebbe Rayatz[4](#_ftn4)).

The explanation for the reason for the postponement of *A-D-V* specifically is according to Kabbalah[5](#_ftn5):

#### 4

The days of *A-D-V* belong to the line of Chesed: Sunday is the sefirah of Chesed; Wednesday is the sefirah of Netzach, a branch of Chesed; and Friday is the day on which "it was doubled with good," which indicates *chasadim*. Since the essence of Rosh Hashanah is the drawing down of His sovereignty through the acceptance of the yoke (*kabalas ol*) specifically — which is the line of Gevurah — therefore its placement is postponed from the days of *A-D-V*, which belong to the line of Chesed, and it is set on the days of *B-G-H-Z*: Monday is the sefirah of Gevurah; Thursday is the sefirah of Hod, a branch of Gevurah; or at the very least on Tuesday, which is the sefirah of Tiferes, the middle line[6](#_ftn6).

Based on this, we can explain the difference between the placement of Rosh Hashanah in all years and the first Rosh Hashanah. The aforementioned reason for the postponement of *A-D-V* applies only now (after the first Rosh Hashanah), when the essence of Rosh Hashanah is achieved through the *avodah* of man (now, *atarusah d'lesata* is the deciding factor[7](#_ftn7)). This is unlike the first Rosh Hashanah, where all matters were from the perspective of "for He desires kindness"[8](#_ftn8); thus, its placement was on Friday, on which "it was doubled with good," the line of Chesed.

*

**B.** The Alter Rebbe once said that on the night of Rosh Hashanah, the *avodah* must be with joy. The Tzemach Tzedek and R' Nachum (son of the Mitteler Rebbe) entered and asked him: Since on Rosh Hashanah there must be *avodah* with joy, why is he — the Alter Rebbe — weeping? The Alter Rebbe replied that his weeping is with tears of joy[9](#_ftn9).

*

**C.** (While walking by the river, the Rebbe searched for a place where fish could be seen, and related:)

It is told regarding the Arizal (R' Chaim Vital) that he was walking by the river to say Tashlich and was saying Torah, when suddenly a frog poked its head out of the water. His son wanted to chase it away, but the Arizal told him not to harm it, for it desired to hear Torah[10](#_ftn10).

*

**D.** Speaking with the mouth, even when one does not have all the proper *kavanos*[11](#_ftn11) —

#### 5

It accomplishes its effect, because in this speech, the true will that comes from the inwardness of the soul is revealed, which is in perfection within every single Jew.

The source for this in the revealed Torah is what the Rambam writes[12](#_ftn12) in explanation of the law "We coerce him until he says 'I want to'": "Since he wants to be of Israel and wants to perform all the mitzvos and distance himself from transgressions, and it is his *yetzer* that overpowered him, and since he was struck until his *yetzer* weakened and he said 'I want to'... (this is) of his own will." That is to say, the statement "I want to" is effective [not because of the coercion, for a will that comes through coercion is not valid; rather, the effect of the coercion is only to nullify the dominance of the *yetzer* that overpowered him, and then the statement "I want to" is effective] because through it, his *true will* is revealed.

From this, it is also understood regarding the matter of *teshuvah* — that when the actual deed is as it should be, and there is also a request for forgiveness in speech at the very least, it is effective even if one does not have all the proper *kavanos*, because in this speech, the true will from the inwardness of the soul is revealed.

Similar to what is told[13](#_ftn13) that the Rebbe Maharash once said on Erev Rosh Hashanah regarding what is explained in Chassidus[14](#_ftn14) that the matter of *tekias shofar* is like the cry "Father, Father, save me": "The main thing is not the 'Father' but the *one who cries out*" [and as a result of this, that year was "a stormy Rosh Hashanah"] — that the cry itself is sufficient (even if the *kavanah* of "Father, save me" is missing), because in the cry, the inwardness of the soul is revealed[15](#_ftn15).

It is also worth noting what is explained in the *maamarim* of the Rebbe Rashab[16](#_ftn16) on the verse[17](#_ftn17) "For Israel is a youth, and I love him," that even though "Israel is a youth," merely a "youth," which indicates a deficiency in comprehension, nevertheless, "and I love him," from the perspective of the essence of the soul.

*

**E.** (To one who asked regarding *tallis katan*[18](#_ftn18), which is customary to wear even while sleeping[19](#_ftn19), whether this does not constitute a violation of *bal tosif* [adding to the mitzvos] — the Rebbe replied:)

#### 6

The prohibition of *bal tosif* is not to perform an actual deed that constitutes an addition to the body of the mitzvah itself. In the case at hand, since the act of wearing the *tallis katan* is not [in itself] a mitzvah [when worn while sleeping], and the fulfillment of the mitzvah happens automatically, there is no violation of *bal tosif*[20](#_ftn20).

## 7

The significance of these days—the ten days between Rosh Hashanah and Yom Kippur in general (regarding which the prophet commanded, "Seek Hashem when He is found, call upon Him when He is near," for then there is a closeness of the Luminary to the spark [1](#_ftn21)), Shabbos Shuvah (for every Shabbos contains the letters *tashuv enosh* [2](#_ftn22), and on this Shabbos in particular it is customary to deliver *drashos* to arouse the people to *teshuvah*), and Yom Kippur in particular (which is a time of *teshuvah* for everyone, for the individual and for the collective... therefore everyone is obligated to perform *teshuvah* and confession on Yom Kippur [3](#_ftn23))—

Their essence is *teshuvah*, and specifically in the two levels of *teshuvah*: 1) *Teshuvah tata'ah*, *teshuvah* for the sin, iniquity, and transgression that one has committed. 2) *Teshuvah ila'ah*, to return one’s spirit in a state of *bitul* and *mesiras nefesh* to the Elokus that gave it, to its root and essential source, just as it was before its descent—*and even beyond that* [4](#_ftn24).

It is understood from this that *teshuvah tata'ah* can apply even to specific matters and only a portion of the soul’s faculties—those specific faculties and matters in which one has sinned and caused a blemish.

However, *teshuvah ila'ah* is "Shema Yisrael"—the gathering and collecting of all the soul’s faculties that had become scattered, elevating them with *kilos hanefesh* (yearning of the soul) from below to above, and subsequently drawing [the light] down from above to below *into all parts of the soul*.

And just as it is in the particular, so too it is in the general, the complete stature of all Bnei Yisrael, "your heads, your tribes... down to the drawer of your water," that they must all be gathered and stand as one, so that the totality of the souls of Yisrael return to their source and root [5](#_ftn25).

Among the factors that assist in the unification of all the particulars is the *hiskashrus* to the collective in which they were all included as one, and where they remain compatible even now.

And regarding us, the Chassidim of my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, *ka*, *anash* who are *mekushar*

#### 8

to him, or even those who are merely associated with him: this is the *hiskashrus* to him through studying his Torah, and walking in the straight path that he taught us, etc.—as has been explained many times.

This is also a preparation and assistance for the fulfillment of the blessing with which my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, *ka*, would bless those who came to him to request a blessing on Erev Yom Kippur after midday. These are his words [6](#_ftn26):

"May the *Ribono shel Olam* [7](#_ftn27) grant a *chasimah* and *gmar chasimah tovah*, a good and sweet year in both material and spiritual matters, to be occupied with Torah and *avodah*. Those who have children, may the *Ribono shel Olam* help them have *nachas* from them, and livelihood in abundance. Those who need to build a home, may the *Ribono shel Olam* help them in both material and spiritual matters."

**Menachem Mendel ben Chana Schneerson**

*Erev Shabbos Shuvah, 5711*

*Brooklyn, N.Y.*

## With the help of Heaven. Erev Yom Kippur, 5711

#### 9

– During the distribution of "lekach" –

(Unedited)

My revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, related[1](#_ftn28): The Baal Shem Tov used to say that the custom of giving lekach on Erev Yom Kippur is an ancient one[2](#_ftn29). When distributing the lekach, he would say, "I give you lekach, and may the Ribono shel Olam grant you a good year." My father, the Rebbe (the Rebbe Rashab), would add, "A sweet year."

[To several of anash, the Rebbe shlita also added personal blessings][3](#_ftn30).

**********

## With the help of Hashem. Blessing of the Rebbe on Erev Yom Kippur, before Kol Nidrei, 5711

#### 10

(Unedited)

May Hashem grant each and every one a true awakening of teshuvah, and a *chasimah v’gmar chasimah tovah* for a good and sweet year, both materially and spiritually.

Our Sages have said [1](#_ftn31) that "a person’s sustenance is allotted to him from Rosh Hashanah," and the Rebbe, my father-in-law, explains in the maamar [2](#_ftn32) that the word *mezonos* (sustenance) is in the plural form, encompassing both spiritual sustenance and material sustenance.

May it be the will of Hashem that the drawing down of this sustenance—both spiritual and material—should be without any concealments or hiddenness, in a revealed and manifest good.

[During the meal on the night following Yom Kippur, the Rebbe spoke about the greatness of *baalei teshuvah*, and mentioned the maamar [3](#_ftn33) that Hashem loves the wicked. He concluded by saying that on the night following Yom Kippur, everything is rectified and in order [4](#_ftn34) ("everything is in order").]

## 11

There is a unique aspect to the fulfillment of the mitzvah of Sukkah, which is the element of *knowledge*. Since it is written, "In order that they may know, etc.," one has not fulfilled the mitzvah properly unless one knows the intent of the mitzvah of Sukkah: that we were commanded to dwell in the Sukkah as a remembrance of the Exodus from Egypt [1](#_ftn35).

It has already been explained in many places [2](#_ftn36) that the essence of *da'as* is not merely knowledge acquired from teachers or books; rather, the essence is to deepen one’s understanding and to fix one’s thought with strength and courage of heart and mind, until one’s thought is bound to this with a firm and powerful bond.

And the knowledge is: "For I made the Children of Israel dwell in Sukkos when I brought them out of the land of Egypt" [3](#_ftn37).

Now, every single day, morning and evening, a person is obligated to see himself as though he is at the time of the Exodus from Egypt. This is the exodus of the *nefesh elokis* from the imprisonment of the body, etc., through engagement in Torah and mitzvos in general, and specifically through the acceptance of the yoke of Heaven [4](#_ftn38).

In the words of my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe [5](#_ftn39):

"The first thing is the exodus from Egypt and limitations. In terms of general *avodah*, these are the overall life-paths that a person plans for himself—the programs and limitations created for him according to his status and situation; that is, how he wants to establish himself in life, etc.

Thus, first of all, it is a necessity that there be an exodus from Egypt—to exit from all constraints and limitations. This means that whatever plans he makes for himself, there must be

## 12

fixed times for Torah study every day, and his *tefillah* must be as it should be—not a *tefillah* of merely fulfilling an obligation, but a *tefillah* in truth, etc.

After the exodus from Egypt comes the splitting of the Red Sea. For when a person begins to engage in the paths of *avodah*, various obstacles immediately arise for him, each one very strong and terrible, just as it was for the Children of Israel when they left Egypt: behind them the enemy, before them the sea, and they themselves were in the desert.

The splitting of the Red Sea was from above; the Holy One, blessed be He, split the sea and paved a path for the Children of Israel like the paths of dry land. But prior to that, it was necessary for there to be one who would jump into the sea. And when there was one who jumped—a person of *mesiras nefesh*—then the Holy One, blessed be He, made the sea into dry land.

And then the Holy One, blessed be He, caused them to dwell in a Sukkah. As in the analogy of an infant: immediately upon being born, they wash him of his filth and wrap him in clean cloths. Through this, aside from being protected from the external filth, his limbs are straightened and strengthened. And even though this is only for a time, it acts to strengthen his limbs for the entire duration of his growth and his becoming a man.

So too it is in *avodah*: when a person effects within himself the exodus from his own Egypt and limitations—that he exits the plans he makes for his life-paths, at which point the evil of the *nefesh hativ'is* with its physical and fleshly life-needs becomes more refined—then immediately there must be "and they journeyed to Sukkos."

A Sukkah is a *makif* (encompassing light), but it is a *makif* that acts upon the *pnimiyus* (internal). Just like the wrapping of the infant mentioned above, which touches upon the strengthening of his limbs even as he becomes a man.

And this is: 'For I made the Children of Israel dwell in Sukkos when I brought them out of the land of Egypt.'"

Assistance and strength for this throughout all the days of the year are drawn from the festival of Sukkos in general, and the fulfillment of the mitzvah of dwelling in the Sukkah in particular.

The mention of our *Nesi'im*, their actions, and their Torah assists in this, as is known from the saying of my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe: There are the Chassidic *Ushpizin*: the Baal Shem Tov, the Maggid, the Alter Rebbe, the Mitteler Rebbe, the Tzemach Tzedek, the Rebbe Maharash, and the Rebbe (Rashab).

And we, too, shall add: my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe.

**Menachem Schneerson**

*The day after Yom Kippur, 5711.*
*Brooklyn, N.Y.*

## 13

It is explained at the end of the maamar in this kuntres that Shemini Atzeres is the gathering of all the general lights and revelations that are drawn down during the seventh month—the absorption and retention through "good sowing," so that it may result in growth with an abundance of good.

It is explained even more explicitly elsewhere that "the month of Tishrei is the general head of all the months, and within it are days that serve as roots and sources for the entire year: Rosh Hashanah—the root and source for yirah, for on that day Yisroel receives yirah for the entire year. Yom Kippur—for teshuvah, pardon, and forgiveness. The seven days of Sukkos—for ahavah and simchah for the entire year. But the day of Simchas Torah is a greater generalization, which includes the entire month of Tishrei, for then the level of the supreme, general makif is drawn down—the level of the King’s own delight, the Keter of Torah —and this revelation is drawn down on Simchas Torah through the dancing, which is not a matter of the mochin at all."

And as it is written in the maamar in the kuntres, the simchah relates to the letters of the Torah; in the letters of the Torah, their nekudos, and their teamim—in this study, all of Yisroel are equal. Therefore, the simchah is expressed in dancing, which means that the simchah reaches the ultimate power in the soul and in the lowest vessels—the feet.

The saying of my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe (Rashab), is well known: that after Simchas Torah begins the order of "And Yaakov went on his way"—the way of Havayah, the way of Torah and mitzvos. My revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, explained regarding Shemini Atzeres and Simchas Torah that at a fair, one buys the merchandise, and when one arrives home—throughout the days of the year—one unpacks the sacks and begins to do with them what needs to be done.

So it is with every single one of Yisroel: in the seventh month, which is "satiated"

## 14

with all good, they give them and us "merchandise" with which to sustain ourselves for the entire year. But one must open the sacks, unpack them, and do with the merchandise what needs to be done.

And my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, warned in the name of his father, the Rebbe (Rashab): the forty-eight hours of Shemini Atzeres and Simchas Torah must be cherished most highly. In every moment, one can draw treasures by the bucket and barrel, in gashmius and in ruchnius. And all of this is through the dancing.

**Menachem Schneerson**

*Erev Chag HaSukkos, 5711.*
*Brooklyn, N.Y.*

## With the help of Hashem. Sicha of the evening of the first day of Chol Hamoed Sukkos, Simchas Beis Hashoevah, 5711

#### 15

(Unedited)

**A.** Among the unique aspects of the festival of Sukkos is the recitation of the "Hoshanos," the content of which is that Bnei Yisrael request and demand from the Ribono shel Olam that He bestow upon them all their needs, both in material and spiritual matters.

The concept behind this is as follows:

Chazal stated [1](#_ftn45), "A person’s sustenance is allotted to him from Rosh Hashanah." The Rebbe, my father-in-law, explains in the maamar [2](#_ftn46) that "sustenance" (mezonos) is in the plural, including both material sustenance and spiritual sustenance, and the allotment for all of this already exists from Rosh Hashanah.

However, on Rosh Hashanah, this is only in the manner of "his sustenance... is *allotted* to him"—merely the allotment of the sustenance—whereas the *actual bestowal* occurs on the festival of Sukkos.

The reason for this is that Rosh Hashanah (and likewise Yom Kippur) is a time of weeping (due to the avodah of teshuvah), which is a matter of *ascent*, and therefore the drawing down and bestowal below in actuality cannot take place then. But on the festival of Sukkos, "the day of our festival" [3](#_ftn47), which is "the time of our rejoicing"—since simcha [4](#_ftn48) effects *revelation* (because simcha nullifies dinim and breaks through all boundaries) [5](#_ftn49)—this is the appropriate time for *drawing down and bestowal below in actuality*, which is the content of the recitation of the "Hoshanos."

*

**B.** The beginning of the Hoshanos of this day—the third day of the festival of Sukkos, corresponding to the sefirah of Tiferes [6](#_ftn50), the sefirah of truth, the sefirah of Yaakov, as it is written, "Give truth to Yaakov" [7](#_ftn51)—

#### 16

is with the excellence of Yisrael: "*Um ani chomah* (I am a wall)," as Chazal expound [8](#_ftn52), "I am a wall—this is Knesses Yisrael."

And within Knesses Yisrael itself, the matter of the wall is emphasized more among that type of Bnei Yisrael who are "dwellers of the tent," the students of the yeshivos (who have gathered here), whose primary occupation is the study of Torah—as Chazal expound [8](#_ftn52), "I am a wall—this is Torah," and as we find in the Midrashim of Chazal [9](#_ftn53) that Torah scholars are called "Neturei Karta" (guardians of the city), similar to the wall (including the guards who stand at the gates of the wall) that protects the city.

**C.** An explanation of the matter [10](#_ftn54):

The function of a wall in its literal sense (materially) that surrounds a city is twofold: (a) to protect the city from the enemy so that he cannot enter the city, (b) to restrict the people of the city so that they do not go outside the city.

However, even though the wall surrounds the entire city, nevertheless, the city is not completely sealed off [11](#_ftn55), because there are gates in the wall through which people enter and exit, according to the instructions of the guards who stand watch at the gates of the wall to supervise those entering and exiting.

**D.** This order exists also in the spiritual wall—"I am a wall—this is Torah":

Torah is not merely wisdom and intellect that one must only study; rather, it is a way of life in which one must walk, as it is written [12](#_ftn56), "And they shall keep the way of Hashem." The difference between them is that the study of wisdom and intellect is for a certain duration of time—an hour or two, or even eighteen hours a day—but afterwards, the student is free to himself. Whereas a way of life—the Torah, which is the "way of Hashem"—encompasses the entire existence of the person, similar to the *wall* that surrounds the entire city.

The function of the wall of Torah that surrounds the entire existence of the person is twofold: (a) to protect the person from the yetzer hara and the nefesh habahamit, (b) to restrict the body (which is compared to a city [13](#_ftn57)) so that even from its own side, it will not desire the matters of the world.

And even when the Torah encompasses the entire existence of the person (by the person dedicating himself entirely to the Torah) in a manner that *he is not connected to the matters of the world*, the Ribono shel Olam—

#### 17

(being the Essence of Good, and it is the nature of the good to do good) [14](#_ftn58)—bestows good upon the person and gives him all good also in the material matters of this world. This is the content of the gates of the wall, through which he is not completely sealed off from the matters of the world, but rather he also has everything he needs in the matters of the world.

And this matter is included in the "Hoshana" of "Um ani chomah"—that the Ribono shel Olam should grant a good year in good that is visible and revealed, also in material matters.

And another essential matter regarding the gates of the wall concerning the avodah of the person—as the Rebbe, my father-in-law, instructed and taught—is that a person who is surrounded by Torah does not need to be sealed off in inner chambers; rather, he must *open* the gates of the city in order to *act and influence* those who are in the field outside the city.

[And even though he may argue that he has not yet completed his own avodah, "You have not been permitted to dwell near your palace" [15](#_ftn59), nevertheless, one should not establish an order that first and foremost one must occupy himself with himself until he acquires perfection for himself, and only afterwards occupy himself with others.]

Rather, this matter must be according to the instruction of the *guards of the wall*—the nefesh elokis—who supervise those exiting and entering the gates of the city, as the Rebbe, my father-in-law, said: that one must indeed draw everyone close with words of love and affection ("mit a gut vort"), but one must be watchful and careful not to receive undesirable influence from the other who enters from the field into the city; rather, on the contrary, to influence him, to explain to him the superiority of the city over the field, until he himself does not want to return to the field, but to remain in the city surrounded by a wall, which is Torah.

**E.** And after "Um ani chomah" (this is Torah)—we say "Barah kechamah" (clear as the sun):

Among the differences between the sun and the moon is that the moon was in a state of *feeling and yeshus* (selfhood). From the beginning of its creation with the sun ("the two great luminaries") [16](#_ftn60), its desire was to illuminate the earth alone, saying that "it is impossible for two kings to use one crown" [17](#_ftn61). Therefore, even though it said a "proper thing" [18](#_ftn62) [19](#_ftn63), nevertheless, because it was in a state of feeling and yeshus, it had to descend from its level and be diminished (and only—

#### 18

in the time to come will it return and ascend). Not so the sun—we find in the Midrashim of Chazal [20](#_ftn64) that the reason for the redness of the sun when it goes out to illuminate the earth is because they strike it and force it to illuminate the earth, since it does not desire to illuminate the earth so that the nations of the world will not be able to worship it. That is to say, it does not desire its own greatness—the *opposite of feeling and yeshus*.

This is the precision of "Barah *kechamah*"—that the title "Barah" ("clear") is specifically in the sun, which is not in a state of feeling and yeshus, unlike the moon, which is in a state of feeling and yeshus.

Based on this, we can explain the continuation of "Um ani chomah, barah kechamah":

The study of Torah ("I am a wall," "this is Torah") is liable to bring one to a feeling of yeshus, thinking to himself that because he studies Torah, he is the chosen of the created beings, and the entire world stands upon him, and consequently, everything they give him is not enough for him...

The truth is indeed that he has a valid claim, for he is "doing a favor" to the Ribono shel Olam, as it were, to the Heavenly entourage, and to all the worlds, from the highest of levels down to this material world—for through him, influence is drawn into all the worlds!... But nevertheless, the feeling of yeshus is an undesirable matter.

Therefore, we say after "Um ani chomah," "Barah kechamah"—that the study of Torah ("Um ani chomah") should not be for the sake of calculations of "crowns" (honor and greatness), or in order to refute the words of his fellow (similar to "it is impossible for two kings to use one crown"), but rather, only and exclusively because of the superiority of the Torah, which is the wisdom and will of the Ribono shel Olam. Then the study is in a manner of bitul, which is the matter of "Barah kechamah."

**F.** This matter is relevant to the yeshiva students who are here:

Even though from their own side they do not have a feeling of yeshus, nevertheless, when "they carry them on their hands" ("m'tragt zei oif di hent"), and they speak on the "radio" about the greatness of their stature, that the world stands upon them, and therefore, one must give them everything they need—milk, meat, and so on—and the students—who understand English—hear these things on the radio, it is possible that as a result of this, a feeling of yeshus will be aroused in them.

Therefore, there is a need to emphasize the matter of "Barah kechamah."

#### 19

**G.** And in the continuation of the Hoshanos (after "Um ani chomah, barah kechamah")—"Golah vesurah, damtah letamar":

"Golah" (exile)—in connection to the study of Torah—alludes to the matter of "Be *exiled* to a place of Torah" [21](#_ftn65).

And "surah" (turning away)—alludes to the conduct of "the way of Torah: eat bread with salt, drink water in measure, etc." [22](#_ftn66).

And through this, one becomes "like a palm tree" [23](#_ftn67).

This is the content of the lesson and instruction from the beginning of the Hoshanos of this day—"Um ani chomah, barah kechamah, golah vesurah, etc."—that when the study of Torah is in the manner of "Barah kechamah," through the negation of the feeling of yeshus, "golah vesurah," "exiled to a place of Torah" and conduct in "the way of Torah," then the students of Torah are the true "*chomah*" ("di richtige chome") that surrounds and protects the city, and "Neturei Karta" (guardians of the city) who stand at the gates of the wall to supervise the entry and exit from the city, so that undesirable influence from the field will not enter the city; rather, on the contrary, that even the people of the field will enter and become people of the city that is surrounded by this wall, which is Torah.

***

**H.** Continuing from what was discussed above regarding the matter of the wall in the avodah of the person, we must also explain the lesson and instruction from the connection of the wall to the days of Yehoshua bin Nun—as we find regarding a city surrounded by a wall for halachic purposes (regarding the sale of a house, the reading of the Megillah, and more) that it must be surrounded by a wall from the days of Yehoshua bin Nun [24](#_ftn68):

The simple reason that we determine this according to the situation in the days of Yehoshua bin Nun, and not according to the situation in the days of Moshe—for seemingly, either way: either we determine according to the present situation, a city that is surrounded by a wall in the present, or we determine according to the situation that existed in the days of Moshe Rabbeinu, at the time of the Giving of the Torah—is because the main point in this matter is the situation that existed at the time of the entry into Eretz Yisrael, which was through Yehoshua bin Nun, and not through Moshe.

And in explaining the matter in the avodah of the person, we can say that in the days of Moshe there was no need for the matter of the wall, and only after the passing of Moshe, in the days of Yehoshua bin Nun, was the need for the matter of the wall renewed:

#### 20

And by way of introduction, the well-known saying of the Rebbe, Rabbi Levi Yitzchak of Berditchev: Ribono shel Olam, if You were to place before a person the World to Come and Gan Eden (and, to distinguish, Gehenom), and the desires of this world You had written in the "Reishis Chochmah"—certainly not one of Yisrael would commit a sin; but now that You have placed before a person the desires of this world, and about Gehenom You wrote in the "Reishis Chochmah"—then, etc.

And similarly, it can be said in our case: In the time of Moshe—who himself gave Bnei Yisrael "the tablets of stone, and the Torah, and the mitzvah" [25](#_ftn69)—they saw clearly that the way of Torah and mitzvos is the only way through which one merits all good in spirituality and materiality in everything one needs: bread from heaven, water from the well of Miriam, and the Clouds of Glory that would brush their clothing and iron them (in addition to the fact that their clothing would grow with them) [26](#_ftn70). And on the other hand, they saw clearly the punishment given for not walking in the way of Torah. Therefore, there was no need to add special guarding and caution in walking in the way of Torah through a wall. Not so after the passing of Moshe, when the manna, the well, and the Clouds of Glory ceased, etc. [27](#_ftn71)—then the need was renewed to add special guarding and caution in walking in the way of Torah through a wall, which is the matter of the wall from the days of Yehoshua bin Nun.

—The truth is that "Moshe did not die" [28](#_ftn72); rather, below ten handbreadths his presence is missing, because he "stands and serves *on high*" [29](#_ftn73), and consequently, the manna, the well, and the Clouds of Glory are also missing, etc., and therefore there is a need for the matter of a wall.

However, those for whom Moshe still lives and exists even now below ten handbreadths, for them the effect of the manna, the well, and the Clouds of Glory exists even now, and consequently, even now they do not need the matter of a wall.

**I.** And we must add in explaining the reason for this:

Among the reasons for why Moshe did not enter Eretz Yisrael—for which reason a city is considered surrounded by a wall according to the situation in the days of Yehoshua bin Nun, through whom the entry into Eretz Yisrael took place—is because he did not want to enter Eretz Yisrael alone, without the people of his generation (all Bnei Yisrael who were connected to him, or even those who only had a connection to him), who were not prepared and worthy to enter the land [30](#_ftn74).

#### 21

And the explanation of this in the inner dimension of matters—why Hashem did it such that the entry into the land would be specifically through Yehoshua—is as explained in the discourses of Chassidus [31](#_ftn75): that if the entry into the land had been through Moshe, the avodah would not have needed to be in a manner of *yegiah* (toil). And since it is the will of the Ribono shel Olam that the avodah be specifically in a manner of *yegiah*—due to the nature of the good to do good, for the true perfection of the good is when the bestowal is not in the manner of "bread of shame" [32](#_ftn76), but rather through yegiah by one's own power—therefore, the entry into the land was specifically through Yehoshua.

And in more detail:

Even when Bnei Yisrael were in the desert, in the time of Moshe, there was the matter of avodah (which comes through yegiah), and there were ascents from level to level, and even ascents from day to day,

—And similar to the saying of the Chossid R. Gershon Dov of Pohar [33](#_ftn77) (whose entire matter was Torah and avodah, both regarding himself and regarding arousing others [34](#_ftn78)), who used to say every day: Tomorrow we must be entirely different—

However, all of this is only avodah *with gradation*;

And the will of the Ribono shel Olam is that there be *avodah without gradation*, so that through this there can also be the bestowal of good *without limit*, not in the manner of bread of shame.

For, even when there is avodah (the opposite of bread of shame), if it is not according to the value of the bestowal (because the avodah is with gradation and the bestowal is without limit), the bestowal is considered bread of shame (since the avodah is not equal to the bestowal). Therefore, it is the will of the Ribono shel Olam that the avodah be *without gradation*, and then He has a "pretext" ("an oisreid"), as it were, to bestow upon the body (whose root is from the Essence) [35](#_ftn79) good without limit.

And this is also the content of the matter of a city surrounded by a wall specifically from the days of Yehoshua bin Nun—that in the time of Yehoshua (after the passing of Moshe) a concealment and hiding occurred in relation to the status and situation that existed in the time of Moshe, and therefore there is a need for avodah specifically in a manner of yegiah, and consequently, there is also a need for special guarding and caution through the matter of a wall.

#### 22

**J.** And now, even though we are talking about a matter that occurred three thousand years ago, it is relevant and belongs also to us:

One asks a question: For what purpose was the matter of the passing of the Rebbe, my father-in-law, necessary—we had a Jew who showed miracles openly, and if so, they could have continued and finished together with him the number of years remaining until the coming of Moshiach?!...

—An answer to this question, I do not have.

But, one must know at least that the reality is that "a tzaddik who has passed away is found in all worlds more than in his lifetime" [36](#_ftn80), "meaning that even in this world of action... he is found more" (as explained in Iggeres Hakodesh [37](#_ftn81)), and consequently, even now there are the powers of the Rebbe to go out and draw the other close to Torah, to the Torah of Chassidus, and not only to the general Torah of Chassidus whose matter is faith, but also to the Torah of Chassidus Chabad.

But what is it? There are fools who ask questions... then the advice given is not to listen and not to pay attention to them and not to be affected by them.

And in the style mentioned above—that in the days of Yehoshua bin Nun, after the passing of Moshe, there is a need for a wall that surrounds and guards against the undesirable matters from the outside that can confuse and disturb, etc.; and together with this, not to seal oneself inside the city surrounded by a wall, but rather, on the contrary, to go out from the city in order to draw close also those who are in the field, to bring them into the city surrounded by a wall, which is Torah (as mentioned in section 7).

***

**K.** Regarding the matter of the wall—"I am a wall—this is Knesses Yisrael"—there are two types of avodah: there are those whose primary avodah is *inside the wall*, dwellers of the tent, whose avodah is in the study of Torah, "I am a wall—this is Torah," and there are those whose primary avodah is *outside the wall*, to act so that also those who are in the field will be drawn close to the wall, which is Torah.

And similar to the general division of Bnei Yisrael into dwellers of the tent (Yissachar) and businessmen (Zevulun), who differ from one another in the manner of their avodah in Torah and gemilus chasadim. For, even though also businessmen are obligated to set times for Torah, one chapter in the morning and one chapter in the evening [38](#_ftn82), and likewise dwellers of the tent are obligated in giving tzedakah and gemilus chasadim, as Chazal said [39](#_ftn83), "Whoever says he has only Torah, etc., even Torah he does not have," but rather there must be Torah and gemilus chasadim [and especially since "the primary avodah of Hashem in these times, in the footsteps of Moshiach, is the avodah of tzedakah" [40](#_ftn84)], nevertheless, there is a difference between them regarding abundance and scarcity, that for dwellers of the tent, their Torah is primary and the majority of their days are in it, and the minority of their days in gemilus chasadim, and for businessmen, their primary avodah is in gemilus chasadim, and the minority of the time in the study of Torah.

And it is understood that each one must occupy himself with the avodah that belongs to him, according to the root of his soul, etc., and not with the avodah that belongs to someone else.

—The Rebbe, my father-in-law, said that there are wandering souls (with a tav) that do not know what is the manner of avodah that belongs to them, and as is known the story regarding this [41](#_ftn85).

**L.** An example of this—in the days of the week, for "every single day does its work" [42](#_ftn86):

Regarding the division and separation of the days ("the days are separated from each other" [43](#_ftn87)) in a manner that every evening and morning is a time (day) unto itself [44](#_ftn88)—one must understand what is the reason for the division and separation between one evening and morning and the next. Seemingly, it is more appropriate to make a division and separation between day and night, due to the *change* between light and darkness?

In the Gemara [43](#_ftn87) we learn this matter from what is written [45](#_ftn89), "And there was evening and there was morning, one day," meaning that the creation of time [46](#_ftn90) was in a manner that every evening and morning is a time (day) unto itself. But this itself requires explanation and clarification: what is the reason that the creation of time was in a manner that the separation and division is between one evening and morning and the next, and not between evening and morning in which is the change between light and darkness?

**M.** And one must first introduce the general matter of the creation of darkness according to what is explained in the inner dimension of the Torah,

—As is known [47](#_ftn91) that all the dinim in the revealed Torah are drawn and come from the inner dimension of the Torah, because the revealed Torah is the externality and the garment for the inner dimension of the Torah [48](#_ftn92),

#### 24

similar to a garment that is made according to the measure of the person, like the sleeve which is according to the measure of the hand, that because in the human body there is a hand, therefore one makes a sleeve in the garment (and not the opposite). And similar to this in the Torah, that because these matters exist in the inner dimension of the Torah, they are drawn and come also into the revealed Torah—

For seemingly it is not understood: since the Ribono shel Olam created eyes in order to see, and it is impossible to see without light—why was a duration of time created that in itself is darkness, and there is a need to illuminate it through the light of a candle, the light of a torch, and so on?!

And the explanation of this in the teachings of Chassidus [49](#_ftn93) is that the creation of darkness is not because the intent and will is in the darkness itself (for "from the mouth of the Most High, evil does not emerge" [50](#_ftn94)), but for the avodah of clarifying and illuminating the darkness, until at the completion of all the clarifications, the prophecy will be fulfilled, "The night will shine like the day" [51](#_ftn95).

And it turns out that the darkness in itself has no intent and purpose, and its entire matter is only in order to make light from it. And in the language of Chazal [52](#_ftn96), "First darkness and then light," that the intent of "first darkness" is so that afterwards ("and then") there will be the avodah to make from it "light" (at which time the light is not in the manner of bread of shame).

And this is also the interpretation of "And there was evening and there was morning," that the intent of "and there was evening" is so that "and there was (from it) morning," and this is the true essence of "evening"—according to the interpretation of the Rebbe, my father-in-law [53](#_ftn97), that "evening" (erev) is from the word "arivus" (pleasantness)—that through turning the evening (darkness) into morning (light), the true pleasantness is created [54](#_ftn98).

**N.** Based on this, we can explain the manner of division and separation of the days ("the days are separated from each other") also in the revealed Torah:

Since the darkness (evening) in itself has no intent and purpose, and its entire matter is only together with and for the sake of the light—it is impossible to divide between the darkness (night) and the light (day), that the darkness is a reality unto itself and the light is a reality unto itself, but rather

#### 25

the darkness and the light are one reality, as mentioned, "First darkness and then light," "And there was evening and there was morning."

However, in the clarification and illumination of the darkness itself, there are several manners, and accordingly, there is the division and separation of the days in the manner of "And there was evening and there was morning, *one* day," "And there was evening and there was morning, *second* day," and so on.

And simply—that the clarification and illumination of the darkness on the first day ("one day," "that the Ribono shel Olam was unique in His world" [55](#_ftn99)) in which the light was created, is not like the clarification and illumination of the darkness on the second day, in which the firmament was created that separates and divides [56](#_ftn100) between water and water, between the upper waters and the lower waters that cause all kinds of pleasure to grow [57](#_ftn101), that as a result of this, the possibility is created for the status and situation of "your heart will be seduced, etc." [58](#_ftn102) (as written in the second paragraph of Krias Shema which belongs to the second day), until there is a need for the creation of Gehenom which was created on the second day [59](#_ftn103). And similarly regarding the other days of the week, for "every single day does its work."

And from this it is understood also regarding the avodah of the person—that there are souls for whom the avodah of "one day" must be, and there are souls for whom the avodah of "second day" must be, and so on, and consequently, each one must occupy himself with the avodah that belongs to him, according to the root of his soul, and not look for other matters of avodah that do not belong to him.

**O.** And from this it is understood also regarding those whose avodah must be outside the wall, to act upon those who are in the field:

The Rebbe, my father-in-law, chose shluchim and sent them to the cities of the field,

—The intent of "field" is not specifically outside of Brooklyn and New York, but everything that is outside of "this wall, which is Torah" is called "field"—

And nevertheless, there are among them those who came with complaints to the Rebbe: it is difficult for them to be alone in an environment that does not have Jews who keep Torah and mitzvos, etc., and what will be with the education of the children, etc. And in addition to this, there is also the complaint of the wife who is not satisfied with the apartment (the floor is too high or the ceiling is too low...), and she does not have all the comforts she was accustomed to in the city, etc. And in general he argues: who says that I am the one who needs to fix, etc.—a complaint that is heard both among those who were sent to the cities of the field and among those who were commanded to occupy themselves with the matters of the public.

#### 26

The truth is that if he had "eidelkeit" (refinement) in him, he would not come to the Rebbe with complaints:

The Rebbe—is a general soul, a general in essence that is above all generals to particulars, and he is the intermediary between the Ein Sof, blessed be He, and the worlds [60](#_ftn104), and since the worlds include also the world of Atzilus, it turns out that the Rebbe is above also the world of Atzilus. And without regard to the greatness of the Rebbe’s stature, the Rebbe occupies himself with him, and sends him to a certain town to fulfill his shlichus—which is a matter that is *entirely out of proportion*! And if so, how does he dare to come to the Rebbe with complaints?!...

And regarding the complaint itself—the Rebbe knows better than him the superiority of an environment of Jews who keep Torah and mitzvos (and similarly regarding the other complaints), and the Rebbe desires his spiritual good even more than he does, and nevertheless, the Rebbe sent him on this shlichus, because the Rebbe knows *that this is the avodah that belongs to him*.

And even though in truth he should not have come with complaints to the Rebbe, nevertheless, since the Rebbe is good, and it is the nature of the good to do good, the Rebbe answers him regarding his complaints—that he is not alone ("er is nit elent" [61](#_ftn105)), and to every place that he travels, he—the Rebbe—also travels together with him [62](#_ftn106), and therefore he can and must fulfill his shlichus with the power of the Sender.

And to add, that the answer of the Rebbe that to every place he travels together with him, not only nullifies the complaint, but furthermore, through this, it adds to the *magnitude of the responsibility* regarding the fulfillment of the shlichus [62](#_ftn106)—for, when the Rebbe is with him in the place of his shlichus, then the deficiency in the fulfillment of the shlichus is not only in the category of "damaging *himself*," that even though he is not permitted, he is exempt, but also "damaging *others*," in which case he is liable [63](#_ftn107), and all the more so in our case, that the "others" is the Sender himself!...

**P.** And regarding the avodah of shlichus itself—one must know that even when one meets a Jew who is in the street, outside the wall of Torah, one can and consequently must reveal the spark of Yiddishkeit in him, so that it will be revealed and shine with all its strength, until he also will act upon those who are still outside to draw them close to Torah and mitzvos.

And one must bring for this a parable in the material—as we find in Chassidus a multitude of parables from material matters, because the parable is not a separate thing from the subject, but rather it is drawn down from the subject, from its root and source on high in spirituality [64](#_ftn108):

#### 27

"Naphtha" [65](#_ftn109) ("gasoline")—is found in the depths of the earth, and as a rule, not in a place of precious stones and pearls, but in a place of refuse, a place of creeping things and insects, etc., and nevertheless, when one searches there and hits the right place ("m'treft on in dem richtiken ort"), then the naphtha is revealed [and not only that, but it bursts out with such great strength that one must find ways to limit the strength of the eruption], from which one makes light and heat.

And similar to this in the subject—that even when one meets a Jew in the street, one must know that Divine Providence caused their meeting together so that he will act upon him and draw him close to Torah and mitzvos, and certainly he can (and consequently must) act so that the spark in him will be revealed with all its strength [66](#_ftn110), until he himself will be a source of light and heat of holiness.

**Q.** Furthermore:

When one strives to act upon a Jew who is in the street, and does not succeed, one must know that the deficiency is (not in the other, but) in himself, because the Torah determines that words that come from the heart enter the heart [67](#_ftn111), and since his words are not accepted, this is proof that the words do not come from the heart, but are said out of yeshus and self-feeling.

—The Rebbe, my father-in-law, told [68](#_ftn112) that once his father (the Rebbe Rashab) played with his brother R. Z. A.—in their childhood, when the Rebbe Rashab was four or five and R. Z. A. was five or six—at "Rebbe and Chossid." When they divided the roles of Rebbe and Chossid, the Rebbe Rashab said that he did not want to be the Rebbe, because there is only one Rebbe [69](#_ftn113)... and therefore R. Z. A. played the role of the Rebbe and the Rebbe Rashab the role of the Chossid. The Rebbe Rashab entered to R. Z. A. for "yechidus" and asked him a matter in "haskalah": What is a Jew? And R. Z. A. replied: A Jew is fire. If so—the Rebbe Rashab asked him—why when my hand touches your hand am I not burned? Because you are also fire—R. Z. A. replied—and fire is not burned

## Sicha of Shabbos Chol Hamoed Sukkos, 5711

#### 29

**A.** The *avodah* of the month of Tishrei—both at the beginning of the month, on Rosh Hashanah, and at its conclusion, on Shemini Atzeres and Simchas Torah—is the *avodah* of *kabbalas ol* (acceptance of the yoke).

Regarding Rosh Hashanah, the *avodah* of the day is "Make Me King over you," which is the concept of accepting the yoke of His sovereignty.

This matter is emphasized also regarding the blowing of the shofar, "the mitzvah of the day is with the shofar":

It is stated in the Rambam: "Although the blowing of the shofar on Rosh Hashanah is a *gezeiras hakasuv* (a divine decree), there is a hint in it, meaning: 'Awaken, you sleepers, from your slumber,' etc." Seemingly, this is difficult to understand: since "there is a hint in it," which is a matter of *reason*, how can it be a "*gezeiras hakasuv*"?

The explanation for this is that even for those mitzvos that have a reason, their essence is not the reason, but the command of Hashem—the *gezeiras hakasuv*. They must be fulfilled (not because of the reason, but) because the Ribono shel Olam commanded it, in a manner of *kabbalas ol*. As is brought in the *maamarim* of Chassidus, if we had been commanded to chop wood (a matter that has no reason or hint), we would perform it with the same *kabbalas ol* as all the mitzvos. For the essence of the mitzvah is the fulfillment of His will, through which a *tzavta* (the word *mitzvah* comes from *tzavta*—a bond) and connection is created with the Holy One, Blessed be He, who commands the mitzvos.

Furthermore, when the fulfillment of a mitzvah is only for the sake of the hint (the reason) within it, then not only is the essence of the mitzvah missing, but he does not even possess the hint within the mitzvah. Therefore, one must fulfill the mitzvah through *kabbalas ol*, as a *gezeiras hakasuv*, and consequently, he will also possess the hint within the mitzvah.

The same applies to Shemini Atzeres (and Simchas Torah), on which the absorption of all the matters of Rosh Hashanah takes place; therefore, there must be *kabbalas ol malchus shamayim* at that time.

#### 30

This matter is also emphasized in the joy of Shemini Atzeres and Simchas Torah—for although the joy is connected with Torah, whose essence is understanding and comprehension, nevertheless, the *avodah* of the day is not through studying Torah with *iyun* (depth) and analysis, but through the joy and dancing of the *hakafos*. We circle the *bimah*—the reading table—with the Torah scroll. This is not the table upon which the *geonim* study with *iyun* and analysis, but the table upon which the letters of the Torah are read. This emphasizes that the joy is not in the comprehension of the Torah, but in the letters of the Torah, which is the concept of *kabbalas ol*.

**B.** The point of this is that the *avodah* of the month of Tishrei is the beginning of the *avodah* for the entire year.

The beginning of the *avodah* must be in a manner of *kabbalas ol*, and the *kabbalas ol* at the beginning of the *avodah*, in the month of Tishrei, serves as the preparation for the *avodah* throughout the entire year, so that all matters of *avodah*, even those of understanding and comprehension, will be in an appropriate manner.

This is also emphasized in the *avodah* of every day—that the beginning of the *avodah* is the recitation of "Modeh Ani," which is the concept of *kabbalas ol* at the start of the day, serving as a preparation for the *avodah* of the entire day.

**C.** We find the same regarding building a house in Israel—the birth of sons and daughters:

Regarding birth, there are two modes: son and daughter.

Its meaning in the *avodah* of Hashem—"there is a hint in it"—is that "daughter" hints at the *avodah* of *kabbalas ol*, similar to the Sages' statement, "A worthy woman... does the will of her husband," while "son" hints at the *avodah* based on reason and knowledge.

Regarding this, they said, "A daughter first is a good sign for sons"—that beginning the *avodah* in a manner of *kabbalas ol* ("a daughter first") provides the strength ("a good sign") also for the *avodah* based on reason and knowledge ("sons").

#### 31

Based on this, we can also explain the reason and content of our custom that even upon the birth of a daughter, we bless that "she should grow to Torah, to the *chuppah*, and to good deeds"—because a daughter points to the concept of *kabbalas ol*, which provides strength for all matters of Torah and *avodah*.

*

**D.** The concept of *kabbalas ol* is emphasized most strongly in the relationship of a *chossid* to the Rebbe. For, knowing that he is nothing but a "foot" and the Rebbe is the "head," he surrenders himself completely ("*er git zich iber ingantz*") to the Rebbe and fulfills the Rebbe's instructions out of absolute *kabbalas ol*.

Seemingly, there is room for a question: How can it be said that he himself has no head—since he is commanded in the Torah to put on *tefillin* of the head, it must be that he also has a head?!

The answer to this is clarified by the Rebbe Rayatz in the *sicha* regarding the *kabbalas ol* of an "army man": "The soldier has no head. It was once said that a soldier has a head only to carry the strap of the rifle."

**E.** This matter also relates to writing a *pidyon* to the Rebbe—and by way of introduction:

A certain *shaliach*, a "simpleton," when people would give him a *pidyon* to deliver to the Rebbe, would refuse to take it, saying that one must ask the Ribono shel Olam Himself, and not through intermediaries.

The truth is—as explained in a *teshuva* of the Chasam Sofer,

—and it should be noted that in the books of the Chasam Sofer we find Chassidic ideas ("*es varfn zich durch chassidishe verter*"), for the Chasam Sofer was a prominent student of R' Nosson Adler and a prominent student of the Baal Haflaah, a student of the Maggid—

#### 32

that there is a difference between angels and souls. A request through angels is considered a request through intermediaries, whereas a request through souls (the Jewish people)—who are higher than angels—is not considered a request through intermediaries. This is because "all Jews are partners and one body and one soul, and when one suffers, his fellow also feels it and suffers with him... and since both are in pain, it is better that the head enter (to ask for mercy) than the foot enter. For example, the *talmid chacham* is the head, etc.," and especially the *Nesi'im* of Israel, who are the "heads of the thousands of Israel," the level of "head."

From this it is understood that the rule that "the prayer of the sick person for himself is better than the prayer of others for him" does not apply here—for this rule is regarding "*others*," whereas regarding the *Nesi'im* of Israel, who are not "others" but "*heads* of the thousands of Israel," their prayer is as effective as "the prayer of the sick person for himself"—just as the head prays for the foot.

On the contrary: the prayer of the *Nesi'im* of Israel is better than the prayer of the sick person himself, because the *Nasi*, who is the head, feels the illness more than the foot, for: (a) the head is superior to the foot as it is the dwelling place of the intellect, (b) and even the fact that the foot feels the illness is only through the nerves that extend from the brain, since the entire concept of feeling comes specifically from the brain.

However, all this is only when he knows that he is a "foot" and surrenders himself completely ("*er git zich iber ingantz*") to the "head," which is the Rebbe. But when he thinks that he himself also has a head, and in such a state comes to the Rebbe to give a *pidyon*, then a question arises regarding the matter of an intermediary. Regarding the question of *counsel* from the Rebbe, one can ask for counsel from any Jew, even from a butcher, as it is stated in the Gemara, "Rav Ashi... would gather and bring all the butchers of Mata Mechasia," meaning that he asked for the counsel of every butcher. But regarding giving a *pidyon*—a question arises regarding the matter of an intermediary.

**F.** All those present here are certainly surrendered ("*zeinen ibergegebn*") to the Rebbe,

And even those who are lacking in their surrender, since in their inner essence they are surrendered to the Rebbe, then at the very least, the verbal statement that they are surrendered to the Rebbe is sufficient,

#### 33

—similar to what the Rambam writes in explaining the benefit of "we coerce him until he says 'I want to,'" because the *statement* "I want to" is in accordance with *his true will* "to be of Israel... to do all the mitzvos, etc."—

And consequently, there is no room for a question regarding the matter of an intermediary, not even an intermediary that connects.

**G.** This matter—the knowledge that he is only a "foot" and the Rebbe is the "head"—also relates to the *manner* of fulfilling the Rebbe's command:

When the Rebbe gives a command to do a certain thing that is connected with matters of self-affliction, or even the command to increase in Torah and prayer in a way that requires one to detach ("*oprayzn zich*") from matters of eating, drinking, and sleeping, then even when he fulfills the command out of *kabbalas ol* (knowing that he is nothing but a foot and must fulfill the command of the head), a thought can arise that if the Rebbe knew how difficult it was for him to do this, perhaps he would not have commanded it.

The answer to this—based on what was said above (section 5) regarding the head and the foot—is that in addition to the head feeling better than the foot because it is more elevated, the feeling of pain in the foot is essentially the feeling of the head (and when there is a disconnection, *chas v'shalom*, between the foot and the head, the pain is not felt in the foot). Therefore, when the head commands the foot to put the heel into boiling water, the foot must obey immediately without pondering the matter ("*nit ibertrachtendik*"), and understand [such a level of understanding is "permitted" for him to have...] that the pain is felt by *the head*.

*

**H.** The *avodah* of *kabbalas ol*—where one has no comprehension and acts only out of *kabbalas ol*—is in the category of "from the straits." And regarding this it is said, "From the straits I called to *Ya*; He answered me with the expanse of *Ya*"—that through the straits of *kabbalas ol* one comes to the expanse of comprehension, and furthermore, that afterwards one comes to the comprehension and recognition ("*men derhert*") of the greatness of *kabbalas ol*, which reaches the true expanse.

It should be added that this is also the case regarding physical matters:

When a situation of poverty is decreed upon someone, *chas v'shalom*, a "strait" in physical terms, one must accept it with love, because the truth is that "this too is for the good, only it is not

#### 34

revealed and visible to the eyes of flesh, because it is from the *alma d'is-kasi* (world of concealment) which is above the *alma d'is-galya* (world of revelation)" (as explained in Tanya), and through accepting it with love out of *kabbalas ol*, knowing that this is the will of the Ribono shel Olam, it automatically becomes "He answered me with the expanse," and visible and revealed good is drawn down.

Another piece of advice in the teachings of Chassidus to be rid of the decree of physical poverty is to contemplate his standing and state—that he is far from *Elokus*, from the comprehension of *Elokus*, etc.—until he feels that he is in a standing and state of poverty in spirituality. And through the feeling of poverty in spirituality, he will be rid of the poverty in physicality, and expansion will be drawn down to him in physicality, in visible and revealed good.

## Sicha of the Night of Simchas Torah (Before Hakafos) 5711

#### 35

[The Rebbe addressed the *bochurim* who were going to lead *Hakafos* in various synagogues, and said:]

Although it is the way of a person that when he comes to a strange place, he does not feel as strong as he does in his own home, among *Bnei Yisrael* this is not the case. We see that even after the destruction of the *Beis Hamikdash*, when we were "exiled from our land," *Bnei Yisrael* stand with full strength in the observance of *Torah* and *mitzvos* with *mesiras nefesh*[1].

From this, it is understood regarding going to synagogues:

Even though you are going to a strange place, without knowing what type of synagogue you will enter or what type of Jews you will meet there, you should not fear that you will be influenced by them and fail to influence them. For among *Bnei Yisrael*, wherever they go, they stand with the same full strength as they do in their own place. In this case, you are coming to the synagogues with the same full strength as when you are in the *daled amos* of the Rebbe, and with this power, you will influence them and bring them closer to the Rebbe.

**B**. Regarding this, there is a lesson, instruction, and empowerment from the reading of *Parshas Beracha*—*shnayim mikra v’echad targum*—on the *eve* of Simchas Torah[2] (in the Diaspora on Shemini Atzeres, and in Eretz Yisrael on Hoshana Rabbah):

At the beginning of the *parsha* it is said, "And this is the blessing with which Moshe blessed [the children of Israel] before his death."

The truth is that "Moshe did not die"[3], and "just as he stands and serves on high there, so too he stands and serves on high here"[4]. And not only "on high," but also here below. What is meant by "before his death" is: before there was a place for the *kashya* (the challenge/argument) that Moshe died, *chas v’shalom*.

#### 36

The root of this above is the general concept of *Tzimtzum* and the creation of the worlds, where *Hashem* gave room to think that He removed Himself and His essence, *chas v’shalom*, from the world. This gave room even in *kedusha*, as [it is written regarding] "the error of some of the sages... who erred and strayed... and understood the concept of *Tzimtzum*... according to its literal meaning, etc."[5]. From this, there was also created a place to think that Moshe passed away, *chas v’shalom*, and is not present below.

The verse continues that before his death (before the place was given for the *kashya* that he died), he said, "Hashem came from Sinai[6] and shone forth from Seir to them... from His right hand a fiery law for them."

"Seir"[7] is from the word *searot* (hairs), for the vitality that is drawn into the hairs is only a *tzumtzum* (diminished) illumination, and furthermore, it comes through the barrier of the skull. Nevertheless, "from His right hand a fiery law for them," meaning the influence is drawn from the right hand of *Hashem*, with an open hand, etc.

The explanation of this is: even though the current situation is in the manner of "shone forth from Seir to them," where there is only a diminished illumination, nevertheless, "from His right hand a fiery law for them," meaning that afterwards, the revelation of the *kav hayamin* (the line of the right) will shine.

With this power, you can go to the synagogues and explain to the Jews you meet there that in truth, Moshe did not die, and there is no change at all, except that a place was given for a *kashya*, etc.

If the words are accepted, how good; and if there are questions and difficulties, well, when a child asks a question of his teacher and the teacher does not know how to answer, he slaps his cheek and says to him: "When you grow up, you will understand!" So too, one should say to that Jew who asks questions: "This is the reality, even if you do not understand!"

One can bring an example of this from the *inyana d'yoma* (the theme of the day)—that we hold the *Sefer Torah* while it is covered in a mantle, in such a way that we do not see what is written inside, and nevertheless, we rejoice and dance with it[8].

The main thing—as mentioned—is that the revelation of the *kav hayamin* should already be here, and consequently, the need to answer the arguments will be spared.

#### 37

The *Tzemach Tzedek* once said[9] on an *Erev Shabbos* that *Moshiach* would come. Someone asked: "But it is stated in the *Gemara*[10] that *Moshiach* does not come on *Erev Shabbos*?" The *Tzemach Tzedek* replied: "When *Moshiach* comes and resolves all the questions, he will resolve this question as well!"

(The Rebbe concluded:) May *Hashem* grant that each one of those going to the synagogues will bring with him at least one Jew *to here*, within the four walls of the Rebbe, so that they will be established in Jerusalem and the *Beis Hamikdash*, as our Sages said[11]: "The synagogues and houses of study in Babylonia are destined to be established in Eretz Yisrael," and then Jerusalem will spread throughout all of Eretz Yisrael, and the *Beis Hamikdash* throughout all of Jerusalem[12].

***

**Gimel**. Engaging in the work of influencing another, to reveal the *nefesh elokis* (divine soul) within him, must be done by setting aside one's own self—"putting oneself aside with one's own affairs"—even affairs of *kedusha*. This is the concept of *mesiras nefesh* in spirituality.

This concept is emphasized in the *mitzvah* of *milah* (circumcision) which overrides *Shabbos*, as it is written[13]: "And on the eighth day he shall circumcise," "even on *Shabbos*"[14].

By way of introduction: While it is understandable that communal offerings override *Shabbos*[15] because they possess two virtues: (a) the service of the *Mikdash*, (b) the need of the community; the *mitzvah* of *milah* is not a service of the *Mikdash* and pertains to an individual, yet it overrides *Shabbos*.

One must understand the reason why the *mitzvah* of *milah* overrides *Shabbos*. Seemingly[16], according to the rule[17] that one does not tell a person to sin so that his friend may benefit, why should the *mohel* perform an act of *chillul Shabbos* (desecration of the Sabbath) for the sake of the infant's circumcision?

And all the more so in this case, where the *mohel* (who must perform an act of *chillul Shabbos* for the *milah*) is an adult obligated in *mitzvos* [including the *mitzvah* of *milah* itself, as per the teaching of our Sages[18] "the circumciser shall circumcise"[19], both *milah* and *priah* (for "he who circumcises and does not perform *priah* is as if he did not circumcise"[20]), and its spiritual meaning is that he removed from himself (not only the coarseness of evil,

#### 38

but) even the subtlety of evil[21]], while the one being circumcised is a child who has not reached the age of *chinuch*. If so, why should the *mohel* perform an act of *chillul Shabbos* for the sake of the infant's circumcision?

Especially since the *milah* itself could take place after *Shabbos*, and the discussion is only regarding the *timing* of the *milah*—that the *mohel* must perform an act of *chillul Shabbos* so as not to postpone the *milah* from the eighth day (which falls on *Shabbos*) to the following day!

The explanation for this—in the spirituality of the matters:

It is known[22] that "the completion and essence of the entry of the holy soul into a person is at thirteen years and one day," and "the beginning of the entry of this holy soul is... through the *mitzvah* of *milah*." And since we are talking about the entry of the holy soul, the *nefesh elokis*, which is eternal, it is understood that even one day (a full twenty-four hours) is an eternal matter[23], which is why the *milah* should not be postponed even by one day.

In order to effect the entry of the holy soul in a Jew, one must go with *mesiras nefesh*, to set aside oneself and all one's affairs, even affairs of *kedusha*—like the *mohel*'s act of *chillul Shabbos*—for the sake of the entry of the holy soul into the infant through the *milah*.

This is also the content of the story that once, on Yom Kippur after *Shacharis* prayers, the Alter Rebbe took off his *tallis* and *kittel*, went to the edge of town, chopped wood, and cooked soup to revive the soul of a woman who had just given birth and lived there[24]. Among the arguments the *misnagdim* had against the Alter Rebbe was a complaint about this event: "Why did he do it himself and not send someone else?" The Alter Rebbe replied: "In a case of *pikuach nefesh* (saving a life), the *mitzvah* is best performed by the greatest person[25], and I did not find anyone greater."

**Dalet**. For further clarification:

The entry and revelation of the *nefesh elokis* through the *milah* occurs only when the *mohel* is prepared to set aside himself and go with *mesiras nefesh* for this matter—that if it is necessary to perform *milah* on *Shabbos*, he will sacrifice himself to perform an act of *chillul Shabbos* and perform the *milah* on *Shabbos*.

In other words: The intention is not that one must *seek out* *mesiras nefesh*, but rather that one must perform his service in all ways, and when there is a need for *mesiras nefesh*, he is *prepared* even

#### 39

for *mesiras nefesh*—similar to what is explained in the *Chassidic* discourses[26] regarding the difference between the *mesiras nefesh* of Rabbi Akiva and the *mesiras nefesh* of Avraham Avinu. Rabbi Akiva sought the virtue of *mesiras nefesh*, saying, "All my days I was distressed... when will it come to my hand that I may fulfill it?"[27]. In contrast, Avraham Avinu did not seek the virtue of *mesiras nefesh*, but was dedicated and committed to fulfilling the will of *Hashem* in all ways: if he could fulfill the will of *Hashem* without *mesiras nefesh*, how good, and if not, he was prepared to sacrifice his soul for the fulfillment of the will of *Hashem*.

And so, the *mohel* must be prepared to circumcise the infant, to effect the entry of his holy soul, in all ways: if the time for the *milah* falls during the week—he will circumcise during the week, without *mesiras nefesh*; and if the time for the *milah* is on *Shabbos*—he will sacrifice himself to perform an act of *chillul Shabbos* and circumcise on *Shabbos*.

But if the *mohel* makes his own calculations—that if the *milah* is at a time convenient for him, he will circumcise, but at a time that is not convenient for him, like *Shabbos*, he will postpone the *milah* to Sunday (and at most look for someone else who is willing to circumcise on *Shabbos*)—he cannot circumcise even on Sunday. Because the approach of making calculations is the opposite of the movement of *mesiras nefesh*, and when the movement of *mesiras nefesh* is missing in the *mohel*, he cannot effect the entry and revelation of the *nefesh elokis*[28]. And regarding this it is said[29], "The man who is fearful and faint-hearted (in whom the movement of *mesiras nefesh* is missing)—his service is invalid." Only when his service is without calculations, from a movement of *mesiras nefesh*, "when he gives himself over entirely," and does so with joy[30] ("who rejoices to do justice with gladness"[29]), then he effects in the infant the entry and revelation of the *nefesh elokis*, and he will grow up to be "a *mesiras nefesh* Jew, and a happy Jew."

**Heh**. It should be added that according to what has been said, that the *mitzvah* of *milah* must be from a movement of *mesiras nefesh* to circumcise even on *Shabbos*, it is understood that *milah* on *Shabbos* is (not in a way that *Shabbos* is *deferred* for the *milah*, but) in a way that *Shabbos* is *permitted* for the *milah*[31].

By way of introduction: Regarding the general rule in the entire *Torah* that a positive commandment overrides a negative commandment[32], there is a debate whether this is in a way that the negative commandment is *deferred* or also *permitted*[33].

#### 40

But regarding *milah* on *Shabbos*, according to the above, it is impossible to say that *Shabbos* is *deferred* for the *milah*, but rather that *Shabbos* is *permitted* for the *milah*.

The explanation for this:

One of the differences between "deferred" and "permitted" is that the need to *defer* the negative commandment because of the positive commandment indicates the *existence of the negative commandment* even in the place of the positive commandment. That is, there is a possibility to fulfill the positive commandment by itself even without deferring the negative commandment, in a place where there is no negative commandment, and the innovation is that even in a place where there is a negative commandment, the negative commandment is deferred because of the positive commandment. Whereas the *permission* of the negative commandment because of the positive commandment means that the negative commandment *was not stated from the outset* in the place of the positive commandment.

And since the *mitzvah* of *milah* must be from a movement of *mesiras nefesh* to circumcise even on *Shabbos*, it is impossible to say that *Shabbos* is *deferred* for the *milah*, which would mean that the *mitzvah* of *milah* by itself could be fulfilled even without deferring *Shabbos*. For the essential matter of *milah* is the movement of *mesiras nefesh* to circumcise on the eighth day in all ways, both on weekdays and on *Shabbos*. And if he is not prepared to circumcise on *Shabbos*, he cannot circumcise even on a weekday. Therefore, it must be said that *Shabbos* is *permitted* for the *milah*, meaning that regarding *milah*, the prohibition of *chillul Shabbos* was not stated from the outset.

***

**Vav**. Engaging in the work of influencing another must be both regarding simple matters of observing *Torah* and *mitzvos*, and regarding the study of *Chassidus*.

Seemingly, one could argue: At a time when one needs to arouse [others] regarding putting on *tefillin*, keeping *Shabbos*, and the like—what place is there to speak about the study of *Chassidus*, and especially deep matters in the study of *Chassidus*, such as the worlds of *Ein Sof* that are above *Atzilus*, or explaining the difference between the *bitul* (nullification) of the world of *Atzilus* and the *bitul* of the worlds of *Ein Sof* that are above *Atzilus*?!...

The revelation of the study of *Chassidus*—they continue to argue—is in order to arrive at love and awe [as the *Rambam* writes[34]: "What is the path to His love and awe? At the time that one contemplates, etc." (contemplation of the greatness of *Hashem*)], so that through this there will be an *ascent of the Torah and mitzvos on high*, for "Torah without love and awe does not fly on high"[35]. But what is the connection between the revelation of the study of *Chassidus* and the status and situation where one needs to arouse and act regarding the *observance of Torah and mitzvos*?!

#### 41

The answer to this:

It is known from what the Rebbe (the Rashab) wrote in his famous letter printed in the introduction to *Kuntres Uma'ayan*[36], that "now is the time of the final clarifications of the footsteps of *Moshiach*... there is no longer an order and hierarchy in the ways of the clarifications and rectifications." Consequently, one must engage in all matters, for we do not know what is what in the secret of the clarifications.

Furthermore: Even though the revelation of *Chassidus* is in order to arrive at love and awe, nevertheless, the study of *Chassidus* was not revealed in the early generations (who were more connected to the matters of love and awe), for "it was hidden in their days and concealed from all the sages, except for a select few"[37], but rather in the final generations, in the footsteps of *Moshiach* specifically. And there are two reasons for this[38]: (a) Because in the footsteps of *Moshiach*, the darkness is increasing, there is a need to nullify and illuminate this great darkness through a much greater light. (b) Because we are approaching the days of *Moshiach*, when there will be the perfection of the revelation of the inner dimension of the *Torah*, there must be preparation similar to this through the spreading of the *maayanos* (springs) outward.

From this, it is also understood regarding our situation—that even in a low status and situation where one needs to arouse and act regarding the observance of *Torah* and *mitzvos*, the action must also be through the study of the *Torah* of *Chassidus*.
