On the contrary: Since the study of *Chassidus* is connected with the matter of *teshuvah ila'ah* (the higher repentance)[39], through this, a leap[40] is made to a status and situation that is incomparable to his previous status and situation.

**Zayin**. And an additional matter in the virtue of *teshuvah ila'ah* (which is connected with the study of the *Torah* of *Chassidus*)—regarding the nullification of the matter of punishments:

In explaining the general matter of reward and punishment, there are two schools of thought[41]: (a) The reward and punishment come as a *natural* result of the performance of *mitzvos* and sins (cause and effect). That is, just as *Hashem* made it natural that fire burns and water extinguishes, etc., so too *Hashem* made it natural that the performance of *mitzvos* causes reward and the performance of sins causes punishment (as it is written[42]: "If you walk in My statutes... I will give your rains in their time, etc."). (b) The reward and punishment are a separate matter that *Hashem* brings by way of *segulah* (a divine decree), and not as a natural result of the performance of *mitzvos* and sins.

#### 42

Based on this, one must understand how *teshuvah* (repentance) helps to nullify punishments. While for the opinion that punishment is not a natural result of the sin itself but a separate matter, it is understood that when a person returns in *teshuvah*, *Hashem* forgives him the punishment. But for the opinion (which is the final conclusion) that the punishment is a natural result of the performance of the sin—how does *teshuvah* help to nullify the punishment that has already been caused as a natural result of the performance of the sin, like a burn caused by lighting a fire?

In this matter, there is a special virtue in *teshuvah ila'ah*—that it reaches a very lofty level[43]. And since there it is above time, therefore, the performance of the sin and the punishment (caused by it) that were before this, *do not exist* in the level above time that is reached through the *teshuvah* now.

And furthermore—that through *teshuvah ila'ah*, "intentional sins become for him like merits"[44]. That is, not only does the performance of the sin not exist, etc., but on the contrary, *it is transformed into merits*.

**Ches**. It should be added that just as through *teshuvah ila'ah* one nullifies matters of punishment, so too can one nullify all decrees regarding physical matters—children, life, and sustenance—by replacing them with spiritual matters similar to them regarding the service of man[45].

For example:

When a decree of poverty is issued against a person—he can be saved from this by contemplating his spiritual status and situation until he feels that he is in a status and situation of poverty [and in this itself—not only when his spiritual situation is in an undesirable way, "poor in knowledge"[46], but also when he is in a lofty situation in the matter of knowledge, since "the ultimate knowledge is that we do not know"[47], poverty in knowledge as a virtue], and through this he fulfills the decree of poverty.

Similarly, when a decree is issued against him of the opposite of life, *chas v’shalom*[48]—he can replace this with the matter of "death" in the service of *Hashem*, to kill himself over the words of *Torah*[49].

#### 43

And similarly, when a decree is issued regarding children, *chas v’shalom*—he can replace this by killing his children over the words of *Torah*. In the language of the verse in *Parshas Beracha*[50]: "And he did not know his children"—that regarding matters of *Torah* and *mitzvos*, he behaves as if "he did not know his children," sending them to *yeshiva*, even though it is possible that sometimes they will lack their physical needs ("perhaps sometimes there will be a lack of a snack"), and the like.

To add, that this conduct must be in the general education according to *Torah*—not to think about "practical" matters[51], but to send the children to a *yeshiva* where they study *Torah* all day[52].

—And not like those who think about the "practicality" of their children, and prefer to send their children to "college," and not to a *yeshiva*, and at most they will send him to a modern *yeshiva*, and not to a "lazy" *yeshiva* that does not even have its own "high school," and furthermore, even the little time they give to secular studies, they steal from the study of *Gemara*. To such a *yeshiva* they certainly will not send him, so that he does not remain "a cripple" for all his days...—

And to rely on *Hashem*, who creates and leads the world specifically through the *Torah*, as it is said[53]: "He looked into the *Torah* (not into English studies...) and created the world." Thus, the existence of the world can be even without the study of English, and consequently, one can and must study *Torah* without thinking about "practical" matters, and *Hashem* will certainly fulfill all his needs, etc.

***

**Tes**. It is known[54] that "when ten sit together, the *Shechinah* rests," and all the more so when one is in a gathering of several times ten of Israel, and especially on a *Yom Tov*, the "time of our joy," and on Simchas Torah—then certainly the "*Shechinah* rests."

It is understood that in a place where the "*Shechinah* rests," the *Rebbe* is also present, for he is always together with the *Shechinah*—similar to what we find in our Sages regarding the angel Michael (who stands to the right of the *Shechinah*, "Michael at my right"[55]): "Wherever Michael is seen, there is the glory of the *Shechinah*"[56]. Thus, the presence of the angel Michael indicates the presence

#### 44

of *Hashem*, and the presence of *Hashem* indicates the presence of the angel Michael.

And since there are Jews here who were together with the Rebbe on the past Simchas Torah, and Jews who received blessings and promises from the Rebbe,

—The truth is that blessings are also promises, for the Rebbe once said: "My request is a command"[57]. It is understood that this matter is (not only below, but) also above, and it turns out that the blessing of the Rebbe, which is a request from *Hashem*[58], is a command to *Hashem*, so to speak, and consequently, it is also a promise—

Take *mashke*, visualize the face of the Rebbe, say "L'chaim" to the Rebbe... and ask or even demand the fulfillment of his blessings and promises.

And in order to be "vessels" to receive the blessings and promises—take upon yourselves a specific matter to strengthen the connection (but do not burden yourselves too much)[59].

**Yud**. [The Rebbe gave *mashke* to several of those seated with his holy hand, and when many began to ask that he give them *mashke* himself, he said:]

Listen, Jews!

I repeat once again: Now you must connect *to the Rebbe himself*, not through intermediaries. I am not stingy ("I don't hold back") with *mashke* or with... but now you must connect to the Rebbe himself. That I am giving *mashke* to some of those seated is in connection with private matters that even in the past would pass through me, and consequently, they must also now pass through me, and therefore I am giving them *mashke*. But you must connect to the Rebbe himself[60].

#### 45

[To one who asked for more *mashke*, saying "Be a *mashpia* without interruption," the Rebbe said:] Even one drop can be until infinity.

[One sat opposite him and cried, and the attendees wanted to remove him, and he said:] Leave him alone, he is not disturbing anyone; it is only a pity that he is disturbing himself.

[When the pushing increased, he said:] Why push?! There is no need to push; the Rebbe is everywhere, and whoever pushes shows by this that he is of those of little faith.

[When some of the students who had gone to the synagogues returned, the Rebbe asked if everyone had already returned. He further asked if they had fulfilled what was discussed above (Section 2), that each one of those going to the synagogues would bring with him at least one Jew. He continued to speak about the proof and sign for the fulfillment of the mission in the manner of "a person's agent is like himself"[61][62].]

**Yud-Alef**. [The Rebbe continued to speak about the request and demand for the fulfillment of the blessings and promises of the Rebbe (Rayatz), and said:]

With the Rebbe (Rayatz), there were times when his mind was not at ease that people would return and ask and request again, and there were times when he did not mind that people would return and ask and request again.

The time of Simchas Torah in general, and especially before the *Hakafos*, was always for the Rebbe—an *eis ratzon* (a time of favor)[63].

And since this is so, even those who have asked and requested a certain matter several times—can *now* effect ("*oys-poyeln*") the fulfillment of the matter.

Therefore, take *mashke*, say "L'chaim" to the Rebbe, and take upon yourselves a specific matter to strengthen the connection, and through this, you will certainly effect all matters.

***

**Yud-Beis**. [After the *farbrengen*, the Rebbe went up to the hall of the Rebbe (Rayatz) for *Maariv* prayers and *Hakafos*, and afterwards held a *Yom Tov* meal. Upon leaving the meal, the Rebbe instructed the Chassidim who continued to *farbreng* in the *shul* to study in public the *sicha* from Simchas Torah of the previous year (which was printed in the *Kuntres Shemini Atzeres - Simchas Torah*[64]). After some time, the Rebbe

#### 46

entered the *shul*, brought with him a *challah*, and instructed those present—who had not yet eaten the *Yom Tov* meal—to wash their hands for the *Yom Tov* meal. As he left the *shul* to go to his room, those present began to say "L'chaim" to the Rebbe, and he answered them "L'chaim v'livracha." Suddenly, the Rebbe asked that they give him a *revi'is* of *mashke*[65], saying that one should not separate oneself from the community[66]. And afterwards he said:]

L'chaim. May *Hashem* grant that all the blessings that the Rebbe has already blessed, is blessing now, and will continue to bless, will be fulfilled, both regarding each one individually and regarding the community.

And the channel for receiving the blessings is the fulfillment of the Rebbe's wishes, and especially regarding the work of the community. Even those who do not want to be "communal people," should break their stubbornness and be communal people who engage in the work of the community. This will be the channel for the continuation of the blessings, for him, for his wife, and for his household, including regarding *shalom bayis* (domestic peace).

One should connect this with the matter of *shalom bayis* in spirituality—peace between the *nefesh elokis* and the *nefesh habahamis*, through the *nefesh habahamis* acknowledging and agreeing with the *nefesh elokis* (for it is impossible in the opposite way, *chas v’shalom*, that the *nefesh elokis* would acknowledge and agree with the *nefesh habahamis*, since "even at the time of the sin, it (the *nefesh elokis*) was in faith with Him, may He be blessed"[67]. And just as a Jew cannot become a non-Jew, *chas v’shalom*, but on the contrary, an uncircumcised person can become a Jew, through *milah* and conversion).

And as mentioned, this is the channel for the continuation of the Rebbe's blessings—that it should be a good and sweet year in physicality and spirituality.

[The crowd continued saying "L'chaim," and the Rebbe blessed several people with private blessings[68].]

## Sicha of Simchas Torah, 5711

#### 47

*Unedited*

The Rebbe washed his holy hands for the meal.

**1.** It is known—in the name of the Rebbe (Rashab) *n.e.*—that after Simchas Torah, the concept of "And Yaakov went on his way"[1] begins.

—In the *Hemshech* (discourse series) *V’Kacha*,[3] it is brought that the concept of "And Yaakov went on his way" begins at the *conclusion of Yom Kippur*: "The avodah that follows the teshuvah of Yom Kippur is what is meant by 'And Yaakov went on his way'."[4]

However, the discussion there concerns "And Yaakov went on his way" in relation to avodah in matters of *Torah and Mitzvos*, because on Yom Kippur, forgiveness and atonement for the sins of the entire year are achieved, and afterward begins the path "in the way of Torah and Mitzvos, to be in the state of 'turn from evil and do good'."

In contrast, the concept of "And Yaakov went on his way" in relation to avodah in the affairs of the world—*ovdin d’chol* (mundane activities)—begins only after the totality of the avodah of the festivals of the month of Tishrei.

For even the avodah that follows Yom Kippur [starting from the four days between Yom Kippur and Sukkos (which correspond to the four letters of the Name Havayah[5]), and certainly the festival of Sukkos, Shemini Atzeres, and Simchas Torah] is in matters of holiness, Torah, and Mitzvos.

[And among the differences between them—the avodah of Rosh Hashanah and Yom Kippur pertains to rectifying and completing the avodah of the previous year, both regarding *kabbalas ol* (acceptance of the yoke), which is the theme of Rosh Hashanah, and regarding forgiveness and atonement, which is the theme of Yom Kippur; whereas the avodah from the conclusion of Yom Kippur until after Simchas Torah is the beginning of the avodah of the new year.]

#### 48

Only after the conclusion of all the festivals of the month of Tishrei—at the conclusion of Simchas Torah—does the avodah in the affairs of the world, *ovdin d’chol*, begin.[6]

**2.** Now, when a person makes an accounting of his soul regarding the manner of his avodah throughout the month of Tishrei, a question arises within him: With what ("mit vos") is he setting out to go on his way for the avodah of the entire year?

The answer to this is that the strength for the journey on his way for the avodah of the entire year comes through the *hiskashrus* (connection) to the Rebbe:

It is known[7] that the *hemshech* (drawing down) of vitality for all Bnei Yisrael is from the "heads of the thousands of Yisrael, whose souls are the category of head and brain," analogous to the drawing down of vitality to the limbs of the body from the brain in the head. The essential point here is that there should be no interruption, *chas v’shalom*, between the limbs of the body and the head; rather, all the limbs of the body must be connected to the head, for then the vitality is channeled from the brain in the head to all the limbs of the body. Therefore, one must be connected to the Rebbe, who is the head, and through him, vitality is channeled to all who are connected to him.[8]

From this, it is understood also in our case—that through the *hiskashrus* to the Rebbe, the empowerment for the avodah of "And Yaakov went on his way" throughout the entire year in *ovdin d’chol* is also drawn down.

**3.** And this can be connected to the day’s Torah reading—Parshas Beracha:

In the section of the parsha of "Shlishi"—the most important *aliyah*,

—According to Kabbalah, the most important *aliyah* is Shishi (as is found in the writings of the Arizal[9]), but according to *Nigleh* (the revealed Torah), the most important *aliyah* is Shlishi.[10] And since we desire and need all matters to be drawn down below ten *tefachim* in a *revealed* manner, we emphasize the importance according to *Nigleh* specifically—

It is said: "And of Yosef he said: Blessed of Hashem be his land, with the bounty of heaven, with dew, and with the deep that crouches beneath,"[11] and it continues to detail a multitude of matters in the blessing of Yosef.

And one can say the hint in this is that through the *hiskashrus* to Yosef ("*And of Yosef* he said"), the Rebbe—whose (first) name is Yosef—the blessing of the Holy One, Blessed be He, is drawn down

#### 49

(not only in matters of "heaven," but) also in matters of *earth* ("Blessed of Hashem be his *land*"), from the word *artzios* (earthliness), physicality, and materiality, which is the avodah in the affairs of the world, *ovdin d’chol*. And not only the drawing down of the blessing from the Name *Elokim*, which is the *gematria* of *hateva* (nature),[12] but also the drawing down of the blessing from the Name *Havayah* ("Blessed of *Hashem* be his land"), which is above nature.

And one must add the precision of the verse's wording, "Blessed of Hashem be his *land* (*artzo*)," not just "land" (*eretz*) in general, but specifically "*artzo*" (his land)—for *eretz* is from the word *ratzon* (will),[13] and "*artzo*" is *his will*—the will of Yosef. This hints that one must set aside ("avekleygn") one's own desires ("di aygene retzonos") and dedicate oneself to the will of the Rebbe ("his land," of Yosef).

And through the dedication to the will of the Rebbe ("his land"), the blessing of Hashem ("Blessed of Hashem") is drawn down in all matters, "with the bounty of heaven, with dew, and with the deep that crouches beneath" (as above), and primarily—the blessing regarding the *hiskashrus* to the Rebbe, which is the greatest reward, "the reward of a mitzvah is a mitzvah"[14] ("the reward of a mitzvah is the mitzvah itself"[15]).

*

**4.** The Rebbe gave *mashke*[16] to all the *shluchim* in the provincial cities and blessed them with success in their *shlichus* in the provincial cities, and said:

"Field" (*sadeh*)—generally denotes *kelipah*, which is why Esav is called "a man of the field."[17] And nevertheless, the Rebbe sent *shluchim* to such places that he would call by the name "cities of the *field*" [whether he himself gave this name, or this name was accepted by him], in order to accomplish his *shlichus* also in the "*field*."

[To one whose name was Yaakov, the Rebbe said: "*And Yaakov* went on his way."]

**5.** The Rebbe asked one person what the number of his students and those he educates was, and when he replied that their number was 86 (*Pey-Vav*), the Rebbe said to him:

The number 86 is a lofty number, as it is the *gematria* of the Name *Elokim*. However, it is better that your students and those you educate be the number of the Name *Tzevaos*, for, even though

#### 50

regarding the Names, it is possible that the Name *Elokim* is loftier than the Name *Tzevaos*,[18] nevertheless, the number of the Name *Tzevaos* is in vastly greater abundance compared to the number of the Name *Elokim*.

(And the Rebbe added:) On Simchas Torah, there is no room to fear matters of *yeshus* (ego) (due to the multitude of students). *Yeshus* is never appropriate, but the intention is the feeling of *yeshus*, which on Simchas Torah one need not fear.

**6.** The Rebbe gave *mashke* to several *bochurim* and blessed them with suitable *shidduchim*, and said:

A suitable *shidduch* is connected and belongs to the preparations for the coming of Moshiach ("m'redt doch altz vegn hakonos tzu Moshiach'n"), as our Sages said,[19] "The son of Dovid will not come until all the souls in the 'body' are exhausted"[20] ("a treasury called 'body'"), through a suitable *shidduch* and the establishment of a home in Yisrael.

**7.** The Rebbe gave *mashke* to all the students of the Yeshiva, and said:

Regarding the verse[21] "And you shall teach them to your children," it is stated in the *Sifrei*[22] "To your children—these are the students... for the students are called children." We find in the Gemara[23] the expression "Whoever teaches his fellow's son Torah... *it is as if* he gave birth to him," but in the *Sifrei* the expression is that "the students are called children."[24]

Now, our Sages said,[25] "The power of the son is greater than the power of the father." And one of the explanations for this[26] is that the very concept of "the power of the son is greater" is "from the power of the father," through the son being connected to the father.

And regarding our matter—the power of the students ("the power of the son is greater") to fulfill the great *shlichus* that has been placed upon them is "from the power of the father," through the *hiskashrus* to the Rebbe.

**8.** The Rebbe continued to speak regarding the students of the Yeshiva, and said:

#### 51

It is stated in the Gemara[27] that "the Holy One, Blessed be He, sought to make Chizkiyahu Moshiach, and Sancheriv Gog and Magog," meaning that from the side of Chizkiyahu, the revelation of Moshiach could have occurred, and the category of Moshiach shone within him (only that for some reason it did not come to fruition).[28]

And in the continuation of the passage,[29] the Gemara tells of Chizkiyahu’s action to nullify the undesirable matters of Sancheriv—"He breaks the yoke because of the oil[30]... the yoke of Sancheriv [was broken] because of the oil of Chizkiyahu, which burned in the synagogues and houses of study... They searched from Dan to Beersheba and found no *am ha'aretz* (ignorant person); from Gevas to Antipatris and found no boy or girl, man or woman, who was not expert in the laws of *tumah* and *taharah* (ritual impurity and purity)."

The point of this is that the desire of Sancheriv was to strike primarily at the children of the schoolhouse, and against this stood Chizkiyahu, without taking anything into account, not even the opinion of the other members of the Sanhedrin who did not think as he did,[31] and he dedicated himself to learning Torah with the children of the schoolhouse, in a manner that they would feel that the study of Torah is a matter that is above intellect—which is the precision in learning the "laws of *tumah* and *taharah*" specifically, for "it is a clear and revealed matter that the *tumahs* and *taharahs* are decrees of the Torah, and are not matters that human intellect can determine" (as the Rambam writes[32]).

And similarly regarding the Chizkiyahu of our generation—the Rebbe—who did not take anything into account, even when other great men of Yisrael thought that in certain matters one should concede, etc., but rather dedicated himself to acting regarding the study of Torah by the children of the schoolhouse, and to teach them that Torah is above intellect, etc.

And therefore, from his side, the revelation of Moshiach could have occurred, and the category of Moshiach shone within him.

And when the students fulfill his intention—this will be the preparation and the qualification for the Rebbe to lead us to the true and complete Redemption, speedily in our days, Amen.

*

**9.** The Rebbe continued to explain the verse "And of Yosef he said: Blessed of Hashem be his land, etc." (continuing from what was discussed above, that through the *hiskashrus* to Yosef, the blessing of Hashem is drawn down in all matters), and explained in detail all the verses in the blessing of Yosef, and continued to explain the matter of "And Hashem showed him, etc., to the last sea,"[33]

#### 52

that "the Holy One, Blessed be He, showed him (Moshe) all the events that were destined to happen to Yisrael until the resurrection of the dead."[35]

*

**10.** After *Birkas Hamazon*, the Rebbe said:

A good, healthy, and happy winter, and may we hear only good tidings. May each and every one—of all types—succeed in his own area: students and those who sit in the tent of Torah should succeed in their area, and businessmen in their area. And the main thing—that the Rebbe should lead us toward Moshiach Tzidkeinu, to Eretz Yisrael, to the true and complete Redemption.

After the *Maariv* prayer, the Rebbe said:

May the Almighty help and grant success in the avodah of "And Yaakov went on his way."

## B’s”D. Thursday, Parshas Bereishis, Isru Chag, 5711

#### 53

*Unedited*

It should be established that the *avreichim* (young men) wear *zeidene zupitzes* (silk caftans) on Shabbos and Yom Tov, and may those who do so be commended.

This matter—that Shabbos and Yom Tov clothing should be made of silk—is also brought down in a *maamar* of the Rebbe (Rashab) *n.e.*.

In general, our conduct should be in a manner of "*v'niflinu*" (and we shall be distinguished) (as the Rebbe [Rayatz] expressed it), a concept that is also expressed by wearing *zeidene zupitzes* on Shabbos and Yom Tov.

I am surprised by Chassidim such as so-and-so and so-and-so who do not wear *zeidene zupitzes* on Shabbos and Yom Tov. The reason for this, it seems, is due to the state of poverty that existed in Russia, when it was not possible for them to wear *zeidene zupitzes*.

In any event, the time has come for them to begin wearing *zeidene zupitzes*, and in time, this practice will be established among everyone—that all *avreichim* will wear *zeidene zupitzes* on Shabbos and Yom Tov.

**********

## With the help of Heaven. Sicha of Shabbos Bereishis, Mevarchim Chodesh Mar-Cheshvan, 5711*

#### 54

**1.** Shabbos Bereishis is a continuation of the *mo'adim* of the month of Tishrei in general, and of Shemini Atzeres and Simchas Torah in particular, as the Rebbe, my father-in-law, writes in the letter from the day after Yom Kippur (printed in the *Kuntres* of the Festival of Sukkos)[1](#_ftn261),

— Although the letter is from the year 5689, what difference does it make if the letter is from several years ago? On the contrary, because it is like "old wine (understanding and explanation)—the more aged it is, the more the *daas* of the elders (an elder who has acquired wisdom[2](#_ftn262)) is pleased with it"[3](#_ftn263)—

The letter states: "Let all gather together in the days of joy... Shemini Atzeres and Simchas Torah... and as a form of completion and an *additional* 'light that is good' on the upcoming Shabbos Bereishis." That is to say, Shabbos Bereishis is a "completion and additional light" for the days of joy that preceded it, Shemini Atzeres and Simchas Torah.

**2.** And in greater detail—"completion and additional light that is good":

"*Completion and addition*"—"Completion" means to finish what has not yet been done as it should be, and "addition" means that even when one has done everything that needs to be done as it should be, one must add even more.

"(Addition of) *light*"—that the addition must be in the matter of *light*.

"(Addition of light) *that is good*"—that the addition in light is in a most sublime light, "light that is good"—the language of the verse[4](#_ftn264) regarding the light created on the first day, when "Hashem was *unique* in His world" [before the creation of the angels (which occurred afterward[5](#_ftn265)), at which time the creation of the heavens and the earth (which were created on the first day[6](#_ftn266)) was in a more sublime manner, where there was no room for two authorities, etc.], which is why it is called "day *one*"[7](#_ftn267) (as per the *drash* of Chazal[5](#_ftn265)).

#### 55

**3.** And the matter in this:

Regarding the "light that is good" that was created on the first day—Chazal said[8](#_ftn268) that "He hid it for the *tzaddikim* in the time to come," and the saying of the Baal Shem Tov is well known[9](#_ftn269): "And where did He hide it? In the Torah." That is, the light that will be in the time to come is currently hidden within the Torah. From this it is understood that through the Torah, one can reach the revelation of the light of the time to come even now.

And the explanation for this:

*Yisrael*, the *Oraisah* (Torah), and *Kudsha Brich Hu* (Hashem) are all one[10](#_ftn270). And just as for Hashem, the past, present, and future are as one[11](#_ftn271), so too is it in the Torah; therefore, the light of the time to come is hidden within it now. And the same is true regarding *tzaddikim*—that the matter of "Yisrael and *Kudsha Brich Hu* are all one" is revealed within them—that they possess the light of the time to come even now, as they are above the limitations of time.

**4.** Parenthetical note:

Based on this, one can explain the "story of the Baal Shem Tov’s brother-in-law, R. Gershon Kitover... that the Baal Shem Tov wrote to him the entire event before it actually happened"[12](#_ftn272), because in a more sublime world, time is in a state of inclusion, and the Baal Shem Tov was then in the world of *Yetzirah*, where "it is possible for fifteen years to be included in a single glance"[13](#_ftn273)—for seemingly, it is not understood: why did the Baal Shem Tov not write that this event would happen *in the future*?

And the explanation for this is that *tzaddikim* are not an existence unto themselves; rather, their entire existence is *Elokus*.

As is explained in the *maamarim* of Chassidus in general[14](#_ftn274), and also in the *maamarim* of the Rebbe, my father-in-law, in particular[15](#_ftn275), regarding the interpretation of the *Zohar’s* statement[16](#_ftn276), "Who is the 'Face of the Master, Hashem'? This is R. Shimon bar Yochai"—for seemingly, how is it possible to say "the Face of the Master, Hashem" about a "created being"?—because

#### 56

since R. Shimon bar Yochai was completely *batel* and was not an existence unto himself, therefore one can say about him "the Face of the Master, Hashem."

And therefore, even with *tzaddikim*, the matter of "past, present, and future are as one" exists, just as it is with Hashem, *kivayachol*. For this reason, the Baal Shem Tov did not write that this event would happen in the future, because for him, it was *in the present*.

**5.** And one must add to the interpretation of the light created on the first day, "He hid it for the *tzaddikim* in the time to come" and "He hid it in the Torah"—in greater depth:

The light of the time to come that "He *hid* in the Torah"—is in the *pnimiyus* (inner dimension) of the Torah, the "Tree of Life," which is above the *nigleh* (revealed dimension) of the Torah, etc.[17](#_ftn277).

And similarly regarding "He hid it for the *tzaddikim*"—that the true essence of the *tzaddik* (the *Yesod* of the world, which is above *Malchus*) is specifically through the *pnimiyus* of the Torah, and through this, they become above the limitations of time.

That is to say: through the *pnimiyus* of the Torah ("He hid it in the Torah"), the matter of *tzaddikim* is achieved, and through this, they reach the revelation of the light of the time to come.

**6.** This matter—that even now one can reach the revelation of the light of the time to come—must also be hinted at in the *nigleh* of the Torah:

There is a principle[18](#_ftn278) that "anything that is destined to be cut is considered as if it were already cut," provided that it does not require further preparation. That is to say, if there is no essential matter lacking *in the thing itself*, it is considered as if it were already done, and a lack of time is not considered a lack of action[19](#_ftn279).

And it is hinted at more explicitly (in this case)—in the words of the Gemara[20](#_ftn280): "Three were given a taste of the world to come in this world: Avraham, Yitzchak, and Yaakov." And according to what is written in *Tanna D'bei Eliyahu*[21](#_ftn281) that "every single Jew is obligated to say, 'When will my deeds reach the deeds of my forefathers, Avraham, Yitzchak, and Yaakov?'" it is understood that every Jew can reach a taste of the world to come in this world.

And even if one were to say that *Tanna D'bei Eliyahu* is not a book of *psak din*, one can bring proof from the words of the Gemara in *Maseches Berachos*[22](#_ftn282) in the text of the blessing for R. Ami:

#### 57

"May you see your world in your lifetime," which means that there is a *psak* in the *Shas Bavli* that there exists a standing and state where "your world," which refers to the revelations of the time to come, "you shall see in your lifetime."

**7.** The takeaway from the words of the Rebbe, my father-in-law, in the letter from the day after Yom Kippur regarding "*completion and additional light that is good on the upcoming Shabbos Bereishis*":

If there are matters that were not done during the *mo'adim* of the month of Tishrei, one can complete them on Shabbos Bereishis; and even if all the matters of the *mo'adim* of Tishrei were done as they should be, one should not think that one can rest and wait to receive a reward, but rather one must add even more.

And in greater detail:

Even after all the *avodah* of the *mo'adim* of the month of Tishrei has been performed,

—whether the *avodah* of Rosh Hashanah in the matter of *kabbalas ol*, the *avodah* of Yom Kippur in the matter of *teshuvah*, the *avodah* of the four days between Yom Kippur and Sukkos when "all of Israel are occupied with *mitzvos*, this one is occupied with his *sukkah* and this one with his *lulav*" [which is why the festival of Sukkos is called "the first day"[23](#_ftn283), "the first for the reckoning of sins"][24](#_ftn284), or the *avodah* of Sukkos, "the time of our joy," Shemini Atzeres and Simchas Torah, of which it is said[25](#_ftn285) "they shall be for you alone, and no strangers with you"[26](#_ftn286)]—

one must add even more, an "addition of light," and "light that is good"—which is the light that was created *on the first day*, when "Hashem was unique in His world," which this light (that was created on the first day) He hid for the *tzaddikim* *in the time to come*, and this sublime light—the Rebbe writes—can be drawn down on the upcoming Shabbos Bereishis.

***

**8.** The general *avodah* during the *mo'adim* of the month of Tishrei, leading up to the completion and additional light that is good on Shabbos Bereishis, can be explained through a physical parable of a train journey:

When a person wants to reach his destination quickly, he travels by train.

In general, there are two types of trains: there is an express train that does not stop along its route but travels directly to the designated place, and there is a regular train

#### 58

—which is used most of the time—that does not travel directly to the designated place, but stops along its route at various stations in order to pick up more passengers who did not board at the first station, and also for those passengers who cannot endure the fast journey.

Also, among the stations during the journey, there are two types: there are small stations where they stop for only a short time, and there are large stations where they stop for a longer time, in order to load onto the train large and heavy cargo, and also animals (oxen, sheep, goats, donkeys, and horses). The loading of the animals onto the train requires a long time, because the animals are afraid to board the train; they are afraid of the train itself, of the whistle, of the journey, etc. [And their fear is not a false fear, because when they arrive at the designated place, they will become blood and flesh of his (the person’s) flesh, and they will be nullified from their animalistic nature ("they will become no longer animals"...)], and therefore, at the small stations, there is no time to deal with them, only at the large stations, where they take care to load everything onto the train.

And the order of the journey—before the train begins to move, they sound a whistle to remind the passengers who are waiting—those who are busy with their luggage, or those who forgot entirely that they need to travel—that the train is about to leave. And they do not settle for one whistle, but they whistle again and again, and when the whistles do not help, the train begins to move slightly, to show that they are serious... and only afterward does the train begin to travel at speed.

And according to the principle that everything that exists in the physical world exists because this matter exists in the spiritual realm, and the matter in the spiritual realm is the root of the matter in the physical world—one must explain the root of the matter in the spiritual realm in this case as well.

**9.** And the matter in this:

The advantage of the *speed of the journey* of a train hints at the purpose of the creation of man and the descent of his soul below, that through his *avodah* below, he becomes in the category of a "*walker*"—as is known[27](#_ftn287) that the angels are called "*standers*," for even though they stand in love and fear for two thousand years, and another two thousand years, and another close to two thousand years, and rise from level to level, nevertheless, they are called by the name "standers," because their ascents are *in an order and gradation*. And similarly, the souls before their descent below are called "*standers*,"

#### 59

as it is written[28](#_ftn288), "As Hashem lives... before whom I *stood*." And specifically through the descent of the souls below and their enclothement in a body, at which time their *avodah* must be with the exertion of the soul and the exertion of the flesh—they become "*walkers*," because the ascent that comes through the body is *not in gradation at all*, as they leap ("they jump over") from the *Seder Hishtalshelus* to a level that is above the *Seder Hishtalshelus*, and even to being drawn into the body of the King[29](#_ftn289), reaching the *Atzmus* and *Mahus* of the *Ein Sof*, *baruch Hu*[30](#_ftn290).

And in this itself, there are two modes (similar to the two types of trains): there is the order of "*be'itah*" (in its time), and there is the order of "*achishenah*" (I will hasten it)[31](#_ftn291)—like the words of Yaakov to Esav, that even though he (Yaakov) is already prepared on his part to go to Mount Seir, nevertheless, because "the children are tender, and the flocks and the herds with young are with me, and if they should drive them hard one day, all the flock will die"[32](#_ftn292), therefore, "I will lead on gently"[33](#_ftn293)—that is, the journey to the *Geulah* ("and saviors shall ascend... to judge the mount of Esav"[34](#_ftn294)) must be in the order of "*be'itah*."

**10.** And similarly regarding the order of the journey, starting from the whistle before the journey, and the stations in the middle of the way, etc.—the matter of which is expressed in the *mashal* through the *mo'adim* of the month of Tishrei:

And by way of introduction, the words of the Rebbe, my father-in-law[35](#_ftn295): "The month of Tishrei is the head of all the months, and in it are days that are roots and sources for the entire year: Rosh Hashanah—the root and source for fear... Yom Kippur—for *teshuvah*, forgiveness, and pardon, the seven days of Sukkos—for love and joy, etc."

And in general, they are divided into two types: the *Yamim Nora'im*, in which the *avodah* is done with weeping and bitterness, and the days of joy ("the time of our joy"), in which the *avodah* is done with joy and dancing—as the Rebbe, my father-in-law, explains[36](#_ftn296) that those matters that are accomplished on Rosh Hashanah in the line of bitterness are accomplished on Shemini Atzeres and Simchas Torah in the line of joy.

#### 60

And the *mashal* for this—like the train that has several types of carriages (chariots) according to the types of passengers, so too there are several types of *avodah*, in a manner of weeping and bitterness, or in a manner of joy and dancing.

**11.** And in greater detail:

First and foremost, there is the preliminary *avodah* of the month of Elul, in which it is customary to blow the *shofar* to awaken Israel to do *teshuvah*, as it is said[37](#_ftn297), "Shall a *shofar* be blown in a city, and the people not tremble?" (rhetorically). Truly, one should be "all his days in *teshuvah*"[38](#_ftn298), but in the month of Elul, the awakening for *teshuvah* takes place. And the length of time given for *teshuvah* is forty days (from Rosh Chodesh Elul until Yom Kippur)—similar to what we find with the people of Nineveh[39](#_ftn299), that they were given forty days; if they repent, good, and if not, etc. (as the verses continue).

And similarly, they give in detail the twelve days from Chai Elul until Rosh Hashanah, corresponding to the twelve months of the year, a day for a month, a day for a month, that in these days one can rectify and complete all twelve months of the year[40](#_ftn300).

**12.** After the month of Elul comes Rosh Hashanah, in which one adds to the awakening for *teshuvah* through the blowing of the *shofar*[41](#_ftn301).

And among the differences between them—that in the month of Elul, they blow ten sounds, which can be said to correspond to the ten *kochos* of the soul, whose awakening is done through the ten sounds, and on Rosh Hashanah, they blow one hundred sounds[42](#_ftn302), corresponding to the ten *kochos* included in each one of the ten *kochos* of the soul, because one must awaken all the details within the *kochos* of the soul, ten *kochos* where each one is included of ten.

And the reason for this—because on Rosh Hashanah, "one must be precise and detail things well" (as we find regarding the precision in the punctuation of the word "L'chaim" and the like)[43](#_ftn303), and therefore it is not enough to blow ten sounds, so that there should be no room for error that the rectification is only regarding the ten *kochos* as they are in general, or only regarding the ten specific *kochos* that are included in one of the ten *kochos* (and to leave the nine *kochos*), but one must detail and blow one hundred sounds, corresponding to all ten *kochos* as each one is included of ten.

#### 61

And similarly regarding the ten types of *Bnei Yisrael*, as it is written[44](#_ftn304), "You are standing today (this is Rosh Hashanah[45](#_ftn305)) all of you... your heads, your tribes, etc., from the hewer of your wood to the drawer of your water," "the verse details ten levels"[46](#_ftn306), and each level is included of all ten levels—so that there should be no room for error that one can take ten from only one level, ten from "your heads," and leave the rest of the levels until the "hewer of wood" and "drawer of water," therefore they blow one hundred sounds, corresponding to all ten levels as each one is included of ten, all the details of the levels that are in *Bnei Yisrael*.

**13.** After Rosh Hashanah comes Yom Kippur, in which the *makif* (encompassing light) of "*teshuvah*, forgiveness, and pardon" is drawn down (as the Rebbe, my father-in-law, says[35]).

And one must explain the matter of drawing down the *makif* of forgiveness and pardon—for seemingly, the drawing down of the *makif* of forgiveness and pardon is not similar to the drawing down of the other *makifim*, the *makif* of *teshuvah*, the *makif* of fear, and the *makif* of love and joy, which all depend on the *avodah* of man, whereas the matter of forgiveness and pardon does not depend on man, but comes from above?

And the explanation for this is that the truth is that even the matter of forgiveness and pardon belongs to the *avodah* of man, because when the *avodah* of *teshuvah* is as it should be, then one becomes the "master of the house" over the forgiveness and pardon, that he does not need to *ask* Hashem for forgiveness and pardon, but can *demand* from Hashem forgiveness and pardon.

Similar to the saying[47](#_ftn307), "We have done what You have decreed upon us; do You what is incumbent upon You to do" (which the *Kohanim* also customarily say after the *Duchan*), as the Rebbe, my father-in-law, brings in the *maamar* of Chai Elul[48](#_ftn308).

**14.** After Yom Kippur come the four days between Yom Kippur and Sukkos, in which the *avodah* of *teshuvah* is also drawn down, as the Rebbe, my father-in-law, related[49](#_ftn309) that he once entered on *Motzaei* Yom Kippur to his father, the Rebbe (Rashab), and asked him: "And what now?" And he replied: "Now one must specifically do *teshuvah* ('Now one must first do *teshuvah*')."

#### 62

**15.** And after all the details of the matters of the *avodah* of *teshuvah* come the days of joy, "the time of our joy," the seven days of Sukkos, Shemini Atzeres and Simchas Torah, in which the *avodah* is in the matter of *joy*.

And the matter in this—like the *mashal* of the train that has different types of carriages according to the types of passengers (as mentioned above in section 6), and for those passengers who did not board the carriages on which is written "weeping and bitterness" (because they belong more to the line of joy, and love to dance), they attach and connect another carriage on which is written "joy and dancing," and if they dance for the sake of Heaven, they too will be able to board the train that is traveling to greet *Mashiach*.

**16.** And after all this, there must be "completion and addition... on Shabbos Bereishis":

And by way of introduction to what was explained above (section 7) that the purpose of the creation of man and the descent of his soul below (his destination in the train journey) is to reach the *Atzmus* and *Mahus* of the *Ein Sof*, *baruch Hu*.

And for this, the "revelations" in the *mo'adim* of the month of Tishrei are not enough; rather, there is also a need for the drawing down of "and Yaakov went on his way"[50](#_ftn310), for the *avodah* of the entire year, through which specifically one accomplishes the drawing down of the *Atzmus*.

However, due to the *intensity of the revelations* of the *mo'adim* of the month of Tishrei, both in the "Yamim Nora'im" and in the "time of our joy," it is possible that one will be occupied and caught up ("seized") in the "revelations," to such an extent that when one needs to go out to the *avodah* of the entire year, through which specifically one accomplishes the drawing down of the *Atzmus*—the engagement in this will not be as it should be.

And the *mashal* for this[51](#_ftn311)—from a person who enters the King’s palace in order to see the King, and immediately upon entering the outer chamber, he is so impressed that he forgets...—truly, it is not appropriate to say that he "forgets" the King, *chas v'shalom*, but rather that he does not reach the King, because he forgets that he needs to go further, due to the true goodness of the place where he is now. And in this itself, there are several levels: there are those whose impression is immediately upon their entry into the outer chamber and already there they stop from going further, and there are those who stop from going only when they enter the inner chamber, and there is one who continues to walk through all the rooms of the palace until he reaches the King’s room, but, due to the looking at the "revelations" of the King, he does not reach the King himself.

#### 63

And since this is so, there is a need to awaken those who are occupied and situated in the "revelations" of the *mo'adim* of the month of Tishrei—similar to what the Rebbe, my father-in-law, explains in the *maamar* of Rosh Hashanah[52](#_ftn312) that since the souls in *Gan Eden* are occupied *with the revelations* in *Gan Eden*, one must awaken them in the "middle of the night" that now "*Kudsha Brich Hu* comes to play with the *tzaddikim* in the Garden of Eden"[53](#_ftn313).

And this is the content of the matter of "completion and addition... on Shabbos Bereishis"—that those who did not fulfill completely ("they did not finish doing") the *avodah* of the month of Tishrei due to their engagement in the revelations (or due to another reason), can complete this on Shabbos Bereishis.

**17.** And from this it is understood that on Shabbos Bereishis there is an additional advantage over the *mo'adim* of the month of Tishrei:

Shabbos Bereishis is indeed the "leftovers" of the *mo'adim* of the month of Tishrei,

—which is why we see also in the physical (because so it is also in the spiritual) that when the mistress of the house prepares drinks and snacks for the *Yom Tov*, she does so with the calculation that it is possible to prepare more than what is needed, and what remains from the *Yom Tov* ("leftovers") will be for the "Kiddush" of Shabbos Bereishis—

And "leftovers"—as the simple meaning of the name—is less than half of the main thing,

But, we find that the effect of the "leftovers" can be greater than the "main thing"—as Elisha said to the wife of Ovadiah, "Go, sell the oil, and pay your debt, and you and your sons shall live on the *remainder*"[54](#_ftn314), and Chazal interpreted[55](#_ftn315), "And you and your sons shall live on the remainder *until the dead will live*." And it is found that the "main thing" sufficed only for the payment to the creditors, whereas the "remainder" sufficed not only for a year, two, or three, but "until the dead will live," that the resurrection of the dead will be after the coming of *Mashiach*, after the building of the Third *Beis Hamikdash*, and after the ingathering of all the exiles[56](#_ftn316), and until then—"you shall live on the *remainder*!"

And from this it is understood also regarding Shabbos Bereishis—that despite it being the "leftovers" of the *mo'adim* of the month of Tishrei, its effect can be greater than the effect of the *mo'adim* of the month of Tishrei.

#### 64

**18.** Shabbos Bereishis is not a Shabbos like all other Shabbosos, or even like any *Shabbos Mevarchim*, but an entirely different matter—a general matter, as the Rebbe, my father-in-law, explains in the *sicha* of Erev Sukkos[57](#_ftn317) that the light and vitality that shines on Shabbos Bereishis is drawn down for the entire year.

Similarly, there is a saying from the Tzemach Tzedek: "As one conducts oneself on Shabbos Bereishis, so goes the entire year"[58](#_ftn318).

And although seemingly one must ask[59](#_ftn319) that such a matter belongs to Rosh Hashanah and Yom Kippur, Hoshana Rabbah until Shemini Atzeres, and not to Shabbos Bereishis, as it is in the *Zohar*[60](#_ftn320) that on Hoshana Rabbah and Shemini Atzeres they give the "notes," which is the conclusion and end of all matters—Eliyahu HaNavi will answer this question, as the Tzemach Tzedek said[61](#_ftn321) (regarding the coming of Eliyahu HaNavi on Erev Shabbos Kodesh), that he will come already, and when he comes, he will answer this question as well.

***

**19.** In the aforementioned letter (from the day after Yom Kippur), the Rebbe, my father-in-law, continues regarding the *avodah* required from everyone, and he states:

"Even the weak shall say, 'I am a hero'[62](#_ftn322), because every single one who walks in the paved path, he is a hero through the strengthening of the light of the merit of our holy forefathers and teachers."

That is to say: even though he is "weak," and the Rebbe himself says about him that he is weak, nevertheless, by walking in the paved path that our holy forefathers and teachers paved, he can say "I am a hero," due to the strengthening of the light of the merit of our holy forefathers and teachers.

And although it is speaking about the "strengthening of *light*," and the definition of light is that the further it is drawn, the more it diminishes (as the Rebbe, my father-in-law, explains in the *Hemshech*[63](#_ftn323)), nevertheless, "even the weak shall say, 'I am a hero,'" because, it is true that the light diminishes, and it is true that he is weak, that is only on his own part, but on the part of the light of the *merit of our holy forefathers and teachers*, he is a hero.

***

#### 65

**20.** Continuing from what was mentioned above (section 8) regarding the types of stations, small and large—behold, among the large stations where one can load onto the train everyone with all their matters, is also included *Yud-Tes Kislev*:

Yud-Tes Kislev—the Rebbe says—is the "Rosh Hashanah for Chassidus"[64](#_ftn324), and he adds: "For a good year in the study of Chassidus and the ways of Chassidus, may you be written and sealed"[65](#_ftn325).

And from this it is understood that on Yud-Tes Kislev one can rectify and complete all the matters that one lacked until then.

And therefore, *every Chossid* must strive and occupy himself with this and be confident that toward Yud-Tes Kislev he will receive—he and his wife and his household and all his matters—a good writing and sealing for a good and sweet year, and he will utilize this in the study of Chassidus and the ways of Chassidus, as is known the saying that one must make spirituality out of physicality[66](#_ftn326).

And according to the words of our Rebbe HaZaken that the Torah of Chassidus is not a matter of a party, but for all of Israel[67](#_ftn327)—*every single Jew* must occupy himself with this and be confident that toward Yud-Tes Kislev he will receive—he and all his household and all his matters—a good writing and sealing for a good and sweet year, and make spirituality out of this.

**21.** And since a few weeks remain until Yud-Tes Kislev, at which time they gather and take everyone, and at which time they give everyone a good writing and sealing—I hereby propose,

—both to those who are here and to those who are not here now, and in particular to all those to whom the aforementioned letter from the day after Yom Kippur is addressed: "Our friends, *Anash* and the *Temimim*, may they live," and who would not want to be included at least in the category of "our friends, may they live"—

*that until Yud-Tes Kislev, everyone should strive to act upon at least a minyan of Jews, in the matters of thought, speech, and action—upon each one of the minyan in all three matters, or at least in two or in one of the three matters*:

In action—in what pertains to the fulfillment of practical *mitzvos*; in speech—in matters

#### 66

that depend on speech, and the study of Torah is equivalent to them all[68](#_ftn328), to act upon his minyan to set times for Torah; and in thought—in matters that depend on thought, and among them, to act upon his minyan in one matter of the *avodah* of the heart, which is *tefillah*[69](#_ftn329).

And to add, that in the minyan there can be even children—when they have reached the age of education, as the Rosh writes[70](#_ftn330) that even children are included in the ten upon whom the *Shechinah* rests[71](#_ftn331).

*And when Yud-Tes Kislev comes*, the Rosh Hashanah for Chassidus, in which the matter of "You are standing today (this is Rosh Hashanah) all of you" in the Chassidic sense takes place—*everyone should picture for himself the face of the Rebbe, and say: Behold the minyan that I have gathered—all of you as one man, "when the heads of the people were gathered, together with the tribes of Israel"*[72](#_ftn332). Upon so-and-so I acted in action, upon so-and-so I acted in speech, and upon so-and-so I acted in thought, etc.

And when there is the matter of "when they were gathered... together," the matter of "and He was King in Yeshurun"[72](#_ftn332) is accomplished, which is a preparation *in immediacy and proximity* to the fulfillment of the prophecy[73](#_ftn333), "And Hashem shall be King over all the earth," in the true and complete *Geulah* speedily in our days, *amen*.

**22.** *And it is very proper* that toward *Yud-Tes Kislev*, everyone should send *here* the *names of the minyan that he gathered, their name and their mother’

## Sicha of Shabbos Parshas Lech Lecha, 10 Mar-Cheshvan 5711

#### 67

**A.** The Rebbe Rayatz related in one of his sichos:

The Alter Rebbe said that "one must live with the times." After the Chassidim labored intensely to understand the meaning of this statement, the interpretation was revealed by the Maharil, the brother of the Alter Rebbe, that it means "to live with the parsha of the week."

The week of Parshas Bereishis is generally a joyous week, even though the end of the parsha is not so pleasant. The week of Parshas Noach is a gray and sad week, because we learn about the Flood, the Generation of the Dispersion, and the like. In contrast, the week of Parshas Lech Lecha is the week of true joy, because every day of the week we live with Avraham Avinu, the first Jew who opened the channel of mesiras nefesh and bequeathed it as an inheritance to all Bnei Yisrael for all generations.

[It should be noted that the power of mesiras nefesh that Avraham Avinu bequeathed as an inheritance also applies to converts, since they too are connected to Avraham Avinu and are called children of Avraham. As the Rambam writes in his well-known responsum (based on the words of the Yerushalmi), even converts can say "our forefathers," since Avraham Avinu is the father of all converts. Therefore, they too are required to fulfill the Torah and mitzvos with full strength, which is connected with mesiras nefesh.]

This is the content of the sicha regarding our subject.

**B.** Based on this, it can be said that the week following Parshas Lech Lecha is certainly a joyous week, because it discusses the status and condition of Avraham Avinu *after the bris milah*, through which he attained an *incomparable elevation*:

#### 68

Even before the milah, and even before the command "Go for yourself from your land, etc."—Avraham Avinu was at an *elevated level*. In the words of the Rebbe Rayatz in the sicha of Simchas Torah 5710, Avraham Avinu was then a seventy-five-year-old Jew, a landowner, a master over all his conduct, and he had reached all the levels he could possibly reach through his own power, up to the level of the "intellect hidden from all thought."

And then he was given the command "Go for yourself from your land, etc."—to ascend to an even higher level. And after that, he was commanded regarding the milah—from which we understand the greatness and wonder of the level he reached through the milah.

The concept here is:

All the matters and levels that Avraham Avinu had before the milah were achieved through his own *avodah*, as they were matters and levels that have a connection to *created beings*. This is not the case with milah, through which are drawn down the most sublime lights *that are completely above creation and the Seder Hishtalshelus*, sublime lights that cannot be drawn down through the avodah of man. They come *from above* as a gift, as it is written, "And Hashem your G-d will circumcise your heart," and man's action in the matter of milah is merely the removal of the screen and the obstacle, the removal of the orlah that comes from the kelipos, etc. This is the preparation through which the sublime lights that come from above will be drawn down *automatically*.

[An example of this is in the daily shiur in Tanya—the revelation of the hidden mysteries of Chochma (sparks and sublime lights) that were held captive in the exile within the kelipos, through the prior action of the lower beings who are clothed in a body from kelipas nogah, to weaken its power by breaking the desires. Therefore, the sublime ones come to hear chiddushei Torah from the lower ones.]

And it should be added that the elevation achieved through the milah is completely incomparable—

#### 69

—like the matter of *birth*, where the newborn child is a new existence, connected with the revelation of the power of the Ein Sof below (as explained in Chassidus).

From this, we understand the greatness of the joy of the week following Parshas Lech Lecha, in which we live with Avraham Avinu after the elevation he received through the mitzvah of milah was added to him.

And this joy continues in the weeks that follow, throughout the entire year, similar to the way the joy of Simchas Torah is drawn down for the entire year, as per the words of the Rebbe Rayatz that on Simchas Torah, the general sublime makif is drawn down, which includes all the makifim of the entire year.

**C.** As a preparation for the matter of milah (the revelation and drawing down of the sublime lights whose revelation is the matter of birth)—Avraham Avinu was told "Go for yourself from your land, etc.":

In order to reach these sublime lights, one must first depart from his limitations, even from the limitations of holiness.

The departure from the definitions and limitations of the nefesh habehamis is achieved through conduct according to the Shulchan Aruch and the study of mussar seforim, through which one will understand that physicality has no value at all, and consequently, he will depart from the limitations of the nefesh habehamis, and certainly from the limitations of the body. But the departure from the limitations of holiness—this is an entirely different matter.

**D.** And more specifically:

Regarding the study of Torah—one might argue: It is enough to be a "supporter of Torah," it is enough to study one chapter in the morning and one chapter in the evening, it is enough to attend the shiur after davening, it is enough to study without the exertion of the soul and the exertion of the body, it is enough to study the nigleh of Torah, and what is he missing by not studying Chassidus?!

Regarding avodah (tefillah)—it is enough (he argues) to come to the beis medrash in the middle of davening, and according to the Shulchan Aruch, one can skip most of the pesukei dezimra—to skip three-quarters of the davening—the main thing is that he davens with the tzibbur. To "grind" the words of davening quickly without understanding the words—that is also enough. Understanding the words, even without the hisbonenus of before Whom you are standing—that is more than enough. Having a serious demeanor before davening—he fulfills his obligation by folding his hands

#### 70

with his fingers as a servant before his master, and consequently, he can let his thoughts wander...

Regarding tzedakah—he argues that according to the Shulchan Aruch there are measures for giving tzedakah, there is a measure from the Torah and a measure from the Rabbis, and there is no obligation to give more than the measure. And more than a fifth—(not only is there no obligation to give, but furthermore) it is forbidden to give, as the saying goes, "He who squanders should not squander more than a fifth."

And in general—he argues—one does not need to be stringent with himself more than the command of the Torah. In the words of the Yerushalmi, "It is enough for you what the Torah has forbidden you." And does one need to be more G-d-fearing than the Yerushalmi?!... And he also argues that one should not demand of him matters that are beyond the letter of the law; if only he would conduct himself according to the law, according to the Shulchan Aruch.

These arguments—they are from the side of the limitations of the intellect, including even the intellect of holiness.

**E.** The Rebbe Rayatz once said that in America there exists a disease called: "It is permitted."

And the opposite of this—the Rebbe Rayatz related several times that there is a saying of the Chassidim: "What is forbidden—is forbidden, and what is permitted—is not necessary."

And similar to what is said that "an am ha'aretz is forbidden to eat meat"—that this does not mean a literal prohibition, for a literal forbidden thing is forbidden and bound by the chitzonim, and it is forbidden to make a bracha over it, whereas meat for an am ha'aretz is not forbidden and bound by the chitzonim, and the am ha'aretz who eats meat is obligated to make a bracha before and after it. Rather, this is similar to the aforementioned saying: "What is permitted—is not necessary."

**F.** The explanation for this:

It is explained in Chassidus that the essence of eating is (not for the sake of the person, that he should receive

#### 71

from the food, for the person is at a higher level than the food, but) for the sake of the food, so that the person will clarify and elevate the food, and therefore the food wants and waits for the person to eat it.

—The Rebbe Rayatz related about his father, the Rebbe Rashab, that once the food slipped from the fork into the plate, and he smiled and said: It (the food) does not want to yet. —

And all this (that the food wants the person to eat it)—is when the person's eating is not because of his own desire (the desire of the person), but because of the desire of the food, meaning, that his eating is for the sake of elevating the food. This is not the case when his eating is because of his own desire, meaning, that his eating is for his own sake, that he wants to receive from the food—then not only does he not elevate the food, but on the contrary, the food lowers him. And since the food lowers the person, this causes a descent also in the food itself, because through it the person stumbles.

And similarly, it is explained in a sicha of the Rebbe Rayatz that when one walks in the street, one must contemplate words of Torah [each according to his level—Chassidus, Gemara, Mishnayos, Ein Yaakov, and at the very least a verse of Chumash or Tehillim], and if not, the stone says to him: Golem, why are you stepping on me?!... For, although the person is higher than the stone, a being of speech is higher than the inanimate, yet, the virtue of the being of speech is that he has an intellectual soul and his conduct is according to intellect, but when a spirit of folly has entered him—that he does not fulfill his role—which is why they call him a "golem," then the stone says to him: Golem, why are you stepping on me?!

**G.** However, after all the aforementioned explanations—from the perspective of human intellect, even the intellect of a Jew, the question is ultimately asked:

Granted, what is forbidden according to the Torah is forbidden, but what is permitted according to the Torah, since according to the Shulchan Aruch the matter is permitted, why tell him that what is permitted is not necessary?!

The answer to this—that one should not enter into arguments and counter-arguments according to intellect, for then there are various questions, a question from the Bavli, a question from the Yerushalmi, and the like. Rather, there is a need for *kabbalas ol and mesiras nefesh* specifically. At the beginning of the avodah, this is kabbalas ol, and at an elevated level, this is mesiras nefesh. And as it is explained in Chassidus that mesiras nefesh

#### 72

means the surrender of the will (for nefesh means will), including also the surrender of the will of holiness (which is the true will of a Jew, as per the ruling of the Rambam), that is, to depart from all limitations, even the limitations of holiness.

And with greater emphasis during the time of exile (after "because of our sins we were exiled from our land")—for then avodah according to logic and reason is not enough, but there is a need for the matter of mesiras nefesh, and with this power one "passes through" the exile [and what is written in Tanya in explanation of the reason that "Moshe Rabbeinu commanded... *for the generation that entered the land* to recite Shema twice every day to accept upon himself the Kingdom of Heaven *with mesiras nefesh*"—this is mesiras nefesh *in potential* only, and not in actuality, whereas in the time of exile there is a need for mesiras nefesh *in actuality*]. And one of the proofs for this—that in the time of exile specifically, the matter of mesiras nefesh is found and revealed.

From this, it is understood regarding Avraham Avinu—that when the matter of exile began for him, Hashem said to him: "Go for yourself," to depart from his limitations, and with this power he would be able to go "to the land," to go out into the world, knowing that although "traveling diminishes three things," nevertheless, not only would nothing be weakened in him, but on the contrary: "And I will make your name great," which refers to the Name of Havayah, His essential Name (as explained in Chassidus), until he reaches the level of milah, the revelation of the sublime lights, whose revelation is a matter of birth (as mentioned above in section B).

***

**H.** What was stated above regarding milah (after the preparation of "Go for yourself") through which sublime lights are drawn down whose revelation is a matter of birth—is especially relevant to this day, the tenth of Cheshvan, which marks nine months from the day of the histalkus of the Rebbe Rayatz:

The meaning of "histalkus"—as the Rebbe Rayatz explains

#### 73

in the maamar of the day of the histalkus—is a matter of elevation, from which it is understood that through the histalkus, most sublime lights are drawn down, which are in a manner of elevation, and for this reason their drawing down is called by the name histalkus ("astalk").

And since they are most sublime lights, their revelation (through the histalkus) is similar to the matter of *birth*.

And this matter is emphasized most strongly at the completion of nine months from the day of the histalkus—since the time of birth is after *nine months*, nine months of pregnancy.

**I.** And more specifically:

In pregnancy and birth there are three times: seven months, nine months, and twelve months (according to Rabbah Tosefa'ah. And although in Tosafos it is stated that we do not rule according to Rabbah Tosefa'ah, the Rema rules as halacha that the time of pregnancy can also be twelve months).

The concept here:

The general matter of pregnancy is to clarify and divide between the matters belonging to the head, the body, and the foot, for in the drop, the entire body (from the head to the nails on the foot) is included together (as explained in Tanya), and through the pregnancy, the clarification and division is made so that what belongs to the head will be in the head, what belongs to the body will be in the body, and what belongs to the foot will be in the foot.

From this, it is understood that the longer the time of pregnancy, the more clarification and refinement of the body is achieved. Therefore: the body of Moshe, which was in pregnancy for seven months—requires burial, and the body of Eliyahu, which was in pregnancy for twelve months—does not require burial, since his body was refined to the utmost until he could ascend in a whirlwind to heaven.

However, the time of pregnancy in a balanced manner is nine months: those whose primary avodah is in the clarification of the body—require a pregnancy of twelve months. Those whose primary avodah is in their soul (and the light of the soul will already illuminate the body as well)—a pregnancy of

#### 74

seven months is sufficient for them. And those for whom there must be both the avodah in the body and the avodah in the soul—the way of the beinonim, which belongs to everyone, as the Alter Rebbe said that "the measure of the beinoni is the measure of every person and after it every person shall draw"—the time of pregnancy is nine months.

**J.** Regarding the time of nine months itself, there are two opinions:

1) Nine *full* months—271 days (nine months of thirty days and on the first day of the tenth she gives birth), or 272 days (if the seed did not take the first day, it takes in two days), or 273 days (if it did not take in two, it takes in three, since the taking of the seed can be up to three days).

2) Nine months even *incomplete*—that if nine new moons have passed after the taking, it is considered nine months, and the birth can occur.

And regarding our subject—the calculation of nine months of birth from the day of the histalkus in which most sublime lights are drawn down which are called by the name birth:

According to the opinion that nine incomplete months are sufficient—the matter of birth occurs already from Rosh Chodesh. And according to the opinion that there must be nine full months, 271-273 days—the matter of birth will be on the fourth day after this Shabbos, and consequently, it also pertains to this Shabbos, which gives power for all the days of the week, including also the fourth day.

**K.** And here we see a wondrous thing—"a Baal Shem Tov-style matter"—regarding the shiurim in Tanya for the three days (271-272-273) in which nine months will be completed from the day of the histalkus:

The Rebbe Rayatz arranged the division of the Sefer Tanya to be studied throughout the year. One division for a simple year and one division for a leap year. And according to this division (both in a simple year and in a leap year), the explanation for Siman 27 in the Iggeres HaKodesh (in which the matter of the histalkus is discussed), is divided into three parts, to be studied over three days.

And the wonder of the matter—"a Baal Shem Tov-style matter"—is that according to this division, which was made seven years before the histalkus, it was determined that on the three days of the completion of nine months from the day of the histalkus (14-16 Cheshvan in a simple year) one would study in the Tanya shiurim the explanation for Siman 27, the source of the explanation for the matter of the histalkus!

#### 75

**L.** To explain further the precision of Iggeres HaKodesh Siman 27 and its explanation specifically—the only letter that the Alter Rebbe himself wrote an explanation for, and the sons of the Gaon the author also attached the explanation to the Sefer Tanya, in Iggeres HaKodesh Siman 27:

In the Iggeres HaKodesh in Tanya there are two letters in which the matter of the histalkus is discussed—Siman 27 (which also includes an explanation of the aforementioned), and Siman 28: Siman 28—a letter of consolation on the passing of the son of the great Tzaddik, the holy Rabbi, etc., R' Levi Yitzchak of Berditchev, and Siman 27—a letter of consolation on the passing of the great Tzaddik, the holy Rabbi, etc., R' Menachem Mendel of Horodok.

And among the differences between them: The son of the great Tzaddik, the holy Rabbi, etc., R' Levi Yitzchak of Berditchev was indeed a most elevated person, a tzaddik, a chassid, etc., but he was not a Nasi, for he did not conduct himself in leadership. Whereas the great Tzaddik, the holy Rabbi, etc., R' Menachem Mendel of Horodok was also a general person, a *Nasi* in Yisrael, and furthermore, he had a connection to the *leadership of Chabad Chassidus* in particular, for his leadership was in the region of Reisin, and to such an extent, that even the Alter Rebbe himself would travel for a time to R' Menachem Mendel of Horodok, and this journey was similar to the journey of a chassid to his Rebbe (as the Rebbe Rayatz related).

Based on this, it can be said by way of possibility the reason for the addition of the explanation to the letter of consolation on the passing of R' Menachem Mendel of Horodok:

By way of introduction—that regarding the general matter of the histalkus, regarding every Jew, it is stated in the Gemara that it is "like a Sefer Torah that was burned," and especially the histalkus of a tzaddik (which is like the "breaking of the Tablets"), and especially a tzaddik who is also a general person, a leader of thousands of Yisrael—then certainly his histalkus is a matter that is not understood at all, how such a thing is possible!

And therefore, in order to act so that there will be *consolation* for (the matter of the histalkus, and especially) the histalkus of a Nasi in Yisrael, and especially (as the Alter Rebbe wants) "to comfort them *doubly*," that through the histalkus there will be an addition in a manner of "doubly" [similar to the teaching of Chazal regarding the breaking of the Tablets, that through this there was an addition in the second Tablets in a manner of "doubly"]—which is a *most difficult* matter—the Alter Rebbe himself must add an *explanation* to the letter of consolation!

**M.** The concept here:

The Alter Rebbe saw that through our own power it would be difficult for us to understand the matter of the histalkus, and especially to reach the revelations that come through the histalkus, and therefore he wrote an "explanation" on the matter of the histalkus, through which he *opened the channel* so that others could also reach this—similar to what is explained that the mesiras nefesh of Avraham Avinu was the opening of the channel of mesiras nefesh for all Bnei Yisrael, and similarly it is explicit in the words of Chazal, "The entire world is sustained for the sake of Chanina my son," that "a path is a channel, that he opened a channel and a path of abundance."

And it can also be said, that through the opening of the channel for the understanding of the matter of the histalkus (through the "explanation" in Iggeres HaKodesh Siman 27)—a matter that is not understood at all—the channels are opened automatically for the understanding of every difficult matter in the Sefer Tanya, and consequently also for the understanding of every difficult matter in the Torah of Chassidus, as is the order in the explanation of a difficult matter, that when one resolves the greatest difficulty, the entire matter becomes easier. An example of this—from the raising of the walls of a house, that one must begin to raise the *bottom* beam specifically, and then automatically the ones above it will also be raised (as is brought in Chassidus).

**N.** The truth is that even after the "explanation"—for people of our level, I do not know if the matter has already been explained... and certainly not in a manner of "doubly."

But nevertheless, we can imagine what the situation would have been had the "explanation" not been in the world at all!

And this "explanation"—the understanding of the matter of the histalkus of a Nasi, how from this there can be a matter of birth in a manner of "doubly"—the Rebbe Rayatz determined (in the division of the Sefer Tanya *seven years* before his histalkus) that it should be studied on the three days (271-272-273) connected with the completion of nine months (the time of birth) from the day of his histalkus!

**O.** And the explanation of the matter of birth—in connection with the completion of nine months from the histalkus—in practical avodah:

#### 77

In the matter of birth there are two modes: the birth of a male (son), and the birth of a female (daughter).

By way of introduction—that although in the text of the blessing for the birth of a daughter we find in the seforim only the language "for the chuppah and for good deeds," nevertheless, the Rebbe Rashab writes in one of his letters (and it was given for copying by the Rebbe Rayatz): "I heard in the name of our holy forefathers... that also for a daughter there must be *for Torah* (and for the chuppah and for good deeds), based on what Chazal said, 'By what merit do women attain [the reward of the world to come]? By sending their children to learn Torah... and by waiting for their husbands...'" (and from this we learn many matters regarding the obligations of a woman—that she must strive to influence her husband to set times for Torah, and when the time comes, to strive that the children also learn Torah, so that she will have a share in their learning).

And the difference between them in avodah—that the birth of a male, "it is the way of a man to conquer," indicates the avodah of conquering and clarifying his portion in the world, an avodah that is connected and done according to intellect, and the birth of a female, "there is no woman who is worthy among women except a woman who does the will of her husband," indicates the avodah of kabbalas ol.

And Chazal said, "A daughter first is a good sign for sons... for she raises her brothers," meaning, that the daughter assists in the supervision and care of the sons. And its meaning in avodah—that the prioritization of kabbalas ol (a daughter first) constitutes supervision and care for the avodah of conquering and clarifying his portion in the world (raising her brothers) so that it will be as it should be.

From this, it is understood that after the completion of nine months from the histalkus there must be the matter of birth—a renewal in the avodah of conquering and clarifying the world through the prioritization of kabbalas ol.

**P.** And primarily—regarding the avodah of spreading the Torah of *Chassidus* outward, as hinted in the words of the Gemara regarding the pregnancy of nine full months (271-273 days): "He who says *like the early Chassidim*."

By way of introduction—that every matter, and especially a matter connected with Bnei Yisrael, Torah and mitzvos, is by Divine Providence and not by chance, and it stands out especially in a matter that seemingly, according to the customary order, should have been in a different manner.

#### 78
