And when "in My statutes you shall walk," "that you should be toiling in the Torah," *in the study of Chassidus*—then, as a matter of course, "I will give your rains in their time."

[And it is worth noting the inquiry regarding the general matter of the reward for mitzvos—if the reward is by way of a mystical quality (*segulah*), without a direct connection to the body of the mitzvos, or if Hashem so embedded in the creation that the performance of the mitzvos brings the reward naturally (just as it is the nature of fire to burn and the nature of water to extinguish), and similarly regarding "in My statutes you shall walk," that through this, "your rains in their time" will follow as a matter of course.]

And one must add regarding the precision of the language, "I will give your rains *in their time*," "in their time" specifically:

"Your rains" in general, physical influence—since Hashem is the essence of good, and it is the nature of the good to do good, He will certainly give physical influence ("your rains") even without this (without the study of Chassidus); but, in order that it should be "I will give your rains *in their time*," on the nights of Wednesday and the nights of Shabbos, when the rains do not interfere with other matters, and similarly regarding the general physical influence ("your rains") that Hashem bestows, that it should be in a manner *that will not interfere with Torah and service* ("in their time")—there must be the toil in Torah, the essence of which is *in the study of Chassidus*, and through this, the physical influence ("your rains") will follow *as a matter of course* in a way that will not interfere with Torah and service ("in their time").

***

**F.** Continuing from what was stated above that the teachings of Chassidus have become relevant to all of Israel, since on 19 Kislev the main matter of "may your springs be dispersed outward" began—one must add and refute another argument that can be raised (by Jews in general, and specifically) by those learned in Torah:

It is true—they argue—that the study of Chassidus belongs to all of Israel, but even so, since the study of Chassidus does not relate so much to practical conduct in thought, speech, and action (for which it was sufficient in the past, and is sufficient today, to study the Shulchan Aruch), and on the other hand, it is a study that requires a lot of time—

#### 118

it is better to dedicate the time to the study of the revealed Torah, in which one can "accomplish" (innovate insights) beyond all comparison.

And the answer to this—*Moshiach* clarified (in his words to the Baal Shem Tov regarding the study of his Torah, the teachings of Chassidus) with the precision of the language, "may *your springs* be dispersed outward," "your springs" specifically, as follows.

**G.** An explanation of the difference between a spring and a mikveh:

The waters of a mikveh are *separated from their source* [both in a mikveh of rainwater, where the waters of the mikveh are not as they were at their source in the clouds in the heavens, and all the more so in a mikveh made from ice or snow], whereas the waters of a spring are *connected to their source* (and waters of a spring that have been disconnected do not have the status of a spring).

And among the differences between them in law—(a) that a mikveh only purifies with forty seah, while a spring purifies with any amount (specifically in vessels, and according to many opinions also in a person), (b) a mikveh only purifies when gathered (*ashburin*), while a spring purifies even when flowing (*zochalin*) (and the initial thought of Tosafos is that it purifies specifically when flowing, although the conclusion is that it purifies also when flowing).

**H.** And an explanation of the matter in spirituality:

By way of introduction—that the general matter of the waters of a mikveh *that are separated from their source* does not seemingly apply in spirituality, regarding *Elokus*, since Hashem is the source of all matters, "in the heavens above and on the earth below there is nothing else," and it is not possible to be separated from Him, Heaven forbid.

However, even though the truth is that there is no possibility of separation from Elokus, nevertheless, in order that there could be the matter of choice (as it is written, "See, I have set before you today life... and you shall choose life"), Hashem gave a place *to err* that there are two authorities, which, this matter itself is by the power of the Ein Sof, as our Rebbe explains in Shaar

#### 119

HaYichud VeHaEmunah that "these are the mighty acts of Hashem, for He is all-powerful to contract the life-force and spirituality influenced from the breath of His mouth and to conceal it, etc.," until it appears as if it is separated from Elokus.

And according to this introduction, one must explain the content of the matter of the waters of a mikveh and the waters of a spring regarding immersion *in the Torah*, which is compared to water, "the waters of knowledge"—that even in the study of Torah, the matter of the waters of a mikveh that are separated from their source can apply, due to the deficiency in the feeling of the person studying, and therefore one must strive that the study of Torah should be in the manner of the waters of a spring that are connected to their source.

**I.** And an explanation of the matter:

It is stated in the Gemara, "What is the meaning of the verse, 'Who is the wise man who will understand this... For what was the land destroyed... Because they abandoned My Torah... because they did not recite the blessing of the Torah first?'" And the Ran explains that "certainly they were engaged in Torah constantly... (but) they did not recite the blessing of the Torah first, meaning that it was not so important in their eyes that it was worthy to recite a blessing over it, for they were not engaged in it for its own sake, and because of this they were negligent in its blessing."

And the matter in this—that the study of Torah must be in a manner that it is recognized that the Torah is the *Torah of Hashem*, which is why we precede it by reciting the blessing of the Torah, "Blessed are You, Hashem, Giver of the Torah," through which the connection with the Giver of the Torah is made. And not only that, but we are precise, "*Giver* of the Torah," in the present tense, like at the Giving of the Torah, to the point that the Sages said, "Just as there it was with awe and fear, and with trembling and shaking, so too here, etc." For even though at the Giving of the Torah the Jewish people were at a lofty level until they had a form of the prophecy of Moshe, whereas now, etc., nevertheless, even today there is the matter of the Giving of the Torah, "Giver of the Torah" in the present tense, and therefore the study of Torah must be with awe and fear, etc., like at the time of the Giving of the Torah.

Thus, it is found that the study of Torah with the preceding blessing of the Torah, Torah for its own sake,

#### 120

where the *connection with the Giver of the Torah* is felt—is like the waters of a *spring*, living waters *that are connected to their source*. And in the language of the Sages, "If he merits (to learn for its own sake), it becomes a potion of life for him," due to the connection with Hashem (the Giver of the Torah), the source of life, as it is written, "And you who cleave to Hashem your G-d are alive, etc." Whereas when one learns Torah and forgets about the Giver of the Torah, Torah not for its own sake, of which it is said, "If he does not merit, etc."—this is like the waters of a *mikveh*, water, but not living water that is connected to its source, since *for him* it is in a manner of separation, etc.

And in this matter, the difference between the revealed Torah and the inner dimension of the Torah that was revealed in the teachings of Chassidus is emphasized:

*In the revealed* Torah—the study can be in a manner where one forgets the Giver of the Torah, like the waters of a *mikveh* that are separated from their source; whereas in the study of the teachings of *Chassidus*—since the subject of the study is in matters of Elokus, knowledge of the order of the chain of descent, etc., there is *as a matter of course* the connection with Hashem, the Giver of the Torah, like the waters of a *spring* that are always connected to their source.

**J.** According to this, one must also explain the details of the laws of a mikveh and a spring (forty seah or any amount, gathered or flowing)—regarding the study of Torah:

A *mikveh* (revealed Torah) only purifies with forty seah, where his entire body is covered in them—that there is a need for the study of Torah in excessive abundance, "feed him like an ox," until he becomes *covered* in Torah, meaning, that his physical and material existence is nullified in the Torah ("he becomes so immersed in Torah until his physicality and materiality become nullified in it"), and if not for this, it can be in a manner that "it becomes a potion, etc."

But a *spring* (teachings of Chassidus) purifies with any amount—because, the effect of the teachings of Chassidus is even in the study of *one hour* [similar to the saying of the Sages, "There is one who acquires his world in one hour," "with one turn"], where there is in this *to nullify his entire existence* (including also his trivial matters, similar to what is written, "and he shall wash his flesh," "that which is trivial to his flesh") in the waters of the teachings of Chassidus (spring), as we see tangibly

#### 121

that through the study of Chassidus, all perspectives change, to the point that one is completely transformed from one extreme to the other.

And even according to the opinion that a spring purifies with any amount only for vessels, whereas the purification of a person is only in water where his entire body is covered, nevertheless, when the waters of the spring mix into the waters of the mikveh where his entire body is covered, they elevate the waters of the mikveh to be like the waters of a spring that purify *when flowing*:

Flowing (*zochalin*)—indicates the *vitality*, living water, for every living thing moves, whereas the lack of flowing (gathered) indicates the deficiency in the water that it is not living water [and therefore there is an opinion in Tosafos that a spring purifies specifically when flowing], and when one continues the spring into the mikveh, the waters of the mikveh also become *living water*.

And its matter in Torah—that the study of Chassidus (a spring, which is connected to its source) acts also in the study of the revealed (mikveh), that even in the study of the revealed there will be felt the connection with the Giver of the Torah, Torah for its own sake, "if he merits, it becomes a potion of life."

**K.** And this matter (the effect of the study of Chassidus on the study of the revealed, like the effect of the spring in the mikveh) is hinted at (like all matters) also in the revealed Torah:

On the verse, "And your faith shall be the strength of salvation, wisdom and knowledge, the fear of Hashem is His treasure," it is stated in the Gemara, "'Faith' is the order of Zeraim, 'your times' is the order of Moed, 'strength' is the order of Nashim, 'salvation' is the order of Nezikin, 'wisdom' is the order of Kodashim, and 'knowledge' is the order of Taharos"—all six orders of Mishnah, the *revealed* Torah. And the Gemara concludes: "And even so, 'the fear of Hashem is His treasure,'" and in the continuation of the matter: "If the fear of Hashem is His treasure, yes; if not, no. A parable of a man who said to his messenger, 'Bring me a kor of wheat to the attic.' He went and brought it up. He said to him, 'Did you mix into them a kav of salt, etc.' (salty earth that preserves the fruits from becoming wormy)—that the preservation of all six orders of Mishnah (revealed Torah) that their study should be as it should be (Torah for its own sake), is, "*the fear of Hashem is His treasure*," which is achieved through the study of the inner dimension of the Torah, and specifically *the teachings of Chassidus*, as the ruling of the Rambam, "What is the way to His love and fear? At the time that a person contemplates, etc.," contemplation of the greatness of Hashem, which is the content of the study of Chassidus.

That is to say: The effect of the study of Chassidus on the study of the revealed is like the effect of mixing a kav of salt into a kor of wheat, through which the wheat is preserved. And in the style

#### 122

of the above—like the mixing of the waters of a spring into the waters of a mikveh, through which the waters of the mikveh become living water.

And one must add, that the effect of the study of Chassidus on the study of the revealed must be in a manner that they become one reality—not only like a mixture of dry with dry (like a kav of salt in a kor of wheat), but also like a mixture of wet with wet (like the waters of a spring in the waters of a mikveh), that the mixture is in a manner that they become one thing (as is understood from the differences in the laws between a mixture of dry with dry and a mixture of wet with wet).

**L.** The conclusion from all that was stated above:

There is no room for the argument that it is a pity to waste time on the study of Chassidus when one can in this hour "accomplish" in the study of the revealed beyond all comparison—because the study of Chassidus is like a spring that purifies with any amount, so that through the study of Chassidus, one accomplishes much also regarding the study of the revealed, that it should be in a manner of Torah for its own sake, a "potion of life."

And not only that, but through the study of Chassidus, one gains desire, and through this also understanding and comprehension in the study of the revealed, that his brain and heart become a thousand times more refined also in the study of the revealed.

And as hinted in the saying of the Sages, "A person should always learn Torah in a place that his heart desires, as it is said, 'But in the Torah of Hashem is his desire'": In order to come to a standing and situation that his "*heart desires*" the Torah of Hashem, there must be in him *love of Hashem*—through the study of Chassidus (as brought above the ruling of the Rambam, "What is the way to His love, etc."), and when his heart desires the Torah, then he will succeed beyond all comparison *in the study and understanding* of the Torah.

***

**M.** In the precision of "your springs," a spring specifically that is connected to its source—the connection to the source of the teachings of Chassidus is also emphasized, the *leaders of Chassidus*, starting from the Baal Shem Tov and the Alter Rebbe, and we have no one but the leader of our generation, the Rebbe.

—There are those who engage in inquiry and debate, by way of *kal vachomer* and *gezeirah shavah*, etc., regarding the greatness of our Rebbes, who is greater than whom, etc. And the answer to this—first and foremost—is that this does not concern us, since we have no one but *the leader of our generation*.

#### 123

An example of this in the revealed Torah—the precedence of honoring one's father over honoring one's grandfather:

In honoring father and mother, the father precedes the mother because he and his mother are obligated in the honor of his father. And in honoring his father and his teacher, the teacher precedes the father because he and his father are obligated in the honor of his teacher. And seemingly, according to this, it should be so also regarding his father and his grandfather, that his grandfather precedes his father, since he and his father are obligated in the honor of his grandfather?

And the explanation in this:

The mitzvah of honoring one's father, even though its fulfillment must be from the command of Hashem and not from the reason, is a mitzvah that has a reason—because his father *brought him into the world*.

And therefore, "The lost object of his father and the lost object of his teacher, that of his teacher precedes, for his father brought him into this world, and his teacher who taught him wisdom brings him to the life of the World to Come"—for since the reason for honoring his father is because he brought him into the world, then his teacher who brings him to the life of the World to Come precedes his father who brought him only into this world.

But regarding his father and his father's father—it is understood simply that his father *who brought him into the world* precedes his father's father whose connection to him is only by way of a cause alone.

And an example of this in our case—that we have no one but the leader of our generation, whose connection to us is direct, like his father and his teacher who brings him, etc., whereas the connection to the Rebbes before him is by way of a cause, like his father's father, etc.

And furthermore, and essentially—that in truth there is no difference between the Rebbes:

Every Rebbe has his own special matter, and together with this, he is also "filling the place of his fathers," meaning, *that he fills the entire place* (all the details of the matters) of his fathers without any deficiency at all (for if there is a deficiency in one detail, he is not "filling the place" in relation to this detail).

—We find indeed in the Gemara that it is possible that "he does not fill the place of his fathers *in wisdom*" but rather "*in fear of sin*," but, this does not apply to our Rebbes, because every Rebbe is also a king (fear) and also a teacher (wisdom), like Moshiach, and consequently, he is "filling the place of his fathers" in all matters.

#### 124

And on the contrary: in addition to the fact that every Rebbe is "filling the place of his fathers" in all matters—there is added in him another matter that before this was not in revelation (and it is possible that before this it was not at all, but, for us it concerns only that before this it was not *in revelation*).

And therefore, we have no one but the leader of our generation, the Rebbe, for being "filling the place of his fathers" he includes all the Rebbes, and not only that, but through him there is added another matter that was not revealed until this generation of ours—close to the coming of Moshiach—"*may your springs be dispersed outward*" in a manner that there was nothing like it in all the generations before it!

And two reasons for the special addition in the dissemination of the springs outward in this generation: (a) because of the intensification of the darkness, there is a need for a very great light to illuminate the darkness, (b) because the light of Moshiach is already sparkling.

And from this is understood the greatness of the necessity for the connection and bond with *the spring*—the source of the teachings of Chassidus—the Rebbe, *the leader of our generation*, that through this power the dissemination is made also in the "outside," that is, that not only are they not affected by the "outside," but on the contrary, that the springs come in a manner of dissemination also in the "outside," since the spring has no limitations at all, and purifies even a *zav* and a *metzora*.

And furthermore, and this is the main thing, that this action (the dissemination of the springs outward) becomes the preparation for the coming of Moshiach our righteous one speedily in our days, amen.

**N.** And in this matter (the connection to the Rebbe) one must utilize the time until the "Yahrtzeit"—all twelve (and specifically eleven) months in which the soul is also below (as explained also in the revealed Torah)—that in this time one can "grab" *beyond all comparison* regarding the time after this.

And first and foremost—"grab" regarding the matter of *the connection*:

The Sages said, "The reward of a mitzvah is a mitzvah," meaning, that the greatest reward of a mitzvah is the mitzvah itself, *the bond and the connection* (mitzvah from the language of *tzavta*, connection) *with Hashem*, which, even though "there is no comparison to You... in this world, and there is none besides You... for the life of the World to Come, nothing besides You... for the days of Moshiach, and there is none like You... for the resurrection of the dead" [and as the Rebbe elaborates in the continuation of Rosh Hashanah

#### 125

in the explanation of these four matters], nevertheless, in His great kindness He descended on Mount Sinai and gave the Jewish people the mitzvos through which they would be in *tzavta* and connection with the Commander of the mitzvos—this is the most lofty reward.

And likewise in our case—that the most lofty matter that one can "grab" until the Yahrtzeit, is, *the connection to the Rebbe*, which is made through the study of his teachings and walking in his ways.

**O.** And accordingly—I hereby suggest several things that everyone should do until the Yahrtzeit:

Regarding the study of Mishnayos—everyone should take upon themselves to learn and complete until the Yahrtzeit five chapters of Mishnayos, for, Mishnah is the letters of *neshamah* (soul), and five chapters in Mishnah are corresponding to the five names that are called for the soul, *nefesh, ruach, neshamah, chayah, yechidah*.

—The first time I saw that they light five candles during the prayer on the Yahrtzeit (and likewise in the year of mourning), when I was with the Rebbe in Paris, I asked him the reason for the matter, and he did not answer, and after some time he said, that the five candles are corresponding to the five names that the soul is called by, *nefesh, ruach, neshamah, chayah, yechidah*.

And through the study of the five chapters of Mishnayos, there will be added in the strengthening of the connection with the Rebbe—not only *nefesh* with *nefesh* (which is made through the study of one chapter), and not only *ruach* with *ruach* (through two chapters), and not only *neshamah* with *neshamah* (through three chapters), and not only *chayah* with *chayah* (through four chapters), but also *yechidah*... (The Rebbe paused in tears and then finished) *with yechidah* (through five chapters),

And more than this—that through *yechidah*, even though it is only a *name* for the essence of the soul, nevertheless, since it is called "yechidah" because it is unified with the level of the *Yachid* (the Unique One), through it is made also the connection and the cleaving of *the essence with the essence*!

[After they divided the Mishnayos—the Rebbe said, that since

#### 126

they already divided the Mishnayos once, they should add and divide again tomorrow for those who have not yet participated in the division, and he concluded:]

And the main thing—that they should learn the Mishnayos, by heart or from the text, with many commentaries or few commentaries, etc., and finish until the Yahrtzeit, and that there should be no need to awaken and remind about this, for certainly everyone took this upon themselves out of affection (similar to the saying of the Sages regarding the mitzvah of circumcision—"a mitzvah that they accepted upon themselves with joy").

**P.** And another suggestion—regarding the study of his teachings:

One asked in a letter to the Rebbe how his connection to him would be since he does not know him face to face,

—The questioner did not see the Rebbe, and it seemed to him that the Rebbe also did not see him...—

And the Rebbe answered him that the connection is through the study of his teachings and keeping the regulations, etc.—The Rebbe did not tell him to connect to him through matters of miracles, or through traveling to him, but through the study of his teachings, etc.

And accordingly, I hereby suggest that towards the Yahrtzeit everyone should study the Maamar (all of it or part of it) that the Rebbe gave for the day of his passing, and from time to time, when one is in confusion, or has doubts, or in a situation where "this scoundrel has struck you"—he should repeat this Maamar in his thought.

—In the Sicha of 19 Kislev, the Rebbe told that in the year 5680, the year of separation, in which he parted from his father, the Rebbe, his father spoke much with him about the Maamar "VeHadarata Pnei Zaken" in Likutei Torah (end of Parshas Kedoshim). In this Maamar, he explains the greatness of the virtue that the words of Torah are engraved

#### 127

in his brain, that then, even at a time when he is not engaged in Torah, Hashem dwells within him (and therefore one must stand before a Torah scholar even at a time when he is not engaged in Torah, because the words of Torah are engraved in his brain).

And similarly in our matter: The review and proficiency in the Maamar—besides the benefit for the connection at the time of repeating the Maamar, even at other times his brain will be filled with the teachings of the Rebbe, for in these teachings the Rebbe gave himself ("the Rebbe gave himself") to the Chassidim, and consequently, he is *in constant connection* with the Rebbe, and in the language of Likutei Torah: "Without any interruption and separation forever, even for one moment."

And in this matter, the *quantity* does not concern so much, reviewing the entire Maamar, or (if for some reason he cannot review all of it) half the Maamar; the *quality* concerns—that they should be *engraved* in his brain, the letters of engraving, living water, flowing, waters of a spring, that are connected with the source, the essence of the soul...

**Q.** And a third suggestion—that every day until the Yahrtzeit everyone should add

## B’s”D. Sicha of Shabbos Parshas Vayeshev, Mevarchim Chodesh Teves, 5711

#### 139

*Unedited*

**A.** On this Shabbos, there are several matters:

First and foremost, it is Shabbos Mevarchim Teves. In this regard, its placement this year [1] (as in most years) falls between 19 Kislev and Chanukah.

Since from the day of Shabbos all the days are blessed [2], all the days of the coming week are included in the day of Shabbos, including Rosh Chodesh Teves, and consequently, the entire month of Teves. This is because Rosh Chodesh is not merely the beginning of the month, but the "head" of the entire month, which contains the vitality of all the days of the month, just as Rosh Hashanah contains the vitality of the entire year [3] (as discussed previously [4]).

Furthermore, on this Shabbos, through Divine Providence, there are several occasions of joy for Bnei Yisrael—*Yiddishe simchas* [5].

**B.** We must explain the content of the concept that from the day of Shabbos all the days are blessed:

By way of introduction, it is sometimes explained that the three days preceding Shabbos and the three days following Shabbos belong to the day of Shabbos [6]. However, it is also explained that all the days of the week belong to the Shabbos that precedes them, from which all the days of the week are blessed [2].

Moreover, the *vitality* of all the days of the week is drawn from the day of Shabbos—as the holy Ohr HaChaim [7] explains regarding the verse [8], "For in *six* days Hashem made the heavens and the earth," and not "*in* six days" [9]. "For at the time of creation, Hashem did not create power in the world other than to stand for six days... and through the day of Shabbos, He influences the worlds in general with the spirit that sustains them for another six days... for the existence of Shabbos in the world is its sustenance, etc."

#### 140

The explanation of the matter and the lesson for man’s *avodah*:

The primary occupation of a person during the days of the week is with mundane matters that are not matters of holiness [10]—the thirty-nine *melachos* of the workdays. Through these, man’s *avodah* is performed (so that it should not be in the manner of "bread of shame" [11]) by refining and purifying mundane matters and elevating them to holiness. Through this, the *avodah* of the six days of the week also becomes a *mitzvah*, as the verse states [12], "Six days you shall work"—a language of command [13].

The *empowerment* for the *avodah* of the six days of the week—in refining mundane matters and elevating them to holiness—comes from the day of Shabbos, which is dedicated entirely to Torah and *avodah* (prayer), "entirely for Hashem" [14]. From it, one draws strength for all the days of the week to extend holiness even into mundane matters (as explained in Chassidus [15] regarding the concept of *Havdalah*).

**C.** Similarly, regarding Shabbos Mevarchim Chodesh Teves, from which blessing and vitality are drawn for (all the days of the week, and also) Rosh Chodesh Teves, which includes all the days of the month of Teves:

The month of Teves is "a month when the body enjoys the body" [16].

Its relevance to man’s *avodah*—regarding the *avodah* of the body:

By way of introduction, as discussed previously [17], the *mitzvos* were given to souls in bodies and specifically for the sake of the body. Therefore, the primary obligation of fulfilling *mitzvos* is the act—the *body* of the *mitzvah*. For if one intended all the *kavanos* but did not perform the act of the *mitzvah*, he has not fulfilled his obligation (and not only did he not fulfill the *mitzvah*, he also committed a transgression by neglecting a positive commandment). Conversely, if he performed the act of the *mitzvah* without the *kavanah* of the *mitzvah*—the *soul* of the *mitzvah*—although he will be punished for the lack of *kavanah*, he has nevertheless fulfilled the obligation (which is why he is obligated in the *bracha* of the *mitzvah*, and we answer *Amen* to his *bracha*).

Regarding the manner of the body’s *avodah*—the teaching of the Baal Shem Tov [18] is well-known regarding the verse [19], "If you see the donkey of your enemy crouching under its burden, you shall not refrain from helping him; you shall surely help him with him." One must not leave the body in its state and condition as it "crouches under its burden"

#### 141

(the burden of Torah and *mitzvos*) and break it through fasts and afflictions, but rather, "you shall surely help him *with him*." The *avodah* must be *with the body* specifically, to refine and purify it.

This is emphasized even more regarding the month of Teves. The period of Teves is the period of cold, which indicates a lack of the warmth and vitality of holiness (the opposite of the period of Tammuz, the period of heat, which indicates the warmth and vitality of holiness [20]). Thus, the state and condition of the body is in a state of extreme descent. Nevertheless, even in this state and condition, one must not leave the body "crouching under its burden," but one must work *with* the body, to refine and purify it, until the *avodah* of the body is in a manner where "the body enjoys."

And although the essence is the *avodah* of the body, the empowerment for the *avodah* of the body is drawn through the soul—analogous to the empowerment for the *avodah* of the weekdays (the body) from the day of Shabbos (the soul).

**D.** This can be explained regarding the entirety of the Jewish people and the entirety of human life—for the concept that "from it all the days are blessed" exists in all levels of *Olam, Shanah, Nefesh* (World, Year, Soul):

The Jewish people are divided into two types: Yissachar and Zevulun, as it is written, "Rejoice, Zevulun, in your going out, and Yissachar in your tents" [21]. They are analogous to Shabbos and the weekdays: Yissachar, who engage in Torah, are analogous to Shabbos, and Zevulun, who engage in worldly matters, are analogous to the weekdays. Just as the empowerment for all the days of the week is drawn from the day of Shabbos, so too, the empowerment for Zevulun to engage and succeed in livelihood is through Yissachar—meaning, "Rejoice, Zevulun, in your going out" is through the fact that "Yissachar is in your tents."

That is to say: Even though Yissachar’s livelihood is provided by Zevulun ("Zevulun... goes out to trade... and earns and gives into the mouth of Yissachar, and they sit and engage in Torah; therefore Zevulun preceded Yissachar, for Yissachar’s Torah was through Zevulun" [22]), just as the eating of Shabbos is through the toil of all the days of the week ("He who toils on Erev Shabbos will eat on Shabbos" [23]), and as it is stated in the Zohar [24], "Those sages who are like Shabbos and Yom Tov have nothing except what those commoners (the *chulin*) give them, just as the day of Shabbos has nothing except what is prepared for it on the weekday"—the engagement of Zevulun in livelihood is through

#### 142

the empowerment he receives from Yissachar, just as the empowerment for the weekdays is from the day of Shabbos.

The same applies to the entirety of a person’s life—which is divided into two types: up to age twenty and after age twenty, which are analogous to Shabbos and the weekdays. Up to age twenty ("At five years old for Scripture, at ten for Mishnah... at fifteen for Gemara" [25]), the primary engagement is in Torah and *avodah*—analogous to the day of Shabbos. After age twenty ("At twenty to pursue" [25]), the engagement in worldly matters begins—analogous to the weekdays. The empowerment for the *avodah* in the world after age twenty is from the engagement in Torah and *avodah* until age twenty, analogous to the empowerment for the weekdays from the day of Shabbos.

*

**E.** What was said above regarding the entirety of human life—that the empowerment for *avodah* in the world comes from the years where the primary engagement was in Torah and *avodah*—is highlighted in the conduct of Yaakov [26]:

Regarding the verse [27], "And he lay down in that place," the Midrash [28] states, "Here he lay down, but all the fourteen years that he was hidden in the house of Ever, he did not lie down." Another interpretation: "Here he lay down, but all the twenty years that he stood in the house of Lavan, he did not lie down" (as it is written [29], "And my sleep fled from my eyes," and more than that—that "he did not lie down").

Seemingly, this is difficult to understand: It is understandable that "all the fourteen years that he was hidden in the house of Ever, he did not lie down" because he was engaged in Torah. But "all the twenty years that he stood in the house of Lavan"—why did he toil and sacrifice himself to the point that "he did not lie down"?!

The explanation for this is that Yaakov’s toil, to the point of *mesiras nefesh* that "he did not lie down," was certainly not for the sake of guarding Lavan’s sheep [30], but for the *avodah* of *birurim*—the refining of the sparks of holiness that were in the house of Lavan. For this, he needed to be awake during the entire time ("he did not lie down") in order to overcome Lavan, who opposed Yaakov’s activity in the *avodah* of *birurim*.

#### 143

Lavan claimed to Yaakov Avinu (and this is what Lavan’s heirs in every generation claim to Yaakov’s grandchildren), "The daughters are my daughters, and the sons are my sons, and the sheep are my sheep" [31]:

It is understandable that you (Yaakov) yourself—an old Jew who belongs to the old generation—can conduct yourself as you wish, to study Torah day and night. But what do you want from the children?! The young children who are in modern times—Lavan claims—belong to *me*, "the daughters are *my* daughters and the sons are *my* sons." Why are you making them "cripples" (*kalikes*) who will not be able to adapt themselves to the conduct of the world?! You want to teach them Judaism—so be it, but you must do it in a modern way, with new methods, and not make them "idlers"!

Similarly—he continues to claim—"the sheep are my sheep": Regarding Torah and prayer—I do not interfere. But matters of commerce, "the sheep"—"*my* sheep"—you must conduct yourself according to my ways, the ways of Lavan the Aramean, not to take into account the prohibitions of deceit, encroachment, and the like. For, in your conduct of engaging in commerce according to Torah, it is difficult to "make a living."

For this, Yaakov sacrificed himself all the twenty years he was in the house of Lavan—"And my sleep fled from my eyes," until "he did not lie down"—not only for spiritual matters, like the study of Torah in the house of Ever, but also for matters about which Lavan claims belong to him: "The daughters are my daughters, and the sons are my sons, and the sheep are my sheep." For these matters, Yaakov sacrificed himself (as he said, "*I served you* fourteen years for your two *daughters* and six years for your *sheep*" [32]) so that they would be according to Torah, so that through this, the sparks of holiness that are in Lavan’s domain would be refined, and *Elokus* would be drawn even into material things.

**F.** Based on this, we can also explain the continuation of the Midrash [33]—"And what was he saying (all the twenty years he did not lie down in Lavan’s house)? The fifteen *Shir HaMaalos* in the Book of Psalms... *A Song of Ascents of David: If it had not been for Hashem who was for us, let Israel say* [34], Israel the Elder":

Seemingly, the Midrash’s question, "And what was he saying" (what did Yaakov do during the nights he did not lie down in Lavan’s house), is difficult to understand—was he not busy guarding Lavan’s sheep?

Rather—as stated—Yaakov would certainly not have sacrificed himself not to lie down for twenty years for the sake of guarding Lavan’s sheep, but rather for the refining of the sparks of holiness in Lavan’s house.

#### 144

Regarding this, the Midrash asks, "What was he saying"—by what power did Yaakov perform the *avodah* of *birurim*, such that not only did the lowly matters of Lavan the Aramean not cause him a descent, but on the contrary, he elevated them to holiness?

The answer to this is—"The fifteen *Shir HaMaalos* in the Book of Psalms... *If it had not been for Hashem who was for us, etc.*"—*by the power of the Holy One, Blessed be He*, including also "*A Song of Ascents... From where will my help come?*" [35]. He felt that with his own powers ("*mit aygene koichos*") it is impossible to accomplish anything, and only "from *Ayin*"—which indicates his total *bitul*—"will my help come" [36]. "My help is from Hashem, Maker of heaven and earth" [37]. He drew to himself the help of the Holy One, Blessed be He, in the *avodah* of *birurim*, revealing in his *avodah* that the Holy One, Blessed be He, is the Master of the house not only in matters of heaven, but also in matters of earth, in the lowly matters of Charan ("the burning anger of the Place in the world" [38]), in the world of Lavan the Aramean.

**G.** The empowerment for all this—his conduct "all the fourteen years that he was hidden in the house of Ever" that "he did not lie down" because he was engaged in Torah:

During the fourteen years that he was hidden in the house of Ever, which were dedicated to the study of Torah day and night until "he did not lie down," Yaakov worked on himself so that his entire existence and all his affairs, even his material affairs, would be permeated with holiness and *Elokus*, until he became a chariot for *Elokus*, as our Sages said [39], "The Patriarchs are the chariot," and as explained in *Tanya* [40] that "all their limbs were holy and separated from the matters of this world, and they were made a chariot only for the Supreme Will alone all their days."

With this power, he was able to go out and perform his *avodah* all the twenty years he was in the house of Lavan in refining the matters of the world—that even while in the house of Lavan, "he was saying the fifteen *Shir HaMaalos*," "*From where will my help come*," "*My help is from Hashem, Maker of heaven and earth*," as stated, to permeate even the matters of the world with *Elokus*.

*

**H.** Regarding the study of Torah before marriage, our Rebbe the Alter Rebbe rules in *Hilchos Talmud Torah* [41]: "Anyone whose mind and power of memory are good, so that he can learn and remember the entire Oral Torah, he should not marry a woman until he learns

#### 145

first the entire Oral Torah, which are all the *halachos* with their reasons in a concise way... for if he marries a woman first, he will have millstones around his neck, the livelihood of his wife and children, and he will not be able to engage in Torah as properly... and therefore the great *mitzvah* of *pru u'rvu* (procreation) is deferred for the sake of this study... And therefore, in their days, when they would learn with the youths from age ten and onwards, five years of Mishnah and five years of Talmud, which are the reasons in a concise way, if he did not marry when he reached twenty, he would be transgressing the positive commandment of the Torah, *pru u'rvu*. And its beginning time is from age eighteen, for even after marriage he can learn for two or three years (to complete the five years of Talmud) without great distraction before he has many children."

In explaining the precision of the Alter Rebbe’s language regarding the completion of the five years of Talmud, that "even after marriage he can learn *two or three* years, etc."—it can be said that this refers to the two opinions regarding the interpretation of "At eighteen for the *chuppah*" [25]: whether it is at the end of eighteen, eighteen full years, according to which two years are sufficient to complete the five years of Talmud, or whether it is the beginning of eighteen, according to which three years are needed to complete the five years of Talmud [42].

From this, it is seemingly proven that the matter of marriage is in contradiction to the study of Torah.

And nevertheless, according to Torah, there is an obligation both regarding the study of Torah in the manner of "And you shall meditate in it day and night" [43], and regarding marriage, which is a "great *mitzvah*" [44],

[Unless "one whose soul desires Torah constantly and he is engrossed in it like Ben Azzai and cleaves to it all his days," if "he did not marry a woman, there is no sin in his hand" [45]. And nevertheless, even regarding Ben Azzai’s conduct, we find that this is conduct in the manner of *Tohu*, and not in the manner of *Tikkun* [46]],

And we even find that Torah study and marriage were equated to one another—regarding leaving the Land of Israel [47] and selling a Torah scroll [48].

And since "the Holy One, Blessed be He, does not come with grievances against His creatures" [23], it must be that the powers required for this were given, so that the matter of marriage would not be in contradiction to the study of Torah, and even after marriage he can fulfill the *mitzvah* of Torah study in the manner of "And you shall meditate in it day and night."

#### 146

**I.** This matter is emphasized most among those from whom the Rebbe demanded that even after marriage their settlement should be in the tent of Torah. And since it is clear that the Rebbe will fulfill his will ("*der Rebbe vet geviss oisfiren*"), certainly the matter of marriage will not be in contradiction to Torah for them.

However, there are still those who ask regarding livelihood—"*From where will my help come*?"

The answer to this is—"*From where will my help come*" in a tone of acceptance: "*Ayin*" (nothingness) is the concept of *bitul*. That is, one must nullify his intellect, his logic and knowledge, and fulfill the command of the Rebbe, and then "*will my help come*," for the Rebbe will already ensure that the influence of the Holy One, Blessed be He, is drawn into everything he needs (not only in spirituality, but) also in physicality.

—In what manner the influence will be ("*From where will my help come*" literally) is not our concern. We must only fulfill the command of the Rebbe out of *bitul*, "*Ayin*," and through this, "*will my help come*."

**J.** When one hears a certain thing from the Rebbe (and in this case, regarding the settlement after marriage in the tent of Torah), one must accept and fulfill it immediately, without prior deliberation,

[When one sees a certain thing in a book, then there can be investigation and deliberation, but when one hears from the Rebbe, one must fulfill it immediately],

And afterwards, whoever wants to, can toil to understand the matter with his intellect as well. But this does not affect the actual fulfillment, which must be immediately, without regard to whether he understands it with his intellect or not.

In the language of the Gemara [49]: "In matters of the Sages, we perform the act and then we raise the objection." That is, first and foremost, there must be the actual act, *and afterwards* one can ask questions, debate, etc.

There are those who, even if they do what they are told, nevertheless need prior deliberation, to explain the matters to themselves, to the bride, and to the in-laws on both sides, and then they will do what they are told. But the truth is that "in matters of the Sages—in the words of the Rebbe—we perform the act," that there must be the performance of the act immediately, without prior deliberation.

—The Rebbe Rayatz once told [50] about two Chassidim of our Rebbe the Alter Rebbe who were divided in their manner of *avodah*. For one, the order was from bottom to top: first the act and then the understanding. And for one, the order was from top to bottom: first understanding and knowledge and then the act. Once, the Alter Rebbe sent a messenger to ask them for money. Both obeyed, but the first gave immediately—he says and does; while the second waited until he could enter to the Rebbe [and it is impossible to enter for *yechidus* only after the prerequisite of immersion in the *mikveh*, etc., etc.] to ask what amount to give, and then he would give as the Rebbe told him—deliberation first and then obedience.

Similarly in our case: he will indeed fulfill what he is told, but first he needs to absorb the matters into his ten powers of the soul, of the bride, of the in-laws, and after the matters penetrate all ten powers as they are included from ten, a hundred powers, then he will go to immerse in the *mikveh*, and will wait until Rabbi Hodakov [51] allows him to enter in order to return and ask...

The required conduct is—that when the Rebbe says, one must fulfill immediately, without prior thought and deliberation.

And in the style mentioned—to fulfill the words of the Rebbe out of *bitul*, the level of *Ayin*, and through this, *will my help come*.

*

**K.** The concept of *bitul* and *kabbalas ol* is also hinted at in the conduct of Yaakov Avinu when he went out to Charan [52], after the fourteen years that he was hidden in the house of Ever and engaged in Torah—"And he took the stone... and set it as a monument, and poured oil on its head" [53]:

Seemingly, it is difficult to understand what the connection of oil to a monument is? For a monument, one needs a stone, and in order for the monument to be stronger, there is a need for a larger stone, which is more *material*—the opposite of the concept of oil?

The answer to this is—that in order for the monument to be "the house of G-d" ("And this stone which I have set as a monument shall be the house of G-d" [54]), there is a need for oil, whose extraction from the olive is through crushing, which is done with the feet, which is the concept of *bitul* and *kabbalas ol*.

The point is—that upon his departure from the house of Ever after fourteen years that he engaged

#### 148

in Torah, there needed to be in him the concept of *the crushing of the olive*, to put aside the study and depth in Torah study, and to fulfill the mission that was placed upon him to engage in the refining of the world [55].

**L.** From this, we learn a lesson that applies especially to *bnei Torah* when they go out into the world:

Since in his youth he studied Torah *for his own sake*,

—For if Rav Sheshes could study "for his own sake," as he said, "Rejoice, my soul, for you I read, for you I studied" [56], certainly he too can study "for his own sake"—

Therefore, when they tell him that he needs to study with a Jewish child *Aleph-Beis*, *Ivri*, or *Chumash* with *Rashi*—he claims that for this one should turn to a "teacher of children," while he needs to thrive in Torah study ("*shteigen in lernen*")!

At the time, the *Rosh Yeshivah* told him that he has a good head, *bli ayin hara*... and since so, he needs to utilize his time to toil in Torah study, to innovate innovations in Torah, and even such innovations that even Moshe Rabbeinu would not understand... as we find in the Gemara [57] that when the Holy One, Blessed be He, showed Moshe Rabbi Akiva, who was expounding on every thorn and thorn heaps upon heaps of *halachos*, "he (Moshe) did not know what they were saying," and "his strength weakened," until he reached one thing about which Rabbi Akiva said, "It is a *halacha* to Moshe from Sinai," and then "his mind was settled."

And for this comes the lesson from Yaakov’s action, "And he poured *oil* on its head"—to take the "olive" that is full and overflowing with *lomdus*, lessons in Torah for review and study, etc., *and to crush* it, which is the concept of *bitul* and *kabbalas ol*, and to study with a Jewish child *Aleph-Beis*, etc.

**M.** One must act and influence the entire environment even in simple matters, such as the observance of Shabbos and the like.

When one sees a store of a Jew that is open on Shabbos, one must speak with the owner and influence him to close the store on Shabbos, and not look for various excuses

#### 149

—that this is the job of the Rabbi, the *shochet*, or the teacher, for since they receive payment for such matters, they must take care of it, but as for him, it is not his business; or that his speaking will not achieve its effect anyway—besides the fact that the other will look at him as an "idler"... And in order to achieve the effect of Shabbos observance, there is a need for the *Rabbi* specifically to speak with him, who is expert in the *halachos* of Shabbos, and can show the sign and the paragraph in the *Shulchan Aruch* where the prohibition is explained regarding every detail.

To what is this comparable—to a person who sees a fire, and the firefighters delay coming because they are sleeping... surely he will not claim that he will do nothing, because the extinguishing of the fire must be by the "firefighters" with the red hats specifically... rather, he will try himself to do everything in his power to extinguish the fire [58].

And especially after the Rebbe has illuminated him ("*der Rebbe hot im baleichtn*"), he must fulfill the will and mission of the Rebbe to illuminate other Jews. And consequently, seeing that a Jew opens his store on Shabbos, which adds darkness and causes disaster for himself and his environment, the obligation is upon him to do everything in his power to prevent this.

The point of the matter—that the *avodah* must be out of *bitul* and *kabbalas ol*, without calculations, and then there is an additional benefit also regarding himself—that the conduct with him will not be according to the calculations of the *Midat HaDin* ("*Midat HaDin vet zich mit im nit porken*").

*

**N.** What was said above regarding the matter of *bitul* and *kabbalas ol* is also connected with the birth of a daughter:

The difference between a son and a daughter [59]—that a son, a man whose way is to conquer [60], indicates conduct according to intellect, and a daughter (a woman), "You have no woman who is fit among women except a woman who does the will of her husband" [61], indicates the conduct of *kabbalas ol*.

Its relevance to *avodah*—the difference between the study of Torah and the fulfillment of *mitzvos*: The study of Torah—must be in a manner where one understands with his intellect specifically, the concept of a son. And the fulfillment of *mitzvos*—must be out of *kabbalas ol* specifically, the concept of a daughter.

And it is explained in Chassidus [62] that in the time to come, the superiority of a daughter over a son will be revealed

#### 150

—that not only will there also be "the voice of a bride" [63] (unlike in this time when "a woman’s voice is *ervah*" [64]), but more than that, that "a female shall encompass a male" [65]. And the preparation for this—through the *avodah* in this time in the manner of *kabbalas ol*, the concept of a daughter.

*

**O.** As mentioned above, this is with extra emphasis in these days—between 19 Kislev and Chanukah:

The concept of 19 Kislev is the victory of the Torah of Chassidus and the *Nesi’im* of Chassidus—*Didan Netzach* [66].

From this, we come to Chanukah (which begins in the seven days of the *hakafah* [67] of 19 Kislev)—in which there was the victory over the Greeks who wanted to "make them forget Your Torah," "*Your* Torah" specifically [68], meaning, that they agreed that they should study Torah in general, but that they should forget, G-d forbid, about the "Giver of the Torah," and it should not be evident that this is the Torah of the *Holy One, Blessed be He* ("Your Torah"). The victory is in that the study of Torah is permeated with the knowledge and feeling that the Torah is the Torah of the Holy One, Blessed be He—a matter that is achieved through the study of the inner dimension of the Torah, the Torah of Chassidus [69].

And this is also the content of the miracle that they found one cruse of oil that was sealed with the seal of the *Kohen Gadol* [70]—for oil indicates the inner dimension of the Torah [71], the Torah of Chassidus, and the *Kohen Gadol* (with whose seal the oil is placed) indicates our *Rabbeim Nesi’im* in every generation, until the *Nasi* of our generation, the Rebbe Rayatz.

Thus, in these days, there is a special empowerment for victory in all matters that are done in the mission of the Rebbe in spreading Torah and Judaism and spreading the wellsprings outward, and through this, we will merit that the Rebbe will lead us to the great light of the true and complete Redemption.

**********

## B"H

#### 151

. . . In connection with the conclusion of the recitation of Kaddish[1](#_ftn829) for the passing of my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory . . .

***

There are several opinions regarding the duration of the recitation of Kaddish[2](#_ftn830): for the entire duration of one’s life; twelve months and eleven days; a full year, including the leap month; twelve months; twelve months minus one week; eleven months; and eleven months minus one day.

As for us, we follow only the custom of our Nesi'im, based on what is recorded in a segment of the testament of my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe (Rashab), of blessed memory: regarding the eleven months, one should stop one month and one day prior. For example, if the Yahrtzeit is on the 10th of Shevat[3](#_ftn831), one recites Kaddish through the 9th of Teves, inclusive[4](#_ftn832). This is also the opinion of the overwhelming majority of the later halachic authorities.

***

It is stated in the writings of the Arizal[5](#_ftn833)—and cited by the halachic authorities—that the recitation of Kaddish is also relevant to the soul’s ascent from level to level within Gan Eden itself.

It is understood from this that with the conclusion of the recitation of Kaddish for the eleven months, this order of ascents is completed, and a new order of the soul’s ascents begins; for our Sages have said that Torah scholars have no rest in the World to Come, for they go from strength to strength.

It is therefore necessary for everyone who is connected to my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, to now increase their courage in strengthening their hiskashrus, to make an accounting

#### 152

within their soul—and according to their own capacity—regarding what they have accomplished during these eleven months, to fill in what is lacking, and through the methods that our Nasi, my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, instructed—to connect with him with even greater intensity and strength, meaning to him, so that he, too, may be elevated in his ascent.

And whoever sanctifies himself a little below—they sanctify him much from above.

**Menachem Schneerson**

*Erev Shabbos, Vayigash Elav Vayomer Bi Adoni*[6](#_ftn834), 5711.

*Brooklyn, N.Y.*

## With the help of Hashem. Sicha of Shabbos Parshas Vayigash, 7 Teves, 5711

#### 153

(Unedited)

**1.** This Shabbos — Parshas Vayigash — is the Shabbos preceding the day of the conclusion of the eleven months of reciting Kaddish.

According to what was discussed previously [1] (based on the words of the Ohr HaChaim [2]) that the day of Shabbos includes all the days of the week, as they all receive their vitality from the day of Shabbos, and their conduct depends on the manner of conduct of the day of Shabbos — we must explain the connection and relevance of the day of the conclusion of reciting Kaddish to Shabbos Parshas Vayigash, as follows.

Furthermore, this Shabbos also includes the joy of a Yid to whom Hashem showed a miracle regarding the rescue of his daughter for long, good years [3], as well as the joy of a Yid to whom a daughter was born, the joy of a chassan who has just completed his seven days of feasting [4], and also a birthday — for these matters, too, the private affairs of Bnei Yisrael, are under Divine Providence, and consequently, they also relate to Shabbos Parshas Vayigash, as follows.

**2.** Regarding the event of the miracle of the rescue of a daughter (and similarly, the birth of a daughter) of a Yid — we must first preface the root of the concept of "son" and "daughter" Above (as is known [5] that all matters below are drawn down from Above), in the *avodah* of Hashem:

It has been said many times [6] that "son" denotes *avodah* through intellect, and with strength, "it is the way of a man to conquer" [7], and "daughter" denotes *avodah* through *kabbalas ol*, "a worthy woman... does the will of her husband" [8].

A Yid’s *avodah* must be in both manners (son and daughter) — even though they are seemingly opposites:

#### 154

On one hand, a Yid is demanded to have *bitul*, "and my soul shall be as dust to all" [9], not only the negation of pride and ego, but also to set aside his desires, his wishes, and even his intellect, and to conduct himself according to the Shulchan Aruch through *kabbalas ol*, even in a matter that has no place at all in his intellect, and furthermore, even if it seems to him that this matter will cause him harm, *chas v’shalom*, nevertheless, he must nullify his intellect and do what is required through *kabbalas ol* (and then he will see that not only did this not cause harm, *chas v’shalom*, but on the contrary, it brought benefit (not only in spirituality, but) also in physicality).

On the other hand, a Yid is demanded to have *strength and power*, so that, even though "you are the fewest of all the peoples" [10], and within the Jewish people themselves, those who keep Torah and mitzvos are few compared to the rest of Bnei Yisrael, and those who are also particular about *hiddur mitzvah* and going beyond the letter of the law are few among those who keep Torah and mitzvos themselves ("the more *frum* one is, the fewer there are"), nevertheless, he must have the strength and power to conduct himself according to the Torah without being influenced by the majority,

[For example: not to argue that since most of the Yidden in his surroundings pray in a Conservative synagogue, therefore he can also pray there, and similarly regarding matters that are beyond the letter of the law, such as putting on Rabbeinu Tam tefillin and the like — not to argue that since he is not a Rav or an elderly Chassid, he can conduct himself in this matter like the majority of Bnei Yisrael],

And not only should he not be influenced by others, but on the contrary, he should influence others ("it is the way of a man to conquer," not to wait until they come to him, but to go out and influence them) to bring them closer to keeping Torah and mitzvos — initially in a manner of mere closeness, and in time make them keepers of Torah and mitzvos, and eventually to a conduct of *hiddur mitzvah* and beyond the letter of the law.

**3.** And to add, that the strength and power not to be influenced by the majority, and on the contrary, to influence them, etc. — we take from Avraham Avinu, the first Yid:

It is written [11], "Avraham was one" — one and unique against the entire world, as it is in the Midrash [12] that he was called "Avram the Ivri" [13], because "the whole world was on one side, and he was on the other side," for everyone was an idolater, and only he alone "grasped the path of truth... and knew that there is one G-d... and He created everything, etc." [14].

#### 155

And nevertheless, not only did Avraham alone walk the path of truth without being influenced by the entire world, but on the contrary, he also influenced the entire world — "He began to stand and call out in a loud voice *to the entire world* and inform them that there is one G-d and He is worthy to be served... as it is said [15], 'And he called there in the name of Hashem, the G-d of the world'" [14], "Do not read *Vayikra* (he called), but *Vayakri* (he caused to call), teaching that Avraham Avinu *caused* the name of Hashem to be called in the mouths of every passerby" [16], meaning, not only did he influence them that they too should say "G-d of the world," but more than that, he influenced them to such an extent that they themselves *called and proclaimed* (to others) "G-d of the world" ("He spoke so much and reached them so much over the years... until he made them call out themselves"), and not just "G-d of *the* world" (with the addition of the *hei*), that the world is an entity and a thing unto itself and Hashem is the one who gives life to the world, but "G-d of the world," that the reality of the world is Elokus [17].

[It should be noted that even though even after Avraham Avinu’s proclamation that there is one G-d, many errors remained among the nations of the world, nevertheless, the very fact that they stopped worshipping idols (making forms and bowing and sacrificing to them) because they knew there is one G-d (even though they were still mistaken), has a great advantage in it. Similar to what the Rambam wrote [18] (in the old editions that were not touched by the censor) that "all these matters of the Nazarene and this Ishmaelite who stood after him are only to straighten the path for Melech HaMoshiach, and to fix the entire world to serve Hashem together, as it is said [19], 'For then I will turn to the nations a clear language, to call all of them in the name of Hashem and to serve Him with one shoulder'"].

And "the deeds of the fathers [the three fathers, Avraham, Yitzchak, and Yaakov, and especially Avraham, to whom all Bnei Yisrael relate, even converts (as discussed above [20])] are a sign for the children" [21] — that Bnei Yisrael do not need to be influenced by the majority, and not only must they stand their ground, but more than that, they must influence and act upon others, just as Avraham Avinu conducted himself at the beginning of the path of Yiddishkeit.

**4.** And we return to our subject — that a Yid is demanded to have two movements: the movement of *bitul* and *kabbalas ol*, and the movement of strength and power.

And although they are seemingly opposite movements — the truth is that even

#### 156

the strength and power not to be influenced by the world, and on the contrary, to influence the world ("it is the way of a man to conquer"), is a result of the movement of *bitul* and *kabbalas ol* (the *avodah* which is in the category of "daughter," "a worthy woman... does the will of her husband").

The explanation for this — that from the side of *kabbalas ol* and *bitul*, he feels that he is not a reality unto himself and the world is not a reality unto itself, and certainly the conduct of the world is only by Hashem, and since that is so, he must fulfill the will of Hashem and walk the path of Torah, the path of truth, and he has nothing to be influenced by the calculations of majority and minority, etc.

**5.** And it should be added that this matter (that the strength and power is a result of *bitul* and *kabbalas ol*) is also emphasized in the manner of *avodah* which is in the category of "son," "it is the way of a man to conquer":

The order of conduct among Bnei Yisrael regarding the birth of a son — that "on the eighth day he shall circumcise the flesh of his foreskin" [22], that the *bris* is when he is eight days old, when he does not understand anything and cannot resist, etc., even though from the side of "democracy" they should have waited until he reached the age of understanding, when they could deliberate with him if he wants it (like the order of conduct of the children of Yishmael to circumcise at thirteen years old).

The point of this — that in the act of *bris* at the age of eight days, the movement of *mesiras nefesh* to Hashem that is in every Yid from the nature of his birth is emphasized, for since he is born a Yid, his true desire is *to give his life* for the will of Hashem,

[And even if after some time, when he comes to understanding, he says that he does not want this, this is only because "his inclination overpowered him," and even then, the truth is that "he wants (his true and inner desire) to be a Yid... to do all the mitzvos, etc." (as the ruling of the Rambam [23])],

As it is expressed *in the drawing of the blood of the covenant* — "the blood is the soul" [24], that even one drop alone, this is a drop of blood on which the vitality of the soul depends — because of the command of Hashem.

And the reason that the *bris* is on the eighth day and not before — "so that one Shabbos passes over him" [25] — it can be said that the matter of Shabbos which is "sanctified and established" [26] (unlike Yom Tov where Yisrael are the ones who sanctify the times [27]) denotes the giving of strength *from Above* so that the matter of the *bris* can take place [28].

#### 157

And through the *bris* — the movement of *mesiras nefesh* which is the ultimate *bitul* and *kabbalas ol* — the strength and power is created in him not to be influenced by the world, and on the contrary, to influence the world, "it is the way of a man to conquer."

**6.** Based on this, we must also explain regarding the content of the event of the rescue of the daughter:

When Hashem does a miracle for a Yid regarding the rescue of *his daughter*, this is an instruction from Above that there must be *in him* the *avodah* of the category of "daughter" — the matter of *bitul* and *kabbalas ol*, and consequently, he will also have the strength and power not to be influenced by anyone in everything related to fulfilling his decision to walk the path of Torah (without looking at his conduct until now), knowing that this is the path of truth,

Including and especially — regarding the education of this daughter, and also his other children, in the path of Torah and mitzvos.

— There is a *maamar* of the Rebbe [29] that explains the good part that is in the matter of sleep and fainting of Bnei Yisrael during the *galus*, based on a parable of "a father who has children... who went out and departed... nevertheless, the father is not so influenced... (and) he does not feel the pain of the cutting and severing from the root of the son’s soul, and if the father felt the suffering, he could not bear the magnitude of the heartache that the father would have for the separation of the son from his root... and therefore the concealment and darkness does a good deed for the righteous and innocent fathers so they do not feel so much."

However, it is understood and also simple that one should not be satisfied with the good part that the parents *do not feel the pain* from the fact that the children do not walk the path of Torah,

— And especially since regarding the children themselves there is no benefit or good in this, and on the contrary, if the parents felt the pain they would strive to fix the situation, and when they do not feel the pain the children will remain in an undesirable state and situation, and if so, the question is asked: what is the fault of the children that it is decreed upon them to remain in their state and situation only for the good part of the parents so they do not feel the pain?! —

Rather, there is a need for the ultimate good — which is certainly given by Hashem who is the essence of good and it is the nature of the good to do good [30] — that the children return and walk the path of Torah.

And therefore, the parents must strive and do everything that depends on them to educate their sons and daughters in the path of Torah, and prevent them from matters that are not suitable for the path of Torah.

#### 158

To what is this matter similar — to parents who see that their young child is about to do an action that will cause him to be maimed all the days of his life, *chas v’shalom*, they would certainly hurry immediately (without looking at the calendar to see if it is possible to postpone it to a later time) to do everything in their power, in all ways and in all manners, and even "turn worlds upside down"... to prevent this!

And if these things are said regarding matters that concern the life of the body — regarding matters that concern *the life of the soul*, all the more so!

**7.** And in this matter there is a lesson and instruction from the *parsha* of the week, *Parshas Vayigash* — in which we see that for the good of a Jewish child, one child, one must strive to the point of *mesiras nefesh* [31]:

On the verse [32], "And Yehudah approached him," Chazal said [33] that in this approach Yehudah was prepared for everything, even for war (that if Yosef did not agree of his own will to release Binyamin, he would make war with him).

And seemingly it is not understood: how did Yehudah think he could fight against Yosef, at the same time that Yehudah and his brothers are few in number, while Yosef is the ruler over the entire land of Egypt?!

And even though Yehudah and his brothers were great warriors, Yosef (and his sons) were greater warriors, as it is in the Midrash [34] that when Yehudah showed an act of heroism, Yosef also showed an act of heroism like him, and "immediately Yehudah was amazed and said this one is stronger than me," and if so, how did it enter his mind to fight against him?!

And the explanation for this — in the words of Yehudah (why he entered into the struggle) "for your servant *guaranteed the lad* from my father, saying if I do not bring him to you, etc." [35], for since he took upon himself the responsibility to bring Binyamin to Yaakov, he must strive for him to the point of *mesiras nefesh*! And all this — even when it concerns *one* Jewish child (for the danger was only regarding Binyamin, and the rest of the brothers would remain in their wholeness), for him alone there is a need for *mesiras nefesh*, because of the responsibility placed upon him!

And this is the instruction and moral for every father and mother — that since Hashem placed upon them the responsibility for each and every one of their children ("guaranteed the lad"), then, even for *one* child they must strive (that what should not happen with a Jewish child does not happen with him) to the point of *mesiras nefesh*.

**8.** And it should be added in the explanation of the lesson and instruction from "And Yehudah approached him" — Yehudah specifically:

"Yehudah" — is from the language of *hoda'ah* (acknowledgment/thanks), which is the matter of *bitul* and *kabbalas ol* [36].

And "And Yehudah approached him," an approach (also) for war — denotes the strength and power, to such an extent that he is prepared to go out to war, "it is the way of a man to conquer."

And the point of this — as mentioned — is that through *bitul* and *kabbalas ol* the strength and power is created not to be influenced by the entire world, and to walk the path of truth, the path of Torah and mitzvos, and to educate the sons and daughters in the path of Torah and mitzvos, and to strive in this to the point of *mesiras nefesh*.

***

**9.** It was mentioned above (Section 1) that this Shabbos is the Shabbos before the day of the conclusion of the recitation of Kaddish — for although [37] there are several opinions regarding the duration of the recitation of Kaddish, the opinion of the overwhelming majority of the later authorities is that the recitation of Kaddish is eleven months less one day, and so our Rebbes, the *Nesi'im*, practiced, and in this case, the recitation of Kaddish is until the 9th of Teves inclusive [38], which is blessed from the Shabbos of *Parshas Vayigash*.

And according to what is explained in the writings of the Arizal [39] that the recitation of Kaddish relates (not only to the ascent of the soul from *Gehinnom*, but also) to the ascent of the soul from level to level in *Gan Eden* itself (which is why we say Kaddish also on Shabbos), it must be that the cessation of the recitation of Kaddish after eleven months is (not because after eleven months the ascents end, for Chazal said [40] "the righteous have no rest neither in this world nor in the world to come, as it is said [41] 'they go from strength to strength'"), but because then a new order begins in the ascents of the soul — *in a manner incomparably higher* than the ascents during the eleven months [42] — ascents that are above the relevance to the recitation of Kaddish in the world of speech.

#### 160

And based on this, one must explain the story that the Rebbe (Rashab) regretted and was pained that he added one day to the recitation of Kaddish of eleven months [43] — because the recitation of Kaddish in speech makes an impression, and it is possible that it will cause a hindrance, *chas v’shalom*, in the ascents that are above the relevance to the recitation of Kaddish in the world of speech [44].

**10.** And regarding us:

It was discussed above [45] in the interpretation of the words of the Rebbe [46] that the shepherds of Yisrael "do not separate from their flock" — that in all the ascents of the shepherds of Yisrael they take with them also the Chassidim, those who are connected, and even those who had any connection whatsoever, that they too ascend in all their ascents.

— The Rebbe told [47] about the Rebbe Maharash, that on the eve of Rosh Hashanah 5643, the eve of the last Rosh Hashanah in his life in this world, when he entered the room of his wife the Rebbetzin to speak with her [as is the custom of the Rebbes that on the eve of Rosh Hashanah they would enter the room of their wife the Rebbetzin to speak with her [48]], she understood from his words that in this year he would depart from the world, and she argued: how is it possible to leave small children, etc., and in the course of the conversation the Rebbe Maharash said to her: I will ascend 32 levels Above, and you will ascend 32 levels Below. And the Rebbe explained that the 32 levels Below are the 32 years of the life of the Rebbetzin (from the eve of Rosh Hashanah 5643, which still relates to the year 5642, until her passing on the 10th of Shevat 5659), and the 32 levels Above are the 32 *drushim* in *Likutei Torah* for the three *parshios* that were printed after his passing [49].

And seemingly it is not understood: it is well regarding the 32 levels of the Rebbetzin, since they are *Below*, this is expressed in the 32 years of her life *in this world*, but the 32 levels of the Rebbe Maharash, since they are *Above*, what is their connection to the printing of the 32 *drushim* in *Likutei Torah* for the three *parshios* *in this world*?!

And the explanation for this — that the ascents of the Rebbe Above must be reflected ("*opshpiglen zich*") and act to strengthen and add power also to *the Chassidim Below*.

And from this it is also understood in our case — that the new order in the ascents of the Rebbe

#### 161

that begins after the conclusion of the recitation of Kaddish, incomparably to the ascents from before, must be reflected and act to strengthen and add power also to us in our *avodah* Below.

However, for this, each of the Chassidim and those who are connected must add courage in strengthening the connection to the Rebbe, and through this he will also be able to ascend in the ascent of the Rebbe.

And this can be explained based on a physical parable — that when one accompanies a person who walks in the usual way, there is no need for effort to walk with him, unlike when one wants to accompany a person of strength who walks with more speed, there is a need for effort to walk with him, and all the more so when the other begins to run, and furthermore, he adds in his running with the greatest speed, then there is a need for additional power with greater intensity and greater strength to accompany him.

And its parallel in the *nimshal* — that as much as the ascents of the Rebbe increase in greater elevation, there is a need to add courage with greater intensity and greater strength in the connection to him, in order to ascend in his ascents.

And since "Hashem does not come with complaints against His creatures" [50], He certainly gives the powers needed to strengthen the connection with greater intensity and greater strength, in order to ascend with him in the new order of ascents after the conclusion of the eleven months of reciting Kaddish.

**11.** And this giving of strength is hinted at in the *parsha* of the week that we read on the Shabbos from which the day of the conclusion of the recitation of Kaddish is blessed — "And Yehudah approached him," the approach of Yehudah to Yosef:

Yosef — is the *tzaddik* of the world, as is known [51] that the title "Tzaddik" is emphasized especially with Yosef, who is called "Yosef HaTzaddik" (and sometimes also with Binyamin [52]).

And the approach of Yehudah to Yosef ("And Yehudah approached him") — denotes the dedication ("*der ibergeben zich*") to Yosef HaTzaddik, the *tzaddik* of the world, to unite with him (which is the matter of the approach).

And he continues "(And Yehudah approached him) and said *my master*" — that the request from Yosef HaTzaddik, the *tzaddik* of the world, is (not the revelations of the Lower *Gan Eden* or the Upper *Gan Eden*, but) that Yosef HaTzaddik should be *his master*, and through this all the influences

#### 162

of Yosef HaTzaddik will be drawn down to him, as it is written in *Torah Or* [53] "And this is what is meant by 'And Yehudah approached him and said my master,' meaning that through him the influence will be drawn from Yosef HaTzaddik."

**12.** And based on this, one must also explain the continuation of the words of Yehudah to Yosef (after the preface of "my master") — "Let your servant speak a word in the ears of my master and do not let your anger burn against your servant for you are like Pharaoh" — in relation to the connection to Yosef HaTzaddik, the *tzaddik* of the world:

Knowing the lowliness of his status and situation, and the magnitude of the wonder of the greatness of Yosef HaTzaddik,

— And especially according to what is explained in *Chassidus* [54] the greatness of Yosef compared to the tribes and even the fathers, that the tribes and the fathers were shepherds because they needed to be in seclusion from the affairs of the world so that they could be in union with Elokus, unlike Yosef who was occupied with the affairs of the world (as it is written [55] "and he came into the house to do his work," "to check the account books," and all the more so after he became the "ruler over the entire land of Egypt" [56]), and at that time he was in union with Elokus in the category of *Yichuda Ila'ah* —

Then, from the side of the magnitude of the *distance of value* between them — how does *he* ("*vi kumt er*") even come to ask for something (and especially matters of smallness) *from Yosef*?!
