And therefore he prefaces "my master," that the content of this preface is that Yosef is his master, that is, that he is connected to him and united with him, and since he is connected to him and united with him, then he can ask for something from Yosef.

And nevertheless he continues and adds "and do not let your anger burn against your servant" — that there should not be a grievance against him ("*er zol kein faraybel nit hobn*") for the fact that he turns to him and wastes his time for matters of no consequence, matters of *smallness*.

— An *avreich* came to me and argued ("*er tenet zich*") for about half an hour regarding... a *car*!

Regarding his Divine soul and his animal soul and the constant war between them — he does not mention anything, since it did not touch or affect him ("*es rirt im nit on*"); the thing that touches him is — the car, and for this he wastes (not only his time, but also) the time of others.

For what does this *avreich* need a car?! A young *avreich* with two healthy legs

#### 163

thank G-d, can walk on foot, and when he utilizes the time of his walking in the street on foot to think a verse of *Chumash* or *Tehillim*, then, for this alone his entire life is worth it! And in exchange for this — he wants to ride in a car, where he will not be able to think a verse of *Chumash* or *Tehillim*, because he will be busy driving the car, looking at the speedometer ("*speedometer*") at the traffic light if it is red or green, and especially if he wants to prove the "greatness" of his animal soul that he can pass on a red light without a "traffic ticket" ("*ticket*")...

— The Rebbe was talented in all areas, and nevertheless did not know how to drive a car, even though he knew other things, like riding a horse and target practice. — Eliyahu Chaim [57] told me that he once traveled with the Rebbe, in the lifetime of his father the Rebbe, and as they passed near a place intended for target practice, he suggested to the Rebbe — he had "breadth" ("*breitkeit*")... — to compete with him in target practice. The Rebbe agreed. And it is amazing — Eliyahu Chaim told — the Rebbe hit the target in every shot, while I, in every shot, missed the target!...

And we return to our subject — "and do not let your anger burn against your servant" — that the content of this request is that Yosef HaTzaddik, the *tzaddik* of the world, should not be aggrieved at him for turning to him and asking him for matters of smallness.

And the reason for the matter (that he should not be aggrieved at him) — "for you are like Pharaoh":

Pharaoh (of *Kedusha*) — refers to Hashem, as is understood from the interpretation of the *Zohar* [58] that the "house of Pharaoh" [59] is "the house from which all lights and all lamps are revealed and shine."

And just as regarding Hashem (Pharaoh of *Kedusha*) it is not possible that His anger should burn and He should be aggrieved, etc., since He is the essence of good and it is the nature of the good to do good [30],

— One of the great elderly Chassidim of our Rebbe the Alter Rebbe, told, that before he became a Chassid, he would think that Hashem is *hard-hearted* (cruel), for, every year we say *Selichos* and ask many requests, and nevertheless... while after he became a Chassid, he began to appreciate the magnitude of the *good-heartedness* of Hashem, that He does not strike him on his mouth or on his head when He sees the manner of his prayer, etc. —

So too with Yosef ("for you are like Pharaoh") it is not possible that his anger should burn and he should be aggrieved, from the side of the nature of the good to do good.

\*

#### 164

**13.** In continuation of what was said regarding strengthening the connection — one should mention again the suggestion [60] that each one "should approach" the Rebbe with a *minyan* of Yidden that he influenced in thought, speech, and action.

— This suggestion comes on the basis of the knowledge that the Rebbe will certainly have *pleasure* from the fact that each one will influence ten Yidden.

And another matter as a foundation for this suggestion:

The Rebbe told [61] about his grandfather (after whom he was named) that he said about himself that his way was to pray with a *minyan*, and when they found him standing in the middle of prayer after all the *minyanim* had finished, and they asked him how is this possible, for this is not prayer in public, he replied, that prayer in public means to gather all ten powers of the soul [62].

And from this it is understood that the public of the ten powers of the soul relates to the spiritual content of ten Yidden. And therefore, when he brings the Rebbe a *minyan* of Yidden, the Rebbe will see to the wholeness of *his* *minyan*, the ten powers of his soul (for "in the measure that a person measures, they measure for him" [63]), *and when the Rebbe* sees to this — it will certainly be in a higher manner.

There are those who initially walked around with "melancholy," because they did not know how they would succeed in obtaining a *minyan* of Yidden, and in the end, they obtained more than a *minyan*, two *minyanim*, and more than that. And in contrast, there are those who are still debating the matter and asking who says that one needs to obtain a *minyan* at all?!...

And the answer to them — that they will not lose anything if they fulfill this suggestion, for in any case: if there is a need for this for the strengthening of the connection — it is certainly good, and even if not — they have not lost anything [64], for, in addition to the fact that one who acts according to the instruction of a *Beis Din* that erred in their instruction is exempt from a sacrifice since he did not act on his own opinion, but as a student who has not reached the level of instruction and relies on the instruction of the *Beis Din* [65], in our case the suggestion itself — to bring a *minyan* of Yidden to the Rebbe — is *certainly good and positive*!

And another advantage in the fulfillment of this suggestion — that for this he will need to act upon himself *a great self-coercion* and obey... (the Rebbe said his holy name)!

And in any case, even if the matter is not accepted by him, he should do it through *kabbalas ol*, and perhaps, etc., and through this he will succeed in all his affairs in physicality and in spirituality.

***

#### 165

**14.** At the end of the *parsha* it is said "And Yisrael settled in the land of Egypt, etc., and they held onto it and were fruitful and multiplied exceedingly."

And its content in *avodah* — that even while they were in the land of Egypt they were not disconnected from the world, but on the contrary, "and they held onto it," and even in this state and situation their *avodah* was in the manner of "and they were fruitful and multiplied exceedingly," that is, not only "and they were fruitful," that one gives birth to one (and at most a male and a female), but also "and they multiplied," that one gives birth to *many* [66], and even in the manner of "exceedingly," "with all your might" [67], *without limit* [68], which is the *avodah* that is from the side of the level of *Yechidah* [69], which generally relates only to the select few.

And the preface to this — "Yosef said... here is seed for you and you shall sow the land" [70]:

"Here is seed for you" — denotes the influence that they receive from Yosef HaTzaddik, including and especially after the passing, as explained in *Iggeres HaKodesh* [71] regarding the matter of "great growth from the light sown for the righteous in the field which Hashem blessed."

"And you shall sow the land" — that one should not be satisfied with the action of Yosef in giving the seed, but there is a need also for the action of each one to take the seed from Yosef and sow it in the land, that is, to implement the giving of strength that they receive from Yosef in *avodah* in practice, and to do this through *bitul* (the content of the matter of sowing), and through desire and joy (the content of the matter of sowing in the land specifically, which is called *eretz* because *ratza* (it wanted) to do the will of its Creator [72]).

And through this it is created — as it is said at the beginning of the *parsha* that follows — "And Yaakov lived in the land of Egypt seventeen years," that also (or specifically) in the land of Egypt it was created "and he lived" ("*gelebt*"), and not just "and he lived" in general, but "seventeen years," in *gematria* *tov* (good) [73].

And the main thing — regarding us — that also from the land of Egypt the Rebbe will take us out [74], and lead us to our holy land, may it be built and established speedily in our days.

\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*

## With the help of Hashem. Sicha of 9 Teves, 5711

#### 166

– After Mincha –

(Unedited)

**A.** A "conclusion" is associated with a sense of joy. In the present context, this refers to the "conclusion" of reciting Kaddish for the eleven months following the passing of my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe [1].

The content of this "conclusion" can be understood by prefacing it with the story regarding the Rebbe (Rashab), who added one extra day to the eleven months of Kaddish, and subsequently felt regret and sorrow over it. From this, one can understand the great precision required in concluding the recitation of Kaddish (not to add even a single day).

Seemingly, this requires explanation:

The reason we stop saying Kaddish after eleven months is that the recitation of Kaddish is intended to assist the soul in the judgment process and to alleviate punishment, etc. Since "the judgment of the wicked lasts twelve months," we say Kaddish for only eleven months, "so as not to render their father and mother wicked" [3]—meaning, that reciting Kaddish for twelve months is a slight to the departed, as it implies they are wicked. However, "one who knows that his father or mother were wicked, such that they would be judged for twelve months, is worthy and obligated to recite Kaddish for twelve months" [4].

Seemingly, since "a good measure is greater than a measure of retribution" [5], just as there is a change in the law regarding Kaddish when "one knows... that they were wicked," there should likewise be a change in the law when one knows that the departed is a tzaddik, and the concept of judgment and punishment does not apply to him at all—that one should not say Kaddish at all?

The explanation for this is based on what is explained in the writings of the Arizal [6], that the recitation of Kaddish is (not only to alleviate judgment and punishment, but also) for the ascent of the soul from level to level within Gan Eden itself. Therefore, we recite Kaddish even on Shabbos, when the reason of alleviating judgment and punishment does not apply, since on Shabbos there is no judgment or trial

#### 167

above. Thus, it must be that the recitation of Kaddish on Shabbos is for the sake of the ascents in Gan Eden. From this, it is also understood regarding the recitation of Kaddish upon the passing of a tzaddik, which is connected with ascents from level to level within Gan Eden itself.

Based on this, we ask the question from the opposite perspective: What is the precision in *stopping* the recitation of Kaddish after eleven months, and being *careful* not to add even one day—to the point that the Rebbe felt *sorrow* over reciting Kaddish for an extra day? Why should the recitation of Kaddish after eleven months be inferior to the recitation of Kaddish on Shabbos, which brings about ascents in Gan Eden?

**B.** The explanation for this is as follows:

There is a difference between the ascents during the eleven months and the ascents thereafter. The ascents during the eleven months are at a level where one can effect change through speech (the recitation of Kaddish). In contrast, the ascents after eleven months are at a much higher level, where it is impossible to effect change through speech, because speech is not commensurate with that level.

An example of this is the difference between the tefillin of the hand and the tefillin of the head. The blessing is recited over the tefillin of the hand, whereas no special blessing is recited over the tefillin of the head, because the drawing down of light through the tefillin of the head is from a much higher level, which cannot be drawn down through speech [7].

Based on this, we can explain why the Rebbe felt sorrow for adding one day of Kaddish: because, in relation to an ascent to a level where speech has no value, the recitation of Kaddish (an ascent effected by speech) is considered a *slight*!

**C.** However, based on what was said—that we do not recite Kaddish after eleven months because the ascents are at a level beyond what can be drawn down by speech—we must understand the reason for reciting Kaddish on the day of the Yahrtzeit?

[It should be noted that there is an opinion not to recite Kaddish on the day of the Yahrtzeit [8], but this opinion was not accepted among the Jewish people, who customarily recite Kaddish on the day of the Yahrtzeit.]

The explanation for this is:

It is known [9] the difference between all the Yomim Tovim and Purim (and Chanukah)—that all Yomim Tovim are forbidden for work because the revelation of Elokus drawn down in them

#### 168

cannot come and be revealed in the mundane activities of the week. In contrast, on Purim (and Chanukah), a *most lofty* light and revelation is drawn down, *which is not limited at all*, and therefore it can be drawn down and revealed even in the mundane activities of the week.

The same applies here:

On the day of the Yahrtzeit, the ascent is to an even higher level (above the ascents after eleven months), to the ultimate level of elevation. As is known, on the day of the Yahrtzeit, all the matters of the day (and moment) of the passing are reawakened, at which time "all his deeds, his Torah, and his avodah that he performed all the days of his life" are elevated to the ultimate level [10]. As explained in the Siddur, Shaar Lag B'Omer [11], the ascent is "to the beginning and head of all his levels... the root of his root in the highest heights, at the most elevated level."

And because of the greatness of the ascent to the *most lofty* level, it is drawn down and revealed *below*—as explained in the Siddur there, that "the most lofty light can only be revealed in the lowest place." This is the concept of Lag B'Omer, which "is the lowest level... Hod sheb'Hod... and in it specifically is rooted the aspect of the most primary, etc."

It can be said that this matter is emphasized most strongly in a tzaddik, whose entire life was occupied with drawing down the most lofty matters even into the most simple things.

Based on this, we can explain the reason for reciting Kaddish on the day of the Yahrtzeit: because the ascent to the most lofty level, which is drawn down and revealed below, is also effected by the action of those below, which is the concept of reciting Kaddish through speech.

**D.** Thus, it turns out that the time after eleven months and before the Yahrtzeit (the twelfth month) is an *intermediate* time:

The soul's ascents during this time are above the level of speech (unlike the ascents of the eleven months of Kaddish, which are effected by speech). However, it is not yet so exceedingly high that the ascent can be effected by speech below (unlike the ascents of the Yahrtzeit, which, due to their great level, are effected by speech below).

It can be said that this matter applies (not only regarding the effect of the soul's ascent through speech below, but) also regarding the revelation and drawing down below—that during this (intermediate) time, the primary drawing down is regarding spiritual matters, ahavah and yirah, etc., and not so much regarding physical matters.

However, the aforementioned distinctions regarding the effect of speech concern the *mashpia*.

#### 169

But regarding the *mekablim*, even during the intermediate time when they cannot effect change through speech (reciting Kaddish), they must create "vessels" to receive all the influences: the influences drawn down during the eleven months, the influences after the eleven months until the Yahrtzeit, and the influences on the Yahrtzeit and throughout all the time thereafter.

**E.** There are those who ask: Who is capable of accompanying and "running" after the Rebbe in his ascents, from elevation to elevation?!

As we see in the physical world—if a person walks slowly, one can accompany him and walk with him. But when he begins to walk quickly, one must exert effort to keep up with him. When he begins to run, one needs even greater effort, and when he increases his speed, one needs the greatest strength to run after him.

The analogy is similar regarding walking in the Rebbe's ways: If, during his lifetime in this world, one could not accompany and "run" after him—after his passing, when he is not limited by the constraints of the body [12], it is all the more impossible to accompany and "run" after him.

The answer to this is based on the saying of our Sages [13], "A person sanctifies himself *a little below*, and they sanctify him *a lot from above*" [14]:

Here below, a little is sufficient to receive a lot from above, as explained in Iggeres HaTeshuvah [15] with the analogy of "the movement and displacement of a shadow on the ground by a handbreadth, corresponding to the movement of the sun's sphere in the firmament by thousands of miles."

From this, it is also understood regarding walking in the Rebbe's ways—that when one walks a little in his avodah below ("sanctifies himself a little below," including also the "below" of the person), then they give him from above lofty powers ("they sanctify him a lot from above") to accompany the Rebbe in his ascents above, and to receive all the influences that are drawn down from above.

## B’s”d. Sicha of 24 Teves, 5711

#### 170

*Unedited*

**A.** The Rebbe, my father-in-law, exerted great effort in strengthening and disseminating the *takanah* of the Alter Rebbe regarding the *chalukas haShas* (the division of the Talmud for communal study)[1](#_ftn924). He related[2](#_ftn925) that it was once customary to organize the *chalukas haShas* on 19 Kislev, but from the year 5663 onwards, it was organized on 24 Teves, due to the lack of time on 19 Kislev.

One can explain the connection and affinity between 19 Kislev and 24 Teves: in both instances, there was an event of liberation from imprisonment. On 19 Kislev, it was the release from the imprisonment in Petersburg, and on 24 Teves, it was the soul’s release from the "imprisonment" of the body.

The *chalukas haShas* itself is organized (not on the night of 24 Teves, but) on the evening of 24 Teves. This is because, before beginning a new *chalukas haShas*, one must complete the study of the *Shas* that was divided the previous year. Since it is possible that there are those who did not manage to finish the tractate that fell to their share—a matter that could cause a deficiency and loss, *chas v’shalom* (not only regarding their own study, but) also regarding the overall study of all those participating in the *chalukas haShas*—we therefore grant them another 24 hours to complete the study, and postpone the new *chalukas haShas* for the coming year, which is approaching us and all of Israel for good, *amen*, until the evening of the day.

According to the Jewish custom at the conclusion of a tractate (and all the more so in this case—the conclusion of all the tractates in the *Shas*), one says "Hadran." Therefore, I will now say "Hadran" (before or after the *chalukas haShas*).

Last year, too, a *siyum* was held and I said "Hadran"[3](#_ftn926). At the *siyum* this year, I will say the "Hadran" (not in the manner it was said then, but) in a different way, lest there be those who remember the "Hadran" that was said last year. (He added with a smile:) Furthermore, it is possible that the points made in that "Hadran" could be refuted; therefore, it is not worthwhile to say the same "Hadran" that was said last year, as that would mean taking a "risk" on both

#### 171

"Hadranim" (of the two years). Thus, I will say a different "Hadran," so the risk is only regarding one "Hadran."

**B.** The *chalukas haShas* was organized, and in the middle of the distribution, the Rebbe *shlita* said:

In organizing the *chalukas haShas*, one must strive not only for *all the tractates* (to divide all the tractates of the *Shas*), but also for *all the people*—that everyone should participate in the division and study of the *Shas*[4](#_ftn927).

**C.** Regarding the "Hadran" for the conclusion of the *chalukas haShas*: As we stand in the year of the *histalkus* (passing), in proximity to the *yahrzeit*, we will dwell (not on the conclusion of the *Shas* itself, but) on a matter related to *histalkus* in one of the final *sugyos* at the end of *Maseches Niddah*[5](#_ftn928): "The Sages taught: The people of Alexandria asked Rabbi Yehoshua ben Chananya twelve questions: three of wisdom (halacha), three of *aggadah*, three of ignorance, and three of worldly conduct." Further on in the *sugya*[6](#_ftn929), the Gemara details the three questions of ignorance: "Is Lot’s wife susceptible to ritual impurity? He said to them: A corpse imparts impurity, but a pillar of salt does not impart impurity. Is the son of the Shunammite susceptible to impurity? He said to them: A corpse imparts impurity, but a living person does not impart impurity. Do the dead in the future need sprinkling on the third and seventh days, or do they not need it? He said to them: When they return to life, we will deliberate on it; some say: When Moshe Rabbeinu comes with them"—all of which relate to the matter of *histalkus*.

The reason I wish to say the "Hadran" on a subject related to *histalkus*, even though on the face of it there is no connection between the conclusion of the *chalukas haShas* and the matter of *histalkus*, is because the *histalkus* of the Rebbe permeates the entire existence of a Chossid, all of his 248 limbs, and consequently, this is expressed and evident in all his affairs.

The Rebbe, my father-in-law, related[7](#_ftn930) that his father, the Rebbe Rashab, interpreted the verse[8](#_ftn931), "*Ekev* (because/heel) that Avraham listened to My voice," to mean that the greatness of Avraham Avinu was evident not only in his mind and heart (intellect and emotion), but also in his hands and feet (the vessels of action), even

#### 172

to the *heel* of the foot, that even in the heel of the foot it was evident that this was the "heel" of Avraham. It should be noted that this is the content of the ruling of the Rambam[9](#_ftn932): "Just as a wise man is recognized by his wisdom and his opinions... so too must he be recognized by his deeds, his eating and drinking, etc., his walking, etc.," even in the most external matters. The Rebbe Rashab concluded that this is also true regarding a Chossid: the matter of Chassidus must be evident in his entire existence, down to the heel of the foot—"*a Chassidishe pyate*."

The same applies in this case: if the matter of the *histalkus* is evident only in the feeling of the heart or the understanding of the mind, but in matters of action there is no discernible change between the current state (after the *histalkus*) and the state in the years prior, this is proof that the matter of the *histalkus* has not permeated all 248 of his limbs, and the seal of the *histalkus* is not upon him. The matter of the *histalkus* must be permeated throughout his entire existence, and consequently, it must be evident in all matters.

**D.** The "Hadran" is printed in *Reshimot*, booklet 129[10](#_ftn933), and in *Likkutei Sichos*, Vol. 18, p. 239 and onwards.

At the beginning of his remarks, the Rebbe *shlita* prefaced that although there is a distinction between *halacha* and *aggadah*, to the extent that it is said in the *Yerushalmi*[11](#_ftn934) that "one does not derive *halacha* from *aggadah*," this rule applies only where the lesson from *aggadah* contradicts what is explicitly stated in the *halachic* portion. However, where the *aggados* do not contradict the *halachic* portion, one learns from them and relies upon them[12](#_ftn935). Moreover, even where there is a contradiction from the *halachic* portion, one does not derive *halacha l'maaseh* from *aggadah*, but one can certainly derive a *sevara* (logical reasoning) from *aggadah* even where there is a contradiction from the *halachic* portion. Proof of this is that we find that one derives a *sevara* even from the opinion of an individual, even though the majority disagrees with him[13](#_ftn936). Certainly, one can derive a *sevara* from *aggadah*, which is an entire section of Torah! All the more so regarding deriving a *sevara* alone, and in a place where there is no contradiction from the *halachic* portion—one certainly learns from *aggadah*.

And at the conclusion of the matter, he said:

What was said above (in the "Hadran") that "(a corpse imparts impurity, but) the corpse itself is not impure"[14](#_ftn937), which was said regarding all of Israel, is emphasized even more in the case of a *Tzaddik* and *Nasi* of Israel, who does not

#### 173

impart impurity, according to the ruling of R. Chaim Cohen[15](#_ftn938), who "used to say: If I had been present when Rabbeinu Tam passed away, I would have imparted impurity to him." This is especially true regarding a *Nasi*, to whom "everything imparts impurity"[16](#_ftn939), and as is the Jewish custom that even *Kohanim* prostrate themselves at the graves of *Tzaddikim* because *Tzaddikim* do not impart impurity.

[And although there is a debate regarding the words of Rabbeinu Chaim[17](#_ftn940]—this is only according to the *nigleh* (revealed) aspect of Torah, i.e., at the level of Torah as it is clothed in the world, from the word *he'elem* (concealment)[18](#_ftn941). This is not the case according to the *pnimiyus* (inner) aspect of Torah, the Tree of Life, etc.[19](#_ftn942). Especially since even according to the *nigleh* aspect of Torah, there are proofs and supports for the fact that *Tzaddikim* do not impart impurity.]

Not only do they not impart impurity, but on the contrary, through them, an addition and elevation in purity and holiness is brought about, etc.

\*\*\*

**E.** It was discussed above[20](#_ftn943) that regarding the ascent of the soul after *histalkus*, there are two times of ascent: (a) the ascent of the soul during the eleven months, (b) the ascent of the soul on the day of the *yahrzeit* (when a greater ascent occurs, which is why it is customary to receive an *aliyah* to the Torah, etc.). There is the intermediate time between them, in which we stand now, after the completion of the eleven months and before the *yahrzeit*.

According to the well-known saying that for Jews it is never too late[21](#_ftn944), one can still complete all the matters of *avodah*—the study of his Torah and walking in his ways—that should have been done during the eleven months. Thus, approaching the *yahrzeit*, in about two weeks, all the matters that the Rebbe wanted, wants now, and gives the strength to bring from potential into action, will be completed.

And when one completes, in anticipation of the *yahrzeit*, all the matters of *avodah*—the study of his Torah and walking in his ways—then one will receive the reward alluded to in the conclusion of the *Shas*: "Whoever studies *halachos*... is guaranteed that he is a son of the World to Come, for it is said[22](#_ftn945), 'The *halichos* (ways) of the world are His'; do not read *halichos* but *halachos*."

By prefacing the well-known rule[23](#_ftn946) that the teaching of "do not read... but..." does not

#### 174

negate the simple meaning, but rather adds another meaning to it. Thus, both meanings—*halichos* and *halachos*—exist together. That is to say, even in the "ways of the world" (*halichos olam*—while walking in the world), one is "studying *halachos*," through the fact that the *halachos* are engraved in the memory of the mind. Then, "even at a time when he is not engaged in Torah... the Holy One, Blessed be He, dwells within him, even when he is engaged in worldly matters ('*halichos olam*'), since the Torah is engraved in the memory of the mind," as explained in *Likkutei Torah*[24](#_ftn947).

The same applies regarding the study of the Rebbe’s Torah: when his words of Torah are engraved in the memory of the mind, one is in constant *hiskashrus* (connection) (even at a time when he is not engaged in Torah), and in the words of *Likkutei Torah*[24](#_ftn947): "without any interruption or separation ever, even for a single moment"[25](#_ftn948).

And then, "he is guaranteed—they guarantee him with a complete guarantee—that he is a son of the World to Come." One can say the meaning of this is that in this world itself[26](#_ftn949), he is a "son of the World to Come," similar to the saying of our Sages[27](#_ftn950), "You shall see your world in your lifetime." That is, all concealments and hiddenness are nullified, and he merits to see the Rebbe (not only as he "stands and serves on high"[28](#_ftn951), but) also in his coming to this physical world, and in the words of the Gemara (above in the "Hadran"), "that Moshe Rabbeinu—including also the Moshe Rabbeinu of our generation—will come with them."

\*\*\*

**F.** I wish to tell two stories regarding the conduct of our Rebbes, the *Nesi'im*[29](#_ftn952), who placed themselves in mortal danger for the sake of the entirety of Israel, even in situations where, according to *din* (law), the conduct could have been different:

Once[30](#_ftn953), the Rebbe, my father-in-law, traveled to Petersburg to exert effort to annul a decree that was about to be enacted against the Children of Israel in that country. After efforts, he succeeded in obtaining an interview with the minister in charge of this matter (through the efforts of one of the minister's acquaintances), who scheduled the time of the interview for the night of

#### 175

Shabbos. The minister’s residence was in a suburb of Petersburg, outside the *techum Shabbos* (Sabbath boundary). Therefore, the Rebbe, my father-in-law, traveled early to the suburb on Erev Shabbos. Since no Jew lived in the vicinity, he was forced to enter and stay for the entire Shabbos (before the time of the interview and after it) in a tavern, among drunkards and thieves, in a state of *sakonas nefashos* (mortal danger). There he davened, made Kiddush, etc., and from there he went to the minister’s palace, accompanied by the innkeeper who agreed to escort him to the gate of the palace, but not into the palace courtyard, which was a place of danger because of the large dogs that roamed there. Nor did he accompany him on the return trip, so he had to walk alone at night, in the great cold, etc.—even though, according to *din*, it would have been permitted for him to desecrate the Shabbos for the interview with the minister, since it was a matter of *pikuach nefesh* (saving lives) for all the Children of Israel in that country. Thus, he could have spent Shabbos in Petersburg and traveled to the minister on Shabbos, and he would not have needed to spend Shabbos in the tavern with all the dangers involved.

Likewise, there is a story regarding the Alter Rebbe, who placed himself in danger in a situation where, according to *din*, he could have acted differently[31](#_ftn954).

\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*

## Sicha of Shabbos Parshas Va’era, Mevarchim HaChodesh Shevat, 5711

#### 176

**1.** Our Parsha begins as a continuation of the previous Parsha (Parshas Shemos), which concludes with Moshe Rabbeinu’s question to Hashem: "Why have You brought evil upon this people? Why have You sent me?"[1](#_ftn955) Following this, Hashem’s response to Moshe comes at the beginning of our Parsha:[2](#_ftn956) "And Elokim spoke to Moshe and said to him, 'I am Havayah. I appeared to Avraham, to Yitzchak, and to Yaakov as Kel Shad-ai, but by My name Havayah I was not known to them... Therefore, say to the Children of Israel: I am Havayah, and I will take you out from under the burdens of Mitzrayim... and I will take you to Me as a people... and you shall know that I am Havayah.'"

It is explained in *Torah Or*[3](#_ftn957) that the name Havayah (which was not revealed to the Patriarchs) was revealed at the Giving of the Torah. In order for this revelation—"and you shall know that I am Havayah"—to be possible, the preparation of the exile of Mitzrayim, "the evil brought upon this people," was necessary.

It concludes there[4](#_ftn958) that this is also the reason for the length of the final exile—that it is the preparation for the revelations of the time to come.[5](#_ftn959)

**2.** Now, *every* matter in the Torah is true and eternal. From this it is understood that a question in the Torah, even if it has an answer, still leaves room for the question.

—Just as the Rebbe Rayatz once said at a *farbrengen* on Shavuos[6](#_ftn960) regarding the question in Chassidus[7](#_ftn961) as to why Simchas Torah was not established on Shavuos, the "time of the giving of our Torah": since this question is written in the Torah, then even though there is an answer to it, there is still room to say that Simchas Torah should be on Shavuos.—

Likewise in our case: since the question "Why have You brought evil..." is written in the Torah,

#### 177

then even after the answer of "And I appeared...", there is still room for the challenge "Why have You brought evil?"

**3.** One of the reasons for this is:

Although the servitude of exile is necessary because it is a preparation for the revelations of the future, nevertheless, it could have been replaced by spiritual servitude.

As explained in *Torah Or*[8](#_ftn962), all the details of the servitude—"And they embittered their lives with hard labor, with mortar and with bricks, and with all manner of labor in the field"[9](#_ftn963)—are explained in spirituality: "'And they embittered their lives'—this is Torah, for it is our life; 'with hard labor'—this is a *kushya* (difficulty); 'with mortar'—this is a *kal v'chomer*; 'and with all manner of labor in the field'—this is a *baraisa*; 'and with bricks'—this is *libun hilchasa* (clarifying the law),"[10](#_ftn964) see there at length.

**4.** Just as the matter of exile in its literal sense can be replaced by matters of spirituality, so too, the toil and preoccupation of *parnassah* (which is the essence of the matter of exile[11](#_ftn965)) can be replaced by toil and preoccupation in Torah.[12](#_ftn966)

The essence of the preoccupation of *parnassah* is—"Many are the thoughts in a man's heart,"[13](#_ftn967) to the point that he does not know what to do. This matter can be replaced by toil and preoccupation in Torah—to toil in Torah until one has a *sevara* (logical argument) for one side and a *sevara* for the other, and cannot decide between them, which is extremely tiring and preoccupying.[14](#_ftn968)

—The Rogatchover Gaon[15](#_ftn969) once said that for him, the hardest day of the week is Shabbos. During the week, when his intellectual flow is at its peak

#### 178

and *sevaros* for one side and the other arise, he has a solution—writing, because the letters of writing limit the flow of the intellect, and then it is easier to decide. Not so on Shabbos, since he does not have this solution, he is forced to toil more until he can decide.

Similarly, it is told[16](#_ftn970) that when the Mitteler Rebbe would say Chassidus, there was absolute silence,[17](#_ftn971) and nevertheless, he would sometimes say (while saying Chassidus): "Sha, sha." The Rebbe (Rashab) explained that this was to quiet the flow of intellect from the brain.

Seemingly, what is the need to quiet the flow of the *mochin*?

It can be understood based on what was said above—because from the flow of the *mochin* it is difficult to stop and decide definitively. Immediately, an extra depth comes that brings an opposing *sevara*—like the usual style in the Mitteler Rebbe’s *maamarim*: "Not as stated above."

**5.** Now, one of the main matters of the servitude of Mitzrayim[18](#_ftn972) is—"*avodas parech*" (backbreaking labor).

The meaning of *avodas parech* is—as it is in the Gemara,[19](#_ftn973) "that they would exchange... women's work for men's," "and this is difficult, for they were not accustomed to it."

And the matter of *avodas parech* also needs to be exchanged so that it is in spirituality—meaning, that the work in Torah and *mitzvos* must be more than one's habit.

And just as in *avodas parech* in the physical sense, women's work is easier than men's work, for "it is the way of a man to conquer, and it is not the way of a woman to conquer,"[20](#_ftn974) and nevertheless, since they are not accustomed to it, it is *avodas parech*—so too in spirituality, the work itself can be a small thing ("a *kleinigkeit*"), but since for it one must change one's habit, it is a replacement for *avodas parech* in the physical sense.

#### 179

As explained in *Tanya*[21](#_ftn975) regarding the reason for the words of the Gemara[22](#_ftn976) that one who reviews his chapter one hundred times alone is called "one who has not served,"[23](#_ftn977) and one who reviews his chapter one hundred and one times is "a servant of G-d"[22](#_ftn976)—that even though this is only an advantage of *one* time, nevertheless, since there is in this a change of nature, "because in their days the custom was to review every chapter one hundred times," therefore he is called "a servant of G-d" (and through this he reaches the level of the *yechidah* in the soul: one hundred times—ten powers included in ten; one hundred and one times—the level of *yechidah*, whose essence above is the level of *Keter*[24](#_ftn978)).

**6.** And another detail in this:

Not only is it that even through easy work, because it is a change of habit, it is a replacement for *avodas parech* in the physical sense, and he is called "a servant of G-d,"

but more than this: even when the aforementioned change of habit is not internal—meaning, that internally he remains in his previous habit, and it is only that he forces himself against his will—even then he has the merit of "a servant of G-d."

The reason for this is—because the inner will of a Jew is good, only that the *yetzer hara* forces him, and for this, even coercion against his will is sufficient.[25](#_ftn979)

**7.** Based on this, it will also be understood why the Alter Rebbe brings in *Tanya* the parable of the Gemara "from the market of donkey drivers who are hired for ten *parsah* for a *zuz*, and for eleven *parsah* for two *zuzim* because it is more than their habit":

Seemingly, it is not understood: why is it necessary to bring in *Tanya* the parable of the "donkey drivers"—he should have brought only the words of the Gemara regarding the merit of one who reviews his chapter one hundred and one times? It must be that the parable of the "donkey drivers" also relates to the understanding of the matter of changing habit explained in *Tanya*.

It will be understood by prefacing the well-known fact that in a parable in the Torah, all the details of the parable correspond to the *nimshal* (the concept being taught), because the parable evolved from the *nimshal*, and therefore all the details must correspond.[26](#_ftn980)

And likewise in the above: "Donkey" (*chamor*)—is called the body. And they demand of a Jew "you shall surely help with him,"[27](#_ftn981) meaning, not to suffice with work that belongs to the soul alone, but to refine the body as well.

#### 180

And there are two ways in this:

a) To act upon the body so that it ceases to be a donkey ("make the body *ois chamor*"), to make it a "*medaber*" (a speaker)—*at-hafocha* (transformation).

—The story is known[28](#_ftn982) that when the Alter Rebbe was about to travel from Mezritch to his home, the Holy Rabbi, the Rav HaMalach (son of the Maggid of Mezritch), went to accompany him, and the Malach said to the wagon driver: "One must whip the horses" ("*m'darf shmeissen di ferd*") so that they cease to be horses ("*di ferd zolen vern ois ferd*"), and another version: that the horses should know that they are horses ("*di ferd zolen visen az zei zeinen ferd*"). And the Alter Rebbe said that a path in the service of Hashem was added for him, and he delayed his trip and remained for some time longer in Mezritch.—

b) While it is in its essence as it is, he will force himself and change his habit—*iskafya* (coercion). And also through the way of *iskafya*, he is called "a servant of G-d."

And this matter is hinted at in the details of the parable from the market of donkey drivers:

The donkey—he did not buy, meaning, that the donkey did not become his (and in the *nimshal* this is *at-hafocha*), but only hired, and this means that the donkey remained in its previous ownership,[29](#_ftn983) and nevertheless, he does not take into account its habit to walk only ten *parsah*, but works with it more than its habit.

And likewise in spirituality, that even though the body is in its material state as it is, nevertheless, through this that he forces the materiality of the body against its will at least, he is "a servant of G-d."

**8.** And in our times, the *ikvesa d'meshicha* (the footsteps of Moshiach), it is emphasized most strongly that the matter of *avodas parech* in spirituality (through which one merits the revelations of the future) is done through changing the habit even in easy work, a small thing:

They do not demand "great things" from us. The great matters, the refining of the great sparks,[30](#_ftn984) were already accomplished by the work of the Children of Israel in the earlier generations who were on a higher level,

—And in the language of Rashi at the beginning of our Parsha: "That I spoke to the first Patriarchs," it can be said that Rashi’s intention with the word "first" (a word seemingly superfluous) is not only to the "first" in time, but also to the "first" *in merit*, and because of

#### 181

the greatness of their merit they were able to accomplish the great matters, the refining of the great sparks—

While in our generation, the generation of the *ikvesa d'meshicha*, and even to the *ikvesa d'ikvesa d'meshicha* [for in the heel itself there is a depiction of a stature], only small matters remain, small sparks that need to be refined, meaning, that they demand of us matters that in themselves are easy matters, but, these easy matters were given *in a difficult time*, because of the greatness of the concealment and the darkness, double and redoubled, that is in the *ikvesa d'meshicha*.

—Matters that in themselves are great, who knows if we could accomplish in such a difficult time; and therefore they left us only matters that in themselves are easy, but the work in them is in a difficult time.

Only easy matters remain, "small vessels" (*pachim ketanim*)—by *kal v'chomer* from that which we find in Yaakov that "he remained for small vessels and returned for them,"[31](#_ftn985)

[for "the Torah is concerned for the property of Israel,"[32](#_ftn986) even for (small vessels of) earthenware, as it is written in *Negai Batim* (plagues of houses)[33](#_ftn987) "And the Kohen shall command, and they shall clear the house before the Kohen comes to see the plague, so that all that is in the house will not become impure," "For what was the Torah concerned? If for vessels of metal, he can immerse them and they will become pure; and if for food and drink, he can eat them in his days of impurity. The Torah was concerned only for earthenware vessels which have no purification in a *mikveh*."[34](#_ftn988) And to add, that even earthenware vessels which have no purification in a *mikveh* are fit for use in his days of impurity, but he cannot use them in his days of purity, and for this alone the Torah finds a solution to clear the house before the Kohen comes],

and it is explained there[35](#_ftn989) that Yaakov was ready for the coming of Moshiach, but the matter was delayed because of "small vessels";

and all the more so in our time, the *ikvesa d'meshicha*, after "all the *kitzin* (appointed times) have passed,"[36](#_ftn990) including also the *kitzin* that were said for several years in the most recent generations,

—I received a book of Chassidus from Eretz Yisrael, and in one of the *maamarim* it says a "*ketz*" for the year 5638.[37](#_ftn991) And similarly regarding the year 5666, as the

#### 182

Rebbe Rayatz told[38](#_ftn992) that on Rosh Hashanah 5666 his father, the Rebbe Rashab, said that he is afraid of this year because it has a "*ketz*" (in addition to it being the year after a leap year[39](#_ftn993))—

And in addition to all the *kitzin*, all the decrees and destructions have also passed, G-d forbid—then certainly the time for the coming of Moshiach has already arrived, but we need to complete the "small vessels," meaning, matters such that the work in them is *easy*, but there is a need for *a change of habit*.

**9.** And this matter is also emphasized in that the preparation for the coming of Moshiach is through the work of *teshuvah*—"The Torah promised that in the end of their exile, Israel will do *teshuvah* and immediately they will be redeemed,"[40](#_ftn994) "Moshiach comes to bring the righteous to *teshuvah*":[41](#_ftn995)

*Teshuvah*—is not fasts and afflictions (or giving *tzedakah* in place of fasting), and also not saying *vidui* (confession), but "that the sinner should abandon his sin... and resolve in his heart that he will not do it again,"[42](#_ftn996) and as the Alter Rebbe writes in *Iggeret HaTeshuvah*[43](#_ftn997) that "the *mitzvah* of *teshuvah* from the Torah is the abandonment of the sin alone... that he should resolve in his heart with a whole heart not to return to folly again," which this matter can be also on the day of Shabbos, when it is forbidden to fast and to say *vidui*.

And it is found that the essence of the matter of *teshuvah* is *a change of habit*, that "he changes his deeds,"[44](#_ftn998) to the point that "it is a complete sin to say to a *baal teshuvah* 'remember your former deeds',"[45](#_ftn999) since he changed his habit to separate from them.

And therefore, for the work of *teshuvah* there is no need for a lot of time, but also in a little time, and also in a very little time that is not enough even for saying "Al Cheit" or other *viduim*, one can do *teshuvah* [and as we find in the writing of a *get* (divorce document) that they give a little time to the witnesses signing the *get* to contemplate *teshuvah*],[46](#_ftn1000) since the essence of *teshuvah* is that he resolves in his heart, etc., and this matter can be also in a little time, "in one hour and in one moment."[47](#_ftn1001)

#### 183

—The Rebbe Rashab once visited the country of Germany (*Deutschland*), and before his departure from there, several of the Jews of Germany accompanied him to the train station, and as the time of the train's departure approached, saying to the Rebbe that there was only one moment left for the train's departure, the Rebbe replied and said: In one moment—one can still do *teshuvah*.[48](#_ftn1002)

However, in this little time, "one moment," there must be a change of habit (similar to what was said above that even easy work is sufficient, but it must be in a way of a change of habit).

And it can be said that it is also hinted at in the language "in one hour and in one moment"—that "in one moment," a *little* time, there can and must be "one hour," an hour from the word *hifneh* (turning), "a turn,"[49](#_ftn1003) which is the content of the matter of changing habit even in a small thing.

***

**10.** What was said above regarding the change of habit also applies regarding the connection to the Rebbe:

We stand in proximity to the day of the *yahrzeit*, on which a very great ascent occurs for the Rebbe, and consequently, also for those connected to him, as his promise[50](#_ftn1004) that the leaders of Israel will not separate from their flock.

However, for this, a preparation and a vessel is needed—the work of *teshuvah*—a change of habit, through which one ascends with the Rebbe in all his ascents, and furthermore, and essentially, that this is the preparation for the most essential ascent—the coming of Moshiach.

**11.** And similarly regarding the fulfillment of the Rebbe’s blessings and promises, that the vessel for this is the change of habit—and by way of introduction:

The Rebbe once said about himself that he was always a debtor, but, he never went bankrupt ("*er hot keinmol nit bankruptirt*").[51](#_ftn1005) And seemingly, this is a contradiction: since he never went bankrupt, it must be that he paid his debts, and if so, how was he always a debtor?—But the meaning is that with the Rebbe there was always the order that before he paid the previous debts, he took upon himself new debts, greater ones, from other people,

#### 184

and not only that, but even those to whom he returned the old debts came of their own accord and offered to lend him more, so that both things are true, that he never went bankrupt, G-d forbid, and together with this, he was always a debtor, since he took upon himself more obligations.

And regarding our matter:

Since the Rebbe never went bankrupt, G-d forbid, one must know that all the blessings and promises of the Rebbe—the "debts" he took upon himself—will certainly be fulfilled in practice. All those whom the Rebbe blessed with children, life, and ample sustenance, and also those whom the Rebbe blessed that Hashem should provide them with suitable *shidduchim*—will certainly receive the blessings in their fullness.

But, there is a need for making vessels. The influences of the Rebbe exist, but one must make vessels to receive the influences.

And the vessel for receiving the influence of the Rebbe is, as mentioned, a change of habit, and through this one merits receiving the Rebbe’s blessings in all that is needed, children, life, and ample sustenance.

**12.** The influence of the Rebbe in the last year[52](#_ftn1006) was in a way that the Rebbe showed *many miracles*, but there are those who wanted to see this, and indeed saw, and those who did not want to, did not see.—The miracles were there, but they did not see them, similar to the saying of our Sages[53](#_ftn1007) "even the master of the miracle does not recognize his miracle."

And for example:[54](#_ftn1008)

An *avreich* (young married man) comes in and asks about obtaining a certain position, and they answer him—the Rebbe’s answer—that when he receives the position he should give to *tzedakah* a large sum that in his opinion is too much [and in the style mentioned—more than his habit, meaning, that the size of the sum does not matter so much, but rather, that it should be more than his habit].—At the time, I saw that he was not ready for this. A few weeks ago I met the aforementioned *avreich*, and I asked him what is happening regarding receiving the aforementioned position, and he answered me: The owner is not ready yet.

The truth is that if the aforementioned *avreich* was already supposed to receive this position, it is impossible that the matter would be delayed by the owner, because, even if the owner is a Jew with

#### 185

free choice, he does not have free choice regarding the *parnassah* of so-and-so.[55](#_ftn1009) And it must be that *he himself* (the *avreich*) *is not ready* to receive this position, since he did not take upon himself to fulfill the Rebbe’s instruction!

However, since the Rebbe is the ultimate of goodness and kindness,

—as is known[56](#_ftn1010) that when the Rebbe received the leadership from his father, the Rebbe Rayatz, he asked that his leadership should be in kindness and mercy—

therefore, even though he is not yet ready to fulfill the instruction, not only is he not angry at him,

—not only because of the severity of the matter of anger more than all other matters [as is known that anger blemishes the essence of the soul, as our Sages said[57](#_ftn1011) "everyone who is angry, his soul departs from him," and this is the reason that through anger one can forget the laws of the Torah[58](#_ftn1012) (which are the ultimate truth[59](#_ftn1013)), since his soul departs from him], but because he is the ultimate of goodness and kindness, *the matter of anger does not apply to him*—

but on the contrary, he waits and expects that perhaps finally he will be ready to accept the instruction, and helps him in this by *showing him with his finger* that "the owner is not ready yet," so that he will understand *that he*—who should be the owner over the materiality of the body—is not ready yet!

And another example[60](#_ftn1014)—more prominent:

An *avreich* comes in and complains about stones [not precious stones... but stones] that entered where they don't belong—in the kidneys, and the doctor said that he needs to do this and that. And when they tell him not to be impressed by the doctor's words, he goes and turns to another doctor whose opinion is like the first doctor, and he already decides to do as the doctor says, but he cannot find the doctor since he traveled from his home for a while, and in the meantime, the stones came out of the kidneys by themselves!—*A revealed miracle*!...

[The Rebbe Shlita said that certainly the aforementioned *avreichim* will not be offended by the fact that they are being rebuked. And he told that Chanie[61](#_ftn1015) used to say that when he wants

#### 186

to rebuke ("*oisreiden*") someone, he does it after a little *mashke* ("*bei a bissel mashke*"), so that they cannot come to him with complaints, since he can excuse that the words were said under the influence of the *mashke*...].

**13.** This matter that the seeing of miracles depends on the person himself (as mentioned that those who wanted to see saw)—should be explained according to the matter of its example explained in the *maamar* "Zachor Es Yom HaShabbos" 5626 by the Rebbe Maharash:[62](#_ftn1016)

And by way of introduction—this *maamar* is one of the first *maamarim* of the Rebbe Maharash that he said in the lifetime of his father, the Tzemach Tzedek, as is known[63](#_ftn1017) that the Rebbe Maharash began to say *Chassidus* in public in the lifetime of his father the Tzemach Tzedek, who wrote him[64](#_ftn1018) a letter of rabbinate: "I saw your *Chassidus* and it was very pleasing to me." And to note that the desire of the Rebbe Rayatz was to publish the *maamarim* of his grandfather the Rebbe Maharash, and in order, meaning, from when he began to say *Chassidus*, including also the first *maamarim* that he said in the lifetime of the Tzemach Tzedek.

In this *maamar*, it brings the saying of our Sages[65](#_ftn1019) on the verse[66](#_ftn1020) "And He placed him in the Garden of Eden to work it and to guard it," "'To work it'—six days you shall work; 'and to guard it'—guard the day of Shabbos," and he asks, "Is 'to work it' in the Garden of Eden not a command, like 'to work it' is the 248 positive *mitzvos*,[67](#_ftn1021) through which one works and draws down additional light in the Garden of Eden, and 'six days you shall work' is not a command at all?"

And in a slightly different style: since "to work it" is said regarding the Garden of Eden, this is certainly work in matters of *holiness*, and especially according to the interpretation of our Sages "to work it—this is the 248 positive *mitzvos*," the performance of the *mitzvos*; while "to work it—six days you shall work," refers to the work of the weekdays in *work of the mundane*?

And he explains that from the side of creation all matters were in a way of holiness, and "had Adam HaRishon not sinned, there would be no mundane, for it is said 'And He placed him in the Garden of Eden, etc.', and only through the sin, and it is written[68](#_ftn1022) 'also the world He gave in their heart,' and therefore when man became mundane, the days of the week also became mundane... and for this is the work of man to fix the days of the week, etc."

And similarly regarding the private work of each and every Jew, who is called

#### 187

an "entire world" (*olam katan*)[69](#_ftn1023)—that one must know that all matters in themselves are matters of holiness, and the matter depends only on his conduct, that when his conduct is as it should be, then all his matters are matters of holiness, and consequently, all matters are done easily, without concealments and hiding, since they are completely nullified before the holiness [as explained in *Tanya*[70](#_ftn1024) that "all the *kelipos* are null and void and were as if they were not at all before Hashem, as it is written, etc.," and he brings four verses, against the three impure *kelipos* and *kelipat nogah*[71](#_ftn1025)]; and when his conduct is not as it should be, then his matters become mundane work.

And from this it is also understood regarding the matter of miracles—conduct of holiness in relation to conduct in the way of nature—that even when there are miracles one can relate to them as he wishes: when he wants to—he sees miracles, and if not—he looks at them as events that happen in the way of nature, in the category of "the master of the miracle does not recognize his miracle."

**14.** And it should be added that these miracles that do not come immediately in revelation—which is why one can relate to them as natural events—are drawn from a higher level:

And by way of introduction to what is explained in the aforementioned *maamar* "that there are two levels, the first is the order of *hishtalshelus* (evolution), and the second is that which is above *hishtalshelus*... and as it is written in another place[72](#_ftn1026) the difference between the Cause of Causes and the Reason of Reasons, that the source of the *hishtalshelus* of the worlds is called the Cause of Causes, and its root is from the *Kav* (line) and thread and is called *Memale Kol Almin* (filling all worlds), but the Reason of Reasons is the source of the light of *Sovev Kol Almin* (surrounding all worlds) not in the way of the evolution of worlds but the Reason of Reasons in the way of 'for He commanded and they were created',[73](#_ftn1027) and from there it is drawn not in the way of *hishtalshelus*, etc."

And it is understood that when the influence is from the order of *hishtalshelus*, in order and gradation, then it can come immediately in revelation, not so when the influence is above the order of *hishtalshelus*, not in order and gradation, it cannot come immediately in revelation, as in the aforementioned miracles that do not come immediately in revelation.

And from the merits of the influence that does not come immediately in revelation—that being in concealment, there is no need to fear those who seek to prosecute and say that so-and-so is not worthy of this influence, and also there is no need to fear the evil eye (so that there is no need to reach the charms that were brought in the words of our Sages[74](#_ftn1028) to nullify the evil eye).

#### 188

And regarding us—in whatever way the influence will be through the Rebbe, we must make the vessels to receive the influence, as mentioned, through a change of habit, through which one merits receiving the influence in all that is needed.

***

**15.** There is one who merited and volunteered for the printing of a *reshima* (record) from the Rebbe Rayatz in preparation for 24 Teves[75](#_ftn1029) [for various reasons I did not want them to know who he is], and I would like to ask all those present to bless him that the greatness of the merit he merited to print this *reshima* should stand for him and his household in all that they need.

[One of those present announced *Amen*, and the Rebbe Shlita said:] I intended that they also say "*L'chaim*."

*

**16.** In the *reshima* that was printed in preparation for 24 Teves there is a story that has in it a lesson and instruction, like all the stories that the Rebbe Rayatz revealed in his *reshimos*, from which one can learn many matters.

In the aforementioned *reshima*[76](#_ftn1030) the Rebbe Rayatz tells in the name of the Alter Rebbe about the mission that our teacher the Baal Shem Tov gave to his student the Gaon R. Chaim Rappaport,[77](#_ftn1031) and he adds[78](#_ftn1032) that on this trip another great mission was fulfilled—that in that place there was a spring which since Hashem created it, no man had ever blessed over its waters and they had not used its waters for holiness and purity, and for this the spring was always crying, as the saying[79](#_ftn1033) "the lower waters are crying, we want to be before the Holy King," and on this trip, that they drank its waters and washed their hands in it for the *Mincha* prayer, the spring was saved. And he concludes, "And this is the matter of Divine Providence, that every created being has its time of ascent and by whom it will be elevated, and every soul has its purpose, what and in what place it must work and fix."

And one must learn from this, that if the things are said regarding a physical spring, all the more so that it is so regarding a spiritual spring, as follows.

**17.** And the matter in this:[80](#_ftn1034)

#### 189

In the soul of each and every Jew there is a spring, but, there are those whose spring is covered with a thick layer of dirt and stones, and one must dig in depth and remove the abundance of dirt and stones in order to reveal the spring within them, and there are those whose spring is covered with only a thin layer of dirt, so that there is no need to dig in depth to reveal the spring, and there are those for whom the flow of the spring has burst forth in revelation.

And now, when one meets a Jew whose spring has not been revealed for many years, one might err and think that there is no chance to reveal the spring within him, and furthermore, perhaps even in concealment there is no spring within him, for, it is explained in *Chassidus*[81](#_ftn1035) that every thing that exists in concealment must necessarily come to revelation, and since for many years the spring has not been revealed within him, this is proof seemingly that even in concealment there is no spring within him.

And the answer to this—by *kal v

## B"H, Rosh Chodesh Shevat, 5711

Brooklyn, N.Y.

To Anash, the Talmidei HaTemimim, and all who are close to Chassidus and Chassidim, wherever they may be,

May Hashem grant them life,

Shalom and Bracha!

As we approach the great and holy day, the tenth of Shevat, the yom hilula of my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory—I wish to call your attention to the maamar he provided for publication for the day of his passing, the discourse *Basi LeGani*, 10 Shevat 5710.

I trust that you will study it on the night and day of the hilula.

In the words of our Nasi in his letters (Kuntres 3, Kuntres 36):

This day is *mesugal* for connecting to the Tree of Life, that each and every one of Anash may merit that the merit of my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory—who gave and surrendered his holy soul for us, to guide us in the paths of the *tzaddikei yesod olam*, the glory of our holy forefathers and Rebbes, of blessed memory—should shine upon him and upon his entire household, that they may be blessed with children, life, and abundant sustenance.

Anash and Talmidei HaTemimim, may you live, awaken and come to the courtyards of Hashem, in the shuls and batei medrash, for tefillah and for the study of shiurim in public. Gather together with brotherly love to strengthen your studies, to support those who study Torah, and to engage in the *avodah* of the Creator.

Anash, Talmidei HaTemimim, and all who take part in the ways of Chassidim and Chassidus: stand ready, all of you—you, your wives, your sons, and your daughters—to receive the blessing of Hashem with an abundance of life, good livelihood, and *nachas* from your descendants. May the Creator bestow this upon you and upon us through the awakening of great mercy from the Source of true mercy and kindness—in the manner of "those who bring in mercy"—which my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, the *baal hilula*, will awaken. And may you be blessed with children, life, and abundant sustenance.

**Menachem Mendel Schneerson**

## B"H, Rosh Chodesh Shevat, 5711

Brooklyn, N.Y.

To Anash, the students of the Tomim, and all those connected or belonging to the Rebbe, our master, teacher, and leader, of blessed memory, whose merit protects us:

May Hashem grant them life.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to the questions of many regarding a detailed order for the tenth of Shevat, the upcoming Yahrtzeit of the Rebbe, our master, teacher, and leader, of blessed memory, I hereby suggest the following:

On the Shabbos Kodesh preceding the Yahrtzeit, one should endeavor to receive an aliyah to the Torah.

If the number of aliyos is insufficient, they should read from the Torah in different rooms, but *do not add* to the number of those called up.

They should choose the most prominent person in the group to be the Maftir—with the consent of the majority—or by lottery.

They should select and appoint someone to lead the davening at the amud on the day of the Yahrtzeit. It is appropriate to divide the duties so that one person leads Maariv, a second leads Shacharis, and a third leads Mincha, in order to grant this merit to a greater number of Anash.

Light a candle that will burn for the entire twenty-four-hour period. If possible, it should be a beeswax candle.

During the davening, five candles should be lit.

After davening (in the morning, after reciting Tehillim), the person leading the davening should study (and conclude) the twenty-fourth chapter of Keilim and the seventh chapter of Mikvaos. Afterward, he should recite the Mishnah, "Rabbi Chananya ben Akashya," etc., and Kaddish D'Rabanan. In a whisper, he should recite a few lines of Tanya.

After Maariv, they should review a portion of the Maamar of the day of passing (the discourse *Basi L'Gani*, printed in the Kuntres of the same name) by heart. If there is no one who can recite it by heart, they should study it from the text. The same should be done after Shacharis, and it should be concluded after Mincha.

In the morning before davening, study a chapter of Tanya. Do the same after Mincha.

In the morning before davening, each person should give tzedakah for the causes associated with our Nasi, the Rebbe, our master, teacher, and leader, of blessed memory—*on behalf of himself and each member of his household*—and likewise before Mincha.

After Shacharis and the review of Chassidus, each person should read a Pidyon Nefesh (naturally, while wearing a gartel). Those who merited entering for Yechidus, or at least seeing the face of the Rebbe, our master, teacher, and leader, of blessed memory, should visualize themselves, while reading the P.N., as if they are standing before him. Afterward, place the P.N. between the pages of a Maamar, Kuntres, etc., of the Rebbe’s Torah. Then, send it (if possible, *on that very day*) so that it may be read at his resting place.

During the twenty-four hours, study the chapters of Mishnayos corresponding to the letters of his name.

During the twenty-four hours, hold a farbrengen.

Set aside an hour during the twenty-four hours to explain to one’s household about the Rebbe, our master, teacher, and leader, of blessed memory, and the avodah he performed throughout his life.

During the twenty-four hours, visit (those who are suited for this) the shuls and batei medrash in the city to review a saying or aphorism from the Torah of the Rebbe, our master, teacher, and leader, of blessed memory. Speak about his love for *all of Klal Yisrael*, and announce and explain his takanah regarding the recitation of Tehillim and the study of Chumash with Rashi—and in appropriate places, also about the study of Tanya as divided for the days of the year. If possible, all of the above should be done within the framework of a farbrengen.

During the twenty-four hours, visit (those qualified for this) the gatherings of the Chareidi youth—and endeavor, as much as possible through peaceful means, to also visit places where the youth gather who are not yet Chareidi—and explain to them the great love that the Rebbe, our master, teacher, and leader, of blessed memory, always held for them. Explain to them what he demanded of them, and the hope and confidence he placed in them, that they would ultimately fulfill their role in upholding Yiddishkeit and spreading Torah with all the energy, warmth, and vitality that are the unique qualities of youth.

***

It is understood that if it is suitable for local conditions, they should continue all of the above in the days following the Yahrtzeit, and especially on the Shabbos Kodesh that follows.

***

May Hashem hasten the coming of our Redeemer, and may those who dwell in the dust awaken and sing for joy, and may our Nasi, the Rebbe, our master, teacher, and leader, of blessed memory—the master of the Hillula—be among them to bring us tidings of wonders and lead us on the path that ascends to the house of Hashem.

**Menachem Mendel Schneerson**

## B"H. The text of the telegram that the Rebbe shlita was pleased to send to Anash, may they live, throughout the world, in anticipation of the yahrtzeit, 10 Shevat, 5711

#### 191a

On the day of the yahrtzeit from which we draw, the tenth of Shevat, the merit of the master of the yahrtzeit, the supreme tzaddik, is exceedingly great to draw down salvations, blessings, and success for all those who involve themselves in his institutions. Surely, they will gather to inspire many toward Torah and mitzvos, to strengthen his institutions and his takanos, to connect themselves to the "Tree of Life," and to be blessed with everything necessary, both materially and spiritually.

With blessing,

**Menachem Schneerson**

## 10 Shevat, 5711

#### 192

My revered father-in-law, the Rebbe [1], writes in his maamar for the day of his passing, 10 Shevat, 5711: **"I have come into My garden, My sister, My bride" [2].** The Midrash Rabba (in its place [3]) states: "It does not say 'into a garden,' but 'into My garden'—into My *ginuni*, into the place where My essence was initially, for the essence of the Shechinah was in the lower realms." End quote. 

To understand the precision of the phrase "the essence of the Shechinah," we must note that the Alter Rebbe [A] explains that the term *Shechinah* is derived from the fact that it dwells (*shochenet*) and clothes itself, as in the verse, "And I will dwell (*v'shachanti*) among them" [4], which is the beginning of the revelation of the Ohr Ein Sof. Now, from the fact that he writes [5] that the beginning of the revelation of the Ohr Ein Sof is called by the name *Shechinah*, it is understood that the concept of *Shechinah* is far above Atzilus as well, even in the level of the light before the Tzimtzum. For the beginning of the revelation is in the Ohr Ein Sof before the Tzimtzum, and as the Mitteler Rebbe [B] writes, the illumination of the *Kav* (the line) in relation to the essence of the Ohr Ein Sof is called by the name *Shechinah*. 

The concept of *Shechinah* is defined in every place according to its context. In relation to Atzilus, the *Malchus* is called by the name *Shechinah*. Regarding this, the Tzemach Tzedek [C] explains that *Malchus* of Atzilus is called *Shechinah* specifically when it becomes a level of *Atik* for the world of Beriah; however, while it is within Atzilus, it is unified with them (with the Sefiros of Atzilus), and the term *Shechinah* does not apply. Nevertheless, this does not contradict what was written above—that the *Kav* is called by the name *Shechinah*—because the *Shechinah* mentioned by our Sages refers to *Malchus* of Atzilus, and even that is only when it becomes a level of *Atik* for Beriah. But in its root—that is, as it is in relation to the Ohr Ein Sof—the *Kav* itself is also called

#### 193

*Shechinah*. One of the reasons why the *Kav* is called by the name *Shechinah* in relation to the Ohr Ein Sof, the Rebbe Maharash [D] writes, is because the intent of the *Kav's* extension is so that it may be clothed in the worlds and the souls of Israel; therefore, it is called by the name *Shechinah* even at its inception. 

Regarding an even higher level—the *Shechinah* in its primary root above the Tzimtzum—the Rebbe Rashab [E] explains that the revelation of the light as it is before the Tzimtzum is called by the name *Shechinah*. Generally, the light before the Tzimtzum has three levels: the essence of the light, the expansion of the light, and within the expansion of the light, two levels: the revelation of the light as it is for itself (which is the source of the *Ohr Sovev*) and the revelation of the light as it relates to the worlds (which is the source of the *Ohr Memale*). This latter revelation is called by the name *Shechinah*. Even though it is before the Tzimtzum and cannot be a source for the worlds—which is why the Tzimtzum had to occur, and the first Tzimtzum is specifically in the nature of withdrawal—it is still called by the name *Shechinah*. 

This is the precision of the phrase, "The essence of the Shechinah was in the lower realms." It means that the revelation of the Shechinah in the lower realms is not the Shechinah as it is in relation to Atzilus (i.e., *Malchus*), nor as it is in relation to the Ohr Ein Sof (i.e., the *Kav*), but rather the *essence* and *inwardness* of the Shechinah was in the lower realms specifically. For the light [F] that is clothed in the worlds comes in a sequence and gradation. Above, it shines with greater revelation, and the more it is drawn down and evolves, the more the light is diminished. This is the general rule regarding the light of the *Seder Hishtalshelus*. Even though before the sin the light was also in revelation below, there was still a greater revelation of light above. As our Sages say [*], "He stretched out His right hand and created the heavens; He stretched out His left hand and created the earth." The intent is to the light that is above the worlds—the essence of the Shechinah.

B) **Now**, the statement that "the essence of the Shechinah was in the lower realms" is explained by the Midrash to mean that "lower realms" refers to this physical world. As it explains, through the sin of the Tree of Knowledge, the Shechinah withdrew from the earth to the heavens, and through the Giving of the Torah on Mount Sinai, "I have come into My garden, My *ginuni*." The primary withdrawal caused by sin is specifically the sin of the Tree of Knowledge. Just as in the matter of sin, the primary sin was the sin of the Tree of Knowledge—for through it, room was given for all other sins, and it was the cause and factor for the sins of Cain, Enosh, etc.—so too regarding the effect of the sin: the withdrawal that occurred through the sin is primarily the withdrawal that took place through the sin of the Tree of Knowledge from this lower world specifically. Just as the essence of the

#### 194

Shechinah in the lower realms is in this world specifically, so too regarding the withdrawal: the essence of the withdrawal is that it withdrew from the earth specifically. This was caused by the sin of the Tree of Knowledge, through which the Shechinah withdrew from the earth to the heavens. This is also the reason why he (in the maamar) does not group the sin of the Tree of Knowledge with the sins of Cain and Enosh, but considers it separately: because through the sins of Cain and Enosh, the Shechinah withdrew from heaven to heaven, whereas through the sin of the Tree of Knowledge, it withdrew from earth to heaven. Beyond the fact that the withdrawal from the earth is what primarily concerns us, it is also the essence of the matter of withdrawal.

**(He continues** in the maamar): "And afterwards, seven Tzaddikim arose and brought the Shechinah down below. Avraham merited and brought the Shechinah down from the seventh heaven to the sixth, etc." (He abbreviates this and concludes) "until Moshe, who is the seventh (and all sevenths are beloved [8]), brought it down below to the earth." The essence of the drawing down is through Moshe, for Moshe specifically brought it down to the earth. Just as in the matter of the withdrawal from below to above, the essence is the sin of the Tree of Knowledge, where it withdrew from the earth as mentioned above, so too regarding the matter of drawing down from above to below: the essence of the drawing down is below on the earth specifically. Beyond the fact that the drawing down below is what primarily concerns us, it is also the essence of the matter of drawing down. This was accomplished by Moshe specifically. The reason for this is explained in the maamar in parentheses: because "all sevenths are beloved."

C) **Now**, from the language of our Sages, "all sevenths are beloved" and not "all beloved are sevenths," it is proven that the primary level is the one that is seventh, and because it is seventh, that is the source of its belovedness. That is to say, its belovedness is not due to a matter dependent on its own choice, will, or *avodah*, but rather in the fact that it is seventh, which comes from birth. And yet, all sevenths are beloved. Therefore, Moshe merited that the Torah was given through him. Now, my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, explained (at the beginning of his arrival in America) [G] that even in the matter of "the sevenths are beloved," the level of the first is evident, for the entire concept of "seventh" is that it is seventh *to the first*. He then explained the level of the first—Avraham Avinu—because of his *avodah*, and that his *avodah* was with *mesiras nefesh*. He does not stop there, but adds (even though, seemingly, it is not relevant to the core of the matter there) that the manner of his *mesiras nefesh* was that he did not *seek* *mesiras nefesh*. This is the difference between the *mesiras nefesh* of Avraham Avinu and the *mesiras nefesh* of Rabbi Akiva. The *mesiras nefesh* of Rabbi Akiva was that he sought *mesiras nefesh*: "When will it come to my hand and I will fulfill it?" [9]

#### 195

Whereas with Avraham, his *mesiras nefesh* was incidental. Avraham knew that the essence of *avodah* is as it is written [10], "And he called there in the name of Havaya, the Eternal G-d." Do not read "he called" (*vayikra*), but "he caused to call" (*vayakri*), that the other should also cry out. And if *mesiras nefesh* was needed for this incidentally, then that too was present. So great was the level of his *avodah* and his *mesiras nefesh* that even Moshe, who merited that the Torah was given through him, was for the reason that "the sevenths are beloved"—that he is seventh to the first. And the Holy One, Blessed be He, said to him (to Moshe), "In the place of the great (Avraham), do not stand" [12]. Now, even though the belovedness of the seventh is great and does not come through choice or *avodah*, but rather *partikerheit* (as a given) from birth, nevertheless, there is no limitation here to say that it is a wonder and applies only to unique individuals. Rather, it is as explained in *Tanna D'bei Eliyahu* (Ch. 9 and 26) and cited in *Chassidus* that all Jews, and even a servant and even a maidservant [H], can reach the inspiration of the Holy Spirit, and every single Jew is obligated to say, "When will my deeds reach the deeds of my ancestors, Avraham, Yitzchak, and Yaakov?" It is just that one must not be deceived by oneself, and one must know that "in the place of the great, do not stand."
