The entire level of the seventh is that he is seventh to the first, *az er ken durchfihren* (that he can carry out) the *avodah* and mission of the first—that "do not read *vayikra* but *vayakri*." This is the belovedness of the seventh, that he is the one who draws down the Shechinah, and not only that, but he draws down the *essence* of the Shechinah. And even more, that he draws it down into the lower realms.

**Now**, this is demanded of each and every one of us, the seventh generation. For all sevenths are beloved. Even though the fact that we are in the seventh generation is not by our choice and not through our *avodah*, and in many matters it is perhaps not according to our will, nevertheless, all sevenths are beloved. We are in the *ikvesa d'meshicha* (the footsteps of Moshiach), at the very end of the footsteps, and the *avodah* is to complete the drawing down of the Shechinah—and not just the Shechinah, but the *essence* of the Shechinah, and in the lower realms specifically.

D) **Now**, after he explains in the maamar that the essence of the Shechinah was in the lower realms, and that afterwards Moshe (the seventh) drew it down to the earth specifically, he says: "And the essence of the revelation of Elokus was in the Beis Hamikdash" (and he brings the verse for this), "as it is written [4], 'And they shall make Me a Sanctuary and I will dwell among them'—'in it' is not said, but 'among them,' within each and every one of Israel" [13]. This is also what is written [14], "The righteous shall inherit the earth and dwell forever upon it," for the righteous inherit the earth, which is Gan Eden, because they cause the Shechinah (i.e., they draw down [15]) the level of "He who dwells forever, exalted and holy" [16] (this matter of "He who dwells forever" is not explained in the maamar, but is explained in *Likutei Torah* [17] based on the passage in the Zohar [18]) to be in revelation below. This is "I have come into My garden, My *ginuni*," to the place where its essence was initially, for the essence of the Shechinah was in the lower realms. The matter (the explanation to understand why the essence of the Shechinah was in the lower realms specifically) is that the ultimate intent in the creation and evolution of the worlds is that the Holy One, Blessed be He, desired to have a dwelling place in the lower realms [19].

**Now**, our Rebbe the Alter Rebbe explains [I] that the ultimate purpose of the evolution of the worlds and their descent is not for the sake of the higher worlds, since they have a descent from the light of His countenance, and it cannot be said that the intent is for the sake of the descent. For it is known that the creation is only through the power of the *Atzmus* (Essence), as written in *Iggeres HaKodesh*, in the discourse *Ihu V'chayohi* [20], that His essence and being—whose existence is from His essence and has no prior cause, G-d forbid—is the only one with the power and ability to create *yesh me'ayin* (something from nothing) and absolute nothingness. That is, the coming-into-being is not from the revelations but from the *Atzmus*. If so, it is impossible to say that the purpose of the coming-into-being is for the sake of the higher worlds, for even the world of Atzilus is a "revelation of the concealment" [21], and if so, this is a descent from the light of His countenance. For when the lights of Atzilus were in their concealment, they were at a much higher level. Furthermore, since these are only revelations, it cannot be said that the *Atzmus* is for the sake of revelations. Rather, the purpose is this lower world. As the Mitteler Rebbe writes in this *parsha* [J] (*Parshas Beshalach*) regarding the difference between the higher worlds and this world,

#### 197

that in this world it is felt that its existence is from His essence (as explained in the *Hemshech* of Rosh Hashanah of this year [22], the difference between a created being and light: light is a witness to the Source of Light, for when we see light, the light itself shows and reveals that there is a Source of Light. Not so with a created being; not only does it not reveal the Creator, but it even conceals and hides Him, and on the contrary, it is felt that its existence is from its own essence (though from the perspective of intellect, it is certain that this is not so) [23]. Even though this is only in its feeling, nevertheless, the very fact that it appears as if its existence is from its own essence is because its root is from the *Atzmus* whose existence is from His essence. Thus, it is understood that the intent in the creation and evolution is not for the sake of the higher worlds, whose nature is revelations, but the intent is this lower world, which appears to it that it is not a revelation but an essence—that is, its existence is from His essence—and through the *avodah* within it, through *iskafya* and *is'hapcha*, the *Atzmus* is revealed. For its sake was the creation and evolution of the worlds.

E) **Now**, not only according to the view brought by the Tzemach Tzedek [K] that even the *Keilim* (vessels) of Atzilus are a "revelation of the concealment"—for according to this view, certainly the intent is not for the sake of Atzilus, since it is a descent and only revelations—but even according to the second view brought there, that the *Keilim* are a creation *yesh me'ayin*, it is explained in many places [24] that when we say the *Keilim* are a creation *yesh me'ayin*, it does not mean *yesh me'ayin* in the absolute sense. Rather, this is only in relation to the light, because the root of the *Keilim* is from the *Reshimu*, which is a level of concealment, and therefore their existence is also in a manner where their source is in concealment. Therefore, in relation to the light, they are like a creation *yesh me'ayin*, but in relation to the *Reshimu*, they are a revelation of the concealment. If so, it is understood that the intent is not the higher worlds, but the *avodah* in this world of *iskafya* and *is'hapcha*. And even though now, through the performance of the *mitzvos*, we add lights in Atzilus [25], and if so, how can we say that even now the primary intent is this world specifically? Regarding this, the Rebbe

#### 198

Maharash [L] explains that these lights in Atzilus are there "as if placed in a box," for they are not for the sake of Atzilus, but for the need of the lower world, and they are not revealed in Atzilus. This is what the Rebbe Rashab [M] explains regarding the fact that it cannot be said that the intent is for the sake of the higher worlds, since they have a descent from the light of His countenance. The meaning of this is that the higher worlds are revelations, which is a descent, and also that the *Atzmus* is distinct from the matter of revelations. Rather, the purpose is this lower world, for so it arose in His will that there be satisfaction before Him when the *Sitra Achra* is subdued [27] and darkness is turned into light [28]. As he explains in the maamar [29], the entire *avodah* is to turn the "folly" of the *Sitra Achra* into the "folly" of holiness, and through this there is satisfaction before Him, "I spoke and My will was done" [30]. Through this, we draw down that He, may He be blessed, should have a dwelling place in the lower realms [19]. Just as a person dwells in his home with his entire essence and being [31], so too it is with the lower realms, which are a dwelling place for Him—the intent is that we draw down not only revelations, but that the *Atzmus* of the Ein Sof, Blessed be He, is present within them. This is the purpose of the creation and evolution of the worlds.

F) **Now**, at the conclusion of the maamar [32], he explains that since the essence of the Shechinah was in the lower realms, and the primary revelation of this was in the Beis Hamikdash, this is the reason why the *Mishkan* was made specifically of *shittim* wood. Because the intent is to turn the "folly" of the *Sitra Achra* and the "boiling" of the *nefesh habehamis* into the "folly" of holiness. As our Sages say [33], "His folly helped the elder," an *avodah* and *bitul* that is above reason and intellect. Now, all the matters that my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, demanded of us, and likewise the other *Nesi'im*, they fulfilled

#### 199

this themselves. It is similar to what our Sages say regarding the verse [34], "He tells His words to Yaakov, His statutes and His judgments to Israel"—what He does, He tells Israel to do [N]. Similarly, what He commands Israel, He does. It is the same with the instructions of our *Nesi'im*: what they demanded of those connected and belonging to them, they themselves fulfilled and did. And the fact that they revealed to us that they fulfilled this is so that it should be easier for us to fulfill them. For example, regarding the matter of *Ahavas Yisrael*, there are many, many stories from each of the *Nesi'im*. For example, from the Alter Rebbe, who interrupted his prayer to go and chop wood, cook soup, and feed a woman who had just given birth himself, because there were no men there in the house. From the Mitteler Rebbe, how someone came to him for *yechidus* and complained about the matters that young men complain about. The Mitteler Rebbe revealed his arm and said to him, "Do you not see that my skin has shriveled upon my bones, etc." [36] "And all this is from your *chovos hanefesh* (obligations of the soul)." This shows the wonder and loftiness of the level of the Mitteler Rebbe in general, and specifically regarding those who belong to such matters. Nevertheless, the connection with them was so great that because of their matters, which were not as they should be, it caused him extreme physical weakness, until his skin shriveled upon his bones. From the Tzemach Tzedek, how he went before prayer to assist a simple man with a *gemach* (loan fund) because it affected his livelihood [37]. From the Rebbe Maharash, who once [O] traveled specifically from a health resort to Paris and met there a young man and said to him: "Young man, *yayin nesach* (non-kosher wine) dulls the mind and the heart; be a Jew." The young man went home and did not rest until he came to the Rebbe Maharash, repented, and from him came a family of G-d-fearing and pious people. It is known that for the Rebbe Maharash, time was extremely precious, to the point that even the saying of *Chassidus* was brief, and at certain times he was already finished with prayer by eight o'clock in the morning. And yet, he made a long journey and stayed there for a period of time for the sake of a young man, etc. From the Rebbe Rashab at the beginning of his *nesi'us*, when a new decree was issued and he had to travel to Moscow for it. His older brother,

#### 200

the Raza, told him, "Time is precious to you and you do not know the language of the country well" [39] (the Raza was learned in languages), "and you also need to seek connections, so I will travel for this matter according to your instructions." But the Rebbe Rashab did not agree to this and traveled himself and succeeded. And likewise, there are many stories from my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, regarding his efforts to do good, even for a private individual, in spiritual or material matters. He gave of himself for this, not only his material self but also his spiritual self, even though the one he was benefiting was not only not in the category of "your colleague in Torah and *mitzvos*," but was not even on his level at all.

G) **Now**, through *iskafya* and *is'hapcha* to the "folly" of holiness, we fulfill the purpose of creation, which is that He, may He be blessed, should have a dwelling place in the lower realms. And the fact that through *iskafya* and *is'hapcha* a dwelling place is created in the lower realms—"I have come into My garden"—is at a level more exalted than before the sin. Just as when one tears down a previous building in order to build, it is obvious that the new building must be at a more exalted level than the previous one, so too it must be said that through *iskafya* and *is'hapcha*, a dwelling place is created at a more exalted level. As explained in the maamar [40], through the subduing of the *Sitra Achra*, the glory of the Holy One, Blessed be He, is "withdrawn" (*istalek*) in all the worlds [27]—that is, the light that is in all the worlds equally. And even though the language in the maamar is *Ohr Sovev*, it is impossible to say that the intent is that a light that is within the category of the worlds is drawn down, but rather that it surrounds and encompasses them. Instead, the intent is that a lofty light is drawn down that is not in the category of the worlds at all. Therefore, he calls this revelation of light by the name *istalek* (withdrawn/exalted) [41]. Therefore, the passing of Tzaddikim is also called by the name *histalkus* (passing/withdrawal), because *histalkus* is the revelation of an extremely lofty light. Now, there are two letters in *Iggeres HaKodesh* [42] that explain the matter of *histalkus*. In the second letter, the matter of *histalkus* is explained regarding the matter of the Red Heifer. The matters performed inside cannot purify the impurity of death, only the matter performed outside—the heifer performed outside. To this, the death of Tzaddikim is compared [43]. Now, there is no Red Heifer, because due to our sins we had to be exiled from our land [44], but

#### 201

the passing of Tzaddikim occurred. Now, regarding the passing of Tzaddikim, there are two statements of our Sages [P]: "The death of Tzaddikim is as weighty as the burning of the House of our G-d." "The passing of Tzaddikim is harder than the destruction of the Beis Hamikdash." Through all this, the glory of the Holy One, Blessed be He, is *istalek*. The meaning of the matter of *histalkus* was explained by all the Rebbes [45]—the Alter Rebbe, the Mitteler Rebbe, the Tzemach Tzedek, the Rebbe Maharash, the Rebbe Rashab, and my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe—that the intent of the word *histalkus* is not that it is an ascent above, G-d forbid, but that he is present below, only that he is in a state of transcendence. This is what is demanded of us, the seventh generation to the Alter Rebbe. And all sevenths are beloved, *az gem az m'hot dos nit fardint un nit oisgehorevet* (that even though one has not earned it and not labored for it), nevertheless, all sevenths are beloved, and the *avodah* of the seventh generation is to draw the Shechinah down literally below. To turn the "folly" of the *nefesh habehamis*—which a person knows in his soul *az er hot dos* (that he has it), and the "boiling" of the *nefesh habehamis* *vos er hot dos* (that he has it), and perhaps sometimes even lower—to make from this and turn this into the "folly" of holiness.

H) **This is** the matter of *tzaddika d'itpatar* (the Tzaddik who has passed) [46]. Even though there were already many concealments and hidden things and many questions and incomprehensible matters, all this was not enough. And in order for there to be the glory of the Holy One, Blessed be He, *istalek* in all the worlds, there was also the matter of the passing of Tzaddikim, which is hard not only like the destruction, but more than the destruction. The ultimate intent in this is that through this, the glory of the Holy One, Blessed be He, will be *istalek*. This is demanded of each one of us: to know *az m'gefindt zich in dor hashvi'i* (that one finds oneself in the seventh generation), that the entire level of the seventh is that he is seventh to the first, whose conduct was that he did not seek anything for himself, not even *mesiras nefesh*. For he knew that his entire matter is as it is written, "And he called there in the name of Havaya, the Eternal G-d." And the example of the conduct of Avraham Avinu, which is—*gekummen in azelche erter vos m'hot dortn nit gevust fun G-tlichkeit* (he came to such places where they did not know of G-dliness), did not know of Yiddishkeit, and did not know even of the *aleph-beis*, and being there, one set oneself aside, and "do not read *vayikra* but *vayakri*." It is known [47] that in the study of the method of "do not read," both readings exist. And even in this, it is explicit in the Written Torah: *vayikra*. Nevertheless, one must know *az oib er vill im zol aingeyn der vayikra, muz zein der vayikri* (that if he wants the *vayikra* to be accepted by him, there must be the *vayikri*). *Darftu zehen az yener zol nit nor visn* (you must see to it that the other should not only know)

#### 202

but also cry out. Even though until now the other did not know of anything at all, now you must see to it that he should cry out "to the Eternal," not "to the worldly" [Q]—that is, that G-dliness is a matter unto itself and the world is a matter unto itself, but that G-dliness rules and governs the world, and that world and G-dliness are one.

I) **And even** though who is he and where is he who dares to say, "I will perform the *avodah* of Avraham Avinu," nevertheless, a small portion of it belongs to each one, and one is obligated in it [R], and the powers for this were given to him through the conduct shown to us by the first, and from him onwards until, and including, the conduct shown to us by my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe. They paved the way and gave us the powers for this. This itself is the belovedness of the seventh generation, that so many powers were given and revealed for our sake. Through *avodah* in such a manner, the essence of the Shechinah will be drawn down below in this physical and material world, and it will be at a level even more exalted than before the sin. As it is written [48] regarding Moshiach, "He shall be very high," more than Adam HaRishon, and even [49] as it was before the sin [S]. And my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, who "bore our illnesses and suffered our pains" [50], and he was "wounded because of our transgressions, crushed because of our iniquities" [51]—just as he saw our distress, so too, speedily in our days and in our immediate time, may he redeem his flock from the spiritual exile and the physical exile together, and set us upon a pillar of light. But all this is still only revelations, and even more—that He will connect and unify us with the essence and being of the Ein Sof, Blessed be He. This is the inwardness of the intent of the descent and evolution of the worlds, the matter of sin and its rectification, and the matter of the passing of Tzaddikim, through which the glory of the Holy One, Blessed be He, will be *istalek*. And when He takes us out of exile with a high hand [52], and for all the children of Israel there will be light in their dwellings [53], then "Moshe and the children of Israel will sing, etc." [54], "Havaya shall reign forever and ever" [55] (as it is

#### 203

in the text of the prayer) and also in the language of the Targum [T], "Havaya's kingdom stands forever and ever." And we conclude, "And Havaya shall be King, etc., Havaya is One and His Name is One" [56], that there will be no difference between Havaya and His Name [57]. All this is accomplished through the passing of Tzaddikim, which is harder even than the destruction of the Beis Hamikdash. And since *az m'iz shoin di ale inyanim durchgegangen* (since we have already passed through all these matters), now the matter depends only on us—the seventh generation. And we will merit *zehen* [U] (to see) ourselves with the Rebbe here below in a body and below ten handbreadths, and he will redeem us.

## Sicha of 10 Shevat 5711

#### 204

**A.** It is known that there are differences between the first year following a passing and the time thereafter. Among these is that "for all twelve months... his soul ascends and descends; after twelve months... his soul ascends and does not descend again"[1](#_ftn1122)—meaning, he is no longer present below as he was before.

Although this rule applies to all of Israel—to simple Jews, to the great leaders of Israel, and even to the Nesi'im of Israel—nevertheless, due to the immense stature of the Tzaddikim—for a Tzaddik decrees and Hashem fulfills[2](#_ftn1123), and even more so, Hashem decrees and the Tzaddik annuls[3](#_ftn1124), to the point that Tzaddikim can effect a change in the *Maaseh Bereishis*[a](#_ftn1126)—they are able to alter this rule in accordance with their will.

This rule (that "after twelve months... his soul ascends and does not descend again") applies to one who is not the master of the world and all that is in it. This is not the case with Tzaddikim, to whom the keys of *chayah*, rain, and the resurrection of the dead have been entrusted [keys of such a nature that two of them are not entrusted to one person simultaneously[4](#_ftn1125), yet we have seen that these keys are indeed entrusted to Tzaddikim simultaneously[b](#_ftn1127)]. Since they are the masters of all, it follows *a fortiori* that they can choose their own place, to be wherever they deem it to be better.

**B.** And regarding the Rebbe, *kudsha brich hu*—certainly, even now, his desire is to be here, together with us.

#### 205

With the Rebbe, there were the three matters of love of Hashem, love of Torah, and love of Israel (interconnected, to the point of being one thing [as is known from the teaching of our Alter Rebbe[5](#_ftn1128) that "love your fellow as yourself"[6](#_ftn1129) is a vessel (an explanation and interpretation) for "love Hashem your G-d"[7](#_ftn1130)]). Therefore, without making calculations, the Rebbe relinquished ("*er hot farboygen*") his own physicality and even his own spirituality for the sake of love of Israel[c](#_ftn1135).

From this, it is understood that this is his conduct even after his passing [similar to the teaching of our Sages[8](#_ftn1131), "Once a person has spent the majority of his years" [d](#_ftn1136) in good conduct, he is assured that it will remain so thereafter. And if this is true for any person, all the more so for a Tzaddik, a Chossid[e](#_ftn1137), who all his days sacrificed his soul—his natural soul and even his *Elokis* soul]. Even though the matters of below obscure and confuse the matter of "enjoying the radiance of the Shechinah"[9](#_ftn1132), "the radiance of their Torah and their *avodah*," and higher than that[10](#_ftn1133), nevertheless, the Rebbe relinquishes this and desires, even now, to be below, together with us[f](#_ftn1138).

And since this is the Rebbe's desire, he will certainly be together with us, as the Tosafos[11](#_ftn1134) states: "When it (the soul) desires, it descends"[g](#_ftn1139).

#### 206

**C.** The practical takeaway from this:

Although we are already past the first *Yom HaHillula*,

— I refrain from saying or writing "first *yahrzeit*," because we must hope that by next year the prophecy[12](#_ftn1140) "Awake and sing, you who dwell in the dust" will already be fulfilled, and he will be among them, and consequently there will no longer be a "*yahrzeit*"[h](#_ftn1144). Therefore, I am precise in saying "*first Yom HaHillula*," because ascents (which is the concept of *Hillula*) will continue even after that—

If so, there could—*chas v'shalom*—be a weakening in our *hiskashrus*. We must know that, on the contrary: the *hiskashrus* must be strengthened even more. Just as the Rebbe is now ascending from level to level, we too must gird ourselves with additional strength[i](#_ftn1145) so that we may accompany him.

**D.** This is also the answer to those who ask regarding the recitation of Chapter 71 (the chapter of the Rebbe corresponding to his age[13](#_ftn1141))—must it be said even after 10 Shevat[14](#_ftn1142), and until when must it be said? The answer is that it should continue to be said until 12 Tammuz[j](#_ftn1146).

This is preceded by the discussion of whether there is a concept of increase in time even after passing, and whether the concept of growth and maturation is applicable—some say this is a dispute between the Rambam and the Ra'avad[15](#_ftn1143).

#### 207

There are two proofs that these matters are relevant even after passing:

1) It is the custom in all Jewish communities to observe a "*yahrzeit*" every year. Since the concept of a "*yahrzeit*" is that on this day the soul's ascent occurs, it is proven that even for the soul (after passing), an increase dependent on time is applicable.

2) There is a *reshima* from the Rebbe dated 20 Mar-Cheshvan 5705[16](#_ftn1147)—on which day eighty-four years had passed since the birth of his father, the Rebbe (the Rashab) *n.e.*[k](#_ftn1149), and on this day the connection to Chapter 84 ends (as is known regarding the customs of reciting Tehillim[13])—concerning a nocturnal vision in which his father told him to deliver a *maamar* on Chapter 84. From this, it is understood in our case as well (as discussed[14] that the Rebbe clarified in advance ("*bavwarnt*") many matters)—that by writing about the birthday of his father, the Rebbe *n.e.*, many years after his passing, he also ruled regarding himself[17](#_ftn1148), that even now (after passing) he has the concept of a birthday, and even now he has ascents from level to level, where, after every ascent, it is found that the previous *avodah* was a preparation for the subsequent status and situation.

***

**E.** Regarding the Rebbe's *shlichus*, there are several types:

There are those to whom the instruction was openly regarding physicality—meaning, that they should engage in business and the like—but the inner intent was the matter of Torah and *mitzvos*. And there are those to whom the instruction was openly regarding spirituality—meaning, that the Rebbe sent them for the purpose of education, strengthening Torah, spreading Judaism, and even teaching children the *aleph-beis*.

#### 208

Just as regarding those whose instruction was in the matter of physicality, it is understood that this is only the externality, and the inner intent is the matter of Torah and *mitzvos* [just as the primary intent in the general matter of business is for the *mitzvah* of *tzedakah*, *maaser*, or *chomesh*, or more than that (and especially according to what is explained in *Iggeres HaKodesh*[18](#_ftn1150) that in this time the primary *avodah* is *tzedakah*), and the portion given to *tzedakah* elevates everything[19](#_ftn1151)]—so too regarding those whose instruction was openly in a spiritual matter, they too must know that this is an external instruction relative to the inner intent of the matter.

This is similar to the statement of the Zohar[20](#_ftn1152), "This is a brain within a brain... this is a *klipah* to this, and this to this"—meaning, that even a thing that is an interiority and a brain relative to a lower level is only an externality and a *klipah* relative to a higher level.

Therefore, even those whose instruction was in a spiritual matter must contemplate whether this matter is already the ultimate goal, or if it is only the externality and the *klipah*. Just as the instruction in the matter of business is only the externality and has an inner intent, so too the instruction in the matter of spreading Torah, strengthening Judaism, and the like, is also an external instruction relative to the inner intent of the matter[l](#_ftn1155) (as follows).

**F.** All those whom the Rebbe sent to engage in spreading Judaism in the "provinces" (*arei hasadeh*),

— and not necessarily the literal provinces, but rather, once one leaves the Rebbe's chamber, where he received *yechidus*, where he prayed, and where he studied, every place where one is located is a "field" (*sadeh*) relative to the Rebbe's chamber, such that upon stepping over the threshold one is already in the "field," because the "splendor of man to dwell in the house"[21](#_ftn1153) is missing there[m](#_ftn1156) —

must know that in all matters of *shlichus* there is an inner intent.

And the inner intent is—to spread the *Toras HaChassidus*, as the Rebbe said[22](#_ftn1154) that the Alter Rebbe did not want to make the Chassidim into a party, but rather that the *Toras HaChassidus* is for all of Israel.

#### 209

And this is the concept of "May your springs be dispersed outward," which is the preparation[n](#_ftn1163) for the coming of Moshiach[23](#_ftn1157).

**G.** In general, there are four levels: *chullin*, *maaser*, *terumah*, and *kodesh*. And we also find a fifth level—"*mei chatas*" (the waters of purification), which even that which is pure for *kodesh* is insufficient for *chatas*[24](#_ftn1158). Likewise, there are five levels in the soul: *nefesh, ruach, neshamah, chayah, yechidah*[25](#_ftn1159). Accordingly, the Rebbe's speech and instruction were to each person according to his manner and level.

*Nefesh*—pertains to the matter of sin, as it is written[26](#_ftn1160), "If a *nefesh* sins." Therefore, to those at the level of *nefesh*, the instruction was openly regarding physicality. And to those at the level of *ruach* and *neshamah*, and all the more so *chayah* and *yechidah*, which are higher levels—the instruction to them was regarding higher matters, each according to his level.

However, one must know that just as the level of *nefesh* is only a preparation for a higher level, so too the levels of *ruach* and *neshamah*, and even *chayah* and *yechidah*, are only names and vessels for the essence of the soul, as indicated by the phrasing[25](#_ftn1159), "Five names were called *for it*," for the essence of the soul—meaning, that even *yechidah* (which is included in the five names) is only a name and a preparation for the essence of the soul[27](#_ftn1161).

Consequently, it is understood that in the speech to the level of *yechidah, chayah, neshamah, ruach*, or even *nefesh*—the intent and desire was to reach the essence of the soul.

Therefore, it is understood that all those who had a connection to the Rebbe, who now have a connection to the Rebbe, and consequently will have a connection even thereafter—because any holy thing, even if it departs, leaves its root in its place[28](#_ftn1162)—must know that in all the instructions they received from the Rebbe there is an inner intent[o](#_ftn1164), and the inner intent is—the interiority of Torah, "May your springs be dispersed outward," meaning, to spread the Torah of

#### 210

Chassidus in general that was revealed by the Baal Shem Tov and those who followed him, and the Torah of Chassidus Chabad that was revealed by the Alter Rebbe and those who followed him, up to and including the Rebbe, through which the inner intent is fulfilled and completed.

**H.** And when the inner intent is completed, there will be "for all the children of Israel... light in their dwellings"[29](#_ftn1165), and that which is written in our *parsha* will be fulfilled[30](#_ftn1166), "And the children of Israel went out with a high hand,"

— in the previous *parshiyos* the exile is discussed, and in our *parsha* is the matter of the Redemption —

and "Then *yashir* (will sing) Moshe"[31](#_ftn1167)—"It does not say *shar* (sang), but *yashir* (will sing); this is a source for the resurrection of the dead from the Torah"[32](#_ftn1168)—meaning, that very soon and in our days, "Moshe—of our generation—and the children of Israel will sing," with the *vav* of connection (not the *vav* of separation)—*yashir* is in the singular form[33](#_ftn1169),

and that which is written will be fulfilled[34](#_ftn1170), "Hashem shall reign forever and ever," and also in the Aramaic translation: "Hashem's kingdom endures forever and for all eternity,"

and simply—that speedily in our days we will see the Rebbe with physical eyes, and he will lead us to the true and complete Redemption—Amen.

***

**I.** Upon arriving in America, the Rebbe said: "*Azalt l'karta avad k'nimusa*" (When you go to a city, act according to its customs)[35](#_ftn1171). Here in America, they like to hear a proclamation, a statement, something novel, and better yet—something mind-boggling. I do not know if such a format is necessary, but—"*azalt l'karta avad k'nimusa*":

The three loves—love of Hashem, love of Torah, and love of Israel—are all one[36](#_ftn1172). It is impossible to divide between them, because they are all one, like a single essence. In *Toras HaChassidus*, it is brought in the name of the Baal Shem Tov[37](#_ftn1173) in the name of the early authorities: The essence—when you grasp a part of it, you grasp the whole of it. And in our case, since the three loves are one

#### 211

essence, it is understood that in each one of them are all three, because when you grasp a part of it, you grasp the whole of it.

When there is love of Hashem, but there is no love of Torah and love of Israel, this is an indication that there is a lack in love of Hashem as well. On the other hand, when there is love of Israel, even though it is one of the rational *mitzvos* that the intellect necessitates, nevertheless, ultimately, one arrives at love of Torah and love of Hashem. As is known[38](#_ftn1175) the story about the Tzemach Tzedek, that through performing an act of kindness for a Jew, he reached levels he did not reach through Torah and *avodah*.

This "statement" must be proclaimed and made known. When you see a Jew who has love of Hashem but does not have love of Torah and love of Israel, you must tell him that he should know that love of Hashem alone, without love of Torah and Israel, has no existence. On the other hand, when you see a Jew who only has love of Israel, you must strive to bring him to love of Torah and love of Hashem. And likewise, one must strive that his action in love of Israel should be expressed not only in giving bread to the hungry and water to the thirsty, but that out of love of Israel he should bring Jews closer to love of Torah and love of Hashem.

And when the three loves are together, it will be a "threefold cord" that "will not be broken"[39](#_ftn1176).

And through this, the Redemption will also come, for just as the cause for "we were exiled from our land" in the last exile is because of the opposite of love of Israel[40](#_ftn1177), so too through love of Israel will the Redemption come speedily in our days, literally.

***

**J.** (Someone asked regarding a *shlichus* that the Rebbe *z.t.l.k.l.h. n.b.g.m. z.y.e.* had placed upon him, and the Rebbe *shlita* answered:)

When the Rebbe *kudsha brich hu* turned fifteen years old, his father, the Rebbe (the Rashab) *n.e.*, took him as a secretary for communal affairs[41](#_ftn1178). To a certain rabbinical assembly that was held then (I believe in Kovno), the Rebbe *n.e.* sent the Rebbe *kudsha brich hu* as his representative[42](#_ftn1179). Since the Rebbe was young then, fifteen

#### 212

years old, the Rebbe *n.e.* sent the Rashbatz[43](#_ftn1180) with him. The Rashbatz was a very clever Jew, but the Rebbe *n.e.* commanded him to say that although he is sending him with him, he should know that the less he interferes, the better ("*vet zayn alt glaycher*").

(And the Rebbe *shlita* concluded:) And if it was so then, all the more so now: Why must one interfere in the Rebbe's affairs?! There is no need to give him advice or offer opinions. One must fulfill and carry out his will, and the less interference with "one's own interpretations," the better.

***

**K.** The *maamar* *Basi L'Gani*—edited by the Rebbe *shlita*.

[Before opening the *maamar*, he said: The *maamar* that the Rebbe *kudsha brich hu* gave for the day of his passing begins[44](#_ftn1181): *Basi L'Gani*... (until the end of section 3),

Afterward, he paused and commanded to play the *nigun* of the "Beinoni," and said: The Rebbe *kudsha brich hu* used to cherish this *nigun*. Afterward, he commanded to play a *nigun* from the Rebbe *n.e.*,

Afterward, he continued the *maamar*: And now, after he explains in the *maamar* that the essence of the *Shechinah* was in the lower worlds... (until the end of section 5),

Afterward, he paused and commanded to play a *nigun* from the Rebbe Maharash, and afterward a *nigun* from the Rebbe the Tzemach Tzedek,

Afterward, he continued the *maamar*: And now, at the conclusion of the *maamar* he explains... (until the end),

After the recitation of the *maamar* and during the break in the following *sicha*, he commanded to play a *nigun* from the Mitteler Rebbe and the *nigun* of the Alter Rebbe (the four stanzas) as follows.]

***

**L.** [After the *maamar*, the Rebbe *shlita* said:]

Now, listen, Jews!

In general, in Chabad, there was the demand that the *avodah* of each person be his own, and not to rely on the Rebbes.

This is the difference[45](#_ftn1182) between the Polish method and the Chabad method. The Polish method is "and the Tzaddik shall live by his faith"[46](#_ftn1183)—do not read *yichyeh* (with a *sheva*), but *yechayeh* (with a *pasach*). But we, Chabad, must all work ourselves, with the 248 limbs and 365 sinews of the body, and with the 248 limbs and 365 sinews of the soul.

"Everything is in the hands of Heaven except for the fear of Heaven"[47](#_ftn1184). I am not removing myself ("*ich zog zich nit op*") *chas v'shalom* from assisting, assisting as much as I can, but, since everything is in the hands of Heaven except for the fear of Heaven, if there is no *avodah* on your own, what will it help that you give "writings," play *nigunim*, and say *l'chaim*?

The Rebbe would sometimes say: "*Leygt zich nit arayn kayn foygelech in buzhem* (Do not put birds in your bosom)..."

You must *yourself* transform the foolishness of the *sitra achra* and the fervor ("*der koch*") of the animal soul—into holiness[48](#_ftn1185).

**M.** Regarding the *Mishkan*—Moshe could have done it alone, and likewise regarding the *Beis HaMikdash*—David could have done it alone, but their desire was to grant merit to all the children of Israel.

Likewise, when the Rebbe *kudsha brich hu* wrote the *Sefer Torah* for the welcoming of Moshiach *Tzidkeinu*, he said that he did not want to do it alone, but his desire was for the participation of all of Israel, in order to grant merit in the matter to all of Israel[49](#_ftn1186).

And it is obvious that in the making of a dwelling for Him, *yisbarach*, in the lower worlds—we must all participate, and all the children of Israel. Each person must do it himself, to fulfill his *shlichus*. Only small vessels remain, and when they finish them, then the prophecy[50](#_ftn1187) will be fulfilled, "And saviors shall ascend, etc.," meaning, that the three impure *klipos* will be pushed away and annulled, and *klipas nogah*, the totality of the world, will be elevated to holiness, and the purpose of creation will be completed—that there will be a dwelling for Him, *yisbarach*, in the lower worlds[51](#_ftn1188).

***

**N.** (He commanded to play one of the *nigunim* of the Mitteler Rebbe, and after the *nigun* he said:)

It was discussed on 19 Kislev[52](#_ftn1189) that a distribution of Mishnayos should be arranged, that each person should take five

#### 214

chapters and finish them by 10 Shevat, and certainly everyone finished. And according to the Jewish custom to say something at the conclusion, I will say a few words ("*vel ich zogan a por verter*") briefly.

In the *Mishnah* preceding the final *Mishnah*, we learned[53](#_ftn1190): "Honeycomb—from when does it become susceptible to impurity as a liquid? From when one intends [to eat it], Beit Hillel says: From when one crushes it."

Meaning: According to Beit Shammai, the status and situation of a thing changes ("*shtelt zich iber a zach*") through thought alone, and according to Beit Hillel, an action is required.

And now, although "Beit Shammai in the place of Beit Hillel is not a *Mishnah*"[55](#_ftn1192), it is known that in the time to come, the *halachah* will be like Beit Shammai[56](#_ftn1193). And since we are already going toward the time to come ("*itzter geyt doch shoyn tzu l'asid lavo*"), *Erev Shabbos*, there is already the concept of "*toameha*"[57](#_ftn1194), the tasting of the opinion of Beit Shammai—that through thought alone we should already be transferred ("*zol men shoyn ibergeshtelt vern*") to a higher status and situation.

And in our case:

Standing in the presence of ten from Israel, "When ten sit together, the *Shechinah* rests"[58](#_ftn1195), and especially when there are several times ten, and especially in the *shul* and *beis medrash* (as is known[59](#_ftn1196) that there is a merit in the *shul* relative to the *beis medrash* and in the *beis medrash* relative to the *shul*), and with greater intensity and greater strength in the Rebbe's four cubits, in the place where he lived for many years, and where he prayed and studied—each person stands with the awakening that from today onward his conduct will be as it ought to be. And since we are going toward the time to come, then the *halachah* is like Beit Shammai, that thought alone transfers ("*shtelt iber*") to a different status and situation, and there will be the exodus from the straits to the expanse.

**O.** At the conclusion of the Mishnayos: "Hashem did not find a vessel that holds blessing for Israel other than peace." And as we say[60](#_ftn1197), "Bless us, our Father, all of us as one."

#### 215

Through peace, all obscurations, concealments, and limitations are removed.

And since thought is effective[61](#_ftn1198), through deciding that this vessel that holds blessing will be peace, then the exodus from the status and situation of "*be'arvin*" (in the evenings) occurs—as it says at the beginning of the Mishnayos, "From when do we recite the *Shema* *be'arvin*," that even then ("*be'arvin*") there must be the matter of *Krias Shema*, that there should be the recognition that "Hashem is One"[62](#_ftn1199)—only that through peace there will soon, literally, be *Krias Shema* "in the morning."

And although there is also the interpretation of "*shachar*" (morning) from the word *shachrus* (blackness)[63](#_ftn1200), this will be transformed into the interpretation of "*shachar*" from the word *boker* (morning) and day, and "the night will shine like the day"[64](#_ftn1201), that the "*arvin*" itself will shine[65](#_ftn1202).

And all this will be with the coming of Moshiach *Tzidkeinu*, which we will merit speedily and in a near time.

**P.** (He commanded to play a *nigun* of the Alter Rebbe—the four stanzas—and after the *nigun* he said:)

The Rebbe *kudsha brich hu* related[66](#_ftn1203) that when it was discussed regarding the acceptance of the matters of *nesi'us* from his father, the Rebbe (the Rashab) *n.e.*, he requested that it be with kindness and mercy.

Likewise, the Rebbe *kudsha brich hu* said[67](#_ftn1204)—when speaking about the coming of Moshiach—that in his days this matter will occur. And there is no difficulty in the matter—because it is explicit in the *Yerushalmi*[68](#_ftn1205) (and brought also in *Yalkut Shimoni*[69](#_ftn1206)) that when the conduct is in fear before Him under His rule and guidance, then even after twenty years it is considered that he is present here[70](#_ftn1207).

Why was the matter delayed?

— A Jew related to me in his letter, that in the year 5683 he asked the Rebbe *kudsha brich hu* about a trip to Italy, and the Rebbe *kudsha brich hu* answered him: "For everything there is a time," and advised him to go study in Tomchei Tmimim. Only now did he arrive in Italy, and he writes to me that now he understands the words of the Rebbe that he said to him twenty-seven years ago!

#### 216

For us—the matter will not last for years, *chas v'shalom*, but will be with speed.

We only need to complete the *avodah* with the "small vessels," we need to change the habits and assumptions, and then there will be the matter of "the glory of the Holy One, blessed be He, is exalted in all worlds"[71](#_ftn1208), and the supreme intent will be completed.

**Q.** (Before leaving he said:)

"For you shall go out with joy, and be led forth in peace, etc."[72](#_ftn1209).

When there is joy, which will then naturally lead to peace, that all those who are connected to the Rebbe will be in unity—then (as the verse continues) even "the mountains and the hills," not only will they not hinder, but they will assist, "and all the trees of the field," the barren trees that do not bear fruit, will bear fruit, as our Sages say[73](#_ftn1210), "In the future, barren trees will bear fruit"; but all this is on the condition that there be peace, that all those who belong to the Rebbe will be in unity.

And then Hashem will help to complete the intent that the Rebbe placed upon all of us and entrusted to us, which is the ultimate good possible.

## B’s”d. Shabbos Parshas Beshalach, 13 Shevat, 5711

#### 217

**"You who dwell in the gardens, the companions hearken to your voice"**[1](#_ftn1211]. My revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, brings in his maamar[2](#_ftn1212) (a continuation of the maamar on his histalkus) two interpretations that seemingly contradict one another. The first interpretation[3](#_ftn1213) is that "gardens" refers to this world, and "you who dwell in the gardens" refers to the Assembly of Israel, which is scattered in exile, grazing in the gardens of others. Nevertheless, when they sit in shuls and batei medrash, the "companions"—who are the ministering angels, called companions because they possess neither jealousy, nor hatred, nor competition—hearken to your voice. The second interpretation[5](#_ftn1215) is that "gardens" refers to Gan Eden[6](#_ftn1216). Although there are countless levels within it, they are generally divided into two categories: the Lower Gan Eden and the Upper Gan Eden[7](#_ftn1217). "The companions hearken" refers to the souls in Gan Eden, who are called companions, as explained in the parenthetical note[8](#_ftn1218) that sometimes a soul is "emitted" from a soul, etc. One can say the precision here is that it teaches us that the connection between souls is not merely a general connection, but rather that one soul is emitted from another. The definition of this concept of *atzilus* was explained previously (in the maamar *Basi L’Gani*[9](#_ftn1219)), that it is the revelation of

#### 218

the concealment—meaning that it is one thing; it is the very same thing, only it has descended and been revealed from its state of concealment. Just as the concealed powers that subsequently descended and were revealed from their concealment—which is why one cannot say that the purpose of creation is for the world of Atzilus, since because it is a revelation of the concealment, it is a descent—rather, the ultimate purpose is this lower world. Similarly, it is the same regarding the connection of the aforementioned souls, which is the concept of *atzilus* and the revelation of the concealment.

b) **To understand** the connection between these two interpretations: previously in the maamar[10](#_ftn1220), it is explained that when the soul descends below and is enclothed in a body, although the body conceals and hides, nevertheless, through avodah, one removes the concealment and hiding. On the contrary, through this descent and enclothement, it is strengthened with an added measure of power. The precision of the language "on the contrary" is as explained by our Rebbe the Alter Rebbe (Iggeres HaKodesh, section 25[11](#_ftn1221)) regarding the words of the Baal Shem Tov[12](#_ftn1222) concerning anger. For example, if a non-Jew stands before him and speaks and distracts him, not only is he not affected by him, and he davens as if the non-Jew had not distracted him, but even more so, he gains strength and additional power when he contemplates the concept of the exile of the Shechinah, which is enclothed in a state of exile within this distracting speech. It turns out that through this distraction, the person is aroused even more. The Mitteler Rebbe also explains this (in Torah Or[13](#_ftn1223)—the matter is there in brief, but in Toras Chaim on this parsha[14](#_ftn1224) it is explained at length) regarding the verse "And it was when Pharaoh sent out the people"[15](#_ftn1225). The intent is that not only did the kelipah of Pharaoh not conceal and hide, but on the contrary, it even assisted. As it is written[16](#_ftn1226), "And Pharaoh drew near," and it is stated in the Midrash[17](#_ftn1227) that he drew the heart of Israel closer to their Father in Heaven. Furthermore, "Pharaoh sent out the people"—Pharaoh went along with the people—meaning that even the sparks that had fallen there ascended with them. This is also the precision of the language "on the contrary"—meaning not only does the body not conceal and hide the soul, and it remains in its state as if there were no concealment or hiding, but on the contrary, through the initial concealment, the person is strengthened with an added measure of power. This is the primary intent in the creation of the worlds:

#### 219

*iskafya* and *is’hapcha* of the foolishness of the *sitra achra* and the *koach* of the *nefesh habahamit* and the matters of the world—into holiness. And although it is explained in many places that the performance of mitzvos is to add lights in Atzilus, it has already been explained above[18](#_ftn1230) that the essential aspect of this is in this world. As the Tzemach Tzedek and the Rebbe Maharash[19](#_ftn1231) stated, the lights as they are in Atzilus are like items placed in a box. Not only is the primary revelation—the primary Shechinah—in this world (as explained above[20](#_ftn1232) at length by the Rebbe Rashab regarding the concept of "the primary Shechinah"), but even more than this, the Alter Rebbe explains[21](#_ftn1233)—and so too from the Maggid[22](#_ftn1234)—regarding the saying of our Sages[23](#_ftn1235), "Know what is above you": know that "what is above"—all the matters of above—"is from you," and the matter depends on you.

c) **This is** the concept of "You who dwell in the gardens"—the souls dwelling in the Lower Gan Eden and the Upper Gan Eden come to hearken to the voice of the souls of Israel below. The intent is that even the souls as they are above, before their descent into the body, and also those souls that have already been in a body—which possess the advantage that comes from the avodah of the body, for during the time they were in the body, "days were fashioned"[d](#_ftn1228) and one of them was His[24](#_ftn1236), for they drew down the "One" into them and completed all their avodah, for which reason they are called "Israel, the hosts of Hashem"[25](#_ftn1237) (as explained in the aforementioned maamar of my father-in-law, the Rebbe[8](#_ftn1218))—for "host" (*tzava*) has three interpretations: 1) A term for an army, meaning *kabbalas ol* (acceptance of the yoke). 2) A fixed time, meaning that at the time fixed for them, they complete all their avodah. 3) A term for *tzivyon*, which means beauty—not just will, but beauty, which comes from the inwardness of Keter and causes *taanug*[e](#_ftn1229), for which they are called "hosts of Hashem." Nevertheless, they all come to hearken to the voice of the souls enclothed in bodies, even if their avodah is not yet complete—not in the first interpretation of *tzava* as an army, whose matter is *kabbalas ol*; not

#### 220

in the second interpretation of *tzava* as "days were fashioned, and not one was missing"[f](#_ftn1236); and not in the third interpretation of *tzava* as beauty. As the maamar[8](#_ftn1218) concludes, when one studies Torah without mentioning conditions in the manner of Torah study, and performs the mitzvos without mentioning conditions in the manner of performing the mitzvos, then *kesher* (a knot/connection) and *sheker* (falsehood)—the falsehood of the world—is transformed into *keresh* (a plank), "the acacia planks standing"[26](#_ftn1242), connecting the light of the Ein Sof with the world—an *is’hapcha* from one extreme to the other. For one of the permutations of *keresh* is *kesher*. A *kesher* of holiness, whose matter is connection. This is unlike the *sitra achra*, for "you shall not call 'conspiracy' (*kesher*) all that this people calls 'conspiracy'"[g](#_ftn1238), because their matter is separation and division. But the connection of holiness—all are called companions, "the companions hearken." The souls as they are above, and also the souls that have already been in a body—which possess the advantage of avodah that comes from the body, because they completed all their avodah in this world, in all three interpretations of *tzava* mentioned above—all come to hearken and receive the voice of the souls enclothed in bodies, even though they have not yet completed their avodah. For even though they are scattered in exile and grazing in the gardens of others, nevertheless, they tear themselves away from the world, and they take along the body and the *nefesh habahamit*, and they come to shuls and batei medrash, and they recite the Shema, and they occupy themselves with Torah, which is the very concept of *mesiras nefesh*[h](#_ftn1239), and this is possessed only in this world. Therefore, the companions—even the souls in Gan Eden[i](#_ftn1240)—hearken to their voice, and the Holy One, Blessed be He, also says, "I and My entourage come to listen to your voice." And this is "days were fashioned, and not"—it is written "not" (*lo*) but read "for Him" (*lo*)[j](#_ftn1241)—that in their avodah, the avodah of the soul in the body, *in* the body and *with* the body, they draw down from above the *hishtalshelus* into that which is below the *hishtalshelus*, "One" into them, so that "Hashem will be One and His Name One"[27](#_ftn1243).

## With the help of Hashem. Sicha of Shabbos Parshas Beshalach, 13 Shevat, 5711

#### 221

**A.** [The Rebbe] commanded to play a nigun and recited the Maamar entitled *HaYosheves B’Ganim* – which was edited by the Rebbe shlita.

***

**B.** The righteous Rabbanit, whose Yahrtzeit it is, was among those who would copy the writings of the Rebbe Maharash [1].

Since the Rebbe Maharash was extremely organized and his daily schedule was well known, including the times he would go out for a walk, they would sneak in while he was out (after posting a guard to provide advance notice of his return) and copy the writings of Chassidus. In this manner, they copied many manuscripts. One of those who copied them was, as mentioned, the righteous Rabbanit whose Yahrtzeit it is.

In the possession of the Rebbe (Rayatz) were her copies of the Rebbe Maharash’s writings, kept in one folder together with the *hanachos* (transcriptions) of the Rebbe (Rashab) n’e.

**C.** The Rebbe (Rayatz) related that he conducted himself in the same way with his father, the Rebbe (Rashab) n’e.

Once, his father, the Rebbe n’e, caught him copying manuscripts and said to him: "In my own home, am I no longer the master?!"

From these words, the Rebbe (Rayatz) felt a powerful breaking of the heart and asked for a *tikkun* for this.

After some time, his father, the Rebbe n’e, gave him permission and access to the manuscripts, and when he would travel, he would leave him the keys to the cabinets [2].

**D.** Seemingly, this is difficult to understand:

#### 222

The Rebbe Maharash surely surmised, and perhaps even knew clearly, that the manuscripts were being copied during his travels, for he knew the Rebbe (Rashab) n’e and his longing for the writings of Chassidus. If so, one must ask: If he did not want the manuscripts to be copied, he could have secured them in such a way that it would be impossible to copy them; and if he did not mind that they were being copied, he could have granted permission for it. Why did the copying of the manuscripts have to take place in such a manner?

Likewise, it is difficult to understand regarding the manuscripts that the Rebbe (Rayatz) copied from the Rebbe n’e—why did it have to be in such a way, without permission?

The explanation for this is as follows:

In the second Maamar recited after the continuation of the Maamarim of Rosh Hashanah (in the year 5694—printed for this year’s Rosh Hashanah)—the Maamar on Parshas Vayishlach, entitled *Vayomer... Yisrael Yihyeh Shimecha* [3]—it is explained why Yitzchak’s blessings to Yaakov had to be specifically through "deceit" (through the wisdom of his Torah [4], but in a manner called "deceit"), as it is written [5], "Your brother came with deceit and took your blessing." This is because the fall of the *nitzotzoi d'kedusha* (sparks of holiness) below, caused by the sin of the Tree of Knowledge, occurred through deceit, as it is written [6], "And the serpent was cunning..." Therefore, the order of their elevation by Yaakov (who is akin to Adam HaRishon [7]), who takes the blessings from Esav, must also be specifically through deceit, as it is written [8], "With the crooked, you act deviously."

One should also add and explain the words of Rivkah to Yaakov (when she told him to go and take the blessings through deceit), "Upon me be your curse, my son" [9]. If there were to be a curse, Heaven forbid, she takes it upon herself. Seemingly, what comfort is this? Every son, and especially one like Yaakov, worries for his mother; if so, what is the benefit in the response, "Upon me be your curse, my son"? Yet we see that this response did indeed move Yaakov!

The matter, in short:

When one must take a matter of such a nature and from such a place that it is above intellect, choice, and the will of the giver, the recipient must also have a fitting vessel—not intellect, reason, and knowledge, but the movement of *mesiras nefesh*, placing oneself in danger.

#### 223

This is "Upon me be your curse, my son"—that she is prepared even for that. On the contrary: this matter requires *mesiras nefesh*, and it is received only through *mesiras nefesh* specifically, not through calculations based on reason and knowledge. This response also activated in Yaakov a movement of *mesiras nefesh*.

Based on this, it is also understood regarding Torah in general [11], and specifically the inner dimension of the Torah, as in the present case regarding the copying of the manuscripts—that there is a higher level reached through a manner of "deceit of holiness," without the knowledge of the giver and with a movement of *mesiras nefesh* on the part of the recipient [12] (risking receiving a *kpidah* from the Rebbe, etc.).

**E.** This matter (that through deceit one arrives at a higher level) is explained by the Rebbe (Rayatz) in the *Maamar HaHillula* [13]—that the intention is to transform the *shtus* (folly) of the *sitra achra* into the *shtus* of holiness. For, by transforming the *shtus* of the *sitra achra*, one reaches a higher level than through *avodah* that is based on reason and knowledge—a *shtus* of holiness that is above the reason and knowledge of holiness [14].

Based on this, one can explain what the Rebbe (Rayatz) wrote in the *Maamar HaHillula* [15] regarding the concept that "the essence of the *Shechinah* was in the lower worlds" [16], that "the essence of the revelation of Elokus was in the Beis Hamikdash (and proof of this is) as it is written [17], 'And they shall make Me a sanctuary and I will dwell in them'—it does not say 'in it' (singular), but 'in them' (plural), within each and every one of the Jewish people." Seemingly, this is difficult to understand: What is the proof from the indwelling of the *Shechinah* *in the souls of the Jewish people* ("and I will dwell in them," "within each and every one of the Jewish people") regarding the indwelling of the *Shechinah* *in the world* (the essence of the *Shechinah* was in the lower worlds and the essence of the revelation of Elokus was in the Beis Hamikdash)? After all, the souls of the Jewish people are *Elokus*, where the *Elokus* is made into a *yesh* [18]; how can one bring proof from the indwelling of the *Shechinah* *in them* to the indwelling of the *Shechinah* *in the world*?

The matter is—seemingly, it is difficult to understand from the other side: What is the need for the prerequisite, "And they shall make Me a sanctuary," in order for there to be "and I will dwell in them," within each one?

#### 224

Since "the soul You have placed within me is pure" [19], "you are children to Hashem your G-d" [20], etc., etc.—this should be sufficient for there to be "and I will dwell in them." What is the necessity for the prerequisite of "And they shall make Me a sanctuary" so that only afterwards there will be "and I will dwell in them"?

The explanation for this is that the *avodah* of the soul on its own is an *avodah* based on reason and knowledge, whereas its *avodah* through *mesiras nefesh*, *shtus* of holiness, is awakened specifically through the *elem v'hester* (concealment) of the world, the body, and the *nefesh habahamit*. Therefore, the condition for the matter of "and I will dwell in them"—the *essence* of the *Shechinah* and not merely an illumination—is specifically through "And they shall make Me a sanctuary," a "sanctuary which is called a *mishkan*" [21], which is made from "standing acacia wood" [22]. "Acacia wood" (*atzei shittim*) refers to the *shtus* of the *sitra achra* which one transforms into the *shtus* of holiness (as explained in the Maamar [13]), which "stands" and connects the *Ohr Ein Sof* with the lower realms [23].

***

**F.** At the time of the wedding [24], the Rebbe (Rayatz) said [25] that at the joy of a wedding, the souls of the forefathers up to three generations back come from the World of Truth to every Jew, and there are those for whom more and more generations back come. The Rebbe (Rayatz) enumerated all the Rebbes, up to the Alter Rebbe.

Since at that time the Rebbe (Rayatz) did not enumerate further (before the Alter Rebbe), therefore, in the Maamar recited on 10 Shevat [26], I did not mention by name any further than the Alter Rebbe. I am afraid to intervene, and in general, why intervene, since the Rebbe did not mention more?

However, since it bothered me nonetheless ("*es hot mir doch geshtert*"), therefore, today, 13 Shevat, which is still in the continuation of 10 Shevat—as emphasized by the fact that the Maamar *HaYosheves B'Ganim* of 13 Shevat is a continuation of the Maamar *Basi L'Gani* of 10 Shevat—I mentioned [27] by name up to the Baal Shem Tov.

This matter (the mentioning by name) is similar to the well-known concept [28] that one who truly grieves over

#### 225

the scarcity or lack of understanding of the words of our Sages, and mentions their names, and his soul yearns for them, etc.—this is a significant matter and has benefit in several areas. And also, similar to what we find in *avodah*, that they would say, "The entire East illuminated until Chevron," in order to mention and draw down the merit of the forefathers [29].

***

**G.** It is known from the statement of the Baal Shem Tov [30] that he had the ability to ascend in a whirlwind to the heavens [31] like Eliyahu HaNavi, but he wanted to experience the matter of "for you are dust and to dust you shall return" [32].

Seemingly: Since there is a virtue in the matter of "and to dust you shall return," is it possible that Eliyahu HaNavi lacked this perfection?

Rather, the matter is that the perfection of every thing is expressed by the fact that it completes *its* own matter, the matter incumbent *upon it*.

Consequently, it is understood that for Eliyahu HaNavi, who by his nature had to act in a certain way, he needed to ascend in a whirlwind to the heavens—that is his perfection; and for the Baal Shem Tov, who by his nature had to act in a certain way, he needed to undergo the matter of "to dust you shall return"—that is his perfection.

**H.** One may interpret this as follows:

The nature of Eliyahu HaNavi [33] is to come to a *bris milah*, to come on the night of Pesach, to save Rav Hamnuna Sava [34].

The difference between them is that his coming to a *bris milah* and on the night of Pesach is without a body, whereas to save Rav Hamnuna Sava, he clothed himself in a body out of respect for him. Based on this, it is resolved [35] why it is said that Eliyahu HaNavi could not come to the *Idra* of the Rashbi because he was busy saving Rav Hamnuna Sava—seemingly, he is present

#### 226

at many *bris milahs* at the same time, and likewise on the nights of Pesach he comes to all the homes of the Jewish people at the same time; why is the *Idra* of the Rashbi different? Rather, at a *bris milah* he comes without a body, and it is only a spark, and therefore he can be in many places at once. Not so for the honor of the *tzaddikim*; he comes in his body, in his entire essence, and therefore he cannot be in two places at once.

Likewise, it is the nature of Eliyahu to deliver missions to the Sages, and last but not least: before the coming of Moshiach, he comes to bring hearts closer and to announce the coming of Moshiach [36]. And for this purpose, too, he comes in his body, as is necessitated by the fact that in the *Shas* [37] they connect this matter to the law of *techumin* (boundaries) on Shabbos.

Therefore, Eliyahu HaNavi needed to ascend in his body in a whirlwind to the heavens—so that his body would remain in perfection, in the world of *Yetzirah* [38], and when there is a need for it, he returns and clothes himself in his body and comes below. And in that is his perfection.

**I.** And the nature of the Baal Shem Tov—as is known [39] that at the time of the Baal Shem Tov’s birth, the Jewish people were in a state of fainting, and through the soul of the Baal Shem Tov, who is called *Yisrael*, they were awakened, similar to a person who faints and is awakened by calling his name into his ear.

— Several years ago, they approached the Rebbe (Rayatz) regarding a woman who was very ill and had been in a state of unconsciousness for a long time, and the Rebbe (Rayatz) said that they should whisper *his* (the Rebbe’s) name in her ear. They did so, and she regained consciousness, and over time she returned to health [40].

Seemingly: What does the Rebbe’s name have to do with that woman, that whispering the Rebbe’s name in her ear would help her?

The explanation for this is that the reason for awakening from fainting by calling a name is because during fainting, the specific vitality departs, but the general vitality remains. By calling the name, which reaches ("*derlangt*") the general vitality, one awakens the general vitality so that it will be drawn down and come into revelation [41]. From this, it is understood

#### 227

that even when the general vitality is lacking, by whispering the Rebbe’s name in one’s ear—for his soul is a general soul, and in relation to it, even the general vitality of the sick person’s soul is but a detail—then vitality is drawn down even to his general vitality.

This is the matter of the awakening of the Jewish people from fainting through the descent of the Baal Shem Tov’s soul into this world—because the Baal Shem Tov’s soul is a general soul of the Jewish people.

And since it is the nature of the Baal Shem Tov to awaken all the Jewish people, even the lowest of the low and the most insignificant among them, to pass through and reach even the lowest levels, down to the very bottom, and even there to effect the awakening and the connection with the Holy One, Blessed be He, the Essence and Being of the *Ein Sof*—therefore he needed, and consequently it was his will, to experience the matter of "and to dust you shall return."

And since this is the nature of the Baal Shem Tov—it is understood that specifically in this is his perfection.

**J.** The lesson from the above regarding *avodah*, and to us in particular:

Our matter is—not to chase ("*yogen zich*") specifically after greatness and wonders (even if one is certain that he knows what greatness and wonders are), because if it is not of his matter, of the matter of his mission in this world, then, besides the fact that it is highly doubtful whether he will reach it, what is the benefit of greatness and wonders when he is not fulfilling the mission that Divine Providence has placed upon him?! And more simply: what is the benefit of greatness and wonders, and what greatness and wonders are there—if he is not fulfilling the command of the Holy One, Blessed be He, through His servants the *tzaddikim* regarding his *avodah* and his activity?!

And the conclusion regarding us in practice:

When the Rebbe has given him a mission, a specific *avodah*—even if it seems to him that he was created for greater things, and he has blessed himself in his heart saying that he has the strength to reach them—he must know that this is not his path, and not through this will he reach his perfection. May it not be the opposite of this, Heaven forbid.

One must "hold onto the handle" [42], and walk "in the straight path which He has taught us, and we shall walk in His ways" [43], and then it will be good for him in this world and the next.

***

#### 228

**K.** They asked me about the fact that I say that soon the prophecy [44] "Awake and sing, you who dwell in the dust" will be fulfilled, and he—the Rebbe (Rayatz)—will be among them, and he—the Rebbe—will lead us out of exile—after all, the order is (as is also brought in the teachings of Chassidus) [45] that first there will be the coming of Moshiach and the days of Moshiach, and only after a period of time will the dead be resurrected?

The answer to this:

Even though *in general* the order is [46]: the coming of Moshiach, the building of the Beis Hamikdash, the ingathering of the exiles, and the resurrection of the dead, nevertheless, the resurrection of *individuals* has occurred and will occur even before that. As is known, there are many stories in the *Shas* and *Midrashim* and from *tzaddikim* who resurrected the dead, and as our Sages said [47], "The smallest among you resurrect the dead."

***

**L.** It was discussed [48] regarding the matter of *teshuvah*—that it is not a matter of confession specifically; on the contrary, its essence is the nullification of the soul to its root and source, as it is written, "And the spirit shall return to G-d" [49].

This is: "In one moment" (*b'sha'ata chada*) [50]—"one turn" (*ein ker*) (the word *sha'ah* is related to *pina*, to turn) [51].

Consequently, this is permitted, possible, and mandatory even on Shabbos, the letters of which are *tashuv* (return) [52].

The departure from one’s own matters—to above, this is not "work of the weekday," and consequently it is possible on Shabbos [53].

**M.** It was discussed in continuation of the above—that even though it is in one moment, and only small remnants remain, nonetheless, one needs *zerizus* (alacrity) in this, and it is known [54] that *zerizus* is the opposite of sadness, and comes through joy.

#### 229

And the *zerizus* must be in all three interpretations of "army" (*tzava*) explained in the *Maamar HaHillula* [55].

And since the *Nesi'im* demand this matter from us, they certainly do so themselves regarding themselves as our *Nesi'im* and leaders, as explained in the matter of "He tells *His words* to Yaakov" [56].

This is also the help and assistance that they give us in our *avodah*—that it should be in the straight path.

— Easily, I do not know if it should be said, since *avodah* must be by way of *avodah* (toil) specifically, and not served ready-made; but what is certain—without concealments and hiddenness, and with success.

## B"H, 15 Shevat, Rosh Hashanah L'Ilanot 5711

#### 230

Brooklyn, N.Y.

Greetings and blessings!

The year of the histalkus of our Nasi, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, has concluded.

Our longing intensifies, for the summer has passed, the winter has ended, and we have not been saved.

Yet, on the other hand, habit takes its toll. There is room for concern that the matter may become stale, and that the light and warmth of our hiskashrus to our Nasi—to his Torah and his directives, which are all one—will gradually diminish, Heaven forbid.

These are the words that Moshe spoke regarding Torah: "These words that I command you *today*," which is interpreted as a new royal decree that everyone rushes to receive. And regarding mitzvos: "My mitzvos that I command you *today*," which is interpreted to mean that they should be as new to you as if you had heard them that very day.

## With the help of Heaven. Shabbos Parshas Mishpatim, Mevarchim HaChodesh Adar Rishon, 5711

#### 231

(An unedited transcript)

**"And these are the ordinances which you shall set before them; if you buy a Hebrew servant..."**[1] It is well known that there is a nuance here:[2] "Before them" (*lifnehem*) is in the plural, yet afterwards it is written "if you buy" (*ki tikneh*), in the singular. It is explained in this regard[3] that "if you buy" refers not to the word "before them," but to the phrase "which you shall set," which refers to Moshe Rabbeinu. It is of him that it is said, "if you buy a Hebrew servant," because he is the one who draws down *da'as* into the souls of Yisrael.

b) **The explanation of this matter in brief:** It is written,[4] "And I will sow the house of Yisrael with the seed of man and the seed of beast." The totality of the souls of Yisrael is divided into two categories: "seed of man" and "seed of beast." "Seed of man" are the souls of Atzilus, which were few even in earlier generations. "Seed of beast" are the souls of Biyah, and almost all souls in our current generations are "seed of beast,"[5] so called because they lack *da'as*. The role of Moshe Rabbeinu is to draw down *da'as* into the souls that are in the category of "seed of beast." For Moshe is one of the seven shepherds[6] who draw down vitality and Elokus to the totality of the souls of Yisrael—which is why they are called "shepherds"—and Moshe is the totality of them all. He is called *Ra'aya Mehimna* (the Faithful Shepherd), meaning that he draws down the level of *da'as* into them, as he is at the level of *da'as elyon*.[7]

c) **To understand this in greater detail:** Why is the matter of *da'as* specifically necessary,[8] given that it is one of the three *mochin* (intellectual faculties) and the last of them? The virtue of *da'as* is that it is specifically through it that the birth of the *midos* (emotional attributes) occurs. As explained in Tanya,[9] if a person does not bind his *da'as* and fix his thought firmly, then even if he possesses the aspects of *chochma* and *binah* regarding the greatness of Hashem, he will not give birth in his soul to true *yirah* and *ahavah*, but only to false imaginings. Therefore, *da'as* is the sustenance and vitality of the *midos*, and it includes *chesed* and *gevurah*—meaning *ahavah* and its branches, and *yirah* and its branches. This is why[10] a minor, even if he is intelligent and even sharp-witted, is not subject to the obligation and responsibility of Torah and *mitzvos*—neither in the fulfillment of positive commandments nor in the observance of negative ones—because he is not a "master of *da'as*." Even if he knows and understands, he lacks the aspect of *da'as* that would make the matter "touch" him so that he acts accordingly. The matter is as follows: The *moch* of *chochma*, which is the beginning of intellect (and above this there is the aspect of *chochma* which is the source of intellect, but regarding *avodah*, it is the beginning of intellect, the point of *chochma* called *hanacha*), contains the details of the intellect, but they are included within the point of the intellect, and the inclinations toward *chesed* or *gevurah* are also there, but in a state of concealment. The aspect of *binah* is the detailing of the matters included in the point of *chochma*, and the revelation of the inclinations toward *chesed* or *gevurah*, etc. Yet, the matters can still easily change from one side to the other. However, the aspect of *da'as* comes from the language of connection (*hiskashrus*), recognition (*hakara*), and feeling (*hargasha*), which are three levels in this *da'as*, one above the other. At first, one connects himself to the matter; through this, he comes to a recognition of the matter, until he arrives at a feeling—meaning that his recognition of this matter is so forceful that it is not merely a recognition in the mind, but he also feels in his heart that this is how the matter is. When he reaches this state, he then knows his standing and his situation.

**This is the difference** between the souls of Atzilus, which are "seed of man," and the souls of Biyah, which are "seed of beast." In the worlds of Biyah, the *bitul* is only a *bitul* of *yesh* (nullification of existence). This means that even though there is an aspect of grasping Elokus through the intellect, and they know that this is how it should be, nevertheless, in practice, the *bitul* is only a *bitul* of *yesh*—their knowledge does not cause it to be so for them. This is because they lack the aspect of *da'as*. Therefore,[11] the angels are called *chayos* (living beings) and *behemos* (beasts), because they lack the aspect of *da'as*, and for this reason, their *bitul* is only a *bitul* of *yesh*. However, the *bitul* of Atzilus is a *bitul* in reality (*bitul b'metzius*), because the nature of Atzilus is that it is not just that there is an understanding and grasp that it should be so, but that it actually becomes so—and this is due to the aspect of *da'as*. Therefore, the souls of Atzilus are called "seed of man" (*Adam*), and *Adam* has the numerical value of *Mah* (45),[12] for they possess the aspect of *bitul* that comes through *da'as*. This is the role of Moshe, of whom it is written, "if you buy a Hebrew servant," for he is the one who draws down the level of *da'as* into the souls of "seed of beast."

#### 233

d) **However,**[13] one still needs to understand how it is possible to draw down into the souls of "seed of beast" the level of *da'as* that belongs specifically to "seed of man." But regarding this, it is written, "if you buy a Hebrew servant" (*eved ivri*). *Ivri* is named after "your ancestors dwelt beyond the river" (*ever hanahar*),[14] meaning above the level of the "river" (*nahar*). Regarding the level of the river, it is written,[15] "And a river goes out from Eden to water the garden, and from there it parts..." From this, it is understood that the level of the river is above the level of "and from there it parts." However, the level of *ever hanahar* (beyond the river) is above even the level of the river itself. This is "your ancestors dwelt beyond the river"—that all the souls of Yisrael, even the souls in the category of "seed of beast," have their root in the level of *ever hanahar*, which is above even the level of the river. Being there, they possess a very great *da'as*, and therefore it is possible to draw down the aspect of *da'as* into them as well. This is what is meant by "if you buy a Hebrew servant"—"if you buy" (*ki tikneh*) specifically, for a purchase is not the creation of a new entity, nor is it a change in the essence of the thing; it is only a transition from the domain of the seller to the domain of the buyer. So it is with the drawing down of *da'as* into the souls of "seed of beast": it is not a change in their essential existence, but only a revelation of the concealment that exists in them due to their root in the level of *ever hanahar*. This matter is accomplished specifically by Moshe, because Moshe himself is from this level (*ever hanahar*).
