This is why he is called Moshe, "because I drew him out of the water" (*min hamayim meshisihu*),[16] for his root is from the water of the first *shemitah*.[17] Furthermore, the matter of the water is not hinted at in his name, only *meshisihu* (I drew him out), which is his being drawn from the water, because water hints at the level of *chochma*, whereas Moshe's root is above the level of *chochma* [and from this[18] it is understood that Moshe is above even the souls of "seed of man," and therefore he has the power to draw down *da'as* even into the souls of "seed of beast," as he is above the limitations of "seed of man" and "seed of beast"].[19]

**However,** one still needs to understand: all of this is from the perspective of the soul, for since its root is from the level of *ever hanahar* as mentioned, it is possible to draw down the level of *da'as* into it. But the matter of the giving of the Torah is specifically for souls in bodies, and the main intent in drawing down *da'as* to Yisrael is to draw down the level of *da'as* into the souls as they are clothed in bodies. How can the matter of *da'as* be drawn down also from the perspective of the human body? The matter is that the body, too, has its root in this level, for the root of the body is from the 288 sparks of the world of *Tohu*, which is the first *shemitah*, only that through the breaking of the vessels it fell to the lowest depths.[20]

#### 234

And since its root is in the level of the first *shemitah*, from *ever hanahar*, therefore it is possible to draw down into it the level of *da'as* through Moshe, who is also at this level, as mentioned.

e) **However,** from the wording of the verse, "And these are the ordinances which you shall set before them," "before them" without qualification implies that this matter applies to the totality of Yisrael—meaning not only the souls of "seed of beast," but also the souls in the category of "seed of man." Seemingly, it is understandable regarding the souls of "seed of beast" who lack *da'as*, that Moshe is the one who draws down the level of *da'as* into them. But for the souls of "seed of man" who already possess *da'as*, what is the nature of the drawing down that is drawn to them through Moshe, of which it is said, "which you shall set before them"? The matter is that within *da'as* itself, there are two levels. There is the level of *da'as* that comes after grasping or at least intellectualizing—that after one understands and grasps the matter, he then comes to a recognition and feeling, and this recognition is specifically in what one grasps. But there is a level of *da'as* that is above grasping,[21] and that is the recognition of the Essence, which is not captured in grasping—not in the grasping of the positive, nor in the grasping of the negative, nor in intellectualization—and it comes only through recognition. Regarding this, they said,[22] "The ultimate of knowledge is that we do not know," meaning the recognition of the Essence. This level of *da'as* must be drawn down also into the souls of "seed of man," the souls of Atzilus. For the *da'as* of the souls of Atzilus is the level of *da'as* that is based on grasping, since the nature of the world of Atzilus is revelations—meaning it is within the category of revelation and concealment. Therefore, one must draw down into them the aspect of *da'as* that is the recognition of the Essence, "the ultimate of knowledge is that we do not know." And this matter, too, is drawn down by Moshe Rabbeinu, because he is from the level of "I drew him out of the water," above the level of revelation and concealment, and therefore Moshe can draw down the level of the recognition of the Essence even into the souls of "seed of man."

**And just as** it was explained that the drawing down of *da'as* into the souls of "seed of beast" is because they possess this matter due to their root—both in the souls of "seed of beast," of which it is written, "your ancestors dwelt beyond the river," and from the perspective of the body, whose root is from the level of the world of *Tohu*—so too is it regarding the drawing down of the *da'as* of "the ultimate of knowledge is that we do not know" into the totality of souls, even in the souls of "seed of man," for this matter also is due to their root. The matter is, according to what is known[23] regarding the souls of Yisrael "arising in the thought,"[24] that the root of all the souls of Yisrael (even the souls in the category of "seed of beast") is in the most exalted level in the thought, etc., and therefore it is possible to draw down into them the aspect of the recognition of the Essence, "the ultimate of knowledge is that we do not know." And this matter, too, is drawn down specifically by Moshe, because in Moshe shines the Essence that is above, as it is written,[25] "Six hundred thousand footmen are the people in whose midst I am," that in the midst of Moshe shines the aspect of *Anochi* (I am) "He Who I Am," the Essence of the Infinite One, blessed be He. [And furthermore, the revelation of this level in Moshe is specifically through Yisrael, as explained in other places,[26] that the revelation of *Anochi* in the midst of Moshe is through the six hundred thousand footmen of the people.]

**This is** "And these are the ordinances which you shall set before them" (*lifnehem*)—before their inwardness (*lifnimiyusam*), for Moshe is the one who connects the inwardness of the souls with the aspect of the inwardness of the Essence and Being of the Infinite One, blessed be He. Therefore, he is the one who draws down the level of *da'as* into the souls of Yisrael, up to the level of *da'as* of "the ultimate of knowledge is that we do not know." This is also the nuance in "And these are the ordinances which you shall set before them"—"ordinances" (*mishpatim*) specifically, which are rational commandments, meaning that even in rational commandments, Moshe drew down from the level of *da'as*, up to the *da'as* of "the ultimate of knowledge is that we do not know."

f) **The explanation of the matter in the actual *avodah* of man, even in these generations:** In detail, every Jew possesses the aspect of "seed of man" and the aspect of "seed of beast." When he is engaged in Torah and prayer, he is in the category of "seed of man," and when he is engaged during the day in mundane work, even if it is permitted, he is in the category of "seed of beast." The content of a person's *avodah* is to draw down *da'as* into the category of "seed of beast"—meaning that he should draw down the *da'as* of Hashem while he is engaged in mundane work. Furthermore, even in his *avodah* in the category of "seed of man," in his engagement in Torah and prayer, he should draw down from the level of *da'as* of "the ultimate of knowledge is that we do not know." That is, he should not be satisfied with his *avodah* in Torah and prayer in a manner of grasping, but should draw into it the aspect of *da'as* which is the level of the connection of faith. In this connection, a question does not cause weakness, and a proof does not add strength. The drawing down of this level is through Moshe Rabbeinu. And even though Yisrael said, "Speak you with us and we will hear... lest we die,"[27] from which it is implied that the speech of Moshe is a descent relative to the words of Hashem, nevertheless, it is specifically Moshe who draws down the level of *da'as* that is above grasping, even into the souls of "seed of beast." And so it is also with the Moshe of our generation, for "there is an extension of Moshe in every generation,"[28] and all those who were connected to him are connected now, or those who will be connected in the future—Moshe is the one who connects the aspect of the essence of their soul, their *yechidah*, with his *yechidah*.[29] Through this, it is "embraced and cleaved to You, *yechidah* to unite You,"[30] completely above reason and *da'as*.

#### 236

**And he continues** in the verse,[31] "Six years he shall serve, and in the seventh he shall go out to freedom for nothing." Through the completion of the *avodah* now, in the six thousand years of the world,[32] for even though this is a limited time, nevertheless they will complete all the *avodah* in it, then "the earth shall be full of the knowledge of Hashem,"[33] *de'ah* (knowledge) specifically, the aspect of *da'as*, and in a manner that "all shall know Me, from the least of them to the greatest of them."[34] Even if he is a "least" one, and will remain a "least" one in the future, nevertheless, the aspect of *da'as* will be with him, and in a manner of "as the waters cover the sea," that the light and revelation will be in all of them equally. And one should connect this with what is explained in the *maamar* of the *hillula*[35] regarding the "hosts of Hashem" (*tzivos Hashem*). *Tzava* (host) has three meanings: a term for limited time, a term for beauty, and a term for an army and acceptance of the yoke. So it is also in this matter: even though the *avodah* is in the six thousand years, during a limited time—*tzava* as a term for limited time—nevertheless, it contains the perfection of *avodah* and in a manner of beauty, that all his *avodah* is in perfection, in all the inner powers, the encompassing powers, and above the level of encompassing powers. Furthermore, the *avodah* is from a place of acceptance of the yoke, as the third meaning, which is the role of the Hebrew servant. Through this *avodah*, by which the transformation of the falsehood and the "knot" (*kesher*) of the world into the "boards of the Tabernacle" (*karshei hamishkan*)[36] is accomplished, the Moshe of our generation, who is the Rebbe, will connect their *yechidah* with the aspect of his *yechidah*, which is "your yoke, *yechidah* to unite You,"[30] and through this, "and in the seventh he shall go out to freedom for nothing"—meaning the revelation of the future, through Moshe, who is the first redeemer and the final redeemer,[37] that speedily in our days and in our time, he will redeem us from the final, bitter exile, in which there is double and redoubled darkness, and he will redeem us.[38]

## With the help of Hashem. Sicha of Shabbos Parshas Mishpatim, Mevarchim Adar Rishon, 5711

#### 237

(Unedited)

**1.** Regarding the continuation of Parshas Mishpatim (the first parsha after the Giving of the Torah) to Parshas Yisro (the parsha of the Giving of the Torah) — it is stated in the Midrash:

"When Moshe saw that Yisrael were afraid when Hashem was revealed to them and was speaking with them (as it is written, 'And all the people saw the thunder and the lightning... and the people saw and trembled and stood from afar. And they said to Moshe, "You speak with us and we will hear, but let not Elokim speak with us, lest we die"'), Moshe said to them, 'Do not fear,' as it is said, 'And Moshe said to the people, "Do not fear," etc.'... Moshe first appeased Yisrael, and afterwards he set before them the laws of damages and all the attributes of justice, for it is written afterwards, 'And these are the judgments that you shall set before them.'"

And this is also the precision in the phrase "And these are the judgments that you shall *set* before them," implying that from now on, *you* (Moshe) shall set the judgments of the Torah before the Bnei Yisrael, in accordance with their request, "You speak with us and we will hear."

And this matter ("set before them," which is done specifically by Moshe) is explained in the Chassidic discourses on Parshas Mishpatim, both in the printed discourses, in those in manuscript, and in those known orally.

**2.** Maamar beginning "Ve'eileh Hamishpatim Asher Tasim Lifneihem."

***

**3.** Regarding a leap year (like this year), which has an Adar Rishon and an Adar Sheni, there is an inquiry as to which of them is the primary Adar and which is the additional Adar, the month of the leap.

It is possible that this depends on the dispute between Rabbi Meir and Rabbi Yehuda: "For it is taught: In Adar Rishon one writes 'Adar Rishon,' in Adar Sheni one writes simply 'Adar' — these are the words of Rabbi Meir. Rabbi Yehuda says: In Adar Rishon one writes simply 'Adar,' and in Adar Sheni one writes 'Tinein' (second)."

#### 238

Simply put, it stands to reason that the primary Adar is Adar Sheni — for in Adar Sheni we celebrate the days of Purim, with the reading of the Megillah, sending portions, and gifts to the poor (whereas in Adar Rishon it is only Purim Katan). If we were to say that Adar Sheni is the additional month in a leap year, it would mean that in a simple year, the primary month in which we celebrate the days of Purim is missing. Therefore, we must say that Adar Sheni is the primary Adar, and the additional month in a leap year is Adar Rishon (and the deficiency in a simple year is only regarding Purim Katan, which is secondary to the primary Purim).

And as we stand on Shabbos Mevarchim Adar Rishon, which is the additional Adar, the month of the leap — we must explain the content and the special quality of the month of the leap.

**4.** We must first preface the content of the leap year in its literal sense — as the Rambam explains at the beginning of Hilchos Kiddush HaChodesh:

"How much does the solar year exceed the lunar year? By nearly eleven days [for 'the solar year is 365 days and six hours,' and 'the lunar year, if it is twelve months... its total is 354 days, eight hours, and 876 parts,' 'thus the excess of the solar year over the lunar year is ten days, 21 hours, and 204 parts']. Therefore, when this excess accumulates to about thirty days... we add one month and make that year thirteen months, and it is called a leap year."

And the need to calculate the solar year as well, even though Yisrael "count by the moon," is "because of the time of the spring, so that Pesach will be at that time, as it is said, 'Observe the month of spring,' that this month should be in the time of the spring. And were it not for the addition of this month (the month of the leap), Pesach would sometimes fall in the summer and sometimes in the winter."

**5.** The explanation of this in the inner dimension of things:

The deficiency of the lunar year relative to the solar year is connected to the general deficiency of the moon relative to the sun — the diminution of the moon — for at the beginning of creation there were "the two

#### 239

great luminaries," "they were created equal," but afterwards "the moon was diminished because it complained, etc."

And the root of the matter of the diminution of the moon, which is a deficiency of light, is explained in the maamar of the Rebbe Rayatz (which has already been printed), that the cause and the place given for this is "that the attribute of *din* did not suffice for it," which caused the breaking of the vessels of *Tohu*. And before that — "the deficiency of light above, which is the matter of the first *Tzimtzum*." As a result of this, "a place was given for the deficiency of light below due to sin and iniquity," beginning with the sin of the Tree of Knowledge, which is the root of all sins.

And the intent of this is — that "the *avodah* should be through one's own power... and through this, one draws down the missing light in greater abundance, through which the supreme intent of the *Tzimtzum* is fulfilled, that there should be a revelation of the *Etzem* (the Essence)." That is to say, not only will there be a drawing down of light as it was before the sin and before the *Tzimtzum*, but an even higher light will be drawn down than what existed before the sin, which did not shine even before the *Tzimtzum*.

**6.** Based on this, we can explain the content and the quality of the month of the leap:

Since the month of the leap completes and fills the deficiency of the lunar year relative to the solar year, this also hints at the rectification of the diminution of the moon, and consequently, also the rectification of the sin of the Tree of Knowledge and all sins in general,

— and for this reason, some have the custom in a leap year to add in the *Mussaf* prayer of *Rosh Chodesh*: "And for the atonement of transgression" (as is printed in several versions) —

And it goes as far as the rectification of the root of the matter of the diminution of the moon — the breaking of the vessels and the first *Tzimtzum* — that the light that shone before the *Tzimtzum* is drawn down,

And more than that, that a higher light is drawn down and revealed, which did not shine even before the *Tzimtzum* — as is hinted at by the fact that through the addition of the month of the leap, the lunar year becomes greater than the solar year.

And according to what was said above that the month of the leap is Adar Rishon, it turns out that *this month* (which is blessed on this Shabbos) is the time capable of drawing down a light higher

#### 240

than what was before the sin, and before the general matter of the deficiency of light through the first *Tzimtzum* — *the revelation of the Essence*.

*

**7.** What was said above regarding the leap year, that the intent of the descent of the diminution of the moon is so that afterwards a higher light will be drawn down — this applies to all matters of descent, that the intent in them is so that afterwards a higher light will be drawn down.

For example:

It was explained above that "seed of a beast" refers to the souls of *Beriah, Yetzirah, and Asiyah* (the majority of souls in our generations) that lack *Da'as* — which is a matter of descent.

And not only that, but even "seed of man," which refers to the souls of *Atzilus* that possess *Da'as*, is a matter of descent, because: *Atzilus* is also a world (*olam*), from the term *he'elem* (concealment), and therefore, even the *Da'as* they have in *Elokus* is only recognition according to intellect, and not recognition of the Essence (which is above comprehension).

[And this is the difference between "Adam" (man) and "Me'od" (very/exceedingly), whose letters are the same, but their arrangement is different; "Adam" points to intellect and *Da'as*, and "Me'od" points to the absence of the measurement and limitation of intellect and *Da'as*.]

And the question is asked: Why has Hashem done this to us — even regarding the descent of the souls of *Atzilus*, and certainly regarding the descent of the souls of *Beriah, Yetzirah, and Asiyah*?

And similarly regarding the descent that comes from passing away:

In one of the *Igros Kodesh* written by the Mitteler Rebbe after the passing of the Alter Rebbe, he explains several pieces of advice for strengthening *hiskashrus*, for the passing is a matter of descent that can cause, *chas v'shalom*, a weakening in *hiskashrus*, and there is a need to provide advice to strengthen *hiskashrus*.

And here too the question is asked: Why did Hashem do so? What is the intent in this descent?

And the point of the matter is — as explained in the *hemshech* of the *hillula* — that the intent of the descent is so that through it they will effect the matter of "the glory of the Holy One, blessed be He, is exalted in all

#### 241

the worlds," which refers to the light of *Sovev Kol Almin* that shines in all worlds equally, and even to the drawing down of the light that does not belong to the worlds at all (not even in the manner of *Sovev Kol Almin*), as explained above regarding the precision of the phrase "*Ikar* Shechinah" (the essence of the Divine Presence), which refers not only to the *Shechinah* as it is relative to *Atzilus* (*Malchus* of *Atzilus* as it becomes *Keter* and *Atik* for *Beriah*, or even as it is in *Atzilus*), and also not only as it is relative to the *Ohr Ein Sof*, i.e., the *Kav*, and not even as it is relative to the light before the *Tzimtzum*, the revelation of the light itself that belongs to the worlds, but "*Ikar* Shechinah," the essence and the inwardness of the *Shechinah*, which is the revelation of the Essence — which is accomplished specifically in the lower worlds.

***

**8.** At the beginning of the weekly parsha, it speaks about a Hebrew slave — "If you buy a Hebrew slave, he shall serve for six years, and in the seventh he shall go out to freedom for nothing." And in continuation of this, it is told in the *Haftorah* about the covenant that King Tzidkiyahu (who was a righteous king) made with the Bnei Yisrael "to send forth every man his manservant and every man his maidservant, the Hebrew and the Hebrewess, free (after they had served six years), that none should serve himself of them, etc., and they heard and they sent them forth," but afterwards "they turned and brought back the servants and the handmaids whom they had sent forth free, and brought them into subjection for servants and for handmaids."

In order for the conduct in the seventh year to be as it should be ("in the seventh he shall go out to freedom for nothing"), the conduct during the six years must be in a manner appropriate to this, i.e., during the "six years he shall serve," it must be evident and felt that "in the seventh he shall go out to freedom for nothing." And when the conduct in the seventh year is not as it should be (that he does not fulfill the commandment "he shall go out to freedom for nothing"), this is proof that the conduct during the six years was also not as it should be, i.e., that it was not felt in the work of the six years that in the end he would go out to freedom for nothing.

The acquisition ("if you buy") of a Hebrew slave, which must be through *sale* specifically (unlike a Canaanite slave, whose acquisition can also be through a gift) — whether the *Beis Din* sold him (for his theft) or he sold himself (due to his poverty) — this is only relevant when the master *profits from the work* of the slave [and it goes without saying — not in the manner of "a slave who is not worth the bread he eats, what is he needed for by his master and mistress"], so,

#### 242

that there must be *the work of the slave*; but, together with this, it must be felt in the work of the slave that "in the seventh he shall go out to freedom for nothing," and the benefit in this is — that through this he does not feel the difficulty of the work so much, and the work is easier, to the point that he is able to do his work with *taanug*.

**9.** And the explanation of the matter — in the *avodah* of man to his Creator:

It is known that "six years he shall serve" hints at our general deeds and *avodah* during the six thousand years of the world, and specifically during the time of *galus*, and "in the seventh he shall go out to freedom for nothing" hints at the seventh millennium, "the day that is entirely Shabbos and rest for eternal life."

And in order for our deeds and *avodah* during the entire time of *galus* to be as they should be, the *avodah* must be in a manner where it is felt that the intent is so that "in the seventh he shall go out to freedom for nothing," the elevation and perfection of the time to come, through which the *avodah* during the time of *galus* is done easily, and in a higher manner, with *taanug*.

And if these things are said regarding our deeds and *avodah* during the entire time of *galus*, all the more so as we stand at the end of the time of *galus*, in proximity to the seventh millennium, at a time when we add from the profane to the holy [and according to several opinions this is a Torah obligation, and in any case, by Rabbinic law, there must certainly be an addition from the profane to the holy] — surely the time has arrived that in the *avodah* of now, the revelation of the time to come should already be felt, through which there will also be an addition in the *avodah* of now in a higher manner.

And another matter in this — as the words of the Rebbe Rayatz: When Moshiach comes, "one will grab one's head" at how much one could have accomplished through *avodah* during the time of *galus*! And therefore, when one knows that one is now at the end of the time of *galus*, one must seize the opportunity and add with greater strength and greater intensity in all matters of *avodah* of the time of *galus*.

**10.** And it should be added, that when the *avodah* during the time of *galus* ("six years he shall serve") is permeated with the intent of the *Geulah* ("in the seventh he shall go out to freedom for nothing"), this effects that even during the time of *galus* one is in a standing and state that is above *galus*:

And by way of preface, the words of the Rebbe Rayatz upon leaving his imprisonment to travel to his city

#### 243

of refuge: "Only our bodies were given into *galus* and the servitude of kingdoms, but our souls were not given over to *galus* and the servitude of kingdoms."

And seemingly it is not understood: since the intent is that the *avodah* should be with the body specifically,

— as emphasized in the words of the Rebbe Rayatz who revealed and publicized the teaching of the Baal Shem Tov on the verse in the weekly parsha, "If you see the donkey, etc., you shall surely help with him," that "donkey" (*chamor*) refers to the materiality (*chomer*) which is the body, and the *avodah* must be in the manner of "you shall surely help with him," to refine and purify the body —

What is the benefit in that *the soul* was not given over to *galus* — relative to the *avodah* that is from the side of *the body*, which was given over to *galus*?!

And the explanation of this — that through the soul being clothed in the body and united with it in order to fulfill its mission in the refinement and purification of the body and its portion in the world, the soul that was not given over to *galus* effects that the body also will not be given over to *galus*, and will be able to fulfill its role and mission as it should be, without the concealments and hiddenness of the time of *galus*.

And as explained in *Tanya* that when the light of the soul is revealed, then "all the *kelipos* [both the three *kelipos* of impurity, and the *kelipah* of *nogah* "which is the general life-force of this physical and material world"] are null and void and are as if they never were."

And the point of the matter — that Bnei Yisrael are not enslaved, *chas v'shalom*, to the world, "over a Jew, nothing is a master," but on the contrary, the world is enslaved to Bnei Yisrael,

— unless *the Jew himself* causes the world to be a master over him,

[And this is the reason that the betrayal of our Rebbe the Alter Rebbe and the imprisonment of the Rebbe Rayatz were by people from Bnei Yisrael specifically, for, to cause the imprisonment of a soul and body (and especially) on such a high level — this is not within the power of a non-Jew, "a non-Jew is not a master at all over this," such a thing can only be done by a Jew],

As in all undesirable matters whose existence cannot be unless they have a root in *kedushah*, and as emphasized in the sin of the Tree of Knowledge, that the root of this was

#### 244

a matter of *kedushah*, that Chava "added to the commandment" (by saying that the commandment was not only about eating but also about touching), which is a matter of *hiddur* —

And therefore, when a Jew stands with the appropriate strength, from the side of his soul, he overcomes the concealments and hiddenness of *galus*, and succeeds in fulfilling his role and mission in the world as it should be.

**11.** And to add, that in such a case there is also a benefit in the very fact that one decides and accepts upon oneself to ascend to a higher standing and state, even if it is possible that this will be only for the moment, and afterwards one will conduct oneself in a different manner, and not only that, but it is possible that even for the moment this is not yet in actuality but only in potential.

And even in such a manner, the influence of good from above is effected — for our Sages said, "One does not judge a person except according to his deeds of *that moment* and not according to what he is destined to do," and since his standing and state for the moment is as it should be, he merits to receive the influence of good. And all this is even when the desired standing and state (has not yet come into actuality, but) is only *in potential*, because, although below potential lacks actuality, above, potential does not lack actuality, and therefore the drawing down of good from above is effected in actuality.

[And it should be noted, that even if the actuality will be in a different manner, or only for the moment and afterwards it will be in a different manner — then there will be a matter of punishment to remove the sin, etc., but there will not be a hindrance to the influence of good from above].

For example — in private matters:

There is a *segulah* from the Alter Rebbe regarding those who are childless, *rachmana litzlan* — that through the arousal of love and awe, which are "children" in spirituality, they merit children in physicality as well.

And according to what was said that even acceptance in potential is sufficient, it is understood that even when one cannot effect in oneself an arousal of love and awe in actuality, acceptance in potential is sufficient at least regarding the matter of love and awe — through contemplation in one's intellect, as the Alter Rebbe writes that the advice for love and awe is through this "that one binds one's mind with a firm and very strong bond and fixes one's thought strongly in the greatness of the *Ein Sof*, blessed be He," and then, even

#### 245

if due to side circumstances an arousal of love and awe does not come in actuality, since one has done what is dependent on oneself in the matter that the Alter Rebbe rules leads to love and awe, acceptance in potential is sufficient to merit the blessing of the Holy One, blessed be He, regarding children (also) in physicality.

And if there is a deficiency also in the matter of contemplation — then the advice is to connect to Moshe Rabbeinu, and the extension of Moshe in every generation, who draws down and influences *Da'as* into the souls of Yisrael, and as a result of this one will come to an arousal of love and awe in actuality or at least in potential, and surely the Holy One, blessed be He, will not remain a debtor and will give him His blessing regarding children in spirituality and also — and primarily — in physicality.

And similarly also regarding our general deeds and *avodah* during the entire time of *galus* — that the decision and acceptance that one decides and accepts upon oneself to ascend to a standing and state that is above *galus*, even for the moment and in potential only, effects its effect that it will be so also in actuality, through which it is in his power and ability to complete his role and mission during the time of *galus*, and then the intent of "six years he shall serve" will be completed and revealed so that "in the seventh he shall go out to freedom for nothing."

## B’s”D. Remarks during a reception – 1st day of Rosh Chodesh Adar I, 5711

#### 246

(Unedited)

**1.** (The Rebbe inquired about the location of the chuppah, asking whether there was an opening in the roof for the chuppah or if it was being held outdoors. When informed that they had planned to hold the chuppah indoors due to the winter cold, the Rebbe was not pleased and said:) My own wedding also took place in the winter, and the chuppah was held outdoors, under the open sky. (The Rebbe added with a smile:) And thank G-d, I am satisfied with the shidduch...

(Someone remarked that it was likely too late to obtain permission from the owners of the hall—who were not Jewish—to hold the chuppah outdoors. The Rebbe hinted that this was not necessarily the case. They went to arrange the matter, and a few minutes later they returned to announce that everything was ready for the chuppah to be held outdoors. The Rebbe said with a smile:) If only it were possible to influence those with free choice so easily.

**2.** (The Rebbe inquired about the background of the mechutan on the bride’s side. When told that he was from Deutschland, the Rebbe said:) From Deutschland came much Torah and much greatness. (The Rebbe then sighed and added: And also much suffering.)

(The Rebbe then said:) Throughout the generations, the Torah has penetrated and exerted its influence in many countries outside of Eretz Yisrael—beginning with the Babylonian exile, Spain, Ashkenaz, France, Poland, and Russia, and through my father-in-law, the Rebbe—also in America. And now, after the Torah has penetrated and exerted its influence here as well, everything is prepared. Consequently, there can and should already be a gathering of the exiles, in the complete Redemption that will come with the arrival of Moshiach.

**3.** (The Rebbe then said:) Participating in this simcha is my first time going out ("the first time I am traveling out") since, throughout the year of the passing of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, I did not go anywhere, except for the trip to the Ohel.

#### 247

And since this beginning is in a matter of simcha, which breaks through barriers, may the Ribono shel Olam grant that this simcha break through our own barriers, and may there be only simchas always.

## With the help of Heaven. Reshimo, Shabbos Parshas Terumah, 4 Adar Rishon, 5711

#### 248

(Unedited)

(Following davening, the Rebbe said to the chassan who was called to the Torah:)

In the parsha of the week, we speak of the donation for the Mishkan—"gold, and silver, and copper, etc."[1](#_ftn1395]—which are indeed physical things, yet through them, a home is made for the dwelling of His Presence, may He be blessed: "And I will dwell among them."[2](#_ftn1396]

The parallel to this in the personal life of every Jew is that when one builds a home in Israel, a "building of eternal witness," one must take physical things and make of them a Mishkan and a sanctuary for Hashem.[3](#_ftn1397]

## B’s"D. Remarks at a Reception* – 7 Adar Rishon, 5711

#### 249

(Unedited)

**1.** In Parshas Terumah—following the *aufruf* (aliyah to the Torah) that took place on Shabbos Parshas Terumah—it is stated: "Speak to the Children of Israel and they shall take for Me a *terumah*... gold, silver, and copper, etc., and they shall make for Me a *mikdash* and I will dwell within them"[1](#_ftn1398]. This means they were commanded to take physical materials and fashion from them a *mikdash* regarding which Hashem promises to cause His *Shechinah* to dwell: "And I will dwell within them."

Just as this applies to the *Mishkan* and the *Mikdash*, so too does it apply to synagogues and *batei medrash*, which are a "*mikdash me'at* (a miniature sanctuary)"[2](#_ftn1399).

And it is likewise regarding the private *mikdash* within every single Jew—as hinted at by the precision of the language "within them" (*b'socham*): "It does not say 'within it' (*b'socho*), but 'within them' (*b'socham*)—within each and every one"[3](#_ftn1400]. When one builds a home in Israel, an everlasting edifice, one must take physical materials and make of them a *mikdash* for Hashem.

**2.** It can be said that the empowerment to make a *mikdash* for Hashem out of physical materials is hinted at in the verse, "And they shall take *for Me a terumah*."

This is based on what is explained in *Tanya*[4](#_ftn1401): "What is written in the *Zohar*[5](#_ftn1402) regarding the verse 'And they shall take for Me a *terumah*'—'for Me' (*li*) means 'Me' (myself); it should have said 'and a *terumah*,' but the reason is that it is all one." That is, the *terumah* is one with Hashem ("for Me").

From this it is understood that even though the "gold, silver, and copper" and the other materials (thirteen or fifteen[6](#_ftn1403)) enumerated in the verse are physical things, the truth is that in their own essence they are "all one" with Hashem, since "the primary dwelling of the *Shechinah* was in the lower realms"[7](#_ftn1404). Therefore, one can make a *mikdash* for Hashem out of them, because one only needs to reveal their true reality, bringing it from concealment into manifestation.

However, this matter is specifically within the power of the Children of Israel—"Speak to the Children of Israel and they shall take for Me a *terumah*."

#### 250

Even though physical things are in their own essence "all one" with Hashem, and one only needs to bring this from concealment into manifestation, nevertheless, only the souls of Israel can reveal such a thing. For to the souls of Israel, "His Being and Essence, may He be blessed, 'gave Himself' in such a way that they could take Him ('as if He gave us Himself, so to speak')[8](#_ftn1405)," and therefore they are able to reveal the power of the Essence that exists within physical things[9](#_ftn1406).

This is similar to what was explained above[10](#_ftn1407) regarding the matter of "If you purchase a Hebrew slave"[11](#_ftn1408), which refers to Moshe Rabbeinu, who draws down *da'as* into the souls of Israel. The possibility of drawing down *da'as* into the souls of Israel exists because in their root they possess the level of *da'as*, and they only need to reveal it from concealment into manifestation. And yet, even this revelation from concealment into manifestation can only be accomplished through the power of Moshe, because of his connection to this level, of whom it is said[12](#_ftn1409), "I drew him out of the water."

**3.** This is not merely for the sake of homiletical exposition, but rather that these things should be brought into actual *avodah*.

The making of a *mikdash* for Hashem out of physical things is a matter that was already explained in the Torah long ago... and everyone knows that the intention is also for the *mikdash* within every single Jew. Likewise, everyone knows the words of the *Zohar* interpreting "for Me a *terumah*" as being "all one." And yet, it was necessary for the Alter Rebbe to write this in the *Tanya*, and subsequently for our Rebbes, the *Nesi'im*, to explain these matters, up to the statement of the Rebbes that "the primary dwelling of the *Shechinah* was in the lower realms."

Only then are the things said by Moshe Rabbeinu thousands of years ago actually completed—that the matter of "and they shall make for Me a *mikdash* and I will dwell within them" is carried out in practice.

## B's"d. Reshimas Dvarim, Shabbos Parshas Tetzaveh, 11 Adar Rishon, 5711

#### 251

Unedited

(Following davening, the Rebbe said to the chassan who was called to the Torah:)

In one of the maamarim that the Rebbe, my father-in-law, gave to be studied on the day of his hillula, 2 Nissan[1](#_ftn1410), he explains the verse (at the beginning of our parsha): "And you shall command the Children of Israel, that they shall bring to you pure olive oil... to cause a lamp to burn continually."

"On the face of it, it is puzzling: how is it possible for a lamp, which is an illumination, to possess the quality of 'continual' [tamid], which relates only to the luminary itself?"

He explains[2](#_ftn1411) that this is the innovation of "And you shall command": that "Moshe, through his power to command—meaning, to connect and unite the entirety of the Children of Israel (with Hashem)... then, even a lamp, which is an illumination, reveals within it the essential power, such that it, too, is in a state of 'continual,' which is the connection in the eternity of the Ein Sof." He concludes that "the assistance for this is through *hiskashrus to the level of Moshe*, who are the 'heads of the thousands of Israel,' the *atpashuta d'Moshe* (the extension of Moshe) in every generation."

This matter is also relevant to the building of a home in Israel, a "building of eternity" [where the order of this—as with all matters—is first and foremost regarding spirituality, regarding the ahavah and yirah that are called 'son' and 'daughter'[3](#_ftn1412), and through this, also regarding the physical, a son and daughter in the literal sense]. The power for this—that a private home in Israel should possess the quality of *tamid*, which is the concept of a "building of eternity"—is through *Moshe*. Consequently, the assistance for this is through *hiskashrus to Moshe*, the *atpashuta d'Moshe* in every generation[4](#_ftn1413).

## B's"d. Reshimos from the Kabbalas-Panim – Purim Katan 5711

#### 252

Unedited

**1.** (The topic of fasting on the day of a wedding that falls on Purim Katan was discussed. The Admur of Kopishnitz mentioned that it is their custom not to fast, but since the Rebbe had instructed the chassan to fast, he said nothing further. Following this, the Rebbe said:)

The Rebbe Rayatz would also fast on the wedding day of his daughters, and he would complete the fast.

At the wedding of his youngest daughter, the time of the chuppah was delayed significantly (due to one of the guests whom the Rebbe Rayatz was waiting for). Nevertheless, the Rebbe Rayatz continued to sit in his fast until after the chuppah.

*

**2.** At the bar mitzvah celebration of the Rebbe Rayatz’s grandson, they did not interrupt the bar mitzvah boy in the middle of reciting the maamar Chassidus in the presence of the Rebbe Rayatz. Afterward, the Rebbe Rayatz said that since the custom of Poland is to interrupt the bar mitzvah boy, the bar mitzvah boy should begin again, and then they should interrupt him, in accordance with the custom of Poland.

*

**3.** It is stated in the sefarim that a wedding ring should be like a samech and like a mem—round (like a samech) on the inside, and square (like a mem) on the outside. And according to Kabbalah,

#### 253

one should perform the kiddushin with a silver ring. Nevertheless, the actual custom is to perform the kiddushin with a round ring (even on the outside), and specifically of gold.

*

**4.** Regarding the connection between marriage and Matan Torah, we find two perspectives : (a) Hashem is called the chassan and Knesses Yisrael is called the kallah, referring to the drawing down and influence of Torah upon Yisrael; (b) Bnei Yisrael are called the chassan and the Torah is called the kallah, referring to the fact that Bnei Yisrael influence and add to the Torah.

Both are true: initially, there is the influence of the Torah upon Yisrael, and afterward, Bnei Yisrael influence and add to the Torah.

It can be said that these two matters correspond to the two aspects of "gift" and "toil" in Torah :

We find that the Torah was given as a gift, where one does not need to toil for it; on the other hand, we find that it is impossible to attain the Torah except through toil specifically.

The explanation for this is that initially, there is the aspect of the "gift" in Torah, where one receives what is given to him as something ready-made (starting from the matters that a mother teaches a child). Afterward, the aspect of "toil" in Torah is also added, through which one is able to attain matters that he could not attain previously through the manner of a gift.

## B's"d. Reshimos Dvarim, Thursday, 16 Adar Rishon, 5711

#### 254

*Unedited*

**A.** Someone asked me a question on the Tanya:

At the beginning of the Tanya, the Alter Rebbe writes that "even one who transgresses a minor prohibition of the Sages is called a *rasha*, as it is stated in *Perek* 2 of *Yevamos*[1](#_ftn1426) and in the first *perek* of *Niddah*[2](#_ftn1427) . . . and all the more so, *kal v'chomer*, regarding one who neglects a positive *mitzvah* that he is able to fulfill."

He asks: Why does the Alter Rebbe need to derive via *kal v'chomer* that one who neglects a positive *mitzvah* is called a *rasha*—is it not explicitly stated in the Gemara[3](#_ftn1428), "What is the case of a positive *mitzvah*? If he does not perform it, 'the sacrifice of the wicked is an abomination'"[4](#_ftn1429)?

—What is the reason that Chassidim who study Tanya do not grasp (*"chappen zich gor nicht"*) such questions?!

*

**B.** Regarding the matter of answering *Amen*—we must inquire into two possibilities: (a) Answering *Amen* is a matter of obligation—as a completion of the *berachah*. (b) The essence of answering *Amen* is a matter of negation—the negation of the absence of answering *Amen*, so that it does not appear as if he does not agree with, and G-d forbid rejects, the *berachah*.

[Someone wanted to bring a proof from answering *Amen* during an oath, which is a matter of obligation, and the Rebbe Shlita said that in an oath, the concept of negation does not apply, because when one does not answer *Amen*, he has no connection to the oath at all.]

Seemingly, one could bring a proof that answering *Amen* is a matter of obligation:

By way of introduction—the practical difference between the two possibilities is, seemingly, regarding one who is standing in *tefillah* in a place where it is forbidden to interrupt to answer *Amen*: If answering *Amen* is an obligatory matter, then in a place where it is forbidden to interrupt, the obligation is nullified. But if answering *Amen* is a matter of negation—so that it is not interpreted as if he does not agree with the *berachah*—he cannot refrain from answering *Amen*,

#### 255

even when he is standing in a place where he is forbidden to interrupt, and consequently, he has no choice but to leave the *beis medrash* beforehand (so that he does not hear the *berachah*).

And since we do not find anywhere that one who is standing in a place where it is forbidden to interrupt to answer *Amen* must leave the *beis medrash*, it is proven, seemingly, that answering *Amen* is a matter of obligation.

But in truth, this is not a proof, because even if we say that answering *Amen* is in order to negate the possibility that it might be interpreted as if he does not agree, G-d forbid, with the *berachah*, there is no necessity to leave the *beis medrash* when he cannot answer *Amen*. For the negation of the initial thought that he does not agree, G-d forbid, with the *berachah* does not necessarily have to be in the specific formula of answering *Amen* [and a proof for this is that in the *Beis Hamikdash* they would answer with the formula "Blessed be the Name of the glory of His kingdom forever and ever"[5](#_ftn1430), and not necessarily with the formula "Amen"], but rather the very fact that he is standing in his *tefillah* and *praising Hashem* in *Pesukei D'zimra*, "Praise Hashem from the heavens," or that he says "Emes V'yatziv V'nachon," "Ezras Avoseinu," and the like, *negates* the initial thought that he does not agree, G-d forbid, with the *berachah*[6](#_ftn1431).

**C.** Seemingly, one could bring a proof that answering *Amen* is a matter of obligation from the fact that we do not interrupt to answer *Amen* in the middle of *tefillah*:

If we say that answering *Amen* is a matter of obligation, we could explain the *reason* that we do not interrupt to answer *Amen* in the middle of *tefillah* is because "one who is engaged in a *mitzvah* is exempt from [another] *mitzvah*"[7](#_ftn1432) (unlike if we say that answering *Amen* is a matter of negation).

But in truth, it is impossible to say that the reason we do not interrupt to answer *Amen* is because one who is engaged in a *mitzvah* is exempt from a *mitzvah*, because for that reason, one should not interrupt even in a place where it is permitted to interrupt, such as during "Hodu L'Hashem Kir'u Vishmo," and likewise in the middle of studying Torah.

And we must say that "one who is engaged in a *mitzvah* is exempt from a *mitzvah*" is not the reason for not interrupting to answer *Amen* [and the explanation for this is that just as one interrupts for the honor of a mortal king to say "Long live the King," all the more so does one interrupt to say "Long live the King of the world"], and the fact that we do not interrupt to answer *Amen* applies in a place where it is forbidden to interrupt for anything.

**D.** And it is possible to say that this inquiry (whether answering *Amen* is a matter of obligation or

#### 256

negation) depends on the dispute in the Gemara[8](#_ftn1433) regarding one who recites a *berachah* and one who answers *Amen*—"The one who recites the *berachah* is superior to the one who answers *Amen*," or that "the one who answers *Amen* is greater than the one who recites the *berachah*":

The superiority of answering *Amen* over the *berachah* is relevant only if we say that answering *Amen* is a matter of obligation—meaning, since the content of answering *Amen* is a *strengthening* of the *berachah*, therefore it has an added superiority over the *berachah*.

Unlike if we say that it is a matter of negation; it is not possible that the negation of non-agreement with the *berachah* would be greater than the *berachah* itself.

Based on this, it is possible to say that the one who holds "the one who recites the *berachah* is superior to the one who answers *Amen*" holds that answering *Amen* is a matter of negation, and the one who holds "the one who answers *Amen* is greater than the one who recites the *berachah*" holds that answering *Amen* is a matter of obligation.

**E.** Now, regarding the explanation of the matter that "the one who answers *Amen* is greater than the one who recites the *berachah*," it is stated in *drushei Chassidus*[9](#_ftn1434) that answering *Amen* is similar to the matter of the "seal of the *berachah*":

A *berachah*—from the word *himshechah* (drawing down)—its essence is the drawing down of *shefa* from above. And since the drawing down of *shefa* from above can be in a manner that it also draws down nourishment for the *chitzonim*, G-d forbid, there must also be a "seal of the *berachah*," for "the matter of the seal is[10](#_ftn1435) like the language of a seal on a letter from the outside, so that a stranger who is not desired to know what is written there will not read this letter; so too is this seal of the *berachah* and the drawing down . . . [so that] it will be only in the category of *kedushah* alone and the strangers will have no portion or inheritance in it" (as explained in *Torah Or* at the beginning[11](#_ftn1436)).

And this is also the content of the matter of answering *Amen*—the establishment of the *berachah* in a manner that the drawing down will be in *kedushah* alone, and there will be no nourishment for the *chitzonim*.

And from this, it seems, seemingly, that answering *Amen* is a matter of negation—the negation of nourishment for the *chitzonim*. But in truth... (the continuation is missing).

## With the help of Heaven. Shabbos Parshas Vayakhel, Parshas Shekalim, Mevarchim HaChodesh Adar Sheni, 5711

#### 257

"When you take the head of the Bnei Yisrael" — Moshe Rabbeinu, specifically *Ra’aya Meheimna* (the Faithful Shepherd), who shepherds the *emunah* (faith) of the Bnei Yisrael. This is a *makif* (encompassing light), and it must be brought into *pnimiyus* (internality).

**"When** you take the head of the Bnei Yisrael according to their numbers, and they shall give..." Seemingly, it should have said, "When you count the Bnei Yisrael." Why the phrasing "take the head"? To understand this: the content of the parsha consists of two matters. First, that Moshe was to take the half-shekel from each person for the service of the Ohel Moed. Second, the commandment for all generations to give a half-shekel each year to the Temple treasury, from which the communal offerings were brought, as explained in Maseches Shekalim. Now, the first matter was not a permanent obligation, for Moshe was commanded to count the Bnei Yisrael, but this was not a command for all generations; on the contrary, as Yoav said when he avoided counting the Bnei Yisrael. The second matter—that the half-shekels were taken for the sockets—occurred only once, as is understood. The third obligation, which our Sages learned—and which is also proven from Divrei Hayamim II 24:9—is the permanent obligation to give a half-shekel every single year so that communal offerings could be brought from it. In this, the counting of the Bnei Yisrael is entirely irrelevant to knowing their sum, and it is implied in many places that they were not counted at all. If so, a difficulty arises: the plain meaning of the language suggests that the introduction "When you take the head of the Bnei Yisrael" applies to all the matters of the parsha.

**The general** concept of this in *avodah* is that in order to offer the sacrifices upon the Altar—which were offered, and the fire from Above would consume the offerings, and because of this, the *nefesh habehamis* in every Jew was diminished and included in *kedushah* until each person would connect their mind and understanding to the greatness of Hashem to be *batul* to Him—this is now accomplished through *tefillah*, which was instituted in place of the sacrifices. For this, there must first be an infusion of strength and assistance from Above. This is the matter of Moshe shepherding the *emunah* through Torah and *gemilus chasadim*, and through this, the "taking of the head" and the elevation of the Bnei Yisrael is accomplished—the *ha’alaah* (ascent) from below to above through the sacrifices and *tefillah*.

#### 258

**To understand** the connection of this matter specifically to Moshe *Ra’aya Meheimna*, to whom it was said, "When you take the head, this they shall give... a half-shekel": he is called *Ra’aya Meheimna* because he shepherds the *emunah*, feeding and sustaining it. For *emunah* by itself can be in the manner of a *makif*, and "a thief at the mouth of the tunnel calls to Hashem". In subtle ways, one can find among business people that even though they believe "It is He who gives you strength", they still immerse themselves in schemes that distract them from Torah and the fixed *shiurim* that are required even for a business person —this is a contradiction in terms. Similarly, among those who sit in the *ohel* (study hall), one believes that this is the wisdom and will of the Holy One, blessed be He, yet when he succeeds in his learning and achieves greatness, he prides himself on it—and it goes without saying when he learns for that purpose—and consequently, he will sometimes tilt the matter, provided that he has the upper hand. Therefore, one must draw the *emunah* into the *pnimiyus* of his soul’s faculties, so that they behave in practice in accordance with his faith. This is accomplished specifically through his *hisbonenus* (contemplation) *aliba denafshei* (according to his own self), and he must strike his mind with strength so that the result of this will not be false imaginings.

**And what** is this *hisbonenus*? It is known that there is a difference between the *emunah* that comes through the wisdom of philosophical inquiry—which is the *emunah* of the Chassidim of the nations of the world—and the *emunah* of the Bnei Yisrael. [The former is] *Memaleh Kol Almin* (filling all worlds) and *Sovev Kol Almin* (encompassing all worlds). [In the former,] vitality is enclothed and broken down into details, and consequently, the world is a reality, only it is *batul* to the vitality enclothed within it—this is the name *Elokim*. *Sovev Kol Almin* is a general *makif* that is above the limitations of intellect and division; this is the *emunah* of the Bnei Yisrael. This is also the reason why they were not concerned about *shituf* (association/partnership).

## With the help of Heaven. Shabbos Parshas Vayakhel, Parshas Shekalim, Mevarchim HaChodesh Adar Sheni, 5711

#### 259

(Unedited transcript)

**"When you take the sum**[1] of the children of Israel..."[2] One must understand[3] why the verse says "When you take the sum" (*ki tisa*), rather than "When you count" (*ki tifkod*). What is the precision of the expression "take the sum" (*tisa et rosh*), and specifically "take the head"? Rashi explains that when you wish to take the sum of their census to know how many they are, do not count them by head (so that there will not be a plague among them), but rather let each one give a half-shekel, and you shall count the shekels and know their number. According to this interpretation, the matter of "taking the sum" is not a commandment, but rather a matter of choice. However, the Midrash[4] states that the Holy One, Blessed be He, said to Moses, "Go, count the children of Israel..." (and the method of counting shall be through the half-shekel so that there will not be a plague among them), which implies that this is a commandment. Yet, even according to the Midrash, this is a temporary commandment, not a decree for all generations. On the contrary, as Joab said, "May Hashem your G-d add to the people a hundred times as many as they are..."[5]—he evaded counting the children of Israel. There are other matters learned from this Parsha, for it is written,[6] "And you shall take the atonement money and give it for the service of the Tent of Meeting," specifically the sockets that were made from it.[7] This means that even though the giving of the half-shekel for the sockets was only a one-time event—a temporary matter—nevertheless, it became a permanent matter, for the Mishkan exists forever and for all eternity.[8] Furthermore, we learn from this Parsha (and it is also proven from Tractate Shekalim 24a[9]) the commandment of the half-shekel for all generations,[10] a permanent obligation every single year to give a half-shekel to the Temple treasury, from which the communal offerings were brought, as is explicitly stated in the Mishnah in Shekalim.[11] However, regarding the half-shekel for all generations, the obligation is only to give the half-shekel, and this has no bearing at all on counting the children of Israel to know their sum; indeed, it is implied in many places that they did not count them. If so, a difficulty arises: the surface language of the Parsha implies

#### 260

that the introduction "When you take the sum of the children of Israel" applies to all the matters of the Parsha—meaning that "When you take..." is a condition and a fundamental element in all the matters of the Parsha.

**2) The explanation** is that the matter of the half-shekel is for the purpose of bringing the offerings. The general concept of this in *avodah* is that through the fact that they were offered upon the Altar, to be included in the fire from above—the aspect of the "lion that consumes the offerings"[12]—the *nefesh habehamis* in every Jew was diminished and included in holiness,[13] to the point that each person would bind his intellect and understanding to the greatness of Hashem, to be *batel* to Him. Now, this is accomplished through *tefillah*, which was instituted to correspond to the offerings.[14] But there must first be an empowerment and assistance for this from above, which is the concept of "taking the head" (*nisius rosh*) that comes through Moses, and the "extension of Moses in every generation,"[16] "When you take the sum of the children of Israel." For Moses is the *ra'aya mehimna* (faithful shepherd),[17] who shepherds (feeds and sustains) the *emunah*, as it is written,[18] "and feed [on] faith," through Torah and *gemilus chasadim*. Through this, the *nisius* and the raising of the head of the children of Israel is accomplished—that is, the elevation from below to above through the offerings and *tefillah*.

**3) To understand** the relevance of this matter specifically to Moses, the *ra'aya mehimna*, to whom it was said, "When you take the sum... this they shall give... a half-shekel," we must note that Moses is called *ra'aya mehimna* because he shepherds the *emunah* and feeds and sustains it. This is[19] because *emunah* by itself can remain in a state of *makif* (encompassing). As the saying goes,[20] "A thief at the mouth of the tunnel calls to the Merciful One." Even though he is a thief—which is worse even than a robber, as our Sages said,[21] "Why did the Torah treat a thief more severely than a robber? The latter equates the honor of the servant to the honor of his Master, while the former does not equate the honor of the servant to the honor of his Master (for he fears people, but is not careful regarding the Eye from above)"—meaning, the concealment is so great that even though he has a sense of shame (he fears people), he nevertheless "steals" the knowledge of Heaven. Yet, "at the mouth of the tunnel he calls to the Merciful One," meaning that even

#### 261

though he is doing the opposite of the Supreme Will, he asks Hashem to make him successful in this very matter which is the opposite of the Supreme Will. In a subtle way,[22] everyone can find this in himself—both those involved in business and those who "sit in the tent," both those who are within the four cubits of Torah and those who are within the four cubits of *tefillah*—for they also have the element of "a thief at the mouth of the tunnel calls to the Merciful One." Just as with businessmen: even though he believes that "It is He who gives you strength,"[23] he nevertheless delves into schemes that distract him from Torah and *avodah* and the fixed *shiurim* that are for businessmen as well. More specifically, when he succeeds in his business, and then there is some matter that is not as it should be (*s'iz epes nit azoy*), he then thinks of schemes, etc. This is the case even though Hashem made him successful in his business and he turned physicality into spirituality by giving from his money a *ma'aser* or *chomesh* (or what is in between) to *tzedakah*. And the mitzvah of *tzedakah* is the only mitzvah regarding which Hashem says, "And test Me now with this,"[24] and Hashem is surely trustworthy—yet he still thinks of schemes, which is a contradiction, like "a thief at the mouth of the tunnel calls to the Merciful One." And similarly with those who sit in the tent: he believes that the Torah is the wisdom and will of the Holy One, Blessed be He, and when he succeeds in his learning and achieves, he prides himself on it—needless to say when he learns for that purpose—and consequently, he will sometimes tilt the matter just so that he may have the upper hand. And many times they sometimes transgress a law in the *Shulchan Aruch* for the sake of their Torah business. And those who are learned in Torah but do not engage in *tefillah* at length—and certainly not in the *hisbonenus* (contemplation) before *tefillah*, or who do not engage in the three preparations for *tefillah* explained in *Likutei Torah*:[25] learning the inner dimensions of Torah, *taharah*, and *tzedakah*—this is because he thinks that the Torah he is learning is *his* Torah, his own Torah, and he needs to innovate in it with his own human intellect. Therefore, he prevents himself from the aforementioned matters, since they require time, and he needs that time so that he can innovate in Torah. But if he were learning Torah because it is the wisdom and will of the Holy One, Blessed be He, then he would understand that it is impossible that matters which the Holy One, Blessed be He, commanded—to learn Chassidus, to immerse in a *mikveh*, and to give *tzedakah*—would be a hindrance to the study of Torah, which is the wisdom and will of the Holy One, Blessed be He. All of this is because the *emunah* is in the state of *makif*, similar to "a thief at the mouth of the tunnel calls to the Merciful One." Therefore, there must be the influence of Moses, the *ra'aya mehimna*, who feeds and sustains the *emunah*, to draw the *emunah* into the interiority of his soul's powers so that they will behave in practice in accordance with his *emunah*. This is done specifically through his *hisbonenus* *aliba denafsha* (contemplation for himself) and he must fix his thought strongly, so that the result of this will not be false imaginations.[26]

#### 262

**4) And what** is the *hisbonenus*? It is known that there is a difference between the *emunah* that comes through the wisdom of philosophy—which is the *emunah* of the pious among the nations of the world[27]—and the *emunah* of the children of Israel. The *emunah* of the pious among the nations is in the aspect of *memalei kol almin* (filling all worlds), which is the vitality that is enclothed and divided into details; consequently, the world is a reality, only it is *batel* to the vitality enclothed within it, and this is the matter of the Name *Elokim*. The *emunah* of the children of Israel is in the aspect of *sovev kol almin* (encompassing all worlds), a general *makif* that is above intellect and division. More specifically, there are three matters in *emunah*:[19] the *emunah* in *memalei kol almin*, the *emunah* in *sovev kol almin*, and the *emunah* in the aspect of the *Atzmus* (Essence) that is above *sovev* and *memalei*. This refers to the *emunah* that comes through the wisdom of philosophy, which exists also among the nations of the world; a more elevated *emunah* that exists specifically in Israel, who are called "believers"; and furthermore, that Israel are called "children of believers,"[28] which is the *emunah* that comes as an inheritance from our father Abraham.

**The explanation** of the matter is that the first aspect of *emunah* is an *emunah* that is grasped even by human intellect, and it is the *emunah* in the aspect of *memalei kol almin*. As our Sages said,[29] "Just as the soul fills the body, so the Holy One, Blessed be He, fills the world." For man is called a "small world,"[30] and as it is stated in *Avos D'Rabbi Nosson*:[31] "Everything that He created in man, He created in the world," and the world is called a "large body."[32] Therefore, just as the soul fills the body—where the body by itself is inanimate and all its vitality is from the soul—so too the vitality in the worlds is Divine vitality, and the same proofs that exist for the vitality of the soul in the body exist also for the Divine vitality in the world. However, even though this matter is grasped by the intellect, it still requires the matter of *emunah*, because the physicality and materiality of the body covers and conceals the intellect. As we see empirically, because of being deeply immersed in desires, G-d forbid, people do things that are not according to intellect at all—not only the intellect of Israel, regarding which our Sages said,[33] "A person does not commit a sin unless a spirit of folly enters him," but also the intellect of the nations of the world. That is, desires rule and dominate him, and the intellect has no control at all. Therefore, grasping alone is not enough, and there must also be the matter of *emunah*, but nevertheless, it is understood even by the intellect. Above this is the *emunah* in the aspect of *sovev kol almin*. For the aspect of *sovev kol almin* is above the worlds, and it surrounds and encompasses them all equally (unlike the aspect of *memalei kol almin*, in which there is division between one world and another). The example

#### 263

for this in the soul is the general vitality that enlivens the entire body equally, without division between head and foot. This is why Israel are called "believers," because they possess the *emunah* in the aspect of *sovev kol almin*. However, there is an even more elevated *emunah*, which is the *emunah* in the aspect of the Divinity that is above even *sovev kol almin*. For even the aspect of *sovev kol almin* has at least a negative relationship to the worlds, because since we say that this aspect is not in the category of worlds, even though it is not in the category of worlds, the very fact that we relate this aspect to the worlds and say that it is not in the category of worlds—this is at least a negative relationship. But in truth, the essence of Divinity is not that the worlds are created from it,[34] and from this it is understood that His Essence and Being is above even a negative relationship to the worlds. This matter, that Israel are called "children of believers," is from the side of the *emunah* in the aspect of the Essence and Being of the *Ein Sof*, blessed be He, which is above even the aspect of *sovev kol almin*, and this *emunah* is an inheritance from our father Abraham, the head of the believers.[35]

**It should be added** that even in the *emunah* in the aspect of *memalei kol almin*, there is a difference between Israel and the nations of the world. Similar to how the world of *Asiyah* in *Beriah, Yetzirah, Asiyah* is not the same as the *Asiyah* in *Atzilus*, as is understood simply from the fact that there is a *parsah* (partition) between *Atzilus* and *Beriah, Yetzirah, Asiyah*, and the light that passes through the *parsah* is a type of "new light."[36] It is the same regarding the matter of *emunah*: since in Israel there exists the *emunah* in the aspect of *sovev kol almin* and above it, their *emunah* in the aspect of *memalei kol almin* is also of a different type.

**5) The explanation** of the matter is that the aspect of *memalei kol almin* is called by the name "the Supreme Speech,"[37] for just as speech is for the sake of another—meaning it is an aspect of revelation to the other and in the category of the other—and furthermore, there is an interruption in it, as it is written,[38] "a time to speak and a time to refrain from speaking," so too is it with the aspect of *memalei kol almin*, which is the revelation to the other and contains division. The world of speech is called "the city of our G-d,"[39][40] which pertains to the Name *Elokim*. That is, when the Name *Havayah* is in concealment and the Name *Elokim* is in revelation, then it is called "the city of our G-d," the aspect of the world of speech, which contains division, etc. With this, one can also understand the ruling[41] (cited in Chassidus[42]) that the children of Noah were not commanded regarding the "partnership" (*shituf*). For seemingly, since Israel were commanded regarding the "partnership" because the truth is so, why were the children of Noah not commanded regarding the "partnership"? But the matter is that the children of Noah, whose root is in the aspect of *memalei kol almin*—and in the aspect of *memalei kol almin*, the world of speech, there exists the matter of division, as it is written,[43] "which Hashem your G-d has allotted to all the nations..."—therefore, for them, this became the matter of "partnership," that they call Him "the G-d of gods."[44] All of this is the matter of speech, the aspect of *memalei kol almin*. However, the aspect of *sovev kol almin* is the matter of thought, for thought has no interruption and wanders constantly, and furthermore, thought is a garment uniquely bound with the soul. This is[45] the reason why the *emunah* of the nations of the world is in the aspect of *memalei kol almin* and the *emunah* of Israel is in the aspect of *sovev kol almin*. For the nations of the world have their root in the Name *Elokim*, the aspect of *memalei kol almin*, the world of speech, whereas Israel have their root in the aspect of *sovev kol almin*, the world of thought, as it is said,[46] "Israel arose in the thought." And the fact that there is in Israel *emunah* also in the aspect that is above *sovev kol almin* is because Israel *arose* in the thought, as is known the interpretation[47] of the saying "Israel arose in the thought"—that they arose to the most elevated level in thought, which is above all revelations. Furthermore, their root is above the matter of thought entirely. For even the aspect of "arose in the thought" is within the category of thought, only it is an elevated aspect in thought. Similar to the saying of our Sages,[46] "The thought of Israel preceded everything." Even though it preceded everything, nevertheless, we relate this thought to everything, only that it preceded everything. However, the root of the souls is above the matter of thought entirely, above even the most elevated aspect in thought, to the point that it is not applicable to say regarding it a matter of "preceding everything," since there is no relationship between them at all. This is what our Sages said,[48] "With whom did He take counsel? With the souls of the righteous." Meaning, the consultation regarding thought itself is with the souls of Israel, from which it is understood that the souls are above the matter of thought entirely. That is, the matter of "Israel arose in the thought" is in revelation, but their root is above this, regarding which it is said, "With whom did He take counsel," etc. And from the side of their root in this aspect, they possess the matter of *emunah* also in the aspect of the Essence and Being of the *Ein Sof*, blessed be He.

#### 265

**6) And now,** although Israel possess all the aspects of *emunah*—not only the *emunah* in the aspect of *memalei kol almin*, and not only the *emunah* in the aspect of *sovev kol almin*, but also the *emunah* in the aspect of the Essence and Being of the *Ein Sof*, blessed be He—nevertheless, they require Moses, the *ra'aya mehimna*, to feed the *emunah* within them. This means, not only the *emunah* in the aspect of the Essence and Being of the *Ein Sof*, blessed be He—which, being merely an inheritance, could remain in concealment, and Moses must reveal it from concealment into revelation—but also the *emunah* in the aspect of *sovev kol almin* could remain in the state of *makif*, and Moses must draw this *emunah* into the interiority. Furthermore, even the *emunah* in the aspect of *memalei kol almin* that is grasped by the intellect must have in it the matter of "feeding the *emunah*," so that it will penetrate all the internal matters, down to thought, speech, and action. Without this, it is possible to be "a thief at the mouth of the tunnel calls to the Merciful One" in a simple way, as mentioned, that from the side of being immersed in desires, it is possible to do such things that even the pious among the nations of the world do not do. And it is for this that the work of Moses, the *ra'aya mehimna*, who feeds and sustains the *emunah*, exists. This is because regarding Moses it is written,[49] "For I drew him from the water," from the aspect of the Upper Waters that are above the heavens and the heaven of heavens, which are the aspect of *sovev kol almin*. Therefore, he can draw down also the *emunah* in the aspect of the Essence and Being of the *Ein Sof*, blessed be He. And Moses draws this *emunah* specifically into Israel, because from the side of their root, they possess this aspect of *emunah* (and as explained above[50] regarding the matter of "When you acquire a Hebrew slave," that this is like an acquisition that is not a new thing, but only the revelation of the concealment[51]).

**7) And according to this,** the matter of the half-shekel is also understood. Regarding the half-shekel, our Sages said[52] that the Holy One, Blessed be He, showed Moses a coin of fire and said to him, "This they shall give," "Like this they shall give." Meaning, through the giving of the half-shekel from below—the aspect of *is'arusa d'letata* (arousal from below)—they draw down from above the aspect of a coin of fire, *is'arusa d'le'ela* (arousal from above). However, this is only the aspect of *is'arusa d'le'ela* that the *is'arusa d'letata* reaches, which is in its measure and is drawn down through it, and through this, there is subsequently drawn down the aspect of *is'arusa d'le'ela* that the *is'arusa d'letata* does not reach. Similar to what is explained regarding the *re'usa d'liba* (desire of the heart), that there are two aspects to it.[53] There is the aspect of *re'usa d'liba* that comes through *hisbonenus*, meaning that although it is above grasp, nevertheless, it is drawn down through *hisbonenus*. And there is the aspect of *re'usa d'liba* that does not come through *hisbonenus*, but is in the essence of the soul, etc. This is the matter of the half-shekel in the "shekel of the Sanctuary" (*shekel hakodesh*), *kodesh* specifically, which is above *kadosh* (holy), as is known[54]

#### 266

the difference between *kadosh* and *kodesh*. *Kadosh* is the drawing down, as explained regarding the "Holy One, Blessed be He" (*HaKadosh Baruch Hu*), that although *kadosh* is a term of separation—that He is holy and separate—nevertheless, He is also "Blessed" and drawn down, as is hinted at by the fact that *kadosh* is spelled with a *vav*, which indicates the drawing down.[55] That is, He is at least in the category of *sovev kol almin*. Whereas *kodesh* is a word in its own right,[56] which is an aspect that is above even *sovev kol almin*. And this is "And they shall give, each man, a ransom for his soul,"[2] that through the giving of the half-shekel, the aspect of the Essence and Being of the *Ein Sof*, blessed be He, is drawn down, from the side of the *yechidah* in the soul and the aspect of the "Unique One" enclothed in the *yechidah* in the soul,[57] whose root is in the Essence and Being of the *Ein Sof*, blessed be He, as mentioned above. And regarding this it is said, "When you take the sum" (*tisa et rosh*) specifically, for this is that Moses our teacher raises and elevates the head of the children of Israel,[58] through which the matter of "a ransom for his soul" can occur, which is the matter of drawing down the Essence and Being of the *Ein Sof*, blessed be He.

**With this,** one can understand what our Sages said in the Midrash[59] that Moses asked the Holy One, Blessed be He, regarding the commandment of the half-shekel, "What will be with it in the coming generations?" and the Holy One, Blessed be He, said to him that this is why it is written "When you take" (*ki tisa*) in the future tense. Seemingly, it is not understood why Moses asked specifically about this commandment. But the matter is that this commandment includes the general matter of man's *avodah*, which is the matter of the offerings that they brought from the half-shekel, through which the *nefesh habehamis* is diminished and included in holiness. That is, that which cannot be refined is diminished, and that which can be refined is included in holiness, to the point that the *avodah* is in the manner of "And they shall give, each man, a ransom for his soul," through which they reach the aspect of the "shekel of the Sanctuary," *kodesh*—a word in its own right—meaning that there is drawn down not only the aspect of *memalei kol almin*, and not only the aspect of *sovev kol almin*, but also the aspect of the Essence and Being of the *Ein Sof*, blessed be He, before Whom everything is considered as nothing.[60] Therefore, Moses asked specifically about this commandment, "What will be for the coming generations?" and to this the Holy One, Blessed be He, answered him that He is writing in the Torah "When you take" in the future tense, meaning that it applies also to all generations, for the "extension of Moses in every generation," and the Moses in every generation will draw down not only the aspect of *memalei kol almin*, and not only the aspect of *sovev kol almin*, but also the aspect of the Essence and Being of the *Ein Sof*, blessed be He, before Whom everything is considered as nothing, and there is nothing else besides Him.[61]

## With the help of Hashem. Sicha of Shabbos Parshas Vayakhel, Parshas Shekalim, Mevarchim HaChodesh Adar Sheni, 5711

#### 267

(Unedited)

**1.** Regarding Parshas Shekalim, we find a curious Midrash:

"In Parshas Shekalim, Moshe said before the Ribono shel Olam, 'Ribono shel Olam, once I die, I will not be remembered.' The Ribono shel Olam said to him, 'By your life, just as you are standing now and giving them Parshas Shekalim and you are lifting their heads, so too, every year that they read it before Me, it is as if you are standing there at that time and lifting their heads. From where do we know this?
