From what they read in the matter: "Hashem spoke to Moshe, saying, 'When you take the head [Ki Tisa et Rosh]'"—it does not say "Take the head [Seh et Rosh]," but rather "When you take [Ki Tisa].'"

In other words, since it does not say "Take the head" in the imperative, but rather "When you take" in the future tense, this hints also to the "lifting of the head" that will occur in the future, every year, through Moshe—the *atpashuta d'Moshe* (the extension of Moshe) that exists in every generation.

Seemingly, this is puzzling: What is the reason that specifically in Parshas Shekalim did Moshe ask the Ribono shel Olam what would be in future generations ("Once I die"), unlike all the previous parshios where he did not ask what would be in future generations?

**2.** This can be understood by first explaining the content of the mitzvah of Machatzis HaShekel—"They shall give, each man, a ransom for his soul... this they shall give... a half-shekel... the rich shall not increase and the poor shall not decrease."

Regarding the verse "This they shall give," Chazal say: "The Ribono shel Olam brought out a kind of coin of fire... and showed it to Moshe and said to him, 'This they shall give; like this they shall give.'" Regarding the reason why the Ribono shel Olam needed to show Moshe a coin of fire, it is explained in Tosafos that "he (Moshe) was astonished by the matter: 'What can a person give as a ransom for his soul?'"

Seemingly, this is not understood: How was Moshe's astonishment ("What can a person give as a ransom for his soul?") resolved by the fact that the Ribono shel Olam showed him a "coin of fire"?

#### 268

The matter is that by showing Moshe a "coin of fire," He showed him that the Machatzis HaShekel that Bnei Yisrael give ("This they shall give... a half-shekel") *is itself* a "coin of fire," given from within the vitality and heat, the *esh* (fire), of the *etzem hanefesh* (the essence of the soul). Therefore, it becomes a "ransom for his soul"—meaning, the giving of the essence of the soul, not just the level of *nefesh, ruach, neshamah*, but the level of *yechidah* in the soul.

**3.** Based on this, we can explain the reason that the giving of the Machatzis HaShekel is in a manner where "the rich shall not increase and the poor shall not decrease":

Seemingly, this is not understood: Since we are speaking about wealth and poverty *in this matter* [for regarding wealth and poverty in other matters, there is no need to say "the rich shall not increase and the poor shall not decrease from the half-shekel"], what is the reason that the rich in this matter shall not increase, and the poor in this matter shall not decrease?

The explanation for this is that the distinction between rich and poor relates to the revealed powers of the soul, but regarding the *etzem hanefesh*, the level of *yechidah*, the rich and the poor are equal; the poor has no less and the rich has no more. It is like in the physical realm, where the distinction between strong and weak is in the revealed powers, but in the general vitality, the strong and the weak are equal, for even the weak is alive, and the strong is no more than alive.

And since the Machatzis HaShekel is a "ransom for his soul," which is connected to the *etzem hanefesh* (as mentioned above), it is in a manner where "the rich shall not increase and the poor shall not decrease."

**4.** Based on this, we can also explain the special connection of Parshas Shekalim to Moshe:

In order for the giving of the Machatzis HaShekel to be from the side of the *etzem hanefesh*, a "ransom for his soul," there is a need for the action of Moshe (to whom it was said, "When you take the head of Bnei Yisrael"), because specifically Moshe can awaken the level of *yechidah* in the soul, which is the concept of the "lifting of the head" of Bnei Yisrael.

And this is the reason that specifically in Parshas Shekalim, Moshe asked the Ribono shel Olam what would be in future generations ("Once I die")—because for the purpose of giving a "ransom for his soul," the *etzem hanefesh*, the action of Moshe specifically is necessary.

And to this, the Ribono shel Olam replied, "It does not say 'Take the head,' but rather 'When *you* take [Ki Tisa],'" in the future tense: "Just as you are standing now and giving them Parshas Shekalim and you are lifting their heads, so too, *every year* that they read it before Me, it is as if *you are standing there at that time and lifting their heads*"—that when Bnei Yisrael read Parshas Shekalim every year from within renewed vitality (fire), "every day they should be in your eyes as new," the matter of the lifting of the head is accomplished through the *atpashuta d'Moshe* in that generation, who awakens the level of *yechidah* in the soul.

***

**5.** Maamar beginning "Ki Tisa et Rosh Bnei Yisrael."

***

**6.** (After the maamar, the Rebbe said:)

In the maamarim of Parshas Tisa that were said by our Rebbeim Nesi'im—the Alter Rebbe, the Mitteler Rebbe, the Tzemach Tzedek, the Maharash, the Rashab, and the Rayatz—the same matters are explained as were explained in the maamar above: the action of Moshe, who feeds and sustains the *emunah* (faith) of Bnei Yisrael, the essence of which is in the level of *sovev kol almin*, etc.

And in continuation of what was discussed in the maamar regarding the superiority of the *emunah* of Bnei Yisrael over the nations of the world, who are not commanded against *shituf* (associating other powers with Hashem), because the root of the nations of the world is from the level of *dibbur* (speech), which contains division (which is why division in Elokus occurred among them)—it should be added that in one of the maamarim of the Rebbe Rashab (which was also said by the Rayatz), he also explains regarding *angels*, whose formation is from the level of *dibbur*. (The Rebbe smiled and said:) However, he does not conclude there regarding the matter of *shituf*.

Seemingly: How is it possible to say such a thing (a connection to the matter of *shituf*) regarding angels?!

—When I studied the maamar, an explanation of the matter occurred to me:

Regarding the reason for the creation of the angels on the second day and not on the first day, Chazal say: "Nothing was created on the first day, so that you should not say that Michael was stretching in the south of the firmament and Gavriel in the north, and the Ribono shel Olam was arranging in the middle; rather, 'I, Hashem, make everything, stretching out the heavens by Myself, spreading out the earth by Myself'—it is written 'Who is with Me,' who was a partner with Me in the creation of the world."

It can be said that from the very fact that the creation of the angels on the first day could have caused a *kas salka da'atach* (a mistaken thought) of *shituf*, G-d forbid, it is proven that the angels have some connection to the matter of *shituf*; otherwise, it would not be possible for their creation to cause a *kas salka da'atach* regarding a matter of *shituf*.

Seemingly, how is such a matter possible among angels—that through them there would be room for a mistake regarding the matter of *shituf*?!

The explanation for this is as explained in the maamar, that the formation of the angels is from the level of *dibbur*, and in *dibbur* there is division, as mentioned above.

*

**7.** It was discussed above that the need for the action of Moshe, who feeds and sustains *emunah*, is because *emunah* is a level of *makif* (encompassing light). Therefore, "a thief at the mouth of the tunnel, Hashem calls to him," as everyone can find this within themselves (in subtlety, at least). For example, among business people: at first they succeed in their business and give tzedakah, etc., and later, when the business is not succeeding so well ("it is somehow not quite right"), they then think of schemes and forget that the success of the business depends on giving tzedakah, etc.

Based on this, we can explain what is written at the beginning of the maamar beginning "His left hand is under my head and His right hand embraces me," in *Torah Or*, at the beginning of Parshas Ki Tisa,

—where the continuation of the matters is missing. The Rayatz related that due to the intensity of the *dveikus* (cleaving) of the Alter Rebbe when saying Chassidus, he would sometimes roll on the floor and continue saying the maamar while rolling, and the main *chozer* (repeater), R' Pinchas Reizes, would roll after the Alter Rebbe in order to hear the continuation of the maamar. Apparently, at the time the aforementioned maamar was said, R' Pinchas was not present, or he did not manage to roll after the Alter Rebbe... and therefore the continuation of the matters is missing—

that "it is the way of Hashem for Bnei Yisrael, His close people, when the level of 'the left pushes away' is awakened Above due to the actions of those below, that it becomes for them a salvation... for the level of 'the left pushes away' is not a total pushing away, G-d forbid, but rather 'the right draws near,' and this is 'His right hand embraces me.'" Seemingly, this is not understood: How is it possible to err and think about "the right draws near" that it is "the left pushes away"?

This can be explained according to what was said above in the maamar—that when one sees that there is an obstacle in the success of the business, one can think that this is a matter of pushing away, "the left pushes away," and one must know that the truth is that this is a matter of "His right hand embraces me."

**8.** The explanation for this:

It is stated in the Midrash that "when Yaakov and Esav were in their mother's womb, Yaakov said to Esav, 'My brother, two worlds are before us, this world and the World to Come... if you wish, take you this world and I will take the World to Come'... at that time Esav took his portion of this world and Yaakov took his portion of the World to Come. And when Yaakov came from the house of Lavan and Esav saw that he had sons and daughters, servants and maidservants, he said to him, 'Yaakov my brother, did you not tell me that you would take the World to Come and I would take this world? From where do you have all this wealth, etc.?'"

What is truly the reason that a Jew (Yaakov) is given physicality, this world? It is only for the sake of spirituality, the World to Come, and in two ways: (a) so that he can engage in Torah and *avodah* without distractions from the worry of livelihood, (b) so that he can make spirituality out of the physicality itself, through giving tzedakah.

Therefore, when a Jew knows that the reason the Ribono shel Olam caused him to succeed in his business is for the sake of spirituality, then, upon seeing that there is an obstacle in the success of the business, he knows and understands simply that the advice for this is—not to look for schemes, etc., but—to strengthen himself in Torah and *avodah*, in giving tzedakah, etc.

And in the style of the maamar in *Torah Or*—that the prevention of success in business matters is not a matter of pushing away from the left line, "the left pushes away," "His left hand is under my head" [meaning: not only is it not a permanent pushing away, G-d forbid, but not even a temporary one], but rather the opposite—this is a matter of drawing near from the right line, "the right draws near," "His right hand embraces me." For the prevention of success is in a manner that "it became for him a salvation," that through this he will be awakened to increase in Torah and *avodah*, in giving tzedakah, and consequently, there will be even more of an increase in the influence of the Ribono shel Olam also in physical matters.

And just as the words are said regarding "abundant sustenance," so it is also regarding "life"—that when there is an obstacle, G-d forbid, in health, one must know that this is not a pushing away, G-d forbid, from the left line, but rather "His right hand embraces me."

And similarly regarding "children"—those who received the blessing of the Rebbe for living and enduring offspring and are waiting all the time for the fulfillment of the blessing, and the matter had already begun ("it had already reached that point") and stopped suddenly, they must know that this is not a pushing away, G-d forbid, even for a moment, but rather the opposite—"it became for them a salvation," that after some time they will see for themselves that this matter itself was from the side of "His right hand embraces me."

***

**9.** The matter of the construction of the Mishkan and its vessels, which was written in Parshas Terumah and Tetzaveh and was repeated in Parshas Vayakhel and Pekudei, was edited by the Rebbe and printed in *Likkutei Sichos*, Vol. 1, p. 195 and onward (and in brief in *Igros Kodesh* of the Rebbe, Vol. 4, p. 190 and onward).

***

**10.** It was discussed above (sections 3-4) that the revelation and drawing down of the level of *yechidah* in the soul, the essence of the soul (which is above the division of rich and poor, for the distinction between them is only in the revealed powers of the soul)—is accomplished specifically by Moshe.

And as explained above, the *emunah* of Bnei Yisrael in the *Atzmus* and *Mahus* (Essence and Being) of the *Ein Sof* is drawn down and revealed specifically by Moshe. For even though this *emunah* is an inheritance from Avraham Avinu, and therefore Bnei Yisrael are called "believers, the children of believers," nevertheless, its drawing down and revelation in an internal way is specifically through Moshe.

And as explained elsewhere, this is in accordance with the distinction between Avraham and Moshe: Avraham, Avraham—there is a *pisek ta'ama* (a pause) between them, meaning there is a difference between the level of Avraham as he is in Atzilus and his descent into *Beriah, Yetzirah, Asiyah*. Whereas Moshe, Moshe—there is no *pisek ta'ama* between them, for even in his descent into *Beriah, Yetzirah, Asiyah*, he is as he is in Atzilus ("the same Moshe"). Therefore, specifically through him is the drawing down of *emunah* in the *Atzmus* and *Mahus* of the *Ein Sof* accomplished internally.

More specifically:

It is stated in the Zohar, "Three bonds are bound one to the other: the Ribono shel Olam, the Torah, and Yisrael, and in all of them there is the hidden and the revealed." It is explained in Chassidus that the revealed of Yisrael is bound to the revealed of the Torah, and through this, it is also bound to the revealed of the Ribono shel Olam; and the hidden of Yisrael is bound to the hidden of the Torah, and through this, it is bound to the hidden of the Ribono shel Olam.

And all of this is accomplished by Moshe—because through him is accomplished the revelation and drawing down of the essence of the soul, the level of *yechidah* in the soul, which is the hidden of Yisrael, which is bound and connected with the hidden of the Torah, the inwardness of the Torah, and through this, also with the hidden of the Ribono shel Olam, the inwardness and *Atzmus* of the *Ein Sof*.

**11.** From this, the great necessity of the matter of connection to the Rebbe—the Moshe of the generation, the *atpashuta d'Moshe* in every generation—is understood:

By way of introduction—even though the term is "*atpashuta* d'Moshe," merely an extension, nevertheless, since we are speaking about the *essence*, it is in a manner that "the essence, when you grasp a part of it, you grasp all of it." Thus, even in the *atpashuta d'Moshe* of the generation, there exists the *entire essence* of Moshe.

And through the connection to the Rebbe—the Moshe of the generation, who possesses the entire essence of Moshe—the Rebbe connects the hidden in the soul (through the hidden of the Torah) with the hidden of the Ribono shel Olam.

Therefore, all of Yisrael must know that through the fulfillment of Torah and Mitzvos alone, without connection to the Rebbe, and without the inwardness of the Torah that was revealed by the Rebbeim, one indeed reaches the most elevated levels in holiness, but the connection of the essence of the soul with the *Atzmus* and *Mahus* of the *Ein Sof* is missing. It is necessary that there be a connection to the Rebbe—the Moshe of the generation, who possesses the entire essence of Moshe—who connects the hidden of Yisrael, the essence of the soul, with the hidden of the Torah, the inwardness of the Torah that was revealed by the Rebbeim, and through this, with the hidden of the Ribono shel Olam.

**12.** And just as the words are said regarding spirituality (that the drawing down of the essence of the soul is accomplished by the Rebbe, the Moshe of the generation)—so it is also regarding physicality:

The essential vitality (which is above the division of strong and weak, for the distinction between them is only in the revealed powers)—its revelation and drawing down is accomplished specifically by the Rebbe, the Moshe of the generation.

In other words: regarding the extension of vitality—when there is some breakdown (not just a concealment of vitality, but a breakdown in the extension of vitality), one can turn to a doctor, and the doctor can help. But regarding essential vitality, a doctor cannot help, and it is necessary to turn specifically to the Rebbe, the Moshe of the generation, who possesses the entire essence of Moshe, and he can draw down essential vitality as well.

From this, it is understood that even when the doctor's opinion is that so-and-so cannot live, G-d forbid, regarding essential vitality, the doctor is not the master, and it is in the power of the Rebbe, the Moshe of the generation, to draw down essential vitality.

**13.** Regarding the connection to the Rebbe, there is also benefit in speaking about it—in the sense of "we will pay with our lips instead of bulls."

(The Rebbe concluded:) May the Ribono shel Olam help that there should be no need for the matter of "we will pay with our lips instead of bulls," but rather the Rebbe himself—"the Rebbe shlita"—will lead us toward Moshiach Tzidkeinu.

## 275

Our Torah, in all its parts, is a Torah of life and is eternal. My revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, explained: "A Torah of life—a Torah that provides instruction for every single person in their daily life," in the life of the individual, and all the more so in the life of the collective. There are many matters in the Torah that, *at first glance*, one might imagine have no relevance to practical life in these days, or to the situation in which we currently find ourselves. Yet, upon reflection, one can find in them a parallel to the present situation—whether in a subtle way[1](#_ftn1543) or the opposite—and derive from these matters clear instructions and absolute directives regarding action: "Arise and do," or "Take heed lest you do."[2](#_ftn1544)

The same applies to the maamar printed here.

It demands with strength that we stand "with mesiras nefesh in the actual fulfillment of Torah and mitzvos,"[3](#_ftn1545) and especially regarding chinuch—without concern for the enemy, "the overt, warring hater," and without concern for the avenger, "the hidden hater who devises plots... regarding the vengeance that goes beyond the bounds of the law."

And it promises that these children—who will continue to be tinokos shel beis raban, or whom we will now make into tinokos shel beis raban despite all the decrees, intimidations, schemes, and deceptions—their learning and their chinuch are precisely what will silence these enemies and avengers. On the contrary, through this mesiras nefesh, they will merit the Geulah.

#### 276

Even now, in every country, there are those—whether enemies who fight openly or avengers who fight with schemes—whose intention is one and the same: to control the children. Their goal is the same as the goal of Achaz: "If there are no small ones, there are no adults... no students... no chachamim... no Torah... no Hashem to cause His Shechinah to dwell in the world."

And just as it was then, so it is promised now: that through *mesiras nefesh and standing without fear* in the fulfillment of Torah and mitzvos, and in the matter of chinuch in particular, all the schemes and decrees "that Torah should, chas v’shalom, be forgotten from Yisrael, and to lead them, chas v’shalom, away from Elokus" will be of no avail. The children will be "for signs and wonders in Yisrael," and "the foundation for 'and your people are all tzaddikim.'"

And great is the power of this mesiras nefesh to merit, through it, the complete and true Geulah, which will come speedily in our days through Moshiach Tzidkeinu.

**Menachem Schneerson**

*7 Adar Sheni, 5711.*

*Brooklyn, N.Y.*

## With the help of Hashem. Recorded at the time of a Bris Milah*, 7 Adar Sheni, 5711

#### 277

Unedited

[Following the Bris, before the meal[1], the Rebbe tasted some mezonos and blessed the father of the child that he should merit to raise him, etc., with abundance. He also blessed the mohel, saying: "You are making Yidden," and blessed him that he should continue his work with success, both materially and spiritually.]

**1.** I once asked the Rebbe about customs—why they were not recorded. He replied: "It was not a priority" (*m'iz nit gelegen in dem*). I asked: "But there are many matters that concern practical application and one needs to know how to conduct oneself?" He replied: "It is indeed a pity" (*es is take a shod*) that they were not recorded.

Therefore, when I observed any custom of the Rebbe, I noted it down, and regarding those that were relevant to many, I understood from the Rebbe that it is worthwhile to publicize them.

**2.** I once had the occasion to be present at a Bris Milah where the Rebbe was honored with sandakaus[2], and I noted in my records several behaviors[3]:

The Rebbe ordered his tallis to be brought, and he wrapped himself in it without a bracha[4].

The Bris Milah took place about three or four hours after Shacharis, after all the shiurim of interruption—as we find in the Shulchan Aruch of the Alter Rebbe several shiurim: until one diverts his attention[5], two hours[6], and the like[7]—and nevertheless, he wrapped himself in his tallis without a bracha.

#### 278

And although he could have wrapped himself in a borrowed tallis, over which one does not make a bracha[8], he nonetheless wrapped himself specifically in his own tallis, and without a bracha, to teach that there is no need to make a bracha again even after a shiur of interruption.

During the Bris Milah, I noticed that the Rebbe—who was the sandak—appeared very pale and white, and at the moment of the cutting, the Rebbe turned his head as one who cannot look at blood.

It is worth noting the wonder of this matter—for the Rebbe was a shochet[9], and yet, he turned his head as one who cannot look at blood.

Likewise, I noticed that during the entire time of the Bris Milah, the Rebbe was whispering with his lips (*gesheptshet mit di lippen*) in a low voice. I do not know what he said at the time, but I observed that he was saying something.

Later, I asked the Rebbe what he said during the Bris Milah (the Rebbe smiled and said:) and I added that this is a matter of practical concern, so that if I am ever honored with sandakaus, I will know what one needs to say... but the Rebbe did not answer me.

(The Rebbe concluded:) Nu, I do not know what he said, but I know at least that he was saying something.

**3.** After the Bris Milah, during the meal[10], the Rebbe said[11]:

The order of avodah after Matan Torah is that first there must be the removal of the orlah of the body, which is the matter of maaseh (action), then the removal of the orlah of the tongue, the matter of speech, and then the removal of the orlah of the heart, the matter of thought.

With Avraham Avinu—before Matan Torah—the order was reversed: "At three years old he recognized his Creator"[12]—which is the matter of thought, then his avodah was in publicizing His divinity in the world[13]—in speech, and then was the milah in its literal sense—in action.

But for us, the beginning is with the primary matter—the matter of *maaseh*.

#### 279

**4.** The Rebbe related[14]:

Regarding a Bris Milah for one of the grandchildren of the Tzemach Tzedek, they had to choose between two mohelim. One mohel was an expert craftsman in his work, but was not so connected to kavanos, etc., and one mohel was connected to kavanos, but was not such an expert craftsman. The Tzemach Tzedek ordered to take the mohel who was an expert craftsman, saying: *Asiyah l'eila*, and "l'eila" on such a level that there is no need there for an "address" (*aza leila vos m'darf dortn nit kein adressen*).

The Rebbe added: Seemingly, one could explain the meaning of these words that the reason one can take the expert mohel even though he is not connected to kavanos is because the other mohel directed the kavanos, as we find in several matters that the kavanah of one is effective also for another[16]. But from the language of the Tzemach Tzedek, "Asiyah l'eila," it is understood that *the asiyah itself* is sufficient and good, and there is no need for kavanos.

**5.** And one should add in explaining the virtue of the asiyah in the mitzvah of milah:

The special virtue in the mitzvah of milah that we do not find a parallel to in other mitzvos (except for Pesach) is that it is a mitzvas asei (positive commandment), and it carries a warning of kares, which is a novelty compared to other mitzvos, because a warning of kares exists only in mitzvos lo saaseh (negative commandments), and only in milah and Pesach is there a warning of kares for the neglect of a mitzvas asei[17].

And the explanation of the matter[18]:

It is explained in the discourses of Chassidus[19] that there is a virtue in mitzvos lo saaseh over mitzvos asei, that mitzvos asei are in the category of *Vav-Hei*, and mitzvos lo saaseh are in the category of *Yud-Hei*, because through the fulfillment of mitzvos asei, one draws down lights that can come and be enclothed in vessels, and therefore their drawing down is through *asiyah*, whereas through mitzvos lo saaseh, one draws down lights that are above enclothement in vessels, and therefore their drawing down is in a manner where through the *absence of asiyah* (refraining from doing the thing), the light is drawn down automatically, but it is impossible to draw them down through asiyah.

That is to say: There is indeed a virtue in drawing down light that can come and be enclothed

#### 280

in vessels, and for this reason[20] a mitzvas asei overrides a mitzvas lo saaseh[21], but nevertheless, mitzvos lo saaseh are higher than mitzvos asei, since through them a more elevated light is drawn down, a light that is above enclothement in vessels.

And because of the great virtue of mitzvos lo saaseh over mitzvos asei—the warning of kares is specifically in mitzvos lo saaseh.

And since in the mitzvah of milah and Pesach there is a warning of kares, it must be that their virtue is as the virtue of mitzvos lo saaseh, meaning that through them one draws down *lights that are above enclothement in vessels*, and furthermore, that even the lights that are above enclothement in vessels, which generally cannot be drawn down through asiyah but only through the absence of asiyah (lo saaseh), are drawn down in milah and Pesach through *asiyah*.

**6.** According to this, one can explain the statement of our Sages[22] regarding the virtue of milah over Shabbos—"Shabbos... is equal to all the mitzvos of the Torah and (nevertheless) milah overrides it, a parable to two matronas who were coming one after the other and you do not know which is greater than the other, the one that descends before the other, you know that the other is greater than it":

Even though "Shabbos is equal to all the mitzvos of the Torah," even on Shabbos there is the definition and distinction of mitzvas asei and mitzvas lo saaseh, as mentioned, that the drawing down of lights into vessels is in the manner of asiyah (mitzvas asei), and the drawing down of lights above enclothement in vessels is in the manner of the absence of asiyah (mitzvas lo saaseh), and it is impossible to draw them down in the manner of asiyah.

And therefore "milah overrides it," that milah is greater than Shabbos—that it possesses the virtue of mitzvos lo saaseh which are higher than mitzvos asei (as is understood from the fact that it has a warning of kares), that through it are drawn down the lights that are above enclothement in vessels, and not only that, but these elevated lights (which generally are drawn down specifically through the absence of asiyah) are drawn down in the manner of *asiyah*.

**7.** And in explaining the reason for this—one can say:

The mitzvah of milah (and likewise Pesach) was stated before the Dibbur (the Giving of the Torah). And even though we fulfill it from the perspective of the command after the Dibbur[23], nevertheless, it also relates to the mitzvah of milah as it was before the Dibbur[24].

#### 281

[And it is worth noting that we find similarly regarding the teachings of Chassidus—that the Tanya relates to the manner of the revelation of Chassidus after Petersburg, even though its writing was before Petersburg[25].]

And it can be said that the distinction between the manner of drawing down lights into vessels through asiyah and the drawing down of elevated lights above enclothement in vessels through the absence of asiyah was innovated after the Dibbur, but before the Dibbur there was no such measurement and limitation, and therefore, in the mitzvah of milah which was stated and relates to before the Dibbur, one can draw down lights that are above enclothement in vessels through asiyah[26].

**8.** (The Rebbe continued to tell about the Bris Milah at which the Rebbe Rayatz was present:)

At the aforementioned Bris Milah, the Rebbe gave twenty zlotys for the yeshiva, saying that this sum is as a down payment for the child's (the infant being circumcised) learning in the yeshiva[27].

And one should establish this custom at every Bris Milah—to give the yeshiva a down payment for the child's learning in the yeshiva.

(The Rebbe smiled and said:) First of all—there is a benefit in giving money to the yeshiva, and furthermore, and this is the main thing, since this is a practice that the Rebbe established, one should establish this custom.

[The Rebbe gave the father of the child five dollars to give to the yeshiva, saying that the value of twenty zlotys (the sum the Rebbe Rayatz gave) at that time is equal today to five dollars.

The father of the child asked the Rebbe if he could redeem these bills (that he received from the Rebbe) and give the yeshiva other bills, and the Rebbe replied that he could redeem them, and added:]

#### 282

In hekdesh (consecrated property) we do find a leniency in this matter (even though in general it has several stringencies), that "it is redeemed for less than its value," and therefore it should be emphasized that at the very least, the redemption should not be for less than its value[28].

[The Rebbe gave the father of the child a Tehillas Hashem Siddur, Kehot publication 5711, and said:]

Through Hashgacha Pratis, this Siddur arrived today from the printing press, in which the biography of the Rebbe is printed. This Siddur should be kept for the child until he grows up and goes to yeshiva, and he will learn in it Aleph-Beis and Ivri[29].

**********

## B"H. The text of the telegram that the Rebbe shlita was pleased to send to Anash sheyichyu throughout the world in anticipation of the days of Purim, 5711

#### 282a

Please hold a farbrengen on Purim and also on Shabbos with a special awakening toward the avodah of chinuch in yiras shamayim.

With blessings for a happy Purim,

**Menachem Schneerson**

## B’s”D. Purim, 5711*

#### 283

**“The Jews undertook what they had already begun...”** The Rebbe raises a difficulty: it is wondrous that they undertook it at that time, during the exile, and especially during the time of Haman when the decree was hanging over them—that specifically then they fulfilled what they had already begun. He explains that this was because they were in a state of *mesiras nefesh* throughout that entire year. Now, as to why it was necessary to have *avodah* of *mesiras nefesh* specifically to fulfill “what they had already begun,” we must first explain the concept of “what they had already begun,” which refers to the time of *Matan Torah*. As is known, the innovation of *Matan Torah* was the giving of *Torah u’mitzvos* specifically in physicality—that is, to nullify the decree that “the heavenly beings shall not descend [to the lower realms, and the lower beings shall not ascend to the heavenly realms].” Therefore, they were given to souls within bodies, specifically in their union together. Furthermore, in *Torah u’mitzvos* there must be a union of the physical aspect within them and the spirituality—meaning, that one makes it a *mitzvah*—and this is only possible after the refinement [that occurs] in exile.

Therefore, there are several modes in the fulfillment of *Torah u’mitzvos*. The primary ones are: 1) Performing *Torah u’mitzvos* as a “commandment of men learned by rote,” without *chayus*, or not *lishmah*—for the sake of being called “Rabbi,” and the like—which lacks *chayus*. Or [performing them] out of fear of Hashem, which is not *chayus* but, on the contrary, a form of *tzimtzum* and constriction. 2) Performing the above out of *ahavas Havayah* with great *chayus*, which stems from the soul as it expands and gains strength. This category includes *avodah* that is a matter of nature, or a habit that has become nature, or *avodah* that is according to *taam v’daas*. There is also [a level] higher than *taam v’daas*, where one is not an independent existence, but simply desires to fulfill the will of the Creator.

Now, similar to these distinctions, there are also [levels] within the Torah itself. [There is] Torah [studied] in order to know the practical law, which is indeed the ultimate purpose; consequently, this involves limitations—the laws of each holiday, and the like—and specifically [the study of] “four [cubits] of *halacha*.” [Then there is] the study of Torah for its own sake, where one is “constantly intoxicated by her love” due to her *maalah* in and of itself, at the very least according to *taam v’daas*. And higher than all the above is *lishmah* in truth—for the sake of the Torah itself—meaning, above *taam v’daas*, where one also connects the Torah, which “emanates from *Chochmah*,” to its source in *Keter*. And through what can this be achieved? Also through demonstrating within oneself that one is in a state of *mesiras nefesh*. And there must always be a connection of the Torah to its source, for seemingly it could be said...

## Purim 5711

#### 284

**"The Jews accepted"** — and my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, explains in his *maamar* on this subject (which has now been published) that they accepted what they had begun at the time of the Giving of the Torah. For what they said, "We will do and we will hear," was only a beginning ("they began to do"), whereas in the days of Achashverosh (at the time of Haman’s decree) the actual acceptance took place, "the Jews accepted". He highlights that this is seemingly a wonder : at the Giving of the Torah, the Jewish people were at the pinnacle of elevation—both physically, as they were in a most exalted state regarding their freedom, and spiritually, as they experienced a revelation of Elokus at the highest possible level. Conversely, in the days of Achashverosh, the Jewish people were at the nadir of descent. In addition to the concealment and hiding present in every exile, where "darkness covers the earth" through a multitude of *tzimtzumim*, concealments, and hidden states, at that time (during Haman’s decree) the concealment and hiding were even greater. Furthermore, physically they were

#### 285

in a state of utter degradation, for the decree was "to destroy, to kill, and to annihilate, G-d forbid, all the Jews, young and old, infants and women, in one day". Yet, at the time of the Giving of the Torah, when the Jewish people were at the pinnacle of elevation, there was only the beginning ("they began to do"), while at the time of Haman’s decree, when they were at the nadir of degradation, that was precisely when they accepted what they had begun at the Giving of the Torah. He explains that at the time of the decree, their observance of *Torah* and *mitzvos* was with *mesiras nefesh*. [It should be noted that in *Torah Or* it is explained that their *mesiras nefesh* was such that if they had converted, G-d forbid, nothing would have been done to them, as the decree was only against the Jews; yet, the thought of apostasy never entered their minds, G-d forbid. He explains that their *mesiras nefesh* was (not only not to deny their faith, G-d forbid, but) for the observance of *Torah* and *mitzvos*, to the point that they gathered congregations in public to study Torah with *mesiras nefesh*.] The arousal of their *mesiras nefesh* came through Mordechai the Jew, the Moshe of his generation, who gathered congregations in public to strengthen their faith. The essence of Mordechai’s *avodah* was teaching Torah to the children of the *beis medrash*, who are the foundation of all of Israel [as explained at length in the *maamar* regarding the greatness of the breath of the children of the *beis medrash*]. As it is stated in the *Midrash*, Mordechai the Jew gathered 22,000 students and taught them Torah with *mesiras nefesh*, to the point that when Haman the Wicked came and Mordechai said to them, "Flee, so you are not burned by my coals," they replied, "We are with you, whether for life or for death," accepting upon themselves every punishment, provided only that they would not be separated from the Torah. This is the meaning of "The Jews accepted what they began to do": at the Giving of the Torah there was only the beginning, and at the time of Haman’s decree there was the acceptance, because by having

#### 286

at that time *mesiras nefesh* in actual practice for *Torah* and *mitzvos*, they were elevated (in a certain sense) to a level higher than they had been at the time of the Giving of the Torah. Therefore, it was specifically then that the acceptance occurred, "the Jews accepted."

2) **It is necessary** to understand: the core explanation in the *maamar* is that the reason the acceptance occurred specifically during the time of the decree was due to their *mesiras nefesh*. What relevance is there to the fact that the arousal of their *mesiras nefesh* was through Mordechai, and that the essence of Mordechai’s *avodah* was teaching Torah to the children of the *beis medrash*? Furthermore, explanation is needed regarding the precision (at the beginning of the *maamar*) that the fact that at the time of the Giving of the Torah the Jews were at the pinnacle of elevation, and at the time of the decree they were at the nadir of degradation, applies both spiritually and physically. Seemingly, according to the precision of the *maamar*, regarding how it is possible that at the time they were at the pinnacle of elevation there was only the beginning, and at the time they were at the nadir of degradation there was the acceptance, the elevation and degradation in their spiritual state are what matter. Why does the *maamar* bring that the elevation at the time of the Giving of the Torah and the degradation at the time of the decree were also physical?

3) **Now,** in addition to the aforementioned points, one must also understand the content of the explanation (in the *maamar*) that the reason "the Jews accepted" occurred at the time of the decree is because they then had *mesiras nefesh* for *Torah* and *mitzvos*. Seemingly, for the vast majority of *mitzvos*, it is written, "which a man shall do and live by them." Even regarding the three *mitzvos* for which it is said "be killed and do not transgress", this is not a matter of *mesiras nefesh* per se, but rather that the mode of their fulfillment is such that one must fulfill them even if he is killed as a result. The *mitzvah* of *mesiras nefesh* for *Kiddush Hashem* is only one *mitzvah*. What is the necessity for *mesiras nefesh* for the acceptance ("the Jews accepted") of the Torah as a whole? And what is written in *Tanya* —that the reason Moshe Rabbeinu commanded the generation entering the Land to recite the *Shema* twice daily to accept upon themselves the Kingdom of Heaven with *mesiras nefesh* (even though he promised them, "Hashem will place your fear and dread") is because the fulfillment of *Torah* and its *mitzvos* depends on remembering the concept of one's *mesiras nefesh* to Hashem—this *mesiras nefesh* upon which the fulfillment of *Torah* and *mitzvos* depends is *mesiras nefesh* in potential (that if he needs to have *mesiras nefesh* for the fulfillment of *Torah* and *mitzvos*, he is prepared for it), not *mesiras nefesh* in actual practice. And surely, even at the Giving of the Torah, when they said "We will do and we will hear" (and certainly after they were commanded to recite the *Shema* twice daily), they accepted upon themselves to fulfill everything

#### 287

they would be commanded, even if it required *mesiras nefesh*. Yet, it was not a complete acceptance ("the Jews accepted") until the time of Haman’s decree, when they had *mesiras nefesh* in actual practice.

**It is known** that there were two times when there was *mesiras nefesh* in actual practice [of the entire Jewish people] for *Torah* and *mitzvos*: Chanukah (at the time of the Greek decree) and Purim (at the time of Haman’s decree). Since all matters in the Torah are with the utmost precision, it must be said that the fact that the matter of "the Jews accepted" occurred specifically through the *mesiras nefesh* of Purim is (not only because the *mesiras nefesh* of Purim preceded the *mesiras nefesh* of Chanukah, but also) because the *mesiras nefesh* of Purim is more relevant to the (completion of the) acceptance of the Torah. One must understand the difference between the *mesiras nefesh* of Chanukah and the *mesiras nefesh* of Purim, because of which the completion of the acceptance of the Torah is specifically through the *mesiras nefesh* of Purim.

4) **This will be understood** by prefacing the well-known concept that the innovation of the Giving of the Torah regarding the *mitzvos* that existed before the Giving of the Torah is that the *mitzvos* of the Patriarchs (and in general—before the Giving of the Torah) were only in the spiritual realm. In addition to the fact that many *mitzvos* were fulfilled only spiritually (such as *tefillin*, which mentions the Exodus from Egypt, and at that time the Egyptian exile had not yet occurred), even regarding the *mitzvos* they fulfilled physically, the drawing down of holiness was only in the spiritual realm and not in the physical object with which they fulfilled the *mitzvah*. For before the Giving of the Torah, there was the decree that "the higher realms shall not descend below, and the lower realms shall not ascend above". Therefore, there was no connection between the holiness of the *mitzvah* (the higher realms) and the physical object with which the *mitzvah* is performed (the lower realms). This is not the case with the fulfillment of *mitzvos* after the Giving of the Torah, when the

#### 288

decree and the partition between the higher and lower realms were nullified; the connection between the physical object (with which one fulfills the *mitzvah*) and the holiness of the *mitzvah* was created, to the point that in many *mitzvos*, the physical object becomes the *cheftza* (the essential object) of the *mitzvah*. And according to the known concept that the connection of two opposites is through something that transcends both, it is understood that the connection of higher and lower realms created at the Giving of the Torah is because at the Giving of the Torah there was the drawing down of the *Ohr Ein Sof* which transcends the definition of "above" and "below" (higher and lower realms). From all this it is understood that in the *mitzvos* after the Giving of the Torah, there are three aspects: the lower [for even after the Giving of the Torah, the physical object with which one fulfills the *mitzvah* does not turn into something spiritual; it remains a physical object], the higher [for even after the Giving of the Torah, when the holiness of the *mitzvah* is drawn down and established in the physical object, it is a spiritual matter], and the nullification of the definitions of the higher and lower, for the fact that the higher and lower connect with each other (despite being opposites) is through the nullification of their definition, which is accomplished by the drawing down of the *Ohr Ein Sof* that transcends both. It can be said that these three aspects have their counterparts in the fulfillment of *mitzvos*. When a person fulfills the *mitzvos* by way of "rote performance", meaning because of the habit he has become accustomed to —since habit becomes nature —his fulfillment of *mitzvos* is from the nature of the body and the animal soul, the "lower" within man. When he fulfills the *mitzvos* because he loves Hashem and desires to cleave to Him, and it is impossible to truly cleave to Him except through the fulfillment of the 248 *mitzvah* precepts, which are the 248 limbs of the King, his fulfillment of *mitzvos* is from the side of the *neshamah* (the Divine soul), the "higher" within man. And when he fulfills the *mitzvos* for their own sake—not because of the benefit he will derive from it (not even spiritual benefit), but because the *mitzvos* are His will—his fulfillment of *mitzvos* is not from the side of his own existence (not even the existence of the *neshamah*), but in *bitul*, where his entire being (at the time he fulfills the *mitzvah*) is only to fulfill the higher will.

5) **It should be added** that the root of these three modes of fulfilling *mitzvos* is that even in the *mitzvos* themselves there are three aspects (corresponding to the three modes of fulfilling

#### 289

the *mitzvos*). The matter is that the giving of the *mitzvos* (below) is as the Sages said : "The *mitzvos* were given only to refine the creatures." This means that the intent in giving the *mitzvos* is (not for the *mitzvos* themselves, but) for the refinement and purification of the powers and limbs of the person who fulfills the *mitzvah*, and for the refinement and purification of the things in the world with which one fulfills the *mitzvah*. There is a higher aspect in the *mitzvos*: they are the *mitzvos* of the Holy One, Blessed be He, as the Sages expound on the verse, "He declares His words to Yaakov, His statutes and judgments to Yisrael": what He does, He tells Yisrael to do. The fact that the Holy One, Blessed be He, fulfills the *mitzvos* (*before* He tells Yisrael to do them) is from His own perspective (from the perspective of "above"). [This is also understood from the fact that the 248 precepts are the 248 limbs of the King ; the fact that the *mitzvos* are His limbs, as it were, is from the perspective of "above"]. Through Yisrael doing the *mitzvos* that He does, they walk in the ways of the Holy One, Blessed be He, and are attached to Him. Through this, vitality is drawn down to the person who fulfills the *mitzvos*, as it is written, "which a man shall do and live by them," because by doing the *mitzvos* he attaches himself to the Holy One, Blessed be He (as mentioned above), and through "you who cleave to Hashem your G-d, you are all alive today". Since this aspect of the *mitzvos* (that they are the ways of the Holy One, Blessed be He, through His doing them) transcends any relationship to the worlds, therefore, the vitality drawn down to the person who fulfills the *mitzvos* is the vitality of the level of *sovev* (encompassing), which in itself is holy and separate from the worlds, yet through the fulfillment of the *mitzvos* he lives by them with internal vitality. However, even this aspect

#### 290

of the *mitzvos* is at a level that has a configuration. Therefore, the *mitzvos* at this level are in a state of division—"the ways of Hashem" (plural), the 248 limbs of the King—for the drawing down through each *mitzvah* is a specific drawing down (like the power of sight in the eye and the power of hearing in the ear). Therefore, it is possible for man to do the *mitzvos* that the Holy One, Blessed be He, does, for the 248 limbs in the lower man are, as it were, a counterpart to the 248 limbs of the King: "Let us make man in our image, after our likeness". There is a higher aspect in the *mitzvos*: that the *mitzvos* are the higher will (a will that transcends reason), for the will in the *mitzvos* is equal in all 613 *mitzvos* (transcending the 248 limbs). Since the will in the *mitzvos* is incomparably higher than the lower man who fulfills the *mitzvah* (a fortiori, it is higher than the configuration of the higher man), therefore, regarding this level (as it is in itself), man does not occupy space; the *bitul* of the absence of occupying space is *bitul* in essence. Even after there is the command to man, through which he becomes an existence, his entire existence is only to fulfill the command, and by fulfilling the command he connects (*mitzvah* comes from the word *tzavta*—connection) with the Commander (who is incomparably higher than him).

6) **Similarly** regarding Torah study, there are these three modes. In addition to the three modes that exist in the *mitzvah* of Torah study (as in all *mitzvos*), there are also (corresponding to) these three modes in the matter of Torah study itself. When one studies Torah from the perspective of the wisdom and intellect within it—for the Torah is "your wisdom and understanding (even) in the eyes of the nations" —his Torah study is from the perspective of the nature of his body and animal soul, for by nature he loves intellectual pursuits. When his Torah study is from the perspective that the Torah is the intermediary connecting Yisrael and the Holy One, Blessed be He, as the *Zohar* says : "Three bonds are bound

#### 291

one to the other: Yisrael, the Torah, and the Holy One, Blessed be He," for through Yisrael being bound to the Torah, they are bound to the Holy One, Blessed be He—his Torah study is from the perspective of the *neshamah* within him. That is, even this mode of Torah study is from the perspective of his existence (that he should be connected to the Holy One, Blessed be He), but it is the existence of the *neshamah*. There is a higher mode of Torah study: that he studies Torah (not because of the elevation he will derive from it, but) from the perspective of the Torah itself. Since the Torah and the Holy One, Blessed be He, are one, and even more so, that it is one with the Essence—as the Sages said that *Anochi* (I) is an acronym for *Ana nafshi kesvis yehavis* (I have written and given My soul)—for *Ana* (my soul) is His Essence, and the meaning of *Ana nafshi kesvis yehavis* is that He wrote and gave Himself, *Ana nafshi*, for through the Torah "you take Me". Therefore, just as the Holy One, Blessed be He, is not, G-d forbid, a means to some other end, and the "ultimate purpose" is in Him Himself, similarly it is in the Torah study of man, where he feels that the purpose of his Torah study is the Torah itself. The fact that he knows that the Torah and the Holy One, Blessed be He, are one, acts upon him so that he gives and devotes himself to Torah study without any calculations (not even the calculation that through this he will be connected to the Holy One, Blessed be He), and his Torah study is in a state of absolute *bitul*. These three modes in Torah study are drawn down from the three aspects of the Torah itself: that the Torah is wisdom and intellect (meaning it is the wisdom of the Holy One, Blessed be He, and then it descended and was clothed in human intellect), that the Torah is the intermediary connecting Yisrael to the Holy One, Blessed be He, and that the Torah and the Holy One, Blessed be He, are one.

7) **Now,** these three aforementioned matters have their counterparts in the laws and rulings of Torah study. The obligation to study the laws necessary for practice in order to know the action one must perform is *similar* to Torah study from the perspective of the (nature of the) body and animal soul, since the fulfillment of *mitzvos* (including *mitzvos* related to speech) is through the body and the vital soul. The obligation of the *mitzvah* of knowing the Torah—to know the entire Torah

#### 292

(even matters not needed for practice)—since the essence of this *mitzvah* is that *man* should know the Torah, is similar to Torah study for the sake of the *neshamah*. It can be said that this is the reason why there is a measure and limit to the *mitzvah* of knowing the Torah [for what is said, "It is longer than the earth in measure," means there is no end to the depth of the reasons for the laws, but the laws themselves, as well as the *Midrashim*, etc., have an end and a number, and there were many who studied and knew the entire Torah], because since the *mitzvah* of knowing the Torah is that *man* should know the Torah, and man is limited, therefore the Torah (that relates to this *mitzvah*) is also in a state of measure and limitation. The obligation of "you shall meditate in it day and night" [even after one has studied the entire Torah, and similarly regarding those whose knowledge is limited and will not reach the knowledge of the entire Torah] is the obligation of Torah study from the perspective of the Torah itself. Since the Torah (as it is in itself) is above measure and limitation ("longer than the earth in measure"), therefore, the *mitzvah* of Torah study (as it is from the perspective of the Torah itself) is that one should engage in it constantly, day and night, at every free moment, above measure and limitation.

8) **It can be said** more deeply that even the *mitzvah* of "you shall meditate in it day and night," since the *mitzvos* are commands to man [and unlike the Torah as it is the wisdom of the Holy One, Blessed be He (which transcends relationship to the world) and only later descended below], the Torah one studies from the perspective of the *mitzvah* of "you shall meditate in it day and night" is (not the Torah as it is from the perspective of itself, but) as it relates to man. The true essence of Torah study itself (as it is above relationship to man) is in studying Torah *lishmah* (for its own sake), where the study is not in order to fulfill the *mitzvah* of Torah study, but from the perspective of the Torah itself.

**It should be added** that the superiority of studying Torah *lishmah* over studying in order to fulfill the *mitzvah* of Torah study is not only in the intent of the study but also in the study in practice.

#### 293

For when the study is in order to fulfill the *mitzvah* of Torah study, the study is limited, for even in the *mitzvah* of "you shall meditate in it day and night" there are various limitations, as explained in the laws of Torah study. This is not the case in studying Torah *lishmah*; he does not take into account measures and limitations (whether in such a manner he is obligated to study or not), and his study is above the measure and limitation of time, and similarly above the measure and limitation of place, as the Sages said, "If he is forced, it is different." The reason for this (in the inner dimension of things) is that the *mitzvah* of "you shall meditate" is a command to man; therefore, it has limitations (according to man). This is not the case in studying Torah *lishmah*, for since the Torah (as it is from the perspective of itself) is above measure and limitation ("longer than the earth in measure"), therefore, even the Torah study of man, when his study is *lishmah* (from the perspective of the Torah itself), is in a manner that he exits the limitations of time and place.

9) **It can be said** that the connection of higher and lower realms that was innovated at the Giving of the Torah is revealed primarily in Torah study *lishmah*. In addition to the fact that for the connection of higher and lower realms to be possible, it must be through the nullification of the definition of higher and lower by the drawing down of the *Ohr Ein Sof* that transcends both (as mentioned in section 4), which has its counterpart in man when he engages in Torah *lishmah*—where he is in a state of nullification of existence, both regarding the body (lower) and regarding the *neshamah* (higher)—the connection of higher and lower realms itself is revealed in this study, for the *Bli Gvul* (Infinity) of the Torah (higher realms) acts upon man (lower realms) so that his Torah study is above limitation. It should be added that through the *Bli Gvul* of the Torah acting also upon man (and similarly through the descent of the Torah below in general), the *Bli Gvul* of the Torah is revealed even more. The fact that the Torah is *Bli Gvul* is not only in the place and level of the Torah, but it is drawn down also below, and even in its descent below, the *Bli Gvul* within it is felt in revelation, such that even the Torah study of man is in a manner of *Bli Gvul*.

#### 294

10) **Based on all the above,** one can say the reason why the completion of the acceptance of the Torah ("the Jews accepted") depends on *mesiras nefesh* is because the connection of higher and lower realms is through the nullification of the definitions and the existence of higher and lower (as mentioned above). Therefore, for there to be the perfection of the acceptance of the Torah, the nullification of *mesiras nefesh* was necessary. And although even at the time of the Giving of the Torah, when they said "We will do and we will hear," they accepted upon themselves to do everything they would be commanded, even if it required *mesiras nefesh*, as long as the *mesiras nefesh* is in potential, it is from the perspective of the *neshamah* and not in the body. Since the nullification (through which the connection of higher and lower realms is created) must be both in the higher and in the lower, therefore the perfection of the acceptance of the Torah depends on *mesiras nefesh* in actual practice, for *mesiras nefesh* in actual practice is in the body and the animal soul.

**Based on this,** one can also understand the superiority of the *mesiras nefesh* of Purim over the *mesiras nefesh* of Chanukah. For even *mesiras nefesh* in actual practice is primarily from the perspective of the *neshamah*, but the *mesiras nefesh* of the *neshamah* acts also upon the body and the animal soul. Since the body and the animal soul (by their very nature) are an existence, the revelation of the Giving of the Torah (the connection of higher and lower realms) that is drawn down into them through the nullification of *mesiras nefesh* that is from the *neshamah* is an additional matter for them. This is the superiority of the *mesiras nefesh* of Purim over the *mesiras nefesh* of Chanukah: on Purim they were in a state of absolute nullification (and degradation) also from the perspective of the body, for they were completely "ownerless" to be killed by anyone who wished, and by the way of nature there was no way to be saved from this. [And although the decree was only against the Jews, and if they had converted, G-d forbid, nothing would have been done to them (as mentioned above in section 1 from *Torah Or*), nevertheless, since the decree then was not against the observance of *Torah* and *mitzvos* but against the body, to kill and annihilate, G-d forbid, it follows that their bodies were then at the nadir of degradation. For when the decree is against *Torah* and *mitzvos* (as in Chanukah, where the decree was "to make them forget Your Torah and pass them over from the statutes of Your will"), such that if he fulfills *Torah* and *mitzvos* they will kill him, then the body (by *its nature*) is not "ownerless." This is not the case when the decree is to kill and annihilate, G-d forbid, but he has the possibility to be saved from the decree by converting, G-d forbid. Since the decree to kill him is (not because he does not want to convert, but) against the body, it follows that the body (by *its nature*) is like "ownerless"].

#### 295

**This is why** it was specifically through the *mesiras nefesh* of Purim that there was the completion and perfection of the acceptance of the Torah, because through their nullification then being also from the perspective of the body, they were vessels for the revelation of the Giving of the Torah, both from the perspective of the *neshamah* and from the perspective of the body. It can be said that this is also what is meant in the *maamar* that at the time of the decree the Jewish people were at the nadir of degradation also physically, for this hints at the reason why they were then vessels for the revelation of the Giving of the Torah also from the perspective of the body.

11) **Now,** based on what was explained above (section 4) that in the connection of higher and lower there are three aspects—the higher, the lower, and their nullification—it is understood that in order to merit the completion and perfection of the acceptance of the Torah, the nullification of the *neshamah* and the body is not enough; there must also be their existence, as they are in their ultimate perfection, and their existence must be connected and joined with the Torah. This is similar to what was explained above (sections 6 and 8) that the superiority of studying Torah *lishmah* is not only in the matter of nullification (that his study is not for his own perfection, nor for the perfection of the *neshamah*) but also that the existence of the person studying (the *neshamah* and the body) connects with the Torah, through which he exits his limitations and is elevated to the *Bli Gvul* of the Torah. It can be said that this is why the *maamar* brings that the arousal of the *mesiras nefesh* of Yisrael was through Mordechai, the Moshe of his generation, for the Torah study of Mordechai was at the pinnacle of elevation, and by arousing Yisrael to study Torah with *mesiras nefesh* [especially since Mordechai was the head of the generation (similar to Moshe) from whom it is drawn down to all the limbs], he drew down into them (not only the matter of nullification, but) also the elevation of Torah study as it is from the perspective of the perfection of man—the perfection of the *neshamah* and the body.

**Based on this,** one can also explain what the *maamar* brings—that Mordechai gathered 22,000 children of the *beis medrash*—because this superiority in Torah study (which is from the perspective of the perfection of the *neshamah* and the body) is primarily in the children of the *beis medrash*. This will be understood based on what the Sages said : "The world exists only for the breath of the children of the *beis medrash*." Rav Papa said to Abaye, "What about mine and yours?" He replied, "The breath that has sin is not comparable to the breath that has no sin." Even though the Torah study of Rav Papa and Abaye was

#### 296

(certainly) *lishmah* at the highest levels, and the Torah study of the children of the *beis medrash* is from the fear of the rod, nevertheless, there is an advantage in the breath of the children of the *beis medrash*, for it is specifically upon this breath that the world exists. The explanation for this is known : the advantage in the breath of the children of the *beis medrash* is both from the perspective of their *neshamah*, which is closer to Elokus because it has recently come from the spiritual world, and from the perspective of their body, which has not been as coarsened by *avodah zarah* and desires, as explained at length elsewhere. Based on this, it can be said that the fact that the *maamar* brings that at the time of the decree Mordechai gathered 22,000 children of the *beis medrash* is to explain that in the Torah study that occurred then, there was (not only the nullification of the *neshamah* and the body, but) also the perfection of the *neshamah* and the body. [However, the superiority of the *neshamah* of the children of the *beis medrash* is not (so much) related to their Torah study, since their study is because of the fear of the rod (the nature of the body) and not from the perspective of the *neshamah*, and there is also no nullification of *mesiras nefesh* in it. Therefore, the *maamar* brings that the study of the children of the *beis medrash* was through Mordechai, through which their Torah study was also with *mesiras nefesh*, as explained in the *maamar*]. It should be added that by Mordechai gathering 22,000 children of the *beis medrash*, the elevation of the breath of the children of the *beis medrash* was added to him, and through this he drew down this matter also into all the Jews of his generation.

12) **Based on this,** one can also explain why "a person is obligated to become intoxicated on Purim until he does not know", for in the days of Purim every year, the matter of "the Jews accepted" returns and is awakened as it was the first time, and on the contrary—in a manner of "increasing in holiness". [It should be added that the innovation in the days of Purim regarding the Giving of the Torah is in two matters: that in the days of Purim there was the completion and perfection of the

## Sicha of the Festival of Purim, 5711

#### 298

**A.** Regarding the text of the prayer on Rosh Hashanah and Yom Kippur, the Zohar[1] states: "Three times *Uv'chein* (And so), *Uv'chein*, *Uv'chein*." However, according to our custom, we say "Uv'chein" *four* times[2].

This can be explained based on the well-known concept[3] that the fourth "Uv'chein" corresponds to the "Uv'chein" mentioned in the Megillah of Esther[4] — "And so (*Uv'chein*) I will go to the king, which is *not according to the law* (not according to the custom/halacha)[5]." Because it is "not according to the law," it was not initially established in the text of the prayer...

The matter is as follows[6]:

The standard order is that one should not approach the king in the inner courtyard... as it is written: "All the king’s servants... know that whoever, man or woman, comes to the king into the inner courtyard who is not called, there is one law for him..."[7].

However, during the days of Purim, the power is granted to all Bnei Yisrael, each according to his level, that when they proceed with strength... and do not take into account that entering the inner courtyard is "not according to the law,"

— For, knowing that in the inner courtyard is King Achashverosh, "This is the Holy One, blessed be He, whose end and beginning are one"[8], what difference does it make to him ("*Vos iz im di nefka mina*...") whether this conduct is "according to the law" or "not according to the law"... since he knows that through this he will meet ("*er vet zich tsuzamenkumen*") with the Holy One, blessed be He, "whose end and beginning are one" —

Then, He also treats him from Above "not according to the law" — *He brings him* to the king into the inner courtyard, and not only that, but He gives him the "top of the scepter"[9],

#### 299

And afterwards, He gives him the entire scepter, as the details of this matter are explained in the discourses of Purim[10].

**B.** And the power of the days of Purim extends also over the entire year:

The essence of Purim is the completion and perfection of the Giving of the Torah, as it is written[11]: "The Jews confirmed and accepted," "They confirmed what they had already accepted"[12] (at the Giving of the Torah), and it is written[13]: "And the Jews accepted what they had begun to do," meaning that at the Giving of the Torah there was only the beginning ("begun") alone, and the completion and perfection of the acceptance was in the days of Purim[14].

And since the Giving of the Torah is a general matter that concerns the entire existence of Bnei Yisrael (whose existence is Torah and Mitzvos) for the whole year, then certainly the essence of Purim — the completion and perfection of the Giving of the Torah — is a general matter that concerns the entire existence of Bnei Yisrael for the whole year.

And regarding our subject:

From the days of Purim we learn a rule, that when one sees that there is no advice... "All the king’s servants... know" that one should not enter the inner courtyard... one should not be discouraged, but rather push oneself in there ("*shparn zich ahintsu*")!

And accordingly, the conduct for the entire year is determined — that when one sees that there is no other choice, then, "And so I will go to the king, which is not according to the law"...

**C.** The Maamar entitled "And the Jews accepted what they had begun to do"[15] — was edited by the Rebbe Shlita.

***

**D.** Continuing from what was discussed above (in the Maamar[16]) regarding the difference between the *mesiras nefesh* of Chanukah and the *mesiras nefesh* of Purim — one should add another point based on the *nigleh* (revealed) Torah

#### 300

(although I have not found it in the discourses of Chassidus, and therefore I did not want to mention it within the main text[17]).

By way of introduction:

Regarding the obligation of *mesiras nefesh* — "When a gentile stands and forces a Jew to transgress one of all the commandments stated in the Torah or he will kill him, he should transgress and not be killed... In what cases is this said? In other commandments, except for idolatry, forbidden sexual relations, and bloodshed; but these three transgressions, if he tells him to transgress one of them or he will be killed, he should be killed and not transgress"[18].

And "As the matter is said regarding coercion, so it is said regarding illness. How so? One who is ill and near death, and the doctors say that his cure is through something forbidden by the Torah, it is done, and one is cured through all prohibitions of the Torah in a place of danger, except for idolatry, forbidden sexual relations, and bloodshed, which even in a place of danger one is not cured through them"[19].

And nevertheless, there is a difference between them — "Anyone regarding whom it is said 'be killed and do not transgress' and he transgressed and was not killed... because he transgressed under coercion, he is not lashed"[20], whereas regarding illness, "if he transgressed and was cured, the court punishes him with the punishment appropriate for him"[19].

And one must understand the reason for the difference between them — for seemingly, a sick person who is in danger and transgressed and was cured through one of the three prohibitions, is *coerced*, and why do they punish him?

And similarly, we find also in another law — "A woman who was imprisoned by gentiles, if it was for money she is permitted to her husband, if it was for her life (i.e., under threat of death) she is forbidden to her husband"[21], and according to many opinions[22] she is forbidden even to her Jewish husband, since we fear that perhaps she consented to be violated in order to save herself from being killed. And seemingly[23], she consented to be violated so that she would not be killed — she is *coerced*, and a coerced woman is permitted to her Jewish husband?

The Tzemach Tzedek explains[24], "That the coercion of a Jew which makes it permitted is when he coerces her regarding the act of intercourse, unlike here, where he is not coercing her regarding the act of intercourse, but rather they are abandoning her for another reason because she is sentenced to death, and she herself consents in order to save herself, this is not called coercion regarding the intercourse, since the act does not come through coercion at all but rather through will."

And this is also the reason for the difference between one who is told to transgress one of the three

#### 301

transgressions or be killed and he transgressed and was not killed, that he is not lashed, and one who is cured through one of them, that they punish him — that the one who is not lashed because he transgressed under coercion is only when the coercion is regarding the *transgression itself* (that they tell him to transgress or be killed), unlike one who is cured through one of them, since the coercion is not regarding the transgression itself (for the coercion is the danger of the illness), while the transgression itself *is done willingly* (in order to be saved from the danger of the illness), they punish him[25].

**E.** And similarly, one can say also regarding Chanukah and Purim:

On Chanukah[26] — since the decree was regarding the *commandments of the Torah*, that "they nullified their religion and did not allow them to engage in Torah and Mitzvos"[27], that they decreed against Shabbos and Bris Milah[28], "to make them forget Your Torah and to cause them to pass from the statutes of Your will"[29], therefore, even though they were obligated to sacrifice their lives and not transgress the commandments of the Torah [and not only regarding idolatry, forbidden sexual relations, and bloodshed, but also regarding all the commandments, for "at the time of the decree... one should be killed and not transgress even one of the other commandments"[30], and even regarding 'the strap of a sandal'[31]], nevertheless, if they had transgressed and were not killed, *they would not have been punished*, because they were *coerced* regarding the transgression itself.

Unlike Purim[26] — since the decree was (not regarding the commandments of the Torah, but rather) regarding the body, "to destroy, to kill, and to annihilate all the Jews"[32], but if they had converted their religion, G-d forbid, they would not have done anything to them[33], therefore, doing the transgression in order to be saved from the decree has the status of one who is cured through prohibitions of the Torah, and consequently, they would have been *punished* for this [and not only for idolatry, forbidden sexual relations, and bloodshed, but also for other transgressions through which one is cured in a place of danger, because, doing any transgression whatsoever in order to be saved from the decree of *Haman*, who "made himself an *idol*"[34], would be interpreted *as conversion*, G-d forbid], since the coercion is not regarding the act of the transgression itself, which he does willingly in order to save himself.

From this, the difference between the *mesiras nefesh* of Chanukah and the *mesiras nefesh* of Purim is understood — that the *mesiras nefesh* of Chanukah is in a state of measurement and limitation, for they could have transgressed and not been killed, and they would not have received punishment for this; whereas the *mesiras nefesh* of Purim is the truth

#### 302

and perfection of the matter of *mesiras nefesh*, without any limitations at all, that there is no possibility whatsoever to transgress the commandments of the Torah, G-d forbid, for if they had transgressed they would have been punished for it.

**F.** And the reason that the *mesiras nefesh* of Purim is in a manner where there is no possibility whatsoever to transgress the commandments of the Torah — is because on Purim the connection of Bnei Yisrael with the Holy One, blessed be He, His Torah, and His Mitzvos is revealed from the side of the *Essence*, and from the side of the Essence there is no place for an opposite matter:

By way of introduction — we find a difference between the heart and the other organs of the body, that all the organs of the body can tolerate waste [there are organs that can tolerate actual waste, and there are organs that can tolerate at least subtle waste], unlike the heart, which cannot tolerate waste at all[35]. And the reason for this — is because in the heart dwells and is revealed the *essence of vitality* (as is known[36] that the essence of the soul is connected (not so much with the brain, but) with the heart specifically), and in a place where the essence of vitality dwells and is revealed, there is no place for waste at all.

And similarly in spirituality — there are levels in holiness that are not connected with the Essence and therefore can tolerate also an opposite matter, unlike *the Essence*, where there is no place for an opposite matter.

An example of this is the difference between Chanukah and Purim:

On Chanukah — the connection of Bnei Yisrael with the Holy One, blessed be He, His Torah, and His Mitzvos is at such a level that it can tolerate an opposite matter, and therefore they would not have received punishment if they had transgressed the commandments of the Torah under coercion, meaning, that they would not have completely separated, G-d forbid, from His Oneness, may He be blessed; unlike on Purim — the connection of Bnei Yisrael with the *Essence and Being of the Ein Sof, blessed be He*, is revealed, such that there is no place at all for an opposite matter, regardless of whether it is willingly or under coercion, and therefore the decree was also in a manner that they would have received punishment if they had transgressed the commandments of the Torah even under coercion.

And it will be understood more clearly that on Purim the decree (and consequently also the *mesiras nefesh*) was regarding the body — for even the vitality of the body of a Jew is from Divinity, and it cannot receive vitality except from the *sitra d'kedusha* (side of holiness) alone[37], and therefore they would have received punishment if they had transgressed, G-d forbid, the commandments of the Torah even under coercion, because, even transgressions that are done

#### 303

under coercion are from the three completely impure *kelipos* (shells)[38], and consequently, it is impossible that they should have any connection to a Jew, whose entire vitality is only from the *sitra d'kedusha* alone.

**G.** Based on this, one can explain what the Rebbe Rayatz said in the Maamar published in the *Kuntres Purim*[39] that the completion and perfection of the acceptance of the Giving of the Torah was on Purim through the fact that they stood in *mesiras nefesh* in actual deed — that this matter was accomplished through the *mesiras nefesh* of Purim specifically and not through the *mesiras nefesh* of Chanukah:

At the Giving of the Torah it is written[40] "engraved (*charut*) on the tablets," and our Sages expounded[41] "Do not read *charut* (engraved) but *cheirus* (freedom)," "freedom from the Angel of Death"[42], in which is included also "freedom" from the Evil Inclination (for "he is the Evil Inclination, he is the Angel of Death"[43]) and from all matters that are the opposite of holiness, as our Sages said[44] that at the Giving of the Torah "their filth ceased" (similar to and in the likeness of the perfection of the time to come, that "the spirit of impurity I will remove from the earth"[45]).

And therefore, the completion and perfection of the acceptance of the Giving of the Torah through *mesiras nefesh* in actual deed is on Purim specifically — because on Purim the *mesiras nefesh* was in a manner where there is no possibility for a matter of sin at all, not only willingly, but also under coercion, which is a state and situation where there is no connection to a reality of filth at all (unlike on Chanukah, where they could have transgressed the commandments of the Torah due to coercion).

**H.** And one should add, that the virtue of the *mesiras nefesh* of Purim is expressed also in the obligation "to become intoxicated on Purim until one does not know"[46]:
