The content of the obligation of "until one does not know" is the exit from one's own reality[47], "to step out of oneself," and to conduct oneself in a manner that is above reason and intellect, above measurement and limitation.

— The truth is that even after the exit from his limitations he is still in measurement

#### 304

and limitation, but for him, at least, this is a movement that is above measurement and limitation, which is the matter of "with all your might (*me'odecha*)"[48], "your *me'od* (might)," which is connected with the true *Me'od* (without limit)[49].

**I.** And one should connect this with what was said above (section A) that on the days of Purim the conduct is in the manner of "I will go to the king, which is *not according to the law*":

Being in a movement that is above measurement and limitation, "until one does not know" — he does not take into account anything, "according to the law" or "not according to the law," and pushes himself "to go to the king into the inner courtyard," and he does not care what the results will be from the entry not according to the law (even though "all the king’s servants and the people of the king’s provinces know that whoever, man or woman, comes to the king into the inner courtyard who is not called, there is one law for him..."), as the verse continues[4]: "And as I perish, I perish."

— Such conduct (to push oneself to go to the king despite the risk involved, "as I perish, I perish") is *the opposite of intellect*, and seemingly, in such a case it is written[50] "The *folly* of man perverts his way, and his heart rages against Hashem," and as the Rebbe Maharash elaborates in the *Hemshech Mayim Rabim*[51] that a person's conduct of placing himself in danger in order to achieve wealth, etc., is "his folly," through which "he perverts his way," and afterwards "his heart rages against Hashem, why did it happen to him that he was harmed... or endangered at some time, and in truth the man himself caused it, etc." However, in this case, the Holy One, blessed be He, takes the "folly of man" (that he pushes himself to go to the king not according to the law) upon Himself, that through this "folly" blessing and great success will be drawn down to him.

And the explanation for this — is based on our Sages' statement "With the measure that a person measures, they measure to him"[52], "All the measures of the Holy One, blessed be He, are measure for measure"[53],

— For although the Holy One, blessed be He, is without limit, above measure, yet, being all-powerful, it is in His power and ability to connect the without-limit with limit and measure ("measure for measure"). And as is emphasized also in Torah and Mitzvos, that although they are without limit, as it is written[54] "Longer than the earth is its measure and wider than the sea," nevertheless, they were given in measure and limit and specific quantity[55], and were enclothed

#### 305

in physical things[56], which by themselves cannot tolerate the without-limit, for physicality and without-limit are two opposites —

And therefore, when a person pushes himself "to go to the king... not according to the law," they treat him from Above also in a manner of "not according to the law" — they do not make calculations whether he is worthy to go to the king into the inner courtyard or not, since he "pushed and entered"[57], and not only that, but they give him the golden scepter (and not only the "top of the scepter," but also the entire scepter), as mentioned above.

And based on what was said above (in the Maamar) that the matters of Purim extend and act also in physicality ("that also the physicality becomes something else"), as is emphasized in the obligation of feasting and joy with physical food and drink specifically — then the "pushed and entered" to go to the king into the inner courtyard "not according to the law," acts also regarding physical matters, to be blessed with living and enduring offspring, children, life, and ample sustenance.

[When distributing cups of drink among those seated for *L'chaim*, the Rebbe Shlita instructed that they bring larger cups, and said (with a smile):] Regarding *tzedakah* we find[58] that there is a virtue when one gives the same amount in many times, little by little ("*bislach-veiz*"), but regarding drink there is no need to give little by little.

[The Rebbe Shlita instructed to play a *nigun*, and when they played, he said that they should play with greater joy ("*freilicher*"), and he himself played with great joy, and gestured with his holy hand to increase the joy].

***

**J.** Regarding the names of the *Yomim Tovim* — there is a change between Purim and all other *Yomim Tovim*:

All *Yomim Tovim* are named after the miracle that occurred on that day or after the special *mitzvah* of that day: Pesach — after the miracle that "He passed over the houses of Bnei Yisrael in Egypt, etc."[59], or "Chag HaMatzos," after the *mitzvah* of eating *matzah*, "Seven days you shall eat *matzos*"[60]. Shavuos — after the *mitzvah* "Seven weeks you shall count for yourself"[61].

#### 306

Sukkos — after the *mitzvah* of *sukkah*, "In *sukkot* you shall dwell seven days"[62]. Chanukah — after the dedication (*chanukat*) of the Altar and the Temple[63], or after the resting (*chanu*) from the war, "They rested (*chanu*) on the twenty-fifth"[64]. And similarly regarding Rosh Hashanah — the beginning and head of the year[65], and Yom Kippur — "It is a day of atonement (*kippurim*) to atone for you"[66].

Unlike the *Yom Tov* of Purim — it is not named after the *mitzvah* of the day, "days of feasting and joy and sending portions one to another and gifts to the poor"[67], and also not after the miracle of the salvation from the decree of Haman, but on the contrary — "Therefore they called these days *Purim* after the name of the *Pur* (lot)"[68], "the *Pur*" ("which is the lot"[69]) that Haman cast "to destroy them and to annihilate them"[69], G-d forbid!

**K.** And one can say the explanation for this — by way of introduction:

It is written[70] "The beginning of nations is Amalek, and its end shall be destruction," and the Rebbe (Rashab) explains in the Maamar of Purim 5680 entitled *Zeh*[71],

— [On that Purim the Rebbe Rashab said two Maamarim: The first Maamar, entitled *And it was when Moshe raised his hand, etc.*, and the second Maamar, entitled *The beginning of nations is Amalek, etc.*] —

That "from what is written 'and its end shall be destruction,' it is implied that Amalek will not have any clarification and rectification at all, and only his destruction is his rectification, and one must ask, did our Sages not say[72] that from the descendants of Haman studied Torah in public, and it is known[73] that Haman was from the seed of Amalek, and there was clarification in him, etc.,"

And he explains, that "there is a difference here between 'in its time' (*be'itah*) and 'I will hasten it' (*achishenah*), for *be'itah* is that they are destroyed completely, and in *achishenah* then they have clarification, for our Sages said[74] 'if they merit, I will hasten it; if they do not merit, in its time,' and this is when the Jews merit in the matter of clarifications then

#### 307

*achishenah* that the end will be before the appointed time, and then there is added through this light in holiness... And this is 'The beginning of nations is Amalek, and its end shall be destruction,' for the end and conclusion of all the *Sitra Achra* in general and the *kelipah* of Amalek in particular is that they will be destroyed completely at the end of the time appointed for them, for 'He set an end to darkness'[75], etc., and when *achishenah* through the clarifications, there can be clarification also in the *kelipah* of Amalek... And this is also that from the descendants of Haman studied Torah in public, which is the matter of 'if they merit, I will hasten it' through the clarifications of the souls of Israel, that through this is made an advantage and addition of light in holiness, etc."

And he adds to explain, that in the manner of *achishenah* through the clarifications that there can be clarification also in the *kelipah* of Amalek, the meaning of "its end shall be destruction" is "until, but not including" (unlike in the manner of *be'itah*, that they are destroyed completely, where the meaning of "its end shall be destruction" is "until, and including").

And the matter is — that the ultimate perfection is (not only to push away the evil so that it will not confuse and interfere with the good, but more than this) to clarify and refine the evil and even to turn it into good, similar to the exposition of our Sages[76] on the verse[48] "And you shall love Hashem your G-d with all your heart," "with both your inclinations," meaning, that the Evil Inclination (not only will agree against his will, "an evil angel answers amen against his will"[77], but from will and joy) will be turned to love Hashem, which is the matter of "turning darkness into light and bitterness into sweetness"[78], through which is made an advantage and addition of light in holiness.

**L.** And the beginning of this is in the days of Purim:

Our Sages said[46] "A person is obligated[79] to become intoxicated on Purim until he does not know between 'cursed is Haman' and 'blessed is Mordechai'," and it is explained in Chassidus[80], that this is the matter of turning the "cursed is Haman" (matters of the *Sitra Achra*) into "blessed is Mordechai" (matters of holiness), as it is written[81] "And it was turned around," through which is made also the matter of "blessed is Mordechai" in a more elevated manner, since through the turning of the *Sitra Achra* ("cursed is Haman") is made an advantage and addition of light in holiness ("blessed is Mordechai").

But for this, one must reach a most elevated level that is above "cursed is Haman" and "blessed is Mordechai" together ("does not know between cursed is Haman and blessed is Mordechai"), through which one can *turn* the "cursed is Haman" into "blessed is Mordechai."

#### 308

**M.** And this matter is hinted at also in the name of the *Yom Tov* — Purim — which is called "after the name of the *Pur*":

Calling the name of the *Yom Tov* Purim after the name of the *Pur* that Haman cast to destroy them and to annihilate them, constitutes a verdict of Torah [for the name "Purim" is not a conventional name, but a name that is explained in one of the twenty-four holy books of the Tanach] — that even the most severe thing, such as a decree on Bnei Yisrael, which, "whoever touches them is as if he touches the apple of His eye"[82], can be turned and made into a *Yom Tov*!

And it will be understood more clearly based on what is explained in the Midrashim of our Sages[83] that Haman spoke slander about Bnei Yisrael that they have a multitude of *Yomim Tovim*, "Today is Shabbos, today is Pesach"[84], "The Holy One, blessed be He, said to him, 'Wicked one, you cast an evil eye on their festivals, I will cast you before them, and they will add one more festival for your downfall, this is the days of Purim'"[85] — that from the very fact that Haman wanted to nullify the *Yomim Tovim*, another *Yom Tov* was added.

— Some time after the redemption of the Rebbe Rayatz from his imprisonment in the year 5687, they took one of the Rabbis to prison, and among other things they said to him jokingly: Why do you complain about the imprisonment, for as a result of the imprisonment of the Rebbe of Lubavitch, a *Yom Tov* was made afterwards!...

**N.** And behold, it is known that every *Yom Tov* "does its work," that it continues and acts its special matter over the entire year. For example: Pesach — continues and acts over the entire year the matter of faith, Shavuos — the matter of Torah, and Sukkos — the continuation of the *Makifim* (encompassing lights). And from this it is understood also regarding the days of Purim — that they continue and act over the entire year the granting of strength for the turning of undesirable matters into holiness, "does not know between cursed is Haman and blessed is Mordechai."

And its matter in the *avodah* (service) of every day:

Everyone has matters that confuse — both spiritual matters, such as strange thoughts (in subtlety at least) and the like, and physical matters, regarding children, life, and ample sustenance, whose lack interferes with the peace of mind and peace of body required for the service of Hashem, and in the language of the Rambam[86]: "The health and wholeness of the body is from the ways of (the service of) Hashem, for it is impossible that he should understand or know anything of the knowledge of the Creator while he is ill, etc."

#### 309

And one must strive and act not only that these matters should not confuse him from the service of Hashem, but more than this, to turn the confusing matters themselves into holiness.

And for example:

It is explained in the Tanya[88] in the name of the *Tzava'at HaRivash*[89] that when one stands in prayer and there stands before him a gentile speaking and confusing him in his prayer, he must contemplate the matter of the descent and exile of the *Shechinah* that "a spark of its light is enclothed in a state of exile through the speech of this gentile who speaks words that confuse the service of Hashem, which is the intent of the prayer," and to know that the intent in this ("what is this that Hashem has done to him") is "so that he will strengthen and exert himself more in his prayer with the depth of the heart and with great intent, etc."

And similarly regarding all matters that confuse the service of Hashem — that one must know that "it was from Hashem," "and as it is written[90] 'For Hashem said to him (to Shimei) curse (David)... for if the spirit of His mouth, may He be blessed, had been removed for one moment from the spirit of Shimei, he could not have spoken anything'"[91], and since this is so, certainly the intent in this is for the good, that through this he will add strength and great exertion in the service of Hashem, and then, all the *kelipos* fall (which are only a superficial thing, like the shell that covers the fruit) and they are as if they were not, and there remains only holiness alone.

And through this, that one utilizes the confusing matters themselves so that through them will be added strength and courage in the service of Hashem, through this, that one reveals the Divine spark enclothed in them — one turns them into holiness.

**O.** And the strength for this is from the service of the days of Purim in the manner of "does not know" — which is the matter of the exit from one's own reality ("stepping out of oneself"):

When the *avodah* is in a manner of "*knows*" — then even one who reaches elevated levels, "even if he is a completely righteous person serving Hashem with fear and love in delights," he is "a thing unto himself, fearing Hashem and loving Him"[92], "there is one who loves"[93], and similarly "there is one who fears"[94] — *there is a reality*.

And therefore: (a) The confusing matters take up space for him, and he must search for advice and ways to fight with them, and not every time does he find in his soul the strengths required

#### 310

to fight with the confusing matters. (b) The war with the confusing matters is in the way of rejection, meaning, that the entirety of his *avodah* in the matter of clarifications is in a manner that right is right and left is left, and the matters that are from the side of the left must be rejected completely, and it is impossible to clarify them and elevate them to holiness (like the order of "in its time," that the *Sitra Achra* and the *kelipah* will be destroyed completely).

However, when the *avodah* is in a manner of "*does not know*," that he exits from his reality ("he goes out of himself"), and lifts himself from the earth ("he lifts himself up from the earth") a handbreadth or even a finger at least — then the confusing matters do not take up space at all,

[Similar to what is explained in the Maamar in the *Kuntres Purim*[95] that "when he is at the level of truth... we see tangibly that the other does not confuse him at all... the intent is not that he nullifies it, but that the other is literally as if he is not, meaning that there is no thing that confuses him... because it does not take up space and reality for him at all, and the reason for this is his elevation, that he has elevated himself to a higher place and level that is not related to the other... and consequently the other does not take up space and reality at all, and like for example the other of another city does not confuse him"],

And from this one takes strength also for the *avodah* in a manner of "knows,"

— as the Rebbe Rayatz said[96] in the name of our Rebbe the Alter Rebbe, that through the *avodah* of "does not know" on Purim, is made also the *avodah* of "knows" throughout the entire year in a completely different manner —

That there should be the ability (not only to reject and break the confusing matters, but on the contrary) to engage with the confusing matters in a manner of enclothement[97] in order to clarify them and refine them and turn them into holiness, so that through them is added elevation both in physicality and in spirituality (similar to the manner of *avodah* of "if they merit, I will hasten it," that the clarification is made also in the *kelipah* of Amalek, and through this is made an advantage and addition of light in holiness).

**P.** And the beginning of this is in the days of Purim — "A person is obligated *to become intoxicated* on Purim until he does not know."

And although generally one must be careful in such a case since there can be an

#### 311

undesirable result from this, and "a person is always liable... whether awake or asleep, etc."[98] — yet, in what cases is this said? When he does this *on his own opinion*, but, when he does this from the *command of the Torah*, the Torah takes the responsibility that the results from this will be only good, and good that is visible and revealed, both regarding the days of Purim themselves, and regarding their effect on the entire year[99].

And the main point — that through the elevation to the state and situation of "until one does not know between cursed is Haman and blessed is Mordechai," one turns the "cursed is Haman" into "blessed is Mordechai," from bitterness to sweetness and from darkness to light, and to place himself and the entire environment in a ray of light,

— It is written[100] "beaten for the light," and it is explained in the discourses of our Rebbes, the Nesi'im[101], the precision of the language "beaten *for the light*" specifically (and not for light or to illuminate), meaning, that the main emphasis is regarding the "source of light" ("there needs to be the contribution to the source of light"), but afterwards it continues in the verse[100] "to raise a lamp continually," which is the matter of light and revelation —

Until it is drawn down and comes in revelation in good that is visible and revealed, with children, life, and ample sustenance.

***

**Q.** Continuing from what was discussed above that the essence of Purim is "And it was turned around," to turn the "cursed is Haman" into "blessed is Mordechai," similar to that "from the descendants of Haman studied Torah in public" — one should bring an example from a matter that was revealed recently in external sciences, through which is answered a claim and question regarding the

## With the help of Hashem. Shabbos Parshas Shemini, Parshas Parah, Mevarchim HaChodesh Nissan, 5711

#### 328

(Unedited transcript)

**"Hashem spoke to Moshe and to Aharon, saying: This is the statute of the Torah which Hashem has commanded, saying: Take to you a red heifer..."**[1](#_ftn1850) It is necessary to understand[2](#_ftn1851) the reason for the double phrasing, "Hashem spoke... which Hashem has commanded." It should have said, "Hashem spoke... speak to the Children of Israel..." Furthermore, why is the name "Hashem" mentioned twice? Why not say, "Hashem spoke... which I have commanded," and the like?

Now, the Midrash[3](#_ftn1852) states that Shlomo said: "Regarding all these [the other mitzvos of the Torah], I have understood [their reasons]," but regarding the section of the red heifer, "I have investigated, asked, and searched; I said I would become wise, but it is far from me." [4](#_ftn1853) We must understand: there are other mitzvos in the Torah that fall into the category of *chukim* (statutes). How is the mitzvah of the red heifer different, such that Shlomo HaMelech understood the reasons for all the mitzvos, including the *chukim*, yet specifically regarding the red heifer he said, "it is far from me"?

Furthermore, the Midrash[5](#_ftn1854) states regarding the verse "Take to you," that the Ribono shel Olam said to Moshe: "To you I will reveal the reason for the heifer, but to others it remains a statute." This also requires explanation,[6](#_ftn1855) for it implies that there are others who know the reasons for the other *chukim* of the Torah—at the very least, unique individuals. If so, why is it that specifically the reason for the red heifer is unknown to them, and only revealed to Moshe?

b) **The matter is as follows:**[7](#_ftn1856) It is written,[8](#_ftn1857) "And the *chayos* (living beings) ran and returned." The simple interpretation is that this refers to the *Chayos HaKodesh* (the holy living beings), which are in a state of *ratzo* (running/advancing) and *shov* (returning). However, there is another interpretation:[9](#_ftn1858) it refers to the Divine light and vitality, which is in a state of *ratzo* and *shov*. Both interpretations are consistent, for the reason the *Chayos HaKodesh* are in a state of *ratzo* and *shov* is because the Divine vitality that brings the worlds into being and sustains them is itself in a state of *ratzo* and *shov*. This vitality exists in all worlds, from the highest of all levels to the lowest of all levels, including the angels, who are called *Chayos HaKodesh*. Since every agent performs its action according to its own nature, the Divine vitality that sustains them causes them to be in a state of *ratzo* and *shov*.

Even the lower created beings, which appear as independent entities, possess this element of *ratzo* and *shov*; this is the concept of the "beating of the heart." [10](#_ftn1859) However, there is a difference between the lower created beings and the *Chayos HaKodesh*. The *Chayos HaKodesh* (and all higher beings) feel the Divine vitality and, consequently, the *ratzo* and *shov* within it; thus, for them, *ratzo* and *shov* is revealed. In contrast, the lower created beings do not feel the Divine vitality, so the *ratzo* and *shov* remains hidden within them. That is to say, in matters not dependent on their choice, such as the heartbeat, they also possess the element of *ratzo* and *shov*, but in matters dependent on their *avodah*, they do not (openly) possess the element of *ratzo* and *shov*.

c) **The explanation of this matter:** It is known that the light and vitality that sustains worlds and created beings is only in the category of an *ha'arah* (illumination). As it is written,[11](#_ftn1860) "Your kingdom is a kingdom of all worlds." The concept of *Malchus* is merely an *ha'arah*, for "King" is a name applied to them,[12](#_ftn1861) and just as a name is merely an *ha'arah* that does not touch the essence at all, so too is the Divine vitality that sustains the worlds.

Now, this *ha'arah* that is drawn into the worlds, since it is only an *ha'arah*, necessarily has a root and source from which it is drawn. Being included in its source, it exists in a more elevated state; therefore, this *ha'arah* is in a state of *ratzo*—to ascend and be included in its root and source. After the *ratzo*, there is the element of *shov*, because the supreme intent is that there should be a revelation of light below, to illuminate the worlds; therefore, it is in a state of *shov*. Thus, the very cause that prompted the movement of *ratzo*—the feeling of its source—is what causes the *shov*, for the source desires that the light should illuminate below. The reason some created beings are not in a state of *ratzo* and *shov* is because they lack the feeling of their source and *dveikus* (cleaving) to the source.

The same applies to *neshamos*. Although it is known[13](#_ftn1862) that *neshamos* are "that which Elokus becomes a created being," they are still within the category of a "created being," and therefore they are not always in the movement of *ratzo* and *shov*. Furthermore, sometimes the *neshamos* are in the movement of *avodas Hashem*, and sometimes they are not. The reason for this is that, as stated above, the vitality is in a state of *ratzo* and *shov* because it is merely an *ha'arah*. This is only a cause for them to have *ratzo* and *shov*; in addition, there must also be a feeling of the source and *dveikus* to the source. Therefore, created beings that do not feel their source are not in a state of *ratzo* and *shov*.

This is why, within the *neshamah* itself, which is called by five names—*nefesh, ru'ach, neshamah, chayah, yechidah*—[14](#_ftn1863) the *chayah* and *yechidah* levels of the *neshamah*, which are "embraced and cleaved to You,"[15](#_ftn1864) are always in the movement of *ratzo* and *shov*. This is not the case for the *nefesh, ru'ach,* and *neshamah* levels, which are not always in a state of *ratzo* and *shov*, and for this reason, *avodah* and exertion are specifically required.

The same applies to *oros* (lights) and *keilim* (vessels). The *oros*, which are in a state of distinct *dveikus*, [16](#_ftn1865) are in a state of *ratzo* and *shov*. This is not the case for the *keilim*, which are not in a state of distinct *dveikus* to their source; by their own nature, they are not in a state of *ratzo* and *shov*, and only the light reveals in them that they should be in a state of *ratzo* and *shov*. Furthermore, the fact that the *keilim* by their own nature are not in a state of *ratzo* and *shov* is an additional cause for the *ratzo* and *shov* in the light. Since the *keilim* are not in a state of *ratzo* and *shov*, they are the opposite of the light. Therefore, the light is in a state of *ratzo*, and even when the light is drawn in a state of *shov* to be enclothed in the *keilim*, since it encounters something that is the opposite of itself, it cannot be in a state of true settlement (*hityashvus*), and even that settlement is only temporary.

Just as with body and soul: since they are two opposites, and their connection is only through the power of the "One who performs wonders,"[17](#_ftn1866) the vitality of the soul in the body is by way of *ratzo* and *shov*. Similarly, with *oros* and *keilim*: since the *keilim* are opposites of the *oros*, the drawing of the *oros* into the *keilim* is by way of *ratzo* and *shov*. And the *ratzo* and *shov* in the *oros* reveals in the *keilim* that they, too, should be in a state of *ratzo* and *shov*.

d) **With this we can understand** the concept of "This is the statute (*chukas*) of the Torah." *Chukah* is a term for a mode of conduct (*hanhagah*),[18](#_ftn1867) like "the statutes of heaven and earth,"[19](#_ftn1868) meaning that the conduct of the Torah is in a state of *ratzo* and *shov*.[20](#_ftn1869) As it is written,[21](#_ftn1870) "From His right hand, a fiery law (*esh das*) for them." The "right" is the aspect of *himshech* (drawing down), the aspect of *shov*, while *esh das* is the aspect of *ha'alah* (ascent)—like fire, whose nature is to ascend upward[22](#_ftn1871)—which is the aspect of *ratzo*.

From this, it is also drawn into the performance of *mitzvos*, for "study is great because it leads to action,"[23](#_ftn1872) so that the *mitzvos* themselves are in a state of *ratzo* and *shov*. This is the concept of positive *mitzvos* and negative *mitzvos*: positive *mitzvos*, which are by way of "arise and do," are the aspect of *shov*, while negative *mitzvos*, whose essence is "sit and do not do," are in the aspect of *ratzo*.

This is also true of the red heifer, whose essence is *ratzo* and *shov*.[24](#_ftn1873) The waters of purification contain both ash and living water; the ash, which is made through the burning of the heifer, is the essence of *ratzo*, and the living water is in the aspect of *shov*, for water descends from a high place to a low place.[25](#_ftn1874) The reason specifically the red heifer is called "the statute of the Torah" is because there is an advantage in the *ratzo* and *shov* of the red heifer over the *ratzo* and *shov* of other *mitzvos*. In other *mitzvos*, it is by way of detail—there are *mitzvos* that are in the aspect of *ratzo* and *mitzvos* that are in the aspect of *shov*. In contrast, the red heifer is one general mitzvah that contains both elements of *ratzo* and *shov*.

**However,** it is still not understood why we find regarding Moshe and Shlomo that they grasped the reasons for all other *mitzvos*, and only regarding the mitzvah of the red heifer did the Ribono shel Olam say to Moshe, "To you I will reveal the reason for the heifer," and Shlomo said, "I said I would become wise, but it is far from me." Seemingly, if the superiority of the red heifer is only like the superiority of the general over the particular, then when Shlomo grasped all the *mitzvos*—the particulars—why did he not grasp the general automatically? For "there is nothing in the general that is not in the particular." [26](#_ftn1875) Similarly, it is not understood why the Ribono shel Olam said to Moshe, "To you I will reveal the reason for the heifer, and not to others." Since others grasp all the particulars, what is the innovation in the general being revealed to Moshe? We must conclude that the *ratzo* and *shov* of the red heifer is in a more elevated manner than in all other *mitzvos*.

e) **The matter is as follows:**[27](#_ftn1876) As stated above, the cause of *ratzo* and *shov* is the feeling of its source. This has a limitation, for it depends on the manner of the feeling of the source and the elevation of the source. All of this applies even when the source is in a manner that has a connection to the "other"—this is the light of *Memalei Kol Almin* (filling all worlds). As is known, the totality of the light of *Memalei Kol Almin*, even in its most elevated levels, has a connection to the "other." This is because the drawing of the light of *Memalei Kol Almin* is through *Tzimtzum*, for the beginning of the revelation of the *Kav* (line) is through the first *Tzimtzum* [28](#_ftn1877)—which is the removal of the light—and afterwards the *Kav* is drawn by way of skipping. Even though the *Kav* touches and cleaves to the *Ohr Ein Sof*, it is specifically through the interruption of the *Tzimtzum*.[29](#_ftn1878) Therefore, the *Kav*, even though it is drawn from the *Ohr Ein Sof* that is before the *Tzimtzum*—which is that it returned and shone, etc.—is still in the category of a *Kav* that is limited according to the measure of the worlds, and it comes in a state of division between "above" and "below."

Since the light of *Memalei Kol Almin*, even in its root, gives place to the "other," the element of *ratzo* within it (its desire to be included in its source, or its desire that the source be revealed in the place of the light) is not a total nullification of existence, for even in its source there is the element of giving place to the "other." Similarly, the *shov* is in a manner of the settlement of the lights in the vessels, a true settlement.

However, the *ratzo* and *shov* that comes from the light of *Sovev Kol Almin* (surrounding all worlds) is in an entirely different manner. The light of *Sovev Kol Almin*, even though it is also drawn through the *Kav* (for all the *igulim* [circles] are drawn through the *Kav*), its root is from the *Ohr Ein Sof* that is before the *Tzimtzum*, from the great circle that is before the *Kav*, and the *Tzimtzum* does not affect them as much. Therefore, the *ratzo* is in a manner where it desires to be nullified from its existence entirely, for in its source there is no giving place to the "other" at all. And the *shov* is not a settlement of the lights in the vessels, but rather the nullification of the vessels to the lights.

The matter in human *avodah*: the *ratzo* that comes from the light of *Memalei Kol Almin* is that one desires Elokus and does not desire anything else besides Elokus, but this is in a manner where one is not nullified from one's existence; rather, "the closeness of Elokus is good for me,"[30](#_ftn1879) or even in the manner of "the closeness of Elokus is good in essence"—all of this is in a manner where one is not nullified from one's existence. Similarly, the *shov* is that the revelation of the light shines in him in a manner of settlement. In contrast, the *ratzo* and *shov* that comes from *Sovev Kol Almin*: the *ratzo* is in a manner where one is nullified from one's existence entirely, and the *shov* is not a settlement of the lights in the vessels (meaning that the vessel does not disturb the light because it absorbs the light), but rather the *shov* is the nullification of the vessels to the lights.

This is the concept of the *ratzo* and *shov* in the red heifer, which is higher than the *ratzo* and *shov* of all other *mitzvos*.[31](#_ftn1880) For the *ratzo* and *shov* of the red heifer is from the aspect of *Sovev Kol Almin*. Therefore, both movements of *ratzo* and *shov* are in the same matter of the ash of the heifer—the ash and the living water, both together. For the matter of purification is not accomplished by the ash alone, nor by the living water alone, but specifically by both together; this matter is specifically from the aspect of *Sovev Kol Almin*.

f) **This is** "Hashem spoke to Moshe and to Aharon, saying: This is the statute of the Torah which Hashem has commanded..." "Hashem spoke" refers to the aspect of *Havayah* below, the *Havayah* of the *Seder Hishtalshelus*, the aspect of *Memalei Kol Almin*, from where the speech to Moshe and Aharon comes. And what is said afterwards, "which Hashem has commanded," refers to the Name of *Havayah* above, the *Havayah* of *Atik*, which is above the *Seder Hishtalshelus*.[32](#_ftn1881), where there is no giving place to the existence of the "other" at all, and from there the matter of the red heifer is drawn.

Therefore, it is called by the name "statute of the Torah" (*chukas haTorah*), for *chukah* is from the term *chakikah* (engraving).[33](#_ftn1882) As is known, the difference between the letters of engraving and the letters of writing is that the letters of writing are essentially something foreign that is attached to the parchment, whereas the letters of engraving are not something foreign. This is because the red heifer is from the aspect of the *Havayah* of *Atik*, where there is no giving place to the "other" at all.

This is also what our Sages said in the Midrash:[34](#_ftn1883) "When Moshe reached the section of the impurity of the dead, Moshe said [to the Ribono shel Olam], 'Ribono shel Olam, if one becomes impure, how can he be purified?' He did not answer him. At that moment, Moshe's face turned pale. When he reached the section of the red heifer, the Ribono shel Olam said to him... 'This is its purification: take for the impure [person] from the ashes of the burnt sin-offering.'" The fact that Moshe's face turned pale is because in other impure things, there still remains within them Divine vitality.[35](#_ftn1884) In contrast, the impurity of the dead is the "father of fathers of impurity," and there is no vitality in it at all. Moshe wondered how it could be purified, because from the perspective of the *Seder Hishtalshelus*, it is impossible to purify such impurity. However, since the red heifer has its root in the aspect of the *Havayah* above, the aspect of the letters of engraving where there is no existence of the "other" at all, it has no limitations, and it can purify even the impurity of the dead. This is also what Shlomo said, "I said I would become wise, but it is far from me," because the red heifer has its root in the aspect of *Sovev Kol Almin*, the letters of engraving.

**Its meaning in human *avodah*:** It is written,[36](#_ftn1885) "And you shall love... with all your heart, and with all your soul, and with all your might." The beginning of the *avodah* is "with all your heart." Even though it is a complete *ratzo* with all his heart ("with all your heart—with both your inclinations"),[37](#_ftn1886) it is still no more than what the heart contains—only in the vessel of the heart and no more. Above this is the *avodah* of "with all your might," which is in a manner of going beyond the limits of the vessel, and it is above limitation.

This is "Hashem spoke..."—meaning that the order of *avodah* is from below to above. Initially, there must be the *avodah* from the perspective of the *Havayah* below, the *avodah* within the limitation of the *Seder Hishtalshelus*, which is the *ratzo* and *shov* of the aspect of *Memalei Kol Almin*. This is what our Sages said:[38](#_ftn1887) "Initially, when a person acts, he acts for his own sake"—meaning, in order to refine his soul to be in the state of *ratzo* and *shov* through the introduction of the matter of *kabbalas ol* (accepting the yoke), etc. And afterwards is the matter of "This is the statute of the Torah which Hashem has commanded"—the *Havayah* above, which is the *ratzo* and *shov* of *Sovev Kol Almin*, which goes beyond the category of limitation entirely. As our Rebbe the Alter Rebbe said:[39](#_ftn1888) "Whom have I in heaven? And with You, I desire nothing on earth,"[40](#_ftn1889) "I do not want Your Gan Eden, I do not want Your Olam HaBa... I want nothing but You alone." He does not desire revelations, etc.—this is the aspect of *ratzo* and *shov* of *Sovev Kol Almin*, the matter of the red heifer.

With this, we can also understand why we read the section of *Parah* before the section of *HaChodesh*. Through the *avodah* of the red heifer—the *ratzo* and *shov* of *Sovev Kol Almin*, which is in a manner of going beyond the category of limitation—there is then a revelation of the *Atzmus* (Essence), which is the matter of the *Geulah* (Redemption) (the section of *HaChodesh*), the complete *Geulah* that will be speedily in our days.

## With the help of Hashem. Sicha of Shabbos Parshas Shemini, Parshas Parah, Mevarchim HaChodesh Nissan, 5711

#### 335

*Unedited*

**1.** Regarding the Four Parshiyos (the third of which, Parshas Parah, is read this Shabbos)—the first two, Parshas Shekalim and Parshas Zachor, are read before Purim, and the last two, Parshas Parah and Parshas HaChodesh, are read after Purim, between Purim and Pesach.

In the terminology of the Gemara [explaining the reason for reading the Megillah in the Adar adjacent to Nissan, because "it is preferable to connect one redemption to another,"[1] "Purim to Pesach"[2]]—*between one redemption and another*: between the redemption of Purim, which was not a complete redemption, as the Gemara states[3] (explaining why we do not recite Hallel on Purim, because "we are still servants of Achashverosh"), and the redemption of Pesach, which was a complete redemption (and had they been worthy, the redemption from Egypt would have been a redemption after which there is no exile[4]), and like it will be the future redemption, may it come speedily in our days, a true and complete redemption, as it is written,[5] "As in the days of your exodus from the land of Egypt, I will show you wonders."

The reason we read these Parshiyos (Parah and HaChodesh) between Purim and Pesach is because of their connection to Pesach: Parshas HaChodesh speaks of the Korban Pesach, and Parshas Parah serves as a preparation for the Korban Pesach, "to warn the Jewish people to purify themselves so that they may perform their Pesach offerings in purity."[6]

***

**2.** Maamar beginning "Vayedaber... This is the statute of the Torah..."

***

**3.** Based on what was stated above (Section 1), that Parshas Parah is connected to the redemption of Pesach and, consequently, also to the true and complete redemption, it is understood that in Parshas Parah, the joy of the true and complete redemption is already felt.

#### 336

To preface this with the words of the Midrash[7] on the verse[8] "This is the statute of the Pesach" (which comes after the introduction "This is the statute of the Torah... and they shall take to you a red heifer"[9])—"This is what is meant by the verse,[10] 'The heart knows the bitterness of its soul, and in its joy, no stranger shall intermingle'... 'The heart knows the bitterness of its soul' refers to the Jewish people who were in Egypt in servitude, and when they were about to leave and the Holy One, Blessed be He, decreed upon them to perform the Pesach, the Egyptians came to eat with them. The Holy One said to them, 'Heaven forbid! No stranger shall eat of it'... 'In its joy, no stranger shall intermingle'":

The novelty in the words of the Midrash is that *the heart* feels *first*—even before the mind knows and understands. As we see tangibly, the heart feels pain and joy even from matters that have not yet arrived and are not yet known to the intellect in the mind, because the heart feels even that which the mind does not yet know or understand.

As we find in the revealed Torah—regarding the laws of fasting on Yom Kippur: "If a sick person says 'I need to eat' and a doctor says 'He does not need to,' we listen to the sick person. What is the reason? 'The heart knows the bitterness of its soul'"[11] (meaning "he feels within himself that he needs it"[12]). The explanation for this is: seemingly, since the doctor is the *expert in the science of medicine* more than the patient ("the doctor knows better"[11]), why do we listen to the patient and not the doctor? It is because the patient’s statement "I need to eat" does not come from understanding and comprehension in the intellect (in which case we would listen to the doctor, who is the expert in the science of medicine, and not the patient), but because *he feels in his heart* that he needs it, and the heart of the patient feels even that which the doctor does not know.

The reason the heart feels even what the mind does not know is because the heart is connected to the *essence of the soul*, as is known[13] that in the mind there is only the general inspiration of the soul, the general encompassing the details, whereas the essence of the soul (which is above the general and the details) resides specifically *in the heart*.

And this is also the precision of "in its joy (of the heart) no stranger shall intermingle"—that in the joy of the heart, which is connected to the essence of the soul, no one can intermingle, not even the mind, which is also considered a *stranger* in relation to the essence of the soul that resides in the heart.

And based on what was said, that joy is possible even regarding matters that one does not know about, because the heart feels even what the mind does not know—it is also understood regarding

#### 337

the joy connected with the redemption: that even before the mind knows about the redemption, the joy of the redemption can already exist due to the *feeling of the heart*.

And more than that—there must be the joy of the redemption, and the joy itself brings about the revelation of the redemption.

**4.** And more specifically:

The joy of the redemption due to the feeling of the heart is emphasized in our *Rebbes, the Nesi'im*, because the Rebbes are the *heart* of the Jewish people,

—The common expression in such matters is that the Nasi is the *head* (mind) of the Jewish people,[14] but we also find the expression that the Nasi is the *heart* of the Jewish people[15]—

For, in the heart resides the essence of the soul (as above), and likewise in the totality of the Jewish people, the Rebbes are the essence of the Jewish people, and therefore they are called the *heart* of the Jewish people.

And since the Rebbes are the heart of the Jewish people, the joy of the redemption is felt within them, and through them, the joy of the redemption is drawn into the heart of every single Jew (even when, on his own, the matter is not felt in his heart).

**5.** And regarding action—everyone must force himself to be in a state of joy:

Regarding joy that comes from the mind—it is possible to explain ("to argue") and prove that one must be in a state of joy, but regarding joy that is (above the mind) from the heart—everyone must force himself to be in a state of joy.

And it is understood that this matter is a mitzvah that is "in his body," such that one cannot fulfill his obligation through the joy of someone else; rather, everyone must strive himself to be in a state of joy.

(And the Rebbe concluded:) Take *l'chaim* and sing a joyful *nigun*.

[They sang a joyful *nigun*, and the Rebbe gestured with his holy hand to increase the joy.]

***

#### 338

**6.** What was said above regarding the joy of the heart, that "in its joy no stranger shall intermingle" because the heart is connected to the essence of the soul—is relevant to Parshas Parah (not only because it is a preparation for Pesach, but) also on its own merit:

It was explained above (in the *Maamar*[16]) what is stated in Parshas Parah, "This is the *statute* (chukas) of the Torah"—"chukas" comes from the word *chakikah* (engraving), like the letters of an engraving which are of the essence of the good stone upon which the letters are engraved, and they are not something foreign (like the letters of writing). That is to say, the matter of engraving is in a place where there is no room for anything else, because it is an *essential* matter.

[And it is understood that in addition to the essence, there is also the entire expansion,

—as the saying of the Rebbe Rashab, which he said on the last Purim of his life in this world (in the year 5680)[17]: "We will be complete, not only with our essence but also with the entire expansion"—

which is the concept of *ratzo* and *shov* in the red heifer,[18] that the movement of *shov* is from the essence, and the movement of *ratzo* is from the expansion.]

And since the red heifer is a matter of a *chukah*, an essential matter in which there is no room for anything else, for anything foreign—this is connected to the matter of "in its joy no stranger shall intermingle," the joy of the heart, which is from the essence of the soul, in which there is no room for anything else, for anything foreign.

**7.** And this matter is also hinted at in the *Haftorah* of Parshas Parah, in which the redemption is discussed:

In the introduction to the details of the redemption, "And I will take you from the nations and gather you from all the lands, etc.," [19] the verse emphasizes,[20] "*Not for your sake* do I act, O House of Israel, but for the sake of My holy name, which you have profaned among the nations where you have come" (as it elaborates on the details at the beginning of the *Haftorah*).

And seemingly, the emphasis that "not for your sake do I act" leads to *bitterness* ("the bitterness of its soul")—by *kal v'chomer* from what we find[21] regarding Chizkiyahu, that when "it was hung upon *the merit of others* (even though he 'hung it upon his own merit'), as it is written,[22] 'And I will defend this city to save it, for My sake and for the sake of David My servant,'" he said regarding this, "Behold, for peace *it was bitter to me, bitter*,"[23] "even at the time when the Holy One, Blessed be He, sent him peace, *it was bitter* to him," and all the more so

#### 339

in this case, where they emphasize the negation that "*not for your sake* do I act" because of undesirable conduct ("and they profaned My holy name"), this is certainly in a manner of "it was bitter to me, bitter."

And the answer to this:

First and foremost—similar to what we find in the Gemara[24] regarding the "birth pangs of Mashiach," "Let him come, and I will merit to sit in the shadow of the dung of his donkey," "meaning, even in such a way I want it, as long as I see him,"[25] and likewise in this case, that the main thing is that the redemption should come, even if it is not because of the merit of the Jewish people, "not for your sake." — "Let it be with your merit, let it be without your merit, as long as the redemption comes!"

And furthermore, and essentially—in relation to the complete redemption, it *does not matter and does not take up space* whether it is "for your sake" or "not for your sake," because in the complete redemption there will be the revelation of the *Atzmus* (the Essence), which is above all matters.

And this matter is emphasized in the *Haftorah* of Parshas Parah—because Parshas Parah is a "chukah," an essential matter, and in an essential matter (including also its expansion), the matter of "for your sake" or "not for your sake" does not matter, and consequently, the joy is in its completeness ("in its joy no stranger shall intermingle").

*

**8.** And it should be added that in Parshas Parah itself, "This is the statute of the Torah... and they shall take to you a red heifer," the matter of essentiality is emphasized *more* than it is as a preparation for Pesach, about which it is also said "This is the statute of the Pesach."[26]

By way of introduction—the regular order in the *Maamarim* of Chassidus of our Rebbes is that in the *Maamarim* of every *Yom Tov*, the superiority of that *Yom Tov* is explained, to the point that its superiority is magnified relative to other *Yomim Tovim*. For example: in the *Maamarim* of Rosh Hashanah, the greatness of the elevation of Rosh Hashanah is explained, that it is the most exalted matter ("there is no connection to say"...), the building of the *Malchus*, whose root is above all the *Sefiros*, etc.; and in the *Maamarim* of the festival of Pesach, the superiority of Pesach is explained, that it is more exalted than all matters. And likewise in the *Maamarim* of all the *Yomim Tovim*.

The reason for this—because during the time of this *Yom Tov*, the essence of this *Yom Tov* shines Above, and at this time, the superiority of this *Yom Tov* relative to all other *Yomim Tovim* is emphasized. And when the essence of this *Yom Tov* shines Above, this is drawn down and revealed also

#### 340

Below—through our Rebbes, including and especially through their speech in the *Maamarim* of Chassidus explaining the superiority of this *Yom Tov*.

And so it must be also among Chassidim—that at all times they must study (or at least speak) about the special superiority of this time, for through this, they draw down and reveal the matter Below.

And likewise in this case—that as we stand on Shabbos Parshas Parah, we must speak about the superiority of Parshas Parah also in relation to Parshas HaChodesh, in which the Korban Pesach is discussed.

**9.** And the matter of this:

The superiority of Parah relative to Pesach is explained in several *Maamarim* of Chassidus *of Parshas Parah*,[27] starting from the note of the Tzemach Tzedek in his glosses to *Likkutei Torah* [as is his way, clarifying ("warning") several matters in a few lines] at the end of the explanation on "This is the statute of the Torah"[28]: "And see further... regarding the matter of 'This is the statute of the Torah... and they shall take to you a red heifer' in *Midrash Rabbah*, end of Parshas Bo, Chapter 19."

And in the *Midrash* there—after the homily "This is the statute of the Pesach, this is what is meant by 'The heart knows... and in its joy no stranger shall intermingle'"—it says: "Let my heart be perfect in Your statutes,[29] this is the statute of the Pesach and the statute of the red heifer. Why? Because both are similar to one another. In this one it says 'This is the statute of the Pesach,' and in this one it says 'This is the statute of the Torah,' and you do not know which statute is greater than the other. A parable of two noblewomen who were similar, both walking together, appearing equal. Who is greater? The one whose friend accompanies her to her house and walks after her. So too, regarding Pesach it says 'statute,' and regarding the heifer it says 'statute,' *and who is greater? The heifer*, for those who eat the Pesach need it, as it is said,[30] 'And they shall take for the impure from the dust of the burning of the sin-offering.'"

And this is also the reason that we read Parshas Parah before Parshas HaChodesh—because in Parshas HaChodesh, the Korban Pesach is discussed, and since those who eat the Pesach need the purity of the red heifer, we precede Parshas Parah to Parshas HaChodesh.

From this it is understood that the matter of the "statute" in the red heifer is more exalted than the matter of the "statute" in the Korban Pesach—because in the Korban Pesach, the "statute" is only regarding *specific details*, whereas the totality of the matter of the Korban Pesach is not a statute, but rather it has

#### 341

a reason, as it is said,[31] "The Pesach offering is to Hashem, who passed over the houses of the children of Israel in Egypt when He struck the Egyptians and saved our houses," whereas the red heifer *whose entire essence* is a "statute."[32]

**10.** And the explanation of the matters regarding our subject—the essentiality in the "statute," from which the joy of the heart is made ("The heart knows... and in its joy no stranger shall intermingle"):

Seemingly, there is a superiority in Parshas HaChodesh, in which the Korban Pesach is discussed, relative to Parshas Parah, because the red heifer’s matter is purity from the impurity of death, which is connected with the matter of the opposite of purity, and it is only a preparation for the Korban Pesach, whereas the Korban Pesach is connected with the matter of the redemption, including and especially the true and complete redemption, when the prophecy will be fulfilled,[33] "And the spirit of impurity I will remove from the land."

And nevertheless, we emphasize the superiority of Parshas Parah specifically—because through it specifically, one comes to the elevation of the Korban Pesach (Parshas HaChodesh), as follows.

**11.** And it will be understood by way of what is explained regarding the superiority of the time of exile, that through the *avodah* in the time of exile specifically, one comes to the elevation of the days of Mashiach:[34]

The saying of the Rebbe Rayatz is known[35] that at the coming of Mashiach, "one will grab his head and scream" because they did not appreciate properly what they could have accomplished during the time of exile.

And seemingly, the opposite is logical, that at the coming of Mashiach one will be able to accomplish *incomparably more*—because in the time of exile there is double and redoubled darkness, there are worries of livelihood, etc., etc., whereas in the days of Mashiach, "good will be flowing in abundance and all delicacies will be as common as dust," "they will be free to engage in Torah and its wisdom," to the point that "the entire world will be occupied only with knowing Hashem" (as the Rambam states[36]), and if so, what is the matter of the wondrous superiority of the *avodah* of the time of exile specifically?

And the matter of this—that specifically through the *avodah* in the time of exile, one draws down the *Atzmus* (the Essence), because the *avodah* in the time of exile is the breaking and nullification of the concealment that comes from the double and redoubled darkness, and specifically through the breaking and nullification of the concealment, "one takes the *Atzmus*."

[The Rebbe Rayatz told that in Lubavitch there was one Chassid who would

#### 342

speak with fervor and *taanug* ("he used to cook with a taste") *in the parables* that are in the teachings of Chassidus, and one of the elder Chassidim said to him: Why do you speak with such *taanug* about *the parable*? It would be better if you spoke about *the subject of the parable*!

And regarding our subject: It is simple that the intention is not to say that there is a superiority in... double and redoubled darkness; the superiority is *in the breaking and nullification of the concealment*, through which one "takes" the *Atzmus*.]

And even though the revelation of the *Atzmus* will be in the future to come specifically, whereas in the time of exile it is not in revelation but in concealment—the superiority of the future to come is only regarding the matter of *the revelation*, but regarding the action of *drawing down the Atzmus*, "taking the *Atzmus*," this is done (not in the future to come, but) in the time of exile specifically, and therefore, the main superiority is in the *avodah* that is in the time of exile, through which one "takes" the *Atzmus*, and in the future to come there will only be the revelation of the matter.

**12.** According to this, it should also be explained regarding the superiority of Parshas Parah relative to Parshas HaChodesh:

Even though Parshas Parah is connected with the matter of the opposite of purity (impurity of death), and it is only a preparation for Parshas HaChodesh, in which the Korban Pesach and the redemption are discussed—it is similar to the *avodah* of the time of exile, which is connected with undesirable matters, and is only a preparation for the redemption, and nevertheless, the main superiority is in the *avodah* in the time of exile specifically, because through it, the *drawing down of the Atzmus* is accomplished.

And through this, there is also an addition to the joy of the heart connected with the redemption—"The heart knows... and in its joy no stranger shall intermingle," from the essence of the soul in which there is no room for anything foreign, which is the matter of the "statute," "This is the statute of the Torah," *avodah* that is from the essence of the soul through which the drawing down of the *Atzmus* is accomplished—because there is already the action of drawing down the *Atzmus*, even if it is in concealment (in addition to the fact that also regarding the revelation in the future to come—the heart already feels even what the mind does not yet know, as above).

**13.** And it should be added that the above matter is also regarding physical matters, children, life, and ample sustenance:

Even if sometimes there are things that conceal regarding children, life, and ample sustenance, one should not be affected by this, and one must know that afterwards (and through this) there will be an addition in all these matters in a more exalted manner.

And not only that, but even when the drawing down is still in concealment, there can and must already be the joy of the heart, "The heart knows... and in its joy no stranger shall intermingle," because the heart already feels even when the mind does not yet know, as above.

#### 343

And furthermore, and this is the main thing: because "heart" refers to our Rebbes, the *heart* of the Jewish people (as in Section 4)—through them, the drawing down from concealment to revelation is accomplished in all matters of children, life, and ample sustenance, both in spirituality,[37] love and fear (children), vitality in *Elokus* (life), and study of Torah (sustenance, as is known[38] that Torah is food and the *mitzvos* are garments), and in physicality in its literal sense, living and enduring offspring (children), healthy and complete life (life), and livelihood in abundance (ample sustenance).

## B"H

#### 344

It is a well-known saying of the Baal HaHillula regarding his students, that their task is to be "candles that illuminate."

The words of Tzaddikim in general, and specifically the words of the Nesi'ei Yisrael regarding their students and those connected to them, are precise, even in their details. This is also true of the title "candles that illuminate"—it serves as a guide for those connected to him in several fundamental matters.

Among them are the following:

There are several characteristics of a burning candle: The candle itself is a *source* of light—a luminary, albeit in *Ze'er Anpin*.

The candle consists of oil and a wick—and their significance in the analogy is as follows: The oil represents Torah and mitzvos[1](#_ftn1928). The wick represents the person, meaning the body[2](#_ftn1929), or more accurately, that part of the soul—the *nefesh*—which is the partner of the body[3](#_ftn1930), and on a deeper level, the *nefesh elokis* that is enclothed within the *nefesh habahamit*[4](#_ftn1931).

When the wick is lit and it and the oil unite, the candle shines with many lights[5](#_ftn1932). Collectively, these are two[6](#_ftn1933) types of light: *nehora ukma* (black light) and *nehora chivra* (white light)—*ha'alaah* (ascent) and *hamshacha* (drawing down).

Furthermore, there is a unique quality to the light of a candle: it is specifically suited for searching and examining hidden corners, crevices, and cracks—it probes all the chambers of the belly[7](#_ftn1934).

All these matters in the analogy are sufficiently understood and explained.

And the ultimate action—that through the fulfillment of all the above according to the instructions of the Baal

#### 345

HaHillula, the candle illuminates the portion of the world that belongs to it, and all the more so its own *nefesh habahamit* and *nefesh elokis*. This is the purpose of the soul’s descent into this world, and upon this depends the ultimate purpose of the days of Moshiach and the resurrection of the dead[8](#_ftn1935), which should happen speedily in our days, Amen.

**Menachem Schneerson**

*25 Adar Sheni, 5711*

*Brooklyn, N.Y.*

## With the help of Hashem. Resh-Dalet*, Thursday, 6 Nissan, 5711

#### 346

Unedited

My revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, related[1](#_ftn1936) regarding the Chassidim of the Tzemach Tzedek that they used to lend money to one another—not because of a need for the money, but because they possessed an awareness and a feeling ("they grasped") of the greatness of the virtue of the mitzvah of gemilus chasadim!

[And the Rebbe shlita concluded:] May Hashem grant that the giving of loans be not because of a need for the money, but because of an awareness of the greatness of the virtue of the mitzvah of gemilus chasadim.

[Afterward, the Rebbe shlita gave his contribution to the gemach fund.]

## Lot’s Wife: Does She Transmit Tumah?

#### 349

"Lot’s wife—does she transmit *tumah*? He said to them: A corpse transmits *tumah*, but a pillar of salt does not transmit *tumah* (*Niddah* 70b). The Shunamite’s son—does he transmit *tumah*? He said to them: A corpse transmits *tumah*, but a living person does not transmit *tumah*. Will the dead in the future require sprinkling [of the *parah adumah* ashes] for three and seven days, or will they not require it? He said to them: When they are resurrected, we will deliberate regarding them. Others say: When the *Mashiach* comes with them."

In *Tosafos* regarding the Shunamite’s son, it is taken as a given that he does not require sprinkling, as only the dead [require it], because it is written, "And I will sprinkle upon you." We must explain the reason for this distinction. Furthermore, we must address the question brought in the name of the *Rishonim*: Why did they not ask about the Zarephathite’s son, who preceded the Shunamite’s son? Additionally, we must explain why, after the first answer—that only a corpse transmits *tumah*—they continued to ask about the Shunamite’s son. There are several other points of precision as well.

One could explain: For the *tumah* of a corpse, two conditions are necessary: the departure of the soul, as the *Mishnah* in the first chapter of *Ohalos* states, "A corpse does not transmit *tumah* until its soul departs." And it must specifically be the soul of the body, not a specific limb. This is why there are several differences between the *tumah* of a corpse and the *tumah* of a limb from a living creature (*Eduyos*, chapter 6). Also, the preservation of the body’s physical existence is required, even if its form has changed—such as flesh that has dissolved into fluid, which transmits *tumah*, or bones that have decayed, as is found in *Nazir* (49 and there). Similarly, the essence of the blood (*tzalalta d’dama*—*Zevachim* 79a, *Chullin* 87b), and even if it was burned, provided its form was not distorted. But if it was burned until its form was distorted, or if it was crushed into flour, it is *tahor* (*Niddah* 27b, 55a). Perhaps the distinction is that in the latter case, it is no longer comparable to bone and blood, whereas in the former, it is.

Now, a pillar of salt is a miraculous phenomenon, as is found in *Berachos* (54b, *HaRo’eh*). A miracle can be explained in two ways: Either the miracle must be performed throughout the entire duration of its existence—just as in the plague of blood, where at every single moment of the plague, the miracle of turning water into blood was performed—or, conversely, the miracle occurred at the first moment, and from then on it remained water by nature, and it would actually require a miracle to turn it into blood. Now, the *Ribono shel Olam* does not perform a miracle for nothing if it is possible otherwise. If so, the aforementioned question depends on determining which is more difficult: repeating a simple act many times, or performing a difficult act once. This is similar to the *ibya* in *Shabbos* (beginning of *Mapanin*) regarding whether it is preferable to minimize [the *tumah*] by carrying or by walking. There, it is concluded that minimizing by walking is preferable, but *Tosafos* there explains that this only applies when there is no excessive exertion or when there is no need to change the custom. Thus, in our case, it remains a doubt.

This is the question of the men of Alexandria: The soul had departed, but there is a doubt whether at every single moment it is being turned into a pillar of salt. Because we do not perform a miracle for nothing to change its essence, it could be argued that the actual existence of her body did not change, only [to the extent]

#### 350

necessary for her punishment to be *middah k’neged middah*—she sinned with salt, therefore she was punished with salt. But she retained all other characteristics of a human body, as written in *Chiddushei Aggados* regarding the first matter. Consequently, it is a question of whether she transmits *tumah* or not.

An example of this is the ruling regarding *tumah* of food in the tenth chapter of *Mishnayos*: The urine of an animal does not render [food] susceptible to *tumah* (*machshirin*), which is from the *Tosefta* at the end of *Machshirin*. However, in *Bechoros* (7a) and the *Rambam* (*Hilchos Ma’achalos Asuros*, chapter 4, law 6), it is permitted because "water enters and water exits." Therefore, it must be that by entering the animal's body, the characteristic that distinguishes it from fruit juice is removed, yet it does not become like the animal's body, such as its milk.

Rabbi Yehoshua answered that however one resolves the two ways of viewing the miracle, it is irrelevant to our case—and therefore he called their words "words of ignorance"—because a corpse (that which is in the category of death) transmits *tumah*, meaning it was once alive and speaking. But a pillar of salt—which is inanimate or vegetative, as written at the end of *Sotah* 48—means that the miracle was a change to a category in which death is not applicable; therefore, it does not transmit *tumah*.

Regarding your second question: Regarding the Shunamite’s son, the question of the soul’s departure is not in the usual manner—unlike the first question, where the doubt exists because the death of the body is not in the usual manner. This is because in the *Tanach*, there are two similar accounts, that of the Zarephathite’s son and the Shunamite’s son. The *Tanach* distinguishes between them: in one, Eliyahu requested that the child’s soul return to him, and if so, it is obvious that he does not transmit *tumah* now, since the soul and body are as they were at his birth. But regarding the Shunamite’s son, it is recounted that he placed his mouth upon his mouth, and he bowed over him, etc., and it does not say that he returned his previous soul. Therefore, there is room for doubt. The connection between the departure of the soul and the *tumah* can be explained in two ways: Does the *moment* of the soul's departure cause the *tumah* for the entire duration that the corpse's frame is preserved, or does the departure of the soul cause a state of the body that transmits *tumah*? If so, in the case of the Shunamite’s son, where this state was terminated—for whatever reason—he no longer transmits *tumah*.

An example of this: Covering the blood. A special verse is required to make one liable for *kares*, and without that, the law of *hechsher* would be nullified from it, even if it was later revealed, in which case the law is that it does not need to be covered. Another example: One who was circumcised and then his *orlah* stretched—by Torah law, he does not need to be circumcised again and may eat *terumah* and the like (*Yevamos* 70b). Because the moment of circumcision...

Rabbi Yehoshua replied that however we interpret it, there is no practical difference—and therefore he called them "words of ignorance"—because a corpse transmits *tumah* only when its form has not been distorted, and there is no greater distortion of form than when it is alive.

Regarding your third question—and they did not ask about the Shunamite’s son simply, and I did not merit to understand this difficulty of *Tosafos*—for they only asked regarding what is practical now or in the future. But if the Shunamite’s son required sprinkling in his time, what would be the practical difference?

#### 351

The dead in the future: In both matters, it is not in the usual manner, for then the *One who returns* the previous souls to the previous bodies [will act]. And if so, even though it is obvious that they do not transmit *tumah* because a living person does not transmit *tumah*, since there are no "new faces" here at all—unlike the Shunamite’s son, who had a new soul, and therefore it is stated in *Sifrei Zuta* (cited in *Yalkut Shimoni*, *Chukas*, and this appears to be the source for the ruling of *Tosafos* that he does not require sprinkling)—if so, he must require sprinkling because he touched a corpse. And even though one hour before the resurrection of the dead, even the *tzaddikim* become dust (*Shabbos*, end of *Sho’el*), a corpse that has decayed also transmits *tumah*.

Rabbi Yehoshua said to them that these are "words of ignorance," for in any case, why ask about the Shunamite’s son? Because there is no practical difference now, and what is done is done. Similarly, regarding this, there is no practical difference now, for when they come, we will deliberate regarding them.

## Hadran on Shas

#### 352

**A.** The Sages taught: The people of Alexandria asked Rabbi Yehoshua ben Chananya three questions of folly. "Can the wife of Lot become ritually impure?" He said to them: "A corpse transmits impurity, but a pillar of salt does not transmit impurity" (Niddah 70b). "Can the son of the Shunammite woman become ritually impure?" He said to them: "A corpse transmits impurity, but a living person does not transmit impurity." "Do the dead in the time to come require sprinkling [of the ashes of the Red Heifer] on the third and seventh days, or do they not require it?" He said to them: "When they arise, we will deliberate on it for them." Some say: "When Moshe Rabbeinu comes with them."

Now, regarding the question "Do the dead in the time to come require sprinkling," it is stated in **Tosafos**[1](#_ftn1937) that regarding the son of the Shunammite, it is obvious to him that he does not require sprinkling, and the question is **only** regarding the **dead**, **because it is said**[2](#_ftn1938), "And I will sprinkle upon you." And it is **still necessary to understand** the **reason** and logic behind the **distinction** between the dead in the time to come and the son of the Shunammite.

**Likewise, it is necessary to understand the difficulty raised in the name of the Rishonim**[3](#_ftn1939) — **why** did they ask regarding the son of the Shunammite, and **not** regarding the **son of the Zarephathite**, even **though** the son of the Zarephathite, whom Eliyahu revived, **preceded the son of the Shunammite**, whom Elisha revived?

**It is also necessary to understand**: **After the first answer** (to the first question, "Can the wife of Lot become ritually impure?") **that only a corpse transmits impurity** — **why did they ask about the son of the Shunammite**? They already know that only a corpse transmits impurity, and consequently it is understood that the son of the Shunammite, who is not a corpse, does not transmit impurity.

**And several other points of precision.**

**B.** **One may explain** all of this — with a preface**:**

**For the impurity of a corpse** — **there must be two conditions:**

1) **The departure of the soul**, **as** it is stated in the **Mishnah, first chapter of Ohalos**[4](#_ftn1940): "A corpse

#### 353

does not transmit impurity until its soul departs." And specifically the departure of the **soul of the body**, **not** the departure of the vitality of a **specific limb; therefore**, we find **several distinctions between the impurity of a corpse and the impurity of a limb from a living creature (Eduyos, ch. 6**[5](#_ftn1941)**)**, because the law of corpse impurity applies only when the soul of the entire body has departed.

2) **The preservation of the body's existence**, **even if its form has changed**. **As in the case of flesh that has dissolved and become fluid**, **which transmits impurity**, **or bones that have decayed**, **as stated in Nazir (49a and there**[6](#_ftn1942)**)**, **and likewise the essence of the blood, the clear part of the blood (Zevachim 79b; Chullin 87b**[7](#_ftn1943)**)**, **and even if it was burned**, **if its form has not been distorted**, **it transmits impurity**. But if it was burned until its form was distorted**, **or if it was crushed and became like flour**, **it is pure (Niddah 27b, 55a**[8](#_ftn1944)**)**, because the existence of the body was not preserved. **— And perhaps one could say the distinction is that** as long as its form has not been distorted, **then** it is **still considered similar to bone and blood**, and therefore it transmits impurity, **whereas if its form has been distorted**, it does not.

**C.** **Now**, the transformation of Lot’s wife into a **pillar of salt** — **is a miraculous matter**, **as stated in Berachos (54b)** in the discussion regarding one who sees a *kispas* ("the crossings of the sea," the place where the Jewish people crossed the Red Sea) **and the hand of Moshe** ("the stone upon which Moshe sat, as it is written[9](#_ftn1945), 'And the hands of Moshe were heavy, and they took a stone, etc.'") — that one who sees the wife of Lot must offer praise and thanksgiving before the Omnipresent.

#### 354

**And regarding a miracle** — **it can be explained in two ways:**

The first way — **that the miracle must be performed throughout the entire duration of its existence. Just as in the sequence**[10](#_ftn1946) **where the water turned into blood**, **at every single moment of the duration of the plague, the miracle of turning the water into blood was performed.** Or the second way — **the opposite**, **that at the first moment the water turned into blood**, **and from then on it is water**[11](#_ftn1947) **by nature**, **and on the contrary**: in order to return the blood to water, **a miracle is required, similar to the first** miracle, **to turn the water into blood.**

The distinction between them: In the second way — the change is in the very existence of the water, that it turned into blood by nature, which is a greater and more difficult change, but on the other hand, this miracle is only once. Whereas in the first way — the change in the water (that it turned into blood) is only in its externality, and not in the very existence of the water, which is an easier change, but on the other hand, this miracle is repeated at every single moment of the duration of the plague.

**Now**, there is a principle that "**the Holy One, blessed be He, does not perform a miracle for no reason**"[12](#_ftn1948) — **if it is possible otherwise. And if so**, the **aforementioned** distinction regarding the manner of the miracle **depends on clarifying which is more difficult**: **repeating an easy thing** (a change in externality only, but) **many times** (at every moment of the duration of the plague), **or performing a difficult thing** (a change in the very existence of the water, that it became blood by nature, but only) **once.**

**And this is similar to the inquiry in Shabbos, at the beginning of the chapter 'Mefanin'**[13](#_ftn1949): **Is it preferable to minimize the load** and walk more (repeating an easy thing many times), **or** is it preferable to minimize **the walking**, even though it increases the load (performing a difficult thing once)**?**

**Now**, in Shabbos **there it is decided that minimizing the walking** and increasing the load **is preferable**, and from this it is proven also in our case that a miracle of performing a difficult thing once is preferable to repeating an easy thing many times. **However**, **in Tosafos there**[14](#_ftn1950) **it explains that this applies** (that it is preferable to minimize the walking and increase the load) **when there is no excessive exertion,**

#### 355

**or when there is no need to change the custom**, **and if so, in our case**, where it is a matter of performing a miracle whose nature is a change in the custom of the world — **it is still a doubt**, and there is room to say that repeating an easy thing many times is preferable to performing a difficult thing once.

**D.** **And this is the question of the people of Alexandria**, "Can the wife of Lot become ritually impure?":

Regarding the wife of Lot who turned into a **pillar of salt** — **the departure of the soul** (the first condition for corpse impurity) **was present here**, **but** regarding the preservation of the body's existence (the second condition for corpse impurity) — since regarding the manner of the miracle that she turned into a pillar of salt there is a **doubt whether** **at every single moment she is turned into a pillar of salt**, **because one does not perform a miracle for no reason to change** a human body **in its essence** to be a pillar of salt by nature — **then for this very reason one can say that the essence of her body's existence was not changed**, **and only to the extent necessary so that her punishment would be measure for measure**, **that she sinned with salt and therefore was afflicted with salt (Rashi, Vayeira 19:26)**, **but she possesses all the other characteristics of a human body**, **and similar to what is written in Chiddushei Aggados Maharsha**, "that even though she changed to become a pillar of salt in her form, **the original matter**, which is flesh, still exists," **and consequently she also transmits** corpse impurity,
