**Or not** — according to the view that the miracle was in such a way that at the first moment she turned into a pillar of salt and from then on she is a pillar of salt by nature, meaning, that the essence of her body's existence changed, and she no longer has the characteristics of a human body, and since the existence of the body was not preserved, she does not have the status of corpse impurity.

**An example of this** — in Halacha: The Rambam **ruled in Hilchos Tumas Ochlin, ch. 10, law 2, that the urine of an animal** is not like water and **does not render [food] susceptible to impurity**, **and this is from the Tosefta at the end of Machshirin. But in Bechoros 7a** and in Rambam, Hilchos Ma'achalos Asuros, ch. 4, law 6, he ruled **that it is permitted [to drink]**, **because** the existence of the water did not change in the animal's body, but rather "**water enters, water comes out**." And seemingly: since the existence of the water did not change in the animal's body — why does it "not render susceptible"? **And perforce one must say**, **that through the entry** of the water **into the animal's body**, **the characteristic that distinguishes between water** that renders susceptible **and fruit juice** that does not render susceptible **was removed, but** nevertheless, **it does not yet become like the body of the animal, like its milk**, and therefore it is permitted.

And similarly in our case: even though she changed in her form to be a pillar of salt, she did not become like the substance of salt, but rather the original matter of the flesh of a human body still remains, and therefore she transmits impurity[15](#_ftn1951).

#### 356

**And Rabbi Yehoshua answered** them, **that however the clarification of the two ways of the miracle may be**, **it is irrelevant to our case — and therefore it is called** "**words of folly**" **— because**, "a corpse transmits impurity, but a pillar of salt does not transmit impurity": **A corpse — that which is in the category of death — transmits impurity**, **and that is a living being and a speaker** who are in the category of death, **but a pillar of salt — [which is] inanimate and vegetative**, **as written at the end of Sefer Eitz Chayim**[16](#_ftn1952), is not in the category of death, and **this means**, **that the miracle** of the transformation into a pillar of salt **was in the change to the category of** inanimate and vegetative **in which death is not applicable**, and therefore, it makes no difference if the essence of the body's existence changed or if the characteristics of a human body remained in it, since in practice it is a pillar of salt, inanimate and vegetative, which is not in the category of death, and **consequently** **it does not transmit impurity.**

**E.** **And their second question** — "Can the son of the Shunammite become ritually impure?":

The question **regarding the son of the Shunammite** is not similar to the question regarding the wife of Lot, because **there** (regarding the son of the Shunammite) **the question** is from the aspect that **the departure of the soul is not in the usual manner** (as follows) **— whereas** in the **first question** the **doubt** is **because the death of the body is not in the usual manner.**

**And the explanation of this is** — **because in the Scripture** we find **two similar stories**, one story **regarding the son of the Zarephathite**, **and** the second story regarding the **son of the Shunammite**. **And the Scripture distinguishes** between them — **because**: **In the first** story (regarding the son of the Zarephathite) **Eliyahu requested that the soul of the child return to him**[17], **and if so**, **it is obvious that he does not transmit impurity now** (after the departure of the soul was nullified and his soul returned to him), **since the soul and the body** are **as they were at his birth. But regarding the son of the Shunammite it is told that he placed his mouth upon his mouth and he leaned over him, etc.**[18](#_ftn1953), meaning, that he introduced a new vitality into him, **and not that he returned his previous soul to him** (which remained in a state of departure).

**And if so**, regarding the son of the Shunammite there is **room for doubt** whether he transmits impurity or not, **because**, the **connection** of the **departure of the soul to the matter of impurity** — **can be said in two ways:**

**If the moment of the departure of the soul causes the impurity for the entire duration of time that the skeleton of the corpse is preserved**, and if so, the departure of the soul of the son of the Shunammite (whose previous soul departed and never returned to him again) causes the impurity for the entire duration of time that his body exists, even after a new vitality entered him,

#### 357

**or that the departure of the soul causes such a state of the body** (a body without vitality) **that it transmits impurity**, **and if so**, **regarding the son of the Shunammite, where this state** (of a body without vitality) **was terminated — for whatever reason it may be** (even if the reason is that a new vitality entered him) **— he no longer transmits impurity.**

An example[19](#_ftn1954) of this — in Halacha: Covering the blood — **and a special verse is required that** blood that is covered **is liable for Kares**[20](#_ftn1955), **and were it not for this, the law of blood would be nullified from it entirely**[21](#_ftn1956), even regarding the **law of susceptibility to** impurity — **even though it was later uncovered**, **and then the law is that it does not need to be covered** again[22](#_ftn1957), because the moment of covering acts upon the entire duration of time thereafter that it is considered covered blood. Another example: One circumcised and then his foreskin was drawn — **that by Torah law he does not need to be circumcised again**, **and he eats Terumah and the like (Yevamos 72a**[23](#_ftn1958)**)**, because the moment of circumcision acts upon the entire duration of time thereafter that he is not called uncircumcised. And similarly in our case, that the moment of the departure of the soul causes the impurity for the entire duration of time that his body exists.

And according to this, it is well understood that even after the answer to the first question that only a corpse transmits impurity, there is room for the question of whether the son of the Shunammite transmits impurity (even though he is not a corpse) — for since the action of the departure of the soul was not nullified, it causes impurity in the body from which it departed for the entire duration of time thereafter (even after a new vitality entered him).

**And Rabbi Yehoshua answered** them, **that however we interpret** the manner of the connection of the departure of the soul to the matter of impurity, **it makes no difference** to the law of the son of the Shunammite **— and therefore it is called** "**words of folly**" **— because**, "a corpse transmits impurity, but a living person does not transmit impurity": **A corpse transmits impurity**, **but** only on the condition that **its form has not been distorted** (as mentioned above in section 2)**, while in our case, **there is no distortion of the form** of a corpse **greater than this, when he is alive.**

**F. And their third question** — "Do the dead in the time to come require sprinkling on the third and seventh days, or do they not require it?":

And by way of preface **—** that they asked the law of sprinkling regarding the dead in the time to come, **and did not ask regarding the son of the Shunammite**, is understood **simply** — **and I did not merit to understand this difficulty of**

#### 358

**Tosafos — because they only asked regarding what is relevant**, **now**, **or in the future**, **but if the son of the Shunammite required sprinkling in his time, then** — **what difference does it make**[24](#_ftn1959).

And an explanation of the question whether the dead in the time to come require sprinkling:

**The dead in the time to come** are obviously not transmitting impurity, since **in the two matters** that are conditions for corpse impurity — the departure of the soul and the preservation of the existence of the corpse's body — **it is not in the usual manner**[25](#_ftn1960), **because then it will be** **the One who returns** **the previous souls to the previous bodies**.

**And if so**, **even though it is obvious that** the dead in the time to come **do not transmit impurity** because **then** they will be alive and **a living person does not transmit impurity**, **but**, for this very reason there is room to say that sprinkling is required, for **since there are no new aspects at all**, but rather the return of his previous existence, the previous soul in the previous body,

**— whereas regarding the son of the Shunammite there was a new soul**, **and therefore it is stated in Sifrei Zuta, cited in Yalkut Shimoni, Chukas**[26](#_ftn1961) (**and apparently this is the source for the aforementioned ruling of Tosafos**) **that** the son of the Shunammite **does not require sprinkling**[27](#_ftn1962) **—**

**If so**, **he must be in need of sprinkling because he touched a corpse** — his own body which was previously a corpse**.**

**And even though one hour before the resurrection of the dead even the righteous become dust (Shabbos, end of chapter 'Sho'el'**[28](#_ftn1963)**)**, and if so there is no touching of a corpse here — **a corpse that has decayed also transmits impurity** (as mentioned above in section 2)**.**

**And Rabbi Yehoshua said to them that this is** "**words of folly**", **for in any event**:

#### 359

**Why do they not ask regarding the son of the Shunammite** — **because it makes no difference now**, **and what has been, has been**[29](#_ftn1964), **so also in this** (regarding the dead in the time to come) **it makes no difference now**, **because when they come, we will deliberate on it for them.**

\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*

#### 360

Two types of witnesses: Those who *perform* the matter in their presence, whereby it is *clarified* that the matter was performed. Witnesses of action and witnesses of clarification. An example of this: Witnesses who testify that one deposited a deposit with his fellow, that so-and-so killed a person, they do not perform anything by the fact that they were present at the time of the event, rather they *clarify* that so-and-so did this matter.

Now, seemingly, also regarding witnesses of *kiddushin* (betrothal) one could say that this is their function, but in truth it is not so; rather, they are a part of the matter of *kiddushin*. Just as there must be money, a ring, and the intent of the man and the woman, so too there must be the presence of witnesses, because this is a *part* of the matter of *kiddushin*. With this, it is understood why in a *shvuas ha'edus* (oath of testimony) by Torah law, those disqualified from testimony by the Sages are exempt, whereas in *kiddushin* (Shulchan Aruch, Even HaEzer 42:6) it is required that a *get* (divorce) be given out of doubt, as the Tzemach Tzedek questioned in Responsa Even HaEzer, sec. 24, and answered that it is different, for in *shvuas ha'edus* the testimony would not have helped at all. The explanation for this is that those disqualified by the Sages are such that the Sages said not to consider their *testimony*, but it is not that the essence of the person has changed (like one who changed by becoming a relative through marriage, where the essence changed). Therefore, in *shvuas ha'edus*, where their entire function is only the clarification, and this was denied to them, nothing remains and they have no name of testimony at all. Whereas in *kiddushin*, where their presence performs [the act], their essence has not changed.

Also in this, the law of *chakirah v'drishah* (inquiry and interrogation) regarding witnesses of *kiddushin* is understood. For in the Rema (Even HaEzer 42:4) it is ruled that *chakirah v'drishah* is not required. And in the Beis Yosef there, that this is the opinion of most authorities. And even though the Tzemach Tzedek (Responsa Even HaEzer 123) infers that the opinion of the Rambam is not so, the end of the responsum is missing there, and also in this one can say the reason is according to the aforementioned: for *chakirah v'drishah* must be when the testimony is regarding before the final verdict, meaning before the matter (the verdict) was performed, whereas when they testify that the verdict was finalized in such-and-such a court, *chakirah v'drishah* is not required even in capital cases (Rambam, Hilchos Sanhedrin, end of ch. 13; Makkos 5a). And the explanation is that *chakirah v'drishah* is found to be required for the performance of the essence, but not for the clarification. — And according to this, in *kiddushin*, where the *witnesses* perform the essence at the time of the *kiddushin*, then afterwards it is an *additional* matter, like those testifying that the verdict was finalized in such-and-such a court (and see regarding all this in Responsa of the Ridvaz 9-10).

And a moral lesson from the aforementioned. The prophet said (Yeshayahu 43:10), "You are My witnesses, says Hashem, etc., I, I am Hashem." That the entire Jewish people is a witness to the fact that "I am Hashem." Now, there are two ways in this. The lesser way — witnesses of clarification, meaning that all the Jewish people testify that they know from generation to generation until the standing at Mount Sinai that "I am Hashem your G-d," and He is the One who commanded you all the Torah and mitzvos. And this too is a great thing, but for greater things the Jewish people were created, and it is hinted at in the words of our Sages (Shabbos), that one who says "Vayechulu, etc." is a *partner* in the work of creation, that the Jewish people through their deeds are not only

#### 361

publicizing His G-dliness in the world, but also taking an *active* part. In every work of creation, they *make* the physical a *vessel* for G-dliness.

A moral lesson in the life of each and every one: There is a *method* that a person should be satisfied with his own four cubits, that he behaves according to the Torah and mitzvos, and is not active in what is outside of this. And this is not the demand of the Chassidic method, for our Sages said, "All of Israel are responsible for one another," and the slogan is *Ahavas Yisrael* (love of a fellow Jew), and to be interested in all his affairs in an active manner, meaning an essential matter, that in his entire being he performs and draws down G-dliness into the world. The greatest wedding is that of G-dliness and all of creation. And the Jewish people are the witnesses who perform *parts* of the *kiddushin*, and not just to clarify the matter.

In this case, there is the foundation for a sure hope, that the couple will not be satisfied with standing on the sidelines and mere clarification, but based on what they were taught and saw in the home of their parents in the involvement and dissemination of the light of Torah and mitzvos in their entire environment, surely they too will go in this path and build their home on the foundations of Torah and mitzvos, until the righteous Redeemer comes and takes us out of exile in the true redemption and leads us to our Holy Land, may it be built and established speedily in our days, Amen.

\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*

#### 362

**A.** There are **two types of witnesses**[1](#_ftn1965)**:** (a) **Those who perform the matter in their presence,** (b) **Those through whom it is clarified that the matter was performed.** And this is: **witnesses of action and witnesses of clarification.**

**An example of this** (for the second type, witnesses of clarification)**: Witnesses who testify that one deposited a deposit with his fellow,** or **that so-and-so killed a person** — **they do not perform anything by the fact that they were present at the time of the event**, **but rather they clarify that so-and-so did this matter.**

**Now**, **seemingly, also regarding witnesses of kiddushin one could say that this is their function** — only *to clarify* that the kiddushin was performed.

**But in truth it is not so**, **because they** (the witnesses) **are a part of the matter of kiddushin**. **Just as** in kiddushin **there must be money** (or **a ring**) **and the intent of the man and the woman**, **so too there must be the presence of witnesses**, **because this is a part of the matter of kiddushin.**

**B.** **And with this**[2](#_ftn1966) **it is understood why in a shvuas ha'edus (oath of testimony) by Torah law, those disqualified from testimony by the Sages are exempt**[3](#_ftn1967)**, whereas in kiddushin** we rule **(Shulchan Aruch, Even HaEzer 42:6)** regarding one who betroths with those disqualified by the Sages **that a get is required out of doubt**,

— **as the Tzemach Tzedek questioned** in **Responsa Even HaEzer, sec. 24**[4](#_ftn1968), **and answered**[5](#_ftn1969),

#### 363

**that shvuas ha'edus is different, for in the end, his testimony would not have helped at all** —

**And the explanation for this is**:

**That**, indeed, **those disqualified from testimony by the Sages are such that the Sages said not to consider their testimony**, **but it is not that the essence of the person has changed** to be disqualified for testimony **(like one who changed by becoming a relative through marriage, where the essence of the person changed to be disqualified for testimony)**.

**Therefore**, **in shvuas ha'edus, where the entire function** of the witnesses **is only the clarification**, **and this matter was denied to them** by the Sages who said not to consider their testimony — **nothing remains, and they have no name of testimony at all**[6](#_ftn1970)**. Whereas in kiddushin, where their presence performs** the act of kiddushin, **and** indeed **the essence of the witnesses has not changed** due to the disqualification by the Sages.

**C.** **And also**, **in this the law of inquiry and interrogation regarding witnesses of kiddushin is understood**:

**For in the Rema (Even HaEzer 42:4) it is ruled that inquiry and interrogation is not required. And in the Beis Yosef there, that this is the opinion of most authorities**[7](#_ftn1971)**. And even though the Tzemach Tzedek (Responsa Even HaEzer 123**[8](#_ftn1972)**) infers that the opinion of the Rambam is not so, the end of the responsum is missing there**, and consequently the conclusion of the Tzemach Tzedek regarding this was not clarified.

**And also in this one can say the reason is according to the aforementioned**:

**For inquiry and interrogation must be when the testimony is regarding before the final verdict, meaning before the matter (the verdict) was performed, whereas when they testify that the verdict was finalized in such-and-such a court, inquiry and interrogation is not required even in capital cases (Rambam, Hilchos Sanhedrin, end of ch. 13; Makkos 5a**[9](#_ftn1973)**)**?

#### 364

**And the explanation** for this — **that inquiry and interrogation is found to be required for the performance of the essence** (of the matter — the verdict in court, which is performed based on the words of the witnesses, after the inquiry and interrogation, etc.), **but not for the clarification** (when the verdict has already been finalized, and they testify that the verdict was finalized in such-and-such a court)[10](#_ftn1974)**.**

**And according to this**: **In kiddushin**, **where the witnesses perform the essence at the time of the kiddushin**, **then** the testimony **afterwards** (after the kiddushin was performed) **is an additional matter**, **like those testifying that the verdict was finalized in such-and-such a court**, and therefore they do not require inquiry and interrogation **(and see regarding all this in Responsa of the Ridvaz 9-10**[11](#_ftn1975)**).**

**D.** **And a moral lesson from all of the aforementioned**:

**The prophet said (Yeshayahu 43:10-11)**, "**You are My witnesses, says Hashem, etc., I, I am Hashem**"**,** meaning, **that the entire Jewish people is a "witness" to the fact that "I am Hashem."**

**Now**, **there are two ways in this**:

**The lesser way** — **witnesses of clarification**, **meaning that all the Jewish people testify that they know from generation to generation until the standing at Mount Sinai** where **six hundred thousand** Jewish people were present, **that "I am Hashem your G-d,"**[12](#_ftn1976) **and He is the One who commanded you all the Torah and mitzvos.**

**And this too** (the matter of witnesses of clarification) **is a great thing, but for greater things the Jewish people were created** — to also be witnesses of action[13](#_ftn1977),

**And** this matter **is hinted at in the words of our Sages (Shabbos 119b)**, "**One who prays on Erev Shabbos and says 'Vayechulu, etc.' is made a partner to the Holy One, blessed be He, in the work of creation**," meaning, **that the Jewish people through their deeds are not only publicizing His G-dliness in the world** (witnesses of clarification) **but also taking an active part**, witnesses of action, **in the entire work of creation** — **that they make the physical a vessel for G-dliness.**

**E.** And **a moral lesson in the life of each and every one** of the Jewish people:

#### 365

There is **a method that a person should be satisfied** with his action **within his four cubits, that he behaves according to the Torah and mitzvos, and is not active in what is outside of this** (and this is only that his conduct within his four cubits acts in a way of "by itself" also outside, to those who see him, etc. — which is similar to witnesses of clarification).

**And this is not the demand of the Chassidic method** — **for our Sages said**[14](#_ftn1978), "**All of Israel are responsible for one another**," **and the slogan** of the Chassidic method is **Ahavas Yisrael (love of a fellow Jew), and to be interested in all the affairs of the other in an active manner**, **meaning** that his action is **an essential matter**, **that in his entire being he performs and draws down G-dliness into the world.**

**F.** And the general matter of witnesses of action in the service of man belongs to a wedding (as mentioned above that witnesses of kiddushin are witnesses of action) — for, **the greatest wedding** is **that of G-dliness and all of creation**[15](#_ftn1979)**, and the Jewish people are the witnesses who perform parts of the kiddushin, and not just to clarify the matter.**

**G.** **In this case**[16](#_ftn1980) **there is the foundation for a sure hope, that the couple will not be satisfied with standing on the sidelines and mere clarification** (witnesses of clarification), **but rather, based on what they were taught and saw in the home of their parents, in the involvement and dissemination of the light of Torah and mitzvos in their entire environment** (which is the matter of witnesses of action) — **surely they too will go in this path,**

**And build their home on the foundations of Torah and mitzvos,**

**Until the righteous Redeemer comes and takes us out of exile in the true redemption and leads us to our Holy Land, may it be built and established speedily in our days, Amen.**

\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*
